**Yogeshwari**

**ŚRĪMAD BHAGAVAD GĪTĀ**
**A Yogic Commentary**
**Shailendra Sharma**

© 2015 Shailendra Sharma
ISBN-10: 151436610X

Translation by: Maria Pistunova, Lydia Guturenko,
Sergei Nazarov, Aditya Vikram Naredi
Design and layout: Farida Idiyatullina
Author's photograph: Natasha Kurarar

To seekers of truth

Holding this yogic key
To the knowledge of Time,
How much longer must I call out alone?
And who will even listen?
Looking at me, seemingly limited in Time,
Who will believe that I speak
Of Time Itself?

**9**
**Preface**

Scholars who systematically study the Gītā are well aware that it expounds Brahma-vidyā (the teaching of the knowledge of the Absolute) and Yoga-śāstra (the science of yoga). The Gītā elucidates ancient yogic techniques, the practice of which bestows the ability to receive the direct darśana of Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa, the dazzlingly brilliant embodiment of Time.

Many respected scholars have written commentaries on this great sacred scripture. Yet I will venture to state that within the scholarly community, a yogic commentary on the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, set forth by a yogi, is evidently lacking. The only yogic interpretation was left about one hundred years ago by the great Guru of Kriya Yoga, Śrī Śyāmācaraṇa Lahirī Mahāśaya, and was intended for his close disciples. In his commentary, for the benefit of his disciples, he revealed the secret of the ancient practice of yoga expounded in the Gītā.

Taking into consideration the circumstances of time and place, I felt the necessity for a modern yogic interpretation of the Gītā that could be useful both for ordinary people and for experienced practitioners of yoga. The knowledge presented in this commentary was received through the lineage of the great Gurus of Kriya Yoga and is the result of the practice of this ancient discipline.

Shailendra Sharma
1992

**10**
**Brahma, Vishnu, and Shiva**

The ancient sages cognized the three states of the universe and represented the deities presiding over them as Brahmā – the creator of the universe, Viṣṇu – its preserver, and Śiva – the destroyer. Reflecting on these symbols in the light of modern understanding leads us to a new interpretation of them.

The foundation of the universe is matter. Wherever one looks, its many forms are manifested everywhere. From the grossest to the subtlest, matter in all its immensity is manifested in the infinity of the universe. The term "Brahmā" (as well as Brahman) means "boundless immensity." It is a symbol of the limitlessness of matter, the foundation of the entire visible world. It can be said that the essence of the consciousness of Conscious Matter the sages named with the word "Brahmā."

As is known from the sacred scriptures, Lord Viṣṇu, containing the entire universe within Himself, is its preserver and support. Reflecting on this, one can discover that matter is contained within nothing other than emptiness, or free space. This is also confirmed by the following: studying the smallest particle of matter – the atom – we find that between its nucleus and the electrons moving around it, there also exists emptiness. Emptiness is the foundation of the movement of matter. The sages realized the capacity of emptiness to contain matter and gave the consciousness of Conscious Emptiness the name Viṣṇu.

When, dividing matter, we reach the atom, and then split even that, we can obtain pure energy. In our striving to investigate energy, to seek out its primal cause, reaching its true source, we discover that energy arises from pure thought. Pure thought, which we may also call the consciousness of Matter, is generated by Conscious Emptiness. It is pure thought that is the connecting link between Matter and Emptiness.

**11**

Beyond these two there is a third element, which fills both Matter and Emptiness and is also the cause of their complete destruction. This element is outside everything and yet is everywhere; it is motionless, though it appears to move; our consciousness, due to different levels of perception, observes it in different, mutually distinct forms. This element, Time, or Kāla, the sages called Śiva. Time is that element which we constantly perceive, yet it continues to remain beyond perception. The time of Matter is considered limited; the time of Emptiness, which contains matter, was also realized by the sages, but who, other than Time Itself, can comprehend the time of Time?

We often reflect: "What existed when there was no universe, no emptiness, not even the real and the unreal?" Those who have practiced yoga and succeeded in awakening their consciousness have been able to understand: that which existed then was in the womb of Time, and whence it arose there – who will tell of this, other than Time Itself? Perhaps it is for this reason that the sages represented Śiva in the form of Ardhanārīśvara. From this it follows that Time Itself conceived from Time, and in due time, Time was born, taking the form of the universe. And only Time will remain when the time of the universe comes to an end.

**śrīmadbhagavadgītā**
**ŚRĪMAD**
**BHAGAVAD GĪTĀ**

**prathamō'dhyāyaḥ arjunaviṣādayōgaḥ**
**Chapter 1**
**THE YOGA OF ARJUNA'S DESPAIR**

**16**

**dhṛtarāṣṭra uvāca**
**dharmakśētrē kurukśētrē samavētā yuyutsavaḥ |**
**māmakāḥ pāṇḍāvāścāiva kimakurvata sañjaya || 1-1||**

Dhṛtarāṣṭra said:
"O Sañjaya! What did my sons and the sons of Pāṇḍu, gathered on the sacred field of Kurukṣetra, eager for battle, do?"

**sañjaya uvāca**
**drṣṭvā tu pāṇḍavānīkaṁ vyuḍhaṁ duryōdhanastadā |**
**ācāryamupasaṅgamya rājā racanamabravīt || 1-2||**

Sañjaya said:
"Having seen the army of the Pāṇḍavas drawn up in battle array, King Duryodhana approached the ācārya and spoke:

**ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya**
**Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya**

**17**
**Chapter 1**

**paśyaitāṁ pāṇḍuputrāṇāmācārya mahatīṁ camūm |**
**vyūḍhāṁ drupadaputrēṇa tava śiṣyēṇa dhīmatā || 1-3||**

'O teacher, please, look upon this great army of the sons of Pāṇḍu, arrayed by your wise disciple, the son of Drupada¹.

**atra śūrā mahēṣvāsā bhīmārjunasamā yudhi |**
**yuyudhānō virāṭaśca drupadaśca mahārathaḥ || 1-4||**

Here, on this battlefield, are great archers, heroes among heroes, equal to Bhīma and Arjuna in battle. Here are Yuyudhāna, Virāṭa, and the great warrior Drupada.

**dhṛṣṭakētuścēkitānaḥ kāśirājaśca vīryavān |**
**purujitkuntibhōjaśca śaibyaśca narapuṅgavaḥ || 1-5||**

Here are Dhṛṣṭaketu, Cekitāna, the mighty king of Kāśī, Kuntibhoja, Purujit, and Śaibya, the best of men.

**yudhāmanyuśca vikrānta uttamaujāśca vīryavān |**
**saubhadrō draupadēyāśca sarva ēva mahārathāḥ || 1-6||**

The valiant Yudhāmanyu, the mighty Uttamaujas, the sons of Subhadrā and Draupadī – all of them are great warriors.

¹ Dhṛṣṭadyumna, the brother-in-law of Arjuna

**18**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

**asmākaṁ tu viśiṣṭā yē tānnibōdha dvijōttama |**
**nāyakā mama sainyasya saṁjñārthaṁ tānbravīmi tē || 1-7||**

O best of brāhmaṇas! Please, also know the principal warriors on our side. I will enumerate their names for you.

**bhavānbhīṣmaśca karṇaśca kṛpaśca samitiṁjayaḥ |**
**aśvatthāmā vikarṇaśca saumadattistathāiva ca || 1-8||**
**anyē ca bahavaḥ śūrā madarthē tyaktajīvitāḥ |**
**nānāśastrapraharaṇāḥ sarvē yuddhaviśāradāḥ || 1-9||**

You yourself, the great Bhīṣma, Karṇa, Kṛpācārya who is victorious in battles, as well as Aśvatthāmā, Vikarṇa, the son of Somadatta, and many other heroes, ready to sacrifice their lives for me. All of them are well-armed and skilled in combat.

**aparyāptaṁ tadasmākaṁ balaṁ bhīṣmābhirakśitam |**
**paryāptaṁ tvidamētēṣāṁ balaṁ bhīmābhirakśitam || 1-10||**

Our forces, protected by Bhīṣma, are immeasurable, while their forces, protected by Bhīma, are limited.

**ayanēṣu ca sarvēṣu yathābhāgamavasthitāḥ |**
**bhīṣmamēvābhirakśantu bhavantaḥ sarva ēva hi || 1-11||**

Each of you must protect Bhīṣma in every way, having taken your respective positions in the formation on the battlefield.'

**19**
**Chapter 1**

**tasya saṁjanayanharṣaṁ kuruvṛddhaḥ pitāmahaḥ |**
**siṁhanādaṁ vinadyōccaiḥ śaṅkhaṁ dadhmau pratāpavān || 1-12||**

Then Bhīṣma, the valiant elder of the Kaurava dynasty, cheering him², loudly blew his conch, emitting a sound like a lion's roar.

**tataḥ śaṅkhāśca bhēryaśca paṇavānakagōmukhāḥ |**
**sahasaivābhyahanyanta sa śabdastumulō'bhavat || 1-13||**

Then conches and trumpets, large and small drums, sounded forth. This sound was exceedingly terrifying.

**tataḥ śvētairhayairyuktē mahati syandanē sthitau |**
**mādhavaḥ pāṇḍavaścaiva divyāu śaṅkhāu pradaghmatuḥ || 1-14||**

Then, seated on a great chariot yoked with white horses, Mādhava³ and Pāṇḍava⁴ also blew their divine conches.

**pāñcajanyaṁ hṛṣīkēśō dēvadattaṁ dhanañjayaḥ |**
**pauṇḍraṁ dadhmau mahāśaṅkhaṁ bhīmakarmā vṛkōdaraḥ || 1-15||**

Hṛṣīkeśa⁵ blew the conch Pāñcajanya; Dhanañjaya⁶ blew the conch Devadatta; and the terrible in his deeds Vṛkodara⁷ blew the mighty conch Pauṇḍra.

² Duryodhana
³ Kṛṣṇa
⁴ Arjuna
⁵ Kṛṣṇa
⁶ Arjuna
⁷ Bhīma

**20**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

anantavijayaṁ rājā kuntīputrō yudhiṣṭhiraḥ ।
nakulaḥ sahadēvaśca sughōṣamaṇipuṣpakau ॥ 1-16॥

King Yudhishthira, the son of Kunti, blew into Anantavijaya, and Nakula and Sahadeva into Sughosha and Manipushpaka.

kāśyaśca paramēṣvāsaḥ śikhaṇḍī ca mahārathaḥ ।
dhṛṣṭadyumnō virāṭaśca sātyakiścāparājitaḥ ॥ 1-17॥

The great archer, the King of Kashi, the mighty hero Shikhandi, Dhrishtadyumna, Virata, and the invincible Satyaki.

drupadō draupadēyāśca sarvaśaḥ pṛthivīpatē ।
saubhadraśca mahābāhuḥ śaṅkhāndadhmuḥ pṛthakpṛthak ॥ 1-18॥

And also, O Lord of the Earth, Drupada, the sons of Draupadi, and the great hero, the son of Subhadra—all of them blew their conches.

sa ghōṣō dhārtarāṣṭrāṇāṁ hṛdayāni vyadārayat ।
nabhaśca pṛthivīṁ caiva tumulō’bhyanunādayan ॥ 1-19॥

From that terrible sound, which resounded through heaven and earth with a roar, the hearts of the sons of Dhritarashtra trembled.

**21**
**Chapter 1**

atha vyavasthitāndṛṣṭvā dhārtarāṣṭrānkapidhvajaḥ ।
pravṛttē śastrasaṁpātē dhanurudyamya pāṇḍavaḥ ॥ 1-20॥
hṛṣīkēśaṁ tadā vākyamidamāha mahīpatē ।
sēnayōrubhayōrmadhyē rathaṁ sthāpaya mē’cyuta ॥ 1-21॥

Then Kapidhvaja, the son of Pandu, gazing upon the sons of Dhritarashtra who stood there, raised his bow when all was ready for battle, and spoke these words to Hrishikesha: “O Achyuta, I pray you, place my chariot between the two armies,

yāvadētānirikśē’haṁ yōddhukāmānavasthitān ।
kairmayā saha yōddhavyamasmin raṇasamudyamē ॥ 1-22॥

So that I may behold those warriors who stand here eager for battle, and know with whom I must fight.

yōtsyamānānavēkśē’haṁ ya ētētra samāgatāḥ ।
dhārtarāṣṭrasya durbuddhēryuddhē priyacikīrṣavaḥ ॥ 1-23॥

I wish to see the warriors who have gathered here, desiring to please the evil-minded son of Dhritarashtra in this war.”

**22**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

sañjaya uvāca
ēvamuktō hṛṣīkēśō guḍākēśēna bhārata ।
sēnayōrubhayōrmadhyē sthāpayitvā rathōttamam ॥ 1-24॥
bhīṣmadrōṇapramukhataḥ sarvēṣāṁ ca mahīkśitām ।
uvāca pārtha paśyaitānsamavētānkurūniti ॥ 1-25॥

Sanjaya said:
“O Bharata! Thus addressed by Gudakesha, Hrishikesha placed that excellent chariot between the two armies, before Bhishma, Drona, and all the other kings, and said: ‘O Partha! Behold this assembly of Kauravas.’”

tatrāpaśyatsthitānpārthaḥ pitṝnatha pitāmahān ।
ācāryānmātulānbhrātṛnputrānpautrānsakhīṁstathā ॥ 1-26॥
śvaśurānsuhṛdaścaiva sēnayōrubhayōrapi ।
tānsamīkśya sa kauntēyaḥ sarvānbandhūnavasthitān ॥ 1-27॥
kṛpayā parayāviṣṭō viṣīdannidamabravīt ।

Arjuna saw fathers, grandfathers, teachers, maternal uncles, brothers, sons, grandsons, friends, fathers-in-law, and well-wishers, arrayed in both armies. Beholding all those kinsmen standing there, Kaunteya, overwhelmed with profound compassion, spoke thus in despondency.

**23**
**Chapter 1**

arjuna uvāca
dṛṣṭvēmaṁ svajanaṁ kṛṣṇa yuyutsuṁ samupasthitam ॥ 1-28॥
sīdanti mama gātrāṇi mukhaṁ ca pariśuṣyati ।
vēpathuśca śarīrē mē rōmaharṣaśca jāyatē ॥ 1-29॥

Arjuna said:
“O Krishna! Seeing my own people gathered here eager for battle, my limbs grow weak, my mouth becomes dry. My body trembles, and my hair stands on end.

gāṇḍīvaṁ straṁsatē hastāt tvakcaiva paridahyatē ।
na ca śaknōmyavasthātuṁ bhramatīva ca mē manaḥ ॥ 1-30॥

The bow Gandiva slips from my hand, my skin burns, and my mind is bewildered. I am unable to stand steady.

nimittāni ca paśyāmi viparītāni kēśava ।
na ca śrēyō’nupaśyāmi hatvā svajanamāhavē ॥ 1-31॥

O Keshava! I see only inauspicious omens, and I foresee no good in killing my own people in battle.

**24**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

na kāṅkśē vijayaṁ kṛṣṇa na ca rājyaṁ sukhāni ca ।
kiṁ nō rājyēna gōvinda kiṁ bhōgairjīvitēna vā ॥ 1-32॥

O Krishna! I desire neither victory, nor a kingdom, nor pleasures. O Govinda, of what use is a kingdom to us? What is the purpose of enjoyments or even of life itself?

yēṣāmarthē kāṅkśitaṁ nō rājyaṁ bhōgāḥ sukhāni ca ।
ta imē’vasthitā yuddhē prāṇāṁstyaktvā dhanāni ca ॥ 1-33॥

Those for whose sake we desire a kingdom, enjoyments, and happiness—they stand here in this army, having renounced their wealth and their very lives.

ācāryāḥ pitaraḥ putrāstathaiva ca pitāmahāḥ ।
mātulāḥ śvaśurāḥ pautrāḥ śyālāḥ sambandhinastathā ॥ 1-34॥

Here are teachers, fathers, sons, and also grandfathers, maternal uncles, fathers-in-law, grandsons, brothers-in-law, and other relatives.

ētānna hantumicchāmi ghnatō’pi madhusūdana ।
api trailōkyarājyasya hētōḥ kiṁ nu mahīkṛtē ॥ 1-35॥

O Madhusudana! Even if I were to be killed, I do not wish to slay them—not even for the sake of sovereignty over the three worlds; how much less for the earth?

**25**
**Chapter 1**

nihatya dhārtarāṣṭrānnaḥ kā prītiḥ syājanārdana ।
pāpamēvāśrayēdasmānhatvaitānātatāyinaḥ ॥ 1-36॥

O Janardana! What joy could we have in killing the sons of Dhritarashtra? Only sin would accrue to us from slaying these aggressors.

tasmānnārhā vayaṁ hantuṁ dhārtarāṣṭrānsvabāndhavān ।
svajanaṁ hi kathaṁ hatvā sukhinaḥ syāma mādhava ॥ 1-37॥

O Madhava! We ought not to kill the sons of Dhritarashtra, our own kinsmen. How could we be happy by killing our own people?

yadyapyētē na paśyanti lōbhōpahatacētasaḥ ।
kulakśayakṛtaṁ dōṣaṁ mitradrōhē ca pātakam ॥ 1-38॥

Though their minds are clouded by greed, and they see no wrong in the destruction of the family or the sin of betraying friends,

kathaṁ na jñēyamasmābhiḥ pāpādasmānnivartitum ।
kulakśayakṛtaṁ dōṣaṁ prapaśyadbhiranārdana ॥ 1-39॥

O Janardana, why should we not have the wisdom to turn away from this sin, we who clearly see the evil of destroying the family?

**26**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

kulakśayē praṇaśyanti kuladharmāḥ sanātanāḥ ।
dharmē naṣṭē kulaṁ kṛtsnamadharmō’bhibhavaty uta ॥ 1-40॥

With the destruction of the family, the eternal family traditions are destroyed. When dharma perishes, the entire family is overtaken by adharma.

adharmābhibhavātkṛṣṇa praduṣyanti kulastriyaḥ ।
strīṣu duṣṭāsu vārṣṇēya jāyatē varṇasaṅkaraḥ ॥ 1-41॥

O Shri Krishna! When adharma prevails, the women of the family become corrupt. O Varshneya, when women are corrupted, the mixing of varnas arises.

saṁkarō narakāyaiva kulaghnānāṁ kulasya ca ।
patanti pitarō hyēṣāṁ luptapiṇḍōdakakriyāḥ ॥ 1-42॥

This mixing of varnas leads the destroyers of the family and the family itself to hell. For their ancestors fall, deprived of the offerings of pinda and tarpanā.

dōṣairētaiḥ kulaghnānāṁ varṇasaṁkarakārakaiḥ ।
utsādyantē jātidharmāḥ kuladharmāśca śāśvatāḥ ॥ 1-43॥

Through these misdeeds of the destroyers of the family, which cause the mixing of castes, the eternal laws of the jātis and the family traditions are destroyed.

**27**
**Chapter 1**

utsannakuladharmāṇāṁ manuṣyāṇāṁ janārdana ।
narakē’niyataṁ vāsō bhavatītyanuśuśruma ॥ 1-44॥

O Janardana! We have heard that for men whose family traditions are destroyed, an indefinite dwelling in hell is ordained.

ahō bata mahatpāpaṁ kartuṁ vyavasitā vayam ।
yadrājyasukhalōbhēna hantuṁ svajanamudyatāḥ ॥ 1-45॥

Alas! How grievous it is that we are resolved to commit a great sin. Driven by the greed for the pleasures of a kingdom, we are prepared to kill our own people.

yadi māmapratīkāramaśastraṁ śastrapāṇayaḥ ।
dhārtarāṣṭrā raṇē hanyustanmē kśēmataraṁ bhavēt ॥ 1-46॥

It would be better for me if the sons of Dhritarashtra, with weapons in hand, were to slay me in battle, unarmed and unresisting.”

sañjaya uvāca
ēvamuktvārjunaḥ saṅkhyē rathōpastha upāviśat ।
visṛjya saśaraṁ cāpaṁ śōkasaṁvignamānasaḥ ॥ 1-47॥

Sanjaya said:
“Having spoken thus on the battlefield, Arjuna sat down in the chariot, casting aside his bow and arrows, his mind overwhelmed with sorrow.”

**28**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē rjunaviṣādayōgō nāma prathamō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 1॥

Om Tat Sat
Thus ends the first chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Arjuna’s Despair,” from the dialogue between Shri Krishna and Arjuna in the Upanishad of the Shrimad Bhagavad Gita, which expounds the knowledge of Brahman [Brahma-Vidya] and the science of yoga [Yoga-Shastra].

**dvitīyō’dhyāyaḥ sāṅkhyayōgaḥ**
**Chapter 2**
**THE YOGA OF DISCRIMINATION**

**30**

sañjaya uvāca
taṁ tathā kṛpayāviṣṭamaśrupūrṇākulēkśaṇam ।
viṣīdantamidaṁ vākyamuvāca madhusūdanaḥ ॥ 2-1॥

Sanjaya said:
“Then, to Arjuna, who was thus overwhelmed with compassion, his eyes filled with tears of sorrow, Madhusudana spoke these words.

śrībhagavān uvāca
kutastvā kaśmalamidaṁ viṣamē samupasthitam ।
anāryajuṣṭamasvargyamakīrtikaramarjuna ॥ 2-2॥

The Lord said:
“O Arjuna, whence has this delusion come upon you in this hour of crisis? It is not befitting of noble souls; it does not lead to heaven, nor will it bring you glory.

ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya
Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**31**
**Chapter 2**

क्लैब्यं मा स्म गमः पार्थ नैतत्त्वय्युपपद्यते ।
क्षुद्रं हृदयदौर्बल्यं त्यक्त्वोत्तिष्ठ परन्तप ॥२-३॥
klaibyaṁ mā sma gamaḥ pārtha naitattvayyupapadyatē ।
kśudraṁ hṛdayadaurbalyaṁ tyaktvōttiṣṭha parantapa ॥ 2-3॥

“O Pārtha, do not yield to impotence; it does not befit you. O Parantapa¹, cast aside this petty weakness of heart and prepare for battle.”

अर्जुन उवाच
कथं भीष्ममहं संख्ये द्रोणं च मधुसूदन ।
इषुभिः प्रति योत्स्यामि पूजार्हावरिसूदन ॥२-४॥
arjuna uvāca
kathaṁ bhīṣmamahaṁ sāṁkhyē drōṇaṁ ca madhusūdana ।
iṣubhiḥ pratiyōtsyāmi pūjārhāvarisūdana ॥ 2-4॥

Arjuna said:
“O Madhusūdana, how can I shoot arrows in battle at Bhīṣma and Droṇa? For I revere them both!

गुरूनहत्वा हि महानुभावान् श्रेयो भोक्तुं भैक्ष्यमपीह लोके ।
हत्वार्थकामांस्तु गुरूनिहैव भुञ्जीय भोगान् रुधिरप्रदिग्धान् ॥२-५॥
gurūnahatvā hi mahānubhāvān śrēyō bhōktuṁ bhaikśyamapīha lōkē ।
hatvārthakāmāṁstu gurunihaiva bhuñjīya bhōgān rudhirapradigdhān ॥ 2-5॥

It would be better to beg for alms in this world than to slay such great teachers. Having slain them, I would enjoy wealth and sensual pleasures stained with blood.

न चैतद्विद्मः कतरन्नो गरीयो यद्वा जयेम यदि वा नो जयेयुः ।
यानेव हत्वा न जिजीविषामस्तेऽवस्थिताः प्रमुखे धार्तराष्ट्राः ॥२-६॥
na caitadvidmaḥ katarannō garīyō yadvā jayēma yadi vā nō jayēyuḥ ।
yānēva hatvā na jijīviṣāmastē’vasthitāḥ pramukhē dhārtarāṣṭrāḥ ॥ 2-6॥

We do not know which is better for us: whether we shall conquer them or they shall conquer us. Before us stand the sons of Dhṛtarāṣṭra, having slain whom we would not wish to live ourselves.

---

**32**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

कार्पण्यदोषोपहतस्वभावः पृच्छामि त्वां धर्मसम्मूढचेताः ।
यच्छ्रेयः स्यान्निश्चितं ब्रूहि तन्मे शिष्यस्तेऽहं शाधि मां त्वां प्रपन्नम् ॥२-७॥
kārpaṇyadōṣōpahatasvabhāvaḥ pṛcchāmi tvāṁ dharmasammūḍhacētāḥ ।
yacchrēyaḥ syānniścitaṁ brūhi tanmē śiṣyastē’haṁ śādhi māṁ tvāṁ prapannam ॥ 2-7॥

Standing at a crossroads, I am filled with pity and do not understand what my duty is; therefore I, your devoted disciple, ask you: teach me what is best.

न हि प्रपश्यामि ममापनुद्याद् यच्छोकमुच्छोषणमिन्द्रियाणाम् ।
अवाप्य भूमावसपत्नमृद्धं राज्यं सुराणामपि चाधिपत्यम् ॥२-८॥
na hi prapaśyāmi mamāpanud yādyacchōkamucchōṣaṇamindriyāṇām ।
avāpya bhūmāvasapatnamṛddhaṁ rājyaṁ surāṇāmapi cādhipatyam ॥ 2-8॥

Even a kingdom abounding in plenty and sovereignty over the gods could not dispel the grief that withers my senses.”

सञ्जय उवाच
एवमुक्त्वा हृषीकेशं गुडाकेशः परन्तप ।
न योत्स्य इति गोविन्दमुक्त्वा तूष्णीं बभूव ह ॥२-९॥
sañjaya uvāca
ēvamuktvā hṛṣīkēśaṁ guḍākēśaḥ parantapa ।
na yōtsya iti gōvindamuktvā tūṣṇīṁ babhūva ha ॥ 2-9॥

Sañjaya said:
“O Parantapa! Having spoken thus to Hṛṣīkeśa, saying clearly, ‘Govinda, I will not fight!’ – Guḍākeśa fell silent.

तमुवाच हृषीकेशः प्रहसन्निव भारत ।
सेनयोरुभयोर्मध्ये विषीदन्तमिदं वचः ॥२-१०॥
tamuvāca hṛṣīkēśaḥ prahasanniva bhārata ।
sēnayōrubhayōrmadhyē viṣīdantamidaṁ vacaḥ ॥ 2-10॥

O Bhārata! To him, standing in sorrow between the two armies, Hṛṣīkeśa, as if smiling, spoke these words.

---

**33**
**Chapter 2**

श्रीभगवानुवाच
अशोच्यानन्वशोचस्त्वं प्रज्ञावादांश्च भाषसे ।
गतासूनगतासूंश्च नानुशोचन्ति पण्डिताः ॥२-११॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
aśōcyānanvaśōcastvaṁ prajñāvādāṁśca bhāṣasē ।
gatāsūnagatāsūṁśca nānuśōcanti paṇḍitāḥ ॥ 2-11॥

The Lord said:
“You grieve for those who are not to be grieved for, and yet you speak words of wisdom. The wise do not sorrow for the living nor for the dead.

Those who have not attained self-realization, as well as those who do not even suspect the conscious presence manifesting through the body, when faced with death, repeat the sayings of the wise and grieve for what does not deserve grief. But the wise, who have known the immeasurable consciousness hidden in this body, have been able to understand that in reality it is prāṇa interacting with prāṇa, consciousness with consciousness, and the body is merely an intermediary. For such great souls, there is no difference between the presence or absence of the body.

न त्वेवाहं जातु नासं न त्वं नेमे जनाधिपाः ।
न चैव न भविष्यामः सर्वे वयमतः परम् ॥२-१२॥
na tvēvāhaṁ jātu nāsaṁ na tvaṁ nēmē janādhipāḥ ।
na caiva na bhaviṣyāmaḥ sarvē vayamataḥ param ॥ 2-12॥

Never was there a time when I did not exist, nor you, nor these rulers of men. Nor shall we all cease to exist hereafter.

Whether consciousness manifests through the body or not, its unmanifest presence exists eternally. Nor should one think that when any particular manifestation of consciousness comes to an end, consciousness itself also ceases to exist. Whether manifesting or remaining unmanifest, consciousness is always present.

☝
☝

---

**34**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

देहिनोऽस्मिन्यथा देहे कौमारं यौवनं जरा ।
तथा देहान्तरप्राप्तिर्धीरस्तत्र न मुह्यति ॥२-१३॥
dēhinō’sminyathā dēhē kaumāraṁ yauvanaṁ jarā ।
tathā dēhāntaraprāptirdhīrastatra na muhyati ॥ 2-13॥

Just as in this body the embodied one passes through childhood, youth, and old age, so does the embodied one obtain another body. The wise are not deluded concerning this.

That unmanifest consciousness, manifesting through the body and always present in everyone’s mind as the feeling ‘I am’, the ancient ṛṣis called ‘Ātman’. This consciousness, being manifest in the body, appears limited by three states – childhood, youth, and old age. When the body withers, consciousness, leaving the weakened body, manifests itself by means of a new one.

मात्रास्पर्शास्तु कौन्तेय शीतोष्णसुखदुःखदाः ।
आगमापायिनोऽनित्यास्तांस्तितिक्षस्व भारत ॥२-१४॥
mātrāsparśāstu kauntēya śītōṣṇasukhaduḥkhadāḥ ।
āgamāpāyinō’nityāstāṁstitikśasva bhārata ॥ 2-14॥

O Kaunteya! The contacts of the senses with their objects give rise to sensations of cold and heat, pleasure and pain, but these sensations are transient. Endure them calmly, O Bhārata.

Manifesting through the body and accepting the limitations of the body and sense organs, consciousness perceives objects that give rise to sensations of cold and heat, pleasure and pain. One should realize the relativity of these sensations and then, by applying effort, attempt to transcend physical limitations, awakening that immeasurable consciousness which slumbers within everyone.

☝
☝

---

**35**
**Chapter 2**

यं हि न व्यथयन्त्येते पुरुषं पुरुषर्षभ ।
समदुःखसुखं धीरं सोऽमृतत्वाय कल्पते ॥२-१५॥
yaṁ hi na vyathayantyētē puruṣaṁ puruṣarṣabha ।
samaduḥkhasukhaṁ dhīraṁ sō’mṛtatvāya kalpatē ॥ 2-15॥

O Puruṣarṣabha²! That great man who holds pleasure and pain as equal, remaining steadfast – he alone is worthy of immortality.

The sage who has realized the relativity of pleasure and pain knows that, due to differences in points of view, the same situation appears as pain to one and as pleasure to another. He who has realized this truth also understands that life and death are merely different facets of that boundless consciousness, perceived because it changes the means of its manifestation. Understanding this, he awakens the entire boundlessness of his slumbering consciousness, passes through death, knowing the true nature of unmanifest Time, and establishes himself in eternity, beyond death.

नासतो विद्यते भावो नाभावो विद्यते सतः ।
उभयोरपि दृष्टोऽन्तस्त्वनयोस्तत्त्वदर्शिभिः ॥२-१६॥
nāsatō vidyatē bhāvō nābhāvō vidyatē sataḥ ।
ubhayōrapi dṛṣṭō’antastvanayōstattvadarśibhiḥ ॥ 2-16॥

The unreal [Asat] has no existence; the real [Sat] cannot cease to exist. Those who have seen the truth have examined the nature of both.

Ordinary people are able to use only a small part of their total consciousness, which the wise have called the conscious mind. And the boundless consciousness in its fullness, slumbering within everyone and abiding beyond the mind of ordinary people, the wise have called the unconscious mind. When speaking of the true and the untrue, the real and the unreal, it is meant that the dormant consciousness of the mind is
²“Best of men”
☝
☝

---

**36**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

untrue, and the awakened consciousness is true. The wise understand the relativity of sleeping and awakened consciousness. Practicing yoga, they rise above the limitations of the body and succeed in awakening the entire boundlessness of their mind. For such people, the untrue no longer exists. They realize that, although the untrue appears to exist because consciousness sleeps, the truth nevertheless always exists. This applies to all people, whether they have awakened their sleeping consciousness or not – in its fullness, consciousness is present in everyone.

अविनाशि तु तद्विद्धि येन सर्वमिदं ततम् ।
विनाशमव्ययस्यास्य न कश्चित्कर्तुमर्हति ॥२-१७॥
avināśi tu tadviddhi yēna sarvamidaṁ tatam ।
vināśamavyayasyāsya na kaścitkartumarhati ॥ 2-17॥

Know That to be indestructible, by which all this is pervaded. No one is capable of destroying That imperishable one.

This dazzlingly radiant unmanifest Time manifests through the entire visible world. It is indestructible – no one is capable of destroying the truth of this eternal Time.

अन्तवन्त इमे देहा नित्यस्योक्ताः शरीरिणः ।
अनाशिनोऽप्रमेयस्य तस्माद्युध्यस्व भारत ॥२-१८॥
antavanta imē dēhā nityasyōktāḥ śarīriṇaḥ ।
anāśinō’pramēyasya tasmādyudhyasva bhārata ॥ 2-18॥

All physical bodies are declared to be perishable, but That which is embodied in them is indestructible, boundless, and eternal. Therefore, O Bhārata, fight!

All this creation is manifested by That unbearably radiant unmanifest Time. From That same Unmanifest arises the mind, possessing boundless consciousness and manifesting this physical body. Despite the undoubted reality of the physical existence of the body, serving as a means of
☝
☝

---

**37**
**Chapter 2**

obtaining experience for that boundless mind, this body is not the dominant factor in the relationship of mind and body. The boundless mind, by awakening its sleeping consciousness with the help of this body, is able to know the true essence of its Creator – the Light of all light, Time. The body, which is the support of that immeasurable consciousness, is perishable, but that consciousness manifesting through the body is eternal, boundless, and indestructible.

य एनं वेत्ति हन्तारं यश्चैनं मन्यते हतम् ।
उभौ तौ न विजानीतो नायं हन्ति न हन्यते ॥२-१९॥
ya ēnaṁ vētti hantāraṁ yaścainaṁ manyatē hatam ।
ubhau tau na vijānītō nāyaṁ hanti na hanyatē ॥ 2-19॥

Those who think that It kills, and those who think that It can be killed – both are in delusion: It does not kill, nor can It be killed.

Some believe that after the destruction of the physical body, the boundless consciousness manifesting through it also ceases to exist. Others believe that by destroying someone’s body, they are able to destroy their consciousness as well. Both the former and the latter think thus because they do not realize the presence of the boundlessness hidden within the physical body. They cannot understand that that conscious presence which manifests the body is eternal and therefore cannot be destroyed in any way.

न जायते म्रियते वा कदाचिन्नायं भूत्वा भविता वा न भूयः ।
अजो नित्यः शाश्वतोऽयं पुराणो न हन्यते हन्यमाने शरीरे ॥२-२०॥
na jāyatē mriyatē vā kadācinnāyaṁ bhūtvā bhavitā vā na bhūyaḥ ।
ajō nityaḥ śāśvatō’yaṁ purāṇō na hanyatē hanyamānē śarīrē ॥ 2-20॥

It is never born, nor does it ever die. This has neither beginning, nor middle, nor end. It is unborn, eternal, immortal, and ancient. It is not destroyed even when the body is destroyed.

The consciousness that transcends the physical body is boundless.
☝
☝

**38**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

of the mind, manifestations of Time, was never born and never
will die. This unmanifest conscious presence is
eternal, unborn, immortal, and ancient. When one
body that manifests it is destroyed, it creates a new one to again
manifest itself.

वेदाविनाशिनं नित्यं य एनमजमव्ययम् ।
कथं स पुरुषः पार्थ कं घातयति हन्ति कम् ॥२-२१॥
vēdāvināśinaṁ nityaṁ ya ēnamajamavyayam ।
kathaṁ sa puruṣaḥ pārtha kaṁ ghātayati hanti kam ॥ 2-21॥

O Partha! Knowing This as indestructible, constant, unborn,
and unending, how can one kill or cause to kill?

For one who, rising above the limitations of the body, has realized
the entire boundlessness of consciousness, the manifestations of This
dazzlingly radiant Time, the physical body becomes secondary,
and the consciousness that manifests it becomes paramount.
Such people have been able to understand that life and death, essentially,
are different manifestations of that one Presence
and are perceived as such only because of Its limitation by physical
boundaries. For such great people, who have awakened their
consciousness in all its immeasurability by overcoming the limitations
of the body, there is no difference between life and death.

वासांसि जीर्णानि यथा विहाय नवानि गृह्णाति नरोऽपराणि ।
तथा शरीराणि विहाय जीर्णान्यन्यानि संयाति नवानि देही ॥२-२२॥
vāsāṁsi jīrṇāni yathā vihāya navāni gṛhṇāti narō’parāṇi ।
tathā śarīrāṇi vihāya jīrṇānyanyāni saṁyāti navāni dēhī ॥ 2-22॥

Just as a person, casting off worn-out garments, takes up new ones,
so does It abandon old bodies and acquire new ones.

Just as a person leaves his old clothes and
puts on new ones (and by the appearance of the clothes one can guess
the personal qualities and temperament of their owner), the boundless mind manifests
itself through various bodies. When the possibilities of one body
☝
☝

**39**
**Chapter 2**
for acquiring experience are exhausted, this immeasurable consciousness,
for the sake of self-knowledge, manifests itself through a new body.

नैनं छिन्दन्ति शस्त्राणि नैनं दहति पावकः ।
न चैनं क्लेदयन्त्यापो न शोषयति मारुतः ॥२-२३॥
nainaṁ chindanti śastrāṇi nainaṁ dahati pāvakaḥ ।
na cainaṁ klēdayantyāpō na śōṣayati mārutaḥ ॥ 2-23॥

Weapons do not cut It, fire does not burn It, water does not
wet It, wind does not dry It.

That boundless consciousness, abiding beyond the body, cannot
be cut by weapons or burned by flame, wetted by water,
or dried by wind. Like space, it is perceived
by everyone and yet is beyond reach.

अच्छेद्योऽयमदाह्योऽयमक्लेद्योऽशोष्य एव च ।
नित्यः सर्वगतः स्थाणुरचलोऽयं सनातनः ॥२-२४॥
acchēdyō’yamadāhyō’yamaklēdyō’śōṣya ēva ca ।
nityaḥ sarvagataḥ sthāṇuracalō’yaṁ sanātanaḥ ॥ 2-24॥

It is indivisible, incombustible, It cannot be wetted or
dried. It is eternal, all-pervading, immovable,
perfect, and primeval.

The boundless consciousness of the mind is indivisible, it cannot be burned,
wetted, or dried. It is all-pervading, infinite,
constant, perfect, and primeval.

अव्यक्तोऽयमचिन्त्योऽयमविकार्योऽयमुच्यते ।
तस्मादेवं विदित्वैनं नानुशोचितुमर्हसि ॥२-२५॥
avyaktō’yamacintyō’yamavikaryō’yamucyatē ।
tasmādēvaṁ viditvainaṁ nānuśōcitumarhasi ॥ 2-25॥

It is unmanifest, It is inconceivable and is described as unchangeable. Having realized this, you should not grieve.
☝
☝

**40**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

The boundless consciousness, manifesting through the body,
remains hidden for those whose mind is limited by physical boundaries. Being the embodiment of that unmanifest Time, it
is not subject to change. Those who have come to such an understanding
as a result of their practice of yoga do not grieve for those people whose
consciousness is limited by the body.

अथ चैनं नित्यजातं नित्यं वा मन्यसे मृतम् ।
तथापि त्वं महाबाहो नैवं शोचितुमर्हसि ॥२-२६॥
atha cainaṁ nityajātaṁ nityaṁ vā manyasē mṛtam ।
tathāpi tvaṁ mahābāhō naivaṁ śōcitumarhasi ॥ 2-26॥

O Mahabaho³, and even if you consider that It is born
again and again, and also again and again dies, you should not
grieve so.

जातस्य हि ध्रुवो मृत्युर्ध्रुवं जन्म मृतस्य च ।
तस्मादपरिहार्येऽर्थे न त्वं शोचितुमर्हसि ॥२-२७॥
jātasya hi dhruvō mṛtyurdhruvaṁ janma mṛtasya ca ।
tasmādaparihāryē’rthē na tvaṁ śōcitumarhasi ॥ 2-27॥

Since death inevitably follows birth, and birth is inevitable
after death, you should not grieve over these
unavoidable phenomena.

And even if one considers the body as paramount, just as
death is inevitable after birth, birth also must be
inevitable after death. Having understood only this truth,
a person with limited perception is able to overcome
grief.

³"Mighty-armed"
☝
☝

**41**
**Chapter 2**

अव्यक्तादीनि भूतानि व्यक्तमध्यानि भारत ।
अव्यक्तनिधनान्येव तत्र का परिदेवना ॥२-२८॥
avyaktādīni bhūtāni vyaktamadhyāni bhārata ।
avyaktanidhanānyēva tatra kā paridēvanā ॥ 2-28॥

All beings are unmanifest before birth and after death.
They are manifest only in the interval between birth
and death. What is the use of grieving over this?

That boundless consciousness, the manifestation of Time, abides
unmanifest before it gains the support of a body, and even
after it leaves the body. The evidence of that immeasurable consciousness
becomes clear only when it manifests itself through the body. Those
who have transcended physical limitations and established themselves in
that boundless consciousness can understand the interrelation of birth
and death. For such people, there is no difference whether the body
exists or not.

आश्चर्यवत्पश्यति कश्चिदेनमाश्चर्यवद्वदति तथैव चान्यः ।
आश्चर्यवच्चैनमन्यः शृणोति श्रुत्वाप्येनं वेद न चैव कश्चित् ॥२-२९॥
āścaryavatpaśyati kaścidēnamāścaryavadvadati tathaiva cānyaḥ ।
āścaryavaccainamanyaḥ śṛṇōti śrutvāpyēnaṁ vēda na caiva kaścit ॥ 2-29॥

Some perceive This with wonder, others describe
This as a miracle, others listen about This in amazement, but having heard,
still cannot grasp even a particle of This.

That yogi who, through the practice of Kriya, plunges into the depths
of dhyana, experiences the conscious Presence manifesting
through the body. Since this is a new experience, he experiences that
unmanifest consciousness with extreme wonder. The words
used to describe that Presence are also full of amazement.
Those who listen to these accounts are also amazed, since they have
no conception of the unmanifest Presence beyond
life. They are unable to comprehend this unmanifest boundless
consciousness merely by hearing about it.
☝
☝

**42**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

देही नित्यमवध्योऽयं देहे सर्वस्य भारत ।
तस्मात्सर्वाणि भूतानि न त्वं शोचितुमर्हसि ॥२-३०॥
dēhī nityamavadhyō’yaṁ dēhē sarvasya bhārata ।
tasmātsarvāṇi bhūtāni na tvaṁ śōcitumarhasi ॥ 2-30॥

O Bharata! That Presence dwelling in the body of everyone
cannot be killed, therefore do not grieve for all embodied beings.

The conscious Presence that is manifested by infinite
Time through life is also infinite. Only the means of Its manifestation
come to an end.

स्वधर्ममपि चावेक्ष्य न विकम्पितुमर्हसि ।
धर्म्याद्धि युद्धाच्छ्रेयोऽन्यत्क्षत्रियस्य न विद्यते ॥२-३१॥
svadharmamapi cāvēkśya na vikampitumarhasi ।
dharmyāddhi yuddhācchrēyō’nyatkśatriyasya na vidyatē ॥ 2-31॥

And even from the standpoint of dharma you should not waver, for
there is nothing more sacred for a warrior [kshatriya] than a righteous war.

Having told Arjuna about the immeasurable conscious
Presence hidden in the body, Lord Krishna continues his explanations from
the position of one limited by physical boundaries.
Arjuna belonged to the kshatriya varna. The natural duty
of a warrior is not to shrink from battle. It is precisely this quality
of a kshatriya that Shri Krishna points out. He reminds Arjuna of
that which is a warrior, his duty is to fight, and there is nothing
better for a warrior than a sacred war, therefore he should not
be afraid, finding himself in this situation.

यदृच्छया चोपपन्नं स्वर्गद्वारमपावृतम् ।
सुखिनः क्षत्रियाः पार्थ लभन्ते युद्धमीदृशम् ॥२-३२॥
 yadṛcchayā cōpapannaṁ svargadvāramapāvṛtam ।
sukhinaḥ kśatriyāḥ pārtha labhantē yuddhamīdṛśam ॥ 2-32॥

O Partha! Warriors are happy when they get the chance to fight
in such a war, which is like unexpectedly opened
gates of heaven.
☝
☝

**43**
**Chapter 2**

"Warriors consider it auspicious to have the opportunity to participate
in a war. They believe that death in battle will allow them to reach
the heights of bliss."

अथ चेत्त्वमिमं धर्म्यं संग्रामं न करिष्यसि ।
ततः स्वधर्मं कीर्तिं च हित्वा पापमवाप्स्यसि ॥२-३३॥
atha cēttvamimaṁ dhārmyaṁ saṅgrāmaṁ na kariṣyasi ।
tataḥ svadharmaṁ kīrtiṁ ca hitvā pāpamavāpsyasi ॥ 2-33॥

If, however, you do not fight this righteous battle,
then, abandoning your own dharma and glory, you will incur sin.

"If
you
oppose
the
sacred
duties
of
a kshatriya and do not participate in the battle, then, acting against
your nature, you will lose your peace of mind, and your glory
as an unsurpassed warrior will come to an end."

अकीर्तिं चापि भूतानि कथयिष्यन्ति तेऽव्ययाम् ।
सम्भावितस्य चाकीर्तिर्मरणादतिरिच्यते ॥२-३४॥
akīrtiṁ cāpi bhūtāni kathayiṣyanti tē’vyayām ।
saṁbhāvitasya cākīrtirmaraṇādatiricyatē ॥ 2-34॥

All beings will speak of your everlasting disgrace.
For a respected man, such dishonor is worse than death.

"Everyone who knows you as a great warrior will for a long time
discuss your avoidance of battle. For such a great warrior
as you, this will be worse than death."

भयाद्रणादुपरतं मंस्यन्ते त्वां महारथाः ।
येषां च त्वं बहुमतो भूत्वा यास्यसि लाघवम् ॥२-३५॥
bhayādraṇāduparataṁ maṁsyantē tvāṁ mahārathāḥ ।
yēṣāṁ ca tvaṁ bahumatō bhūtvā yāsyasi lāghavam ॥ 2-35॥

Although those great warriors now honor you, you will become
a laughingstock to them, for they will think that you withdrew from war
out of fear.
☝
☝
☝

**44**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

"You have achieved preeminence among outstanding warriors, and
yet, if you leave the battlefield, they will decide that the reason
for this was your cowardice."

अवाच्यवादांश्च बहून्वदिष्यन्ति तवाहिताः ।
निन्दन्तस्तव सामर्थ्यं ततो दुःखतरं नु किम् ॥२-३६॥
avācyavādāṁśca bahūnvadiṣyanti tavāhitāḥ ।
nindantastava sāmarthyaṁ tatō duḥkhataraṁ nu kim ॥ 2-36॥

Your enemies will condemn you and utter many vile
comments. What could be more painful than this?

"If you do not fight, your enemies, ready to challenge
you, will condemn you and in every way mock your abilities.
Can anything be more grievous for a warrior?"

हतो वा प्राप्स्यसि स्वर्गं जित्वा वा भोक्ष्यसे महीम् ।
तस्मादुत्तिष्ठ कौन्तेय युद्धाय कृतनिश्चयः ॥२-३७॥
hatō vā prāpsyasi svargaṁ jitvā vā bhōkśyasē mahīm ।
tasmāduttiṣṭha kauntēya yuddhāya kṛtaniścayaḥ ॥ 2-37॥

Slain, you will attain heaven; victorious, you will enjoy the
earthly kingdom. O Kaunteya! Gather your resolve,
arise and fight!

Having explained this, the Lord introduces Arjuna to the practice of yoga,
which allows one to remain unperturbed in any situation.

"Even dying in this war, you will attain the heights of self-elevation, since, by fighting, you act in accordance with
your nature. If you conquer – you will enjoy the kingdom and
the feeling of victory. Therefore, decide and arise for battle!"
☝
☝
☝

**45**
**Chapter 2**

सुखदुःखे समे कृत्वा लाभालाभौ जयाजयौ ।
ततो युद्धाय युज्यस्व नैवं पापमवाप्स्यसि ॥२-३८॥
sukhaduḥkhē samē kṛtvā lābhālābhau jayājayau ।
tatō yuddhāya yujyasva naivaṁ pāpamavāpsyasi ॥ 2-38॥

Treating equally victory and defeat, gain and loss,
happiness and sorrow, prepare for battle. Thus you will not incur
sin.

"Perceive victory and defeat, gain and loss, happiness and grief
equally and be ready for battle. Having attained such
self-mastery, you will avoid the sin of remorse. Perform all
duties only in the state of samadhi."

एषा तेऽभिहिता सांख्ये बुद्धिर्योगे त्विमां शृणु ।
बुद्ध्या युक्तो यया पार्थ कर्मबन्धं प्रहास्यसि ॥२-३९॥
ēṣā tē’bhihitā sāṁkhyē buddhiryōgē tvimāṁ śṛṇu ।
buddhyā yuktō yayā pārtha karmabandhaṁ prahāsyasi ॥ 2-39॥

O Partha! This knowledge has been imparted to you for your
understanding. Now hear its essence, through which you will attain
wisdom and thus free yourself from the bonds of karma.

Having briefly described the state of samadhi, Lord Krishna makes
Arjuna a medium for transmitting instructions on yoga
to all humanity. The practice of this yoga allows one to achieve
equanimity, and the yogi who practices it, through the attainment
of samadhi, casts off the fetters of karma and unites with
the unmanifest Time, the Light of all light, the indestructible
Supreme, knowing Him through death.
☝
☝

**46**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*nehabhikramanasho’sti pratyavayo na vidyate*
*svalpamapyasya dharmasya trayate mahato bhayat* || 2-40 ||

The benefit of this undertaking is imperishable, nor does it bring any evil. Even a brief practice of this yoga grants freedom from great fears.

It cannot happen that this practice culminates in failure or ever has unfavorable consequences. Even a brief practice of this yoga liberates one from the great fear of death. The yogi who performs this practice comes to know the true nature of death—which instills terror in those whose intellect is limited by physical boundaries—and thus becomes free from the fear of it. It is precisely through death that the great man awakens the boundless consciousness of his mind and transcends physical limitations to himself attain boundlessness.

*vyavasayatmika buddhir ekeha kurunandana*
*bahushakha hyanantashcha buddhayo’vyavasayinam* || 2-41 ||

O Kurunandana!⁴ Only in one path here can there be no doubt, although there are many other options.

Those who follow this path, filled with resolve to awaken the entire immensity of their consciousness, have already recognized the goal of their life, while those who are insufficiently intelligent for this spend their lives in complete confusion.

⁴"Descendant of Kuru"

☝

**47**
**Chapter 2**

*yamimam pushpitam vacham pravadantyavipashchitah*
*vedavadaratah partha nanyadastiti vadinah* || 2-42 ||
*kamatmanah svargapara janmakarmaphalapradam*
*kriyavisheshabahulam bhogaishvaryagatim prati* || 2-43 ||
*bhogaishvaryaprasaktanam tayapahritachetasam*
*vyavasayatmika buddhih samadhau na vidhiyate* || 2-44 ||

O Partha! Those who are absorbed in pleasures echo the scriptures that extol the fruits of karma; those unintelligent ones, in whose judgment heaven is the highest good, speak pompously and grandiloquently.

The voluptuous consider heaven supreme, believing it to be the reward of all earthly deeds. Those whose minds are mired in the desire for wealth and pleasures act only for their attainment. The intellect of such fools is incapable of striving toward samadhi.

Before beginning rituals, such deluded people enchant other deluded people with promises of corresponding results—especially those who give preference to the body and whose minds do not grasp the conscious Presence that manifests the body. These individuals are among the many who consider temporary physical pleasures the highest. For the sake of satisfying their own interests, they allure other deluded people by promising them enjoyments and riches, sweetly describing numerous duties and religious rites.

The intellect of those who are under the influence of such tales remains firmly attached to pleasures and manifold riches and proves utterly incapable of samadhi. Even the revelations of great sages about samadhi they perceive as a flight of fancy, due to this limitation of their consciousness.

☝

**48**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*traigunyavishaya veda nistraigunyo bhavarjuna*
*nirdvandvo nityasattvastho niryogakshema atmavan* || 2-45 ||

O Arjuna! The three fundamental gunas are mentioned in the scriptures. You should transcend them, establish yourself in the unconditional eternal Truth, and attain self-mastery, remaining unmoved by gain and loss.

The boundless consciousness of the mind—the source of all enjoyment and wealth—continues to remain limited by the three gunas and for this reason is unable to attain samadhi. Therefore it is necessary to go beyond the boundaries of these three gunas through yoga, and, establishing oneself in samadhi, to make immense efforts to awaken the dormant immeasurable consciousness of one's mind in order to know the true nature of the Light of all light, the dazzlingly shining Time.

*yavanartha udapane sarvatah samplutodake*
*tavansarveshu vedeshu brahmanasya vijanatah* || 2-46 ||

What use is a well to one who has reached a boundless reservoir? Similarly, there is no use in scriptures for one who has known Brahman.

When the yogi diligently performs the practice of yoga and, overcoming physical limitations, awakens the entire immeasurable consciousness of his mind, the consciousness limited by the senses becomes for him virtually the same as a small reservoir is for a person who has reached the ocean.

☝

**49**
**Chapter 2**

*karmanyevadhikaraste ma phaleshu kadachana*
*ma karmaphalaheturbhurma te sangostvakarmani* || 2-47 ||

You have a right only to activity—do not lay claim to its fruits. You should not act solely for the sake of fruits, but neither should you become attached to inaction.

Everyone has a desire for results, and this desire itself is the motivating cause for action. All actions in this world begin precisely with the desire for fruits, and only yoga is that action at the foundation of which lies the desire for samadhi.

When the yogi plunges deeper into practice and begins to know the immeasurable consciousness abiding beyond the body, he becomes detached from the thought of obtaining the fruits of his actions. At the moment he receives this experience, samadhi begins. When samadhi dawns, the sadhaka becomes capable of performing actions free from the impulses of desires.

*yogasthah kuru karmani sangam tyaktva dhananjaya*
*siddhyasiddhyoh samo bhutva samatvam yoga uchyate* || 2-48 ||

O Dhananjaya! Act, having abandoned attachment and established yourself in yoga. Be equal in both success and failure—this indeed is known as yoga.

By awakening the entire boundlessness of his consciousness through the practice of yoga, the sadhaka rises above physical limitations, and the allure of sensory pleasures accessible through the body vanishes for him. Having realized the relativity of life and death, such a yogi becomes established in a state of equanimity. Life and death, loss and gain, fulfillment and non-fulfillment—all become equal for him.

☝

**50**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*durena hyavaram karma buddhiyogaddhananjaya*
*buddhau sharanamanviccha kripanah phalahetavah* || 2-49 ||

Activity is far inferior to Buddhi-Yoga.⁵ O Dhananjaya! Seek refuge in wisdom, for those who crave reward are utterly pitiable.

Ordinary people, who desire only to gratify the senses and remain within the bounds of physical limitations, make no effort to awaken their dormant boundless consciousness. Herein lies the cause of their wretchedness: possessed of a strong desire for sensory pleasures, such people continue to fear death throughout their lives, and because of this fear they abandon all attempts at self-knowledge.

*buddhiyukto jahatiha ubhe sukritadushkrite*
*tasmadyogaya yujyasva yogah karmasu kaushalam* || 2-50 ||

The wise man frees himself from the fruits of both vice and virtue in this world. Therefore strive only for yoga. This yoga itself is the art of action.

The yogis who, through exceptional mastery in yogic practice, have succeeded in awakening their boundless consciousness and have come to know the relativity of favorable and unfavorable actions, concentrate their boundless consciousness on the immutable Supreme Essence, the Light of all light, the dazzlingly shining Time, and attain union with Him.

⁵"Knowledge of Time"

☝

**51**
**Chapter 2**

*karmajam buddhiyukta hi phalam tyaktva manishinah*
*janmabandhavinirmuktah padam gacchantyanamayam* || 2-51 ||

The sage who has awakened his intellect avoids the fruits of karma, becomes free from the bonds of birth, and attains the flawless, immortal spiritual destiny.

The yogis who, through their practice, have realized that Unmanifest Boundlessness which manifests the body, are able to understand that all incarnations are merely means for the manifestation of that Supreme Consciousness. Establishing themselves in that conscious Presence, they become free from the great fetters—the obligation to take birth—and attain union with that Unmanifest, Supreme, Immutable Highest Spirit.

*yada te mohakalilam buddhir vyatitarishyati*
*tada gantasi nirvedam shrotavyasya shrutasya cha* || 2-52 ||

When your intellect has crossed beyond the mire of delusion, you will become established in indifference toward what has been heard and what is yet to be heard.

When the yogi's consciousness rises above physical limitations, he comprehends the interconnection of the mind and the sense organs. Such a yogi is able to realize the primacy of the mind, which, like an instrument, governs the body and the sense organs. Without the participation of the mind, the body and senses possess no power of their own. Having realized this, he understands the true nature of the attraction of the organs toward sense objects and thus becomes free from this attraction. This state is known as "vairagya."

☝

**52**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*shrutivipratipanna te yada sthatyati nishchala*
*samadhiavachala buddhistada yogamavapsyasi* || 2-53 ||

"When your mind, disturbed by what is set forth in the scriptures, becomes immovably established in samadhi, then you will attain this yoga."

When the mind, which had been unstable due to performing numerous actions for the fulfillment of numerous desires, becomes concentrated on the single desire to awaken its dormant consciousness and becomes established through the practice of yoga in samadhi, the result of the practice is considered attained. This state is called equanimity.

**Arjuna uvacha**

*sthitaprajnasya ka bhasha samadhisthasya keshava*
*sthitadhih kim prabhasheta kim asita vrajeta kim* || 2-54 ||

Arjuna said:
"O Keshava! What are the characteristics of the sage of steady wisdom (sthitaprajna)?⁶ How does one of unwavering intellect speak? How does he sit and how does he move?"

⁶"Possessed of unwavering wisdom"

☝

**53**
**Chapter 2**

**Shribhagavanuvacha**

*prajahati yada kamansarvan partha manogatan*
*atmanyevatmana tushtah sthitaprajnastadochyate* || 2-55 ||

The Lord said:
"O Partha! When a person renounces all the desires of his mind, then he, completely satisfied in himself, is called sthitaprajna.

The yogi who has awakened his dormant consciousness comes to know that unmanifest conscious Presence which manifests itself through the body. Thus he knows the Self through the self, thereby attaining self-satisfaction, and transcends all desires. Such a great yogi is called 'sthitaprajna.'

*duhkheshvanudvignamanah sukheshu vigatasprihah*
*vitaragabhayakrodhah sthitadhir muniruchyate* || 2-56 ||

He whose mind is not agitated by suffering and who is devoid of longing for pleasures, whose attachment, fear, and anger have vanished—such a sage is called sthitabuddhi.⁷

Great persons are able to understand that all experiences, such as grief, pleasure, fear, anger, and attachment, are merely different manifestations of that one Consciousness, just as the same melody can be played on various musical instruments.

⁷"Possessed of unwavering intellect"

☝

54
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
yaḥ sarvatrānabhisnēhastattatprāpya śubhāśubham ।
nābhinandati na dvēṣṭi tasya prajñā pratiṣṭhitā ॥ 2-57॥

One who feels no strong attachment to anything, who neither rejoices nor grieves upon encountering the favorable and the unfavorable—his supreme wisdom is sacred.

Of the *sthitaprajña*, it cannot be said that they are attached to anything or that they are utterly devoid of attachment. For them, the favorable and the unfavorable are but different manifestations of that one Presence. When a great person is established in this state, his supreme wisdom, having become truly boundless, is considered sacred.

yadā saṁharatē cāyaṁ kūrmō’ṅgānīva sarvaśaḥ ।
indriyāṇīndriyārthēbhyastasya prajñā pratiṣṭhitā ॥ 2-58॥

When a person, like a tortoise drawing in its limbs, withdraws the sense organs from their objects, his supreme wisdom is sacred.

A person of unwavering intellect becomes impeccably discerning with regard to his body—the manifestation of that infinite Consciousness. In the process of self-realization, he understands that it is the mind that perceives the objects of the senses through the various organs.

Having realized this, the great person, through the practice of yoga, awakens the consciousness of his mind in its fullness, after which his mind no longer requires the aid of the organs. In this state of awakened consciousness, the yogin abides in indescribable bliss. For such a great person, the body and its sense organs become secondary.

☝
☝

55
Chapter 2
viṣayā vinivartantē nirāhārasya dēhinaḥ ।
rasavarjaṁ rasō’pyasya paraṁ dṛṣṭvā nivartatē ॥ 2-59॥

One who remains without food can renounce the objects of the senses, but not his attraction to them. But one who realizes the Supreme overcomes even that attraction.

Some so-called yogins, who do not understand that it is the mind, receiving experience through the senses, that is sovereign, consider the sense organs their enemies. Many of these yogins, striving to bring the mind under control, attempt to suppress the functioning of the sense organs. In this endeavor, they may be seen remaining without food for long periods. Prolonged fasting leads to their body becoming weak and their sense organs growing feeble. Yet even in this state, they continue to indulge in memories of the experience accessible through the sense organs, unaware that the organs act merely as instruments of the mind. The sense organs have no power of their own, except that which is given to them by the mind. Those who practice yoga are able to understand this, and by comprehending the mind through the mind itself, they can become established in that conscious Presence hidden beyond the body.

yatatō hyapi kauntēya puruṣasya vipaścitaḥ ।
indriyāṇi pramāthīni haranti prasabhaṁ manaḥ ॥ 2-60॥

O Kaunteya! The restless senses forcibly carry away the mind even of a discerning person who strives to restrain them.

Sometimes one may observe a beginning *sādhaka* becoming attached, in the course of his practice, to sensations accessible through the senses. This state must be consciously overcome. Almost all yogins pass through this. Such a phenomenon

☝
☝

56
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
should be regarded merely as a particular state of the mind, and it must be controlled by means of the mind itself.

In the process of understanding the relationship between the sense organs and the mind, sometimes the sense organs dominate, and sometimes the mind. One who performs yogic practice with firm resolve studies all the states of his mind, develops a proper understanding of its sovereign role, and transcends dependence on the senses.

tāni sarvāṇi saṁyamya yukta āsīta matparaḥ ।
vaśē hi yasyēndriyāṇi tasya prajñā pratiṣṭhitā ॥ 2-61॥

Therefore, controlling the senses, follow Me; be perfect and steadfast. For the supreme wisdom of one who has mastery over the senses is unshakable.

When the yogin understands that it is the mind that receives experience through the senses, he comprehends the cause of attraction to sense objects and becomes free from their influence.

dhyāyatō viṣayānpuṁsaḥ saṅgastēṣūpajāyatē ।
saṅgātsaṁjāyatē kāmaḥ kāmātkrōdhō’bhijāyatē ॥ 2-62॥
krōdhādbhavati saṁmōhaḥ saṁmōhātsmṛtivibhramaḥ ।
smṛtibhraṁśādbuddhināśō buddhināśātpraṇaśyati ॥ 2-63॥

A person who indulges in memories of sense objects develops attachment to them; from attachment arises desire, and desire gives birth to anger. Anger leads to delusion; delusion clouds memory; this clouding leads to the destruction of the intellect; and a destroyed intellect destroys the person.

☝

57
Chapter 2
Those perfected through the practice of yoga know that it is their mind that is the foundation of attraction to any sense object. It is in the mind that attraction arises, endowing sense objects with splendor and allure. The awakening of this allure gives rise to the desire to perceive that object. When an obstacle arises on the path to fulfilling this desire, the desire takes the form of anger. Anger leads to the loss of sound judgment, which in turn leads to loss of memory, and in that loss of memory, the intellect fades. In such a state, a person destroys himself.

rāgadvēṣavimuktaistu viṣayānindriyaiścaran ।
ātmavaśyairvidhēyātmā prasādamadhigacchati ॥ 2-64॥

But a person free from attraction and aversion, perceiving objects through his controlled senses, attains perfection.

Yogins who have been able to understand these subtle states of the mind have realized that all the senses are merely instruments of the mind for acquiring experience. Such great sages awaken their boundless consciousness and go beyond physical limitations. They abide in self-satisfaction, because they directly experience that Immensity within themselves, and become free from attraction to sensory pleasures. Having become free from attraction, they also become free from aversion. Such great people attain purity and become established in supreme tranquility.

☝
☝

58
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
prasādē sarvaduḥkhānāṁ hānirasyōpajāyatē ।
prasannacētasō hyāśu buddhiḥ paryavatiṣṭhatē ॥ 2-65॥

All sorrows vanish with this purity, and the intellect of such a person soon becomes unshakable.

For such great people, who have awakened the full consciousness of their mind, there is no longer any difference between happiness and sorrow, loss and gain. Realizing the relativity of these experiences and becoming free from desires, they attain perfection and abide in peace.

nāsti buddhirayuktasya na cāyuktasya bhāvanā ।
na cābhāvayataḥ śāntiraśāntasya kutaḥ sukham ॥ 2-66॥

Worthless people possess neither intellect nor control over the senses. Deprived of sense objects, they lose peace, and how can one with a restless mind attain happiness?

Those who are unable to understand the interrelation of the mind and the sense organs cannot realize that unmanifest Presence manifesting through the body. Since their consciousness sleeps, continuing to strive only for the satisfaction of the sense organs, they can in no way attain peace. Due to restlessness, they lack happiness in life. Unable to awaken their sleeping consciousness, they continue to abide limited by such phenomena as happiness and sorrow, loss and gain, life and death. As a result of this limitation, they spend their lives in anxiety, gripped by the fear of death.

☝
☝

59
Chapter 2
indriyāṇāṁ hi caratāṁ yanmanō’nu vidhīyatē ।
tadasya harati prajñāṁ vāyurnāvamivāmbhasi ॥ 2-67॥

Whichever sense the wandering mind follows, that shakes the intellect of a worthless person, just as the wind rocks a boat adrift on the water.

The intellect of ordinary people, who have not awakened their sleeping consciousness and have not attained boundlessness, considers the senses to be sovereign. Such people do not understand that it is precisely by virtue of their intellect that they give preference to the senses.

tasmādyasya mahābāhō nigṛhītāni sarvaśaḥ ।
indriyāṇīndriyārthēbhyastasya prajñā pratiṣṭhitā ॥ 2-68॥

O Mahābāho! One who has withdrawn his sense organs from their objects—he alone is steadfast in intellect.

For those who have realized the sovereign role of their mind, sense objects lose their former importance. But people with restless minds who give preference to the senses continue to think that the intellect of yogins is steadfast only because they have achieved the subjugation of the sense organs.

In reality, this is not so. When *sādhakas*, through the practice of yoga, awaken the boundless consciousness of their mind, the body loses its importance for them, and they no longer feel attraction to sense objects. Due to the absence of this attraction, the sense organs become their friends. For fools unaware of the boundlessness of their consciousness, the body and sense objects continue to remain sovereign, and the intellect remains unstable.

☝
☝

60
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
yā niśā sarvabhūtānāṁ tasyāṁ jāgarti saṁyamī ।
yasyāṁ jāgrati bhūtāni sā niśā paśyatō munēḥ ॥ 2-69॥

What is night for all beings, in that the *saṁyamī*¹ is awake; and what is waking for all beings, that the sage perceives as night.

*Sādhakas* who have succeeded in yoga and, through practice, have been able to awaken the full consciousness of their mind, are outstanding individuals. Such great people Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa calls *sthitaprajña*.

For those who are able to use only a small part of their mind's capacities, the boundless capacities of their intellect are as if asleep. For sages whose consciousness is awakened, people with sleeping consciousness are as if abiding in sleep.

āpūryamāṇamacalapratiṣṭhaṁ samudramāpaḥ praviśanti yadvat ।
tadvatkāmā yaṁ praviśanti sarvē sa śāntimāpnōti na kāmakāmī ॥ 2-70॥

Just as the ocean remains calm and unmoving when rivers enter it, filling it from all sides, so too does one who remains undisturbed, perceiving the objects of all senses, attain peace—but not one who craves pleasures.

Great people who have succeeded in the full awakening of the entire immensity of their mind cannot be disturbed by the experience acquired through the senses. By awakening all the capacities of their mind through intense practice of yoga, such sages attain ultimate perfection. Uniting with that supreme Radiance, the Light of all lights, the Creator of the entire universe, unmanifest Time, they become *Viśvātman*² and attain peace.

¹ "One who has attained self-realization"
² "Universal Self"

**61**
**Chapter 2**

विहाय कामान्यः सर्वान् पुमांश्चरति निःस्पृहः ।
निर्ममो निरहंकारः स शान्तिमधिगच्छति ॥२-७१॥
vihāya kāmānyaḥ sarvān pumāṁścarati niḥspṛhaḥ ।
nirmamō nirahaṁkāraḥ sa śāntimadhigacchhati ॥ 2-71॥

The great man who, having cast aside all desires, lives without attachment, arrogance, and greed, attains peace.

Such great men are in this world, yet abide beyond its limits; even renouncing everything, they renounce nothing; being filled with love, they appear devoid of feeling; enjoying, they enjoy nothing; and, abiding free from self-complacency, they experience a sense of self-fulfillment. Such fully awakened great personalities abide in absolute peace.

एषा ब्राह्मी स्थितिः पार्थ नैनां प्राप्य विमुह्यति ।
स्थित्वास्यामन्तकालेऽपि ब्रह्मनिर्वाणमृच्छति ॥२-७२॥
ēṣā brāhmī sthitiḥ pārtha naināṁ prāpya vimuhyati ।
sthitvāsyāmantakālē’pi brahmanirvāṇamṛcchati ॥ 2-72॥

O Partha! This is the state of abiding in Brahman, the state of Omnipotence. Having once attained it, a person is forever freed from ignorance. One established in this state, even at the hour of death, attains Brahma-Nirvana¹⁰.

The yogi, knowing the complete boundlessness of his mind and awakening all his dormant consciousness, becomes established in the Infinite. Such a great man is never again limited by a worldly mindset. At the end of his life, such a sage established in Boundlessness overcomes, through death, the limitations of the body that has fulfilled its purpose, concentrates all the immeasurable consciousness of his mind upon the unmanifest Time, and merges with It.

⁹ “The Soul of the Universe”
¹⁰ “The Infinite Bliss of Unity with Time”

☝
☝

**62**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे सांख्ययोगो नाम द्वितीयोऽध्यायः ॥ २ ॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē sāṁkhyayōgō nāma dvitīyō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 2॥

Om Tat Sat

Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the second chapter, “The Yoga of Discrimination,” of the Upanishad “Shrimad Bhagavad Gita,” which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

तृतीयोऽध्यायः कर्मयोगः
tṛtīyō’dhyāyaḥ karmayōgaḥ

**Chapter 3**
**YOGA OF ACTION**

**64**
अर्जुन उवाच
ज्यायसी चेत्कर्मणस्ते मता बुद्धिर्जनार्दन ।
तत्किं कर्मणि घोरे मां नियोजयसि केशव ॥३- १॥
arjuna uvāca
jyāyasī cētkarmaṇastē matā buddhirjanārdana ।
tatkiṁ karmaṇi ghōrē māṁ niyōjayasi kēśava ॥ 3-1॥

Arjuna said:
“O Janardana! If, in Your opinion, wisdom is superior to action, then, O Keshava, why do You engage me in such a terrible deed?

व्यामिश्रेणेव वाक्येन बुद्धिं मोहयसीव मे ।
तदेकं वद निश्चित्य येन श्रेयोऽहमाप्नुयाम् ॥३- २॥
vyāmiśrēṇēva vākyēna buddhiṁ mōhayasīva mē ।
tadēkaṁ vada niścitya yēna śrēyō’hamāpnuyām ॥ 3-2॥

With Your ambiguous words, You confuse my mind. Tell me decisively one thing by which I may attain what is good.”

ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**65**
**Chapter 3**

श्रीभगवानुवाच
लोकेऽस्मिन्द्विविधा निष्ठा पुरा प्रोक्ता मयानघ ।
ज्ञानयोगेन सांख्यानां कर्मयोगेन योगिनाम् ॥३- ३॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
lōkē’smindvividhā niṣṭhā purā prōktā mayānagha ।
jñānayōgēna sāṅkhyānāṁ karmayōgēna yōginām ॥ 3-3॥

The Lord said:
“O Anagha¹! I have declared to you two paths in this world: the yoga of knowledge [Jnana] for the discerning, and the yoga of action [Karma] for the yogis.”

Those who are not initiated into Kriya Yoga will most likely be confused by the statements of the realized ones who have known the Infinite. Without practicing yoga, it is practically impossible to believe that those who know, having understood the interconnection of mind and senses, can control their senses by means of the mind itself. Those who have already realized this by awakening their dormant infinite consciousness are called jnanis, while those who are still in the process of awakening their infinite capacities are called yogis.

न कर्मणामनारम्भान्नैष्कर्म्यं पुरुषोऽश्नुते ।
न च संन्यसनादेव सिद्धिं समधिगच्छति ॥३- ४॥
na karmaṇāmanārambhānnaiṣkarmyaṁ puruṣō’śnutē ।
na ca saṁnyasanādēva siddhiṁ samadhigacchati ॥ 3-4॥

One cannot become nishkarma² merely by inaction, just as samadhi cannot be attained simply by dying.

It is impossible to attain the results of Kriya Yoga without practicing its methods. Those who, hearing the discourses of the knowers, consider themselves to be such, only demonstrate their own inadequacy. If such ignorant people abandon activity, imitating the knower who appears inactive and merely sitting in peace, this does not lead to the awakening of their immeasurable consciousness.

¹ “The Flawless One”
² “Free from karma”

☝
☝

**66**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

Without practicing yoga, such people cannot realize the true nature of death. Not knowing the truth of death, they fear it all their lives. Without attaining boundlessness by going beyond the limits of the body, when death manifests itself, they take another birth and are again caught in the trap of physical bonds.

न हि कश्चित्क्षणमपि जातु तिष्ठत्यकर्मकृत् ।
कार्यते ह्यवशः कर्म सर्वः प्रकृतिजैर्गुणैः ॥३- ५॥
na hi kaścitkśaṇamapi jātu tiṣṭhatyakarmakṛt ।
kāryatē hyavaśaḥ karma sarvaḥ prakṛtijairguṇaiḥ ॥ 3-5॥

No one can remain even for a moment without performing action, for, compelled by the gunas born of nature, everyone is engaged in karma.

Everyone who takes birth and finds themselves limited by physical boundaries is the result of karma performed by someone else. Being the consequence of someone else’s actions, people themselves cannot exist in inaction.

कर्मेन्द्रियाणि संयम्य य आस्ते मनसा स्मरन् ।
इन्द्रियार्थान्विमूढात्मा मिथ्याचारः स उच्यते ॥३- ६॥
karmēndriyāṇi saṁyamya ya āstē manasā smaran ।
indriyārthānvimūḍhātmā mithyācāraḥ sa ucyatē ॥ 3-6॥

One who restrains the organs of action but in mind dwells on the objects of the senses is called a hypocrite.

People whose consciousness is limited by physical boundaries become inspired by the personality of the knower and, with great effort, try by force of will to restrain their organs of action in order to rise above activity and become established in a state of inaction. They act in this way merely by listening to the reasoning of the knowers, but without possessing even a particle of their mind. They scarcely understand that it is not the organs that act, but the human mind itself, using the organs as its instruments. By forcibly restraining their organs of action, such people continue to think about the objects perceived by them and only increase their own dissatisfaction and tension.

☝
☝

**67**
**Chapter 3**

यस्त्विन्द्रियाणि मनसा नियम्यारभतेऽर्जुन ।
कर्मेन्द्रियैः कर्मयोगमसक्तः स विशिष्यते ॥३- ७॥
yastvindriyāṇi manasā niyamyārabhatē’rjuna ।
karmaindriyaiḥ karmayōgamasaktaḥ sa viśiṣyatē ॥ 3-7॥

O Arjuna, only he who, freeing himself from attachments, controls the organs by means of the mind, using them for the practice of the yoga of action, stands out among ordinary people.

Great sadhakas who, through diligent practice of yoga, understand that, essentially, the consciousness of the mind receives experience through the instruments of the various sense organs, studying their mind, also comprehend the nature of attraction to sensory experiences, and, understanding this, become free from this attraction. When yogis reach such a level, they rise above the limitations of the senses and acquire the ability to practice unhindered in order to fully awaken the infinite consciousness of their mind, overcoming physical boundaries. Knowing the truth of death, they also know life in its fullness and thus become free from its allure. They are called “jivanmukta³.” Such great people stand out among those around them.

नियतं कुरु कर्म त्वं कर्म ज्यायो ह्यकर्मणः ।
शरीरयात्रापि च ते न प्रसिद्ध्येदकर्मणः ॥३- ८॥
niyataṁ kuru karma tvaṁ karma jyāyō hyakarmaṇaḥ ।
śarīrayātrāpi ca tē na prasidhyēdakarmaṇaḥ ॥ 3-8॥

Perform your prescribed duty, for action is superior to inaction. By inaction, how can you fulfill your purpose?

A great man, having fully awakened his capacities, becomes the purest manifestation of that boundless unmanifest conscious Presence and performs the karma which he himself has established for himself, in order to inspire beginners. All actions performed by such a person are a form of pious worship (yajna). For ordinary people, it is enough simply to look upon such a great man to catch a clear glimpse of the unmanifest boundless Consciousness manifesting through his body and abiding beyond it.

³ “Free from life”

☝
☝

**68**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

यज्ञार्थात्कर्मणोऽन्यत्र लोकोऽयं कर्मबन्धनः ।
तदर्थं कर्म कौन्तेय मुक्तसङ्गः समाचर ॥३- ९॥
yajñārthātkarmaṇō’nyatra lōkō’yaṁ karmabandhanaḥ ।
tadarthaṁ karma kauntēya muktasaṅgaḥ samācara ॥ 3-9॥

All actions that are performed not for the sake of yajna bind one in the bonds of karma. O Kaunteya, freeing yourself from attachment, act only for the fulfillment of yajna.

Those who perform yogic practice in order to know the unmanifest Presence hidden behind physical manifestation go beyond the attraction of the senses and ultimately become free from their karma. Because the consciousness of an ordinary person abides within the limits of physical boundaries, he cannot even imagine anything that lies beyond these limits. After a slight glimpse of the boundlessness of the dormant consciousness, diligent practice of yoga must be performed for its awakening.

सहयज्ञाः प्रजाः सृष्ट्वा पुरोवाच प्रजापतिः ।
अनेन प्रसविष्यध्वमेष वोऽस्त्विष्टकामधुक् ॥३- १०॥
sahayajñāḥ prajāḥ sṛṣṭvā purōvāca prajāpatiḥ ।
anēna prasaviṣyadhvamēṣa vō’stviṣṭakāmadhuk ॥ 3-10॥

Prajapati⁴ created humanity along with yajna, and then said: “Prosper through this yajna; let it fulfill your desires; let it grant you what you wish for!

☝

**69**
**Chapter 3**

The body, being a manifestation of that unmanifest Time, the Creator of the Universe, contains within itself all the elements of the cosmos. The exceptional feature of this body is that, with its help, one can know the boundless Consciousness that manifests it. The practice of yoga, by means of which the sadhak awakens the infinity of the consciousness of his mind, is known as yajna performed through the body. This yajna raises the one performing it above all desires, fulfilling them. On one hand, this body is a means for performing yogic practice, and thus frees consciousness from physical limitations. On the other hand, the same body, serving only the satisfaction of sensory desires, can also be a cause of bondage.

देवान्भावयतानेन ते देवा भावयन्तु वः ।
परस्परं भावयन्तः श्रेयः परमवाप्स्यथ ॥३- ११॥
dēvānbhāvayatānēna tē dēvā bhāvayantu vaḥ ।
parasparaṁ bhāvayantaḥ śrēyaḥ paramavāpsyatha ॥ 3-11॥

Let the gods also prosper through your yajna, and let them in turn care for you. Nourishing each other, may you attain the supreme good!

Because the Supreme Essence is present in this body, all gods also abide in it. In other words, the mind itself, due to its immeasurability, is like the Supreme Essence, and all the sense organs and organs of action, serving it merely as instruments, are forms of the gods. The yogi, who through his intellect catches a glimpse of the boundless capacities of the mind, makes efforts to awaken these capacities, and all his sense organs together with the organs of action become focused on That Boundlessness. The mind and the organs interacting with it of such a yogi become divine.

⁴ “The Lord Creator”

☝
☝

**70**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*iṣṭānbhōgānhi vō dēvā dāsyantē yajñabhāvitāḥ |
tairdattānapradāyaibhyō yō bhuṅktē stēna ēva saḥ || 3-12 ||*

"Satisfied by yajña, the gods will bestow upon you the desired enjoyments. One who enjoys their gifts without offering anything in return is a thief."

All the senses of a sādhaka who has attained limitlessness of mind become his friends. After the awakening of this boundlessness, the yogin no longer needs to receive any experience through the organs of perception, and they become means of his recreation. Such a yogin finds the source of satisfaction within himself.

Ordinary people, who cannot avail themselves of this knowledge, continue to assign primary importance to the sense organs, as they have no conception of the full potentialities of the mind. Due to the limitation of their own intellect, they do not understand that the senses are merely instruments of the mind for obtaining experience, and they continue to indulge in the gratification of sensual desires. Not knowing their own dormant, immeasurable Consciousness, such people rob themselves.

Great people, who awaken their immeasurable consciousness, understand the significance of the organs and throughout their entire lives treat them and their body with complete respect.

*yajñaśiṣṭāśinaḥ santō mucyantē sarvakilbiṣaiḥ |
bhuñjatē tē tvaghaṁ pāpā yē pacantyātmakāraṇāt || 3-13 ||*

"Saints who partake of what remains after yajña are liberated from all sins. Sinners, however, who cook only for themselves, partake only of sins."

Great people, who sacrifice their body to the fire of yoga, transcend all sins by awakening the immeasurable Consciousness, which is the result of this great yajña. There is no heavier sin

☝
☝

**71**
**Chapter 3**

than not attempting to awaken one's consciousness. Those who are unable to kindle the fire of yoga and cannot offer their body as an oblation to this fire remain confined within physical limits their entire lives and therefore partake only of sins.

*annādbhavanti bhūtāni parjanyādannasambhavaḥ |
yajñādbhavati parjanyō yajñaḥ karmasamudbhavaḥ || 3-14 ||*

*karma brahmōdbhavaṁ viddhi brahmākśarasamudbhavam |
tasmātsarvagataṁ brahma nityaṁ yajñē pratiṣṭhitam || 3-15 ||*

"All beings are created from food; food is produced by rain; rain comes from yajña; and yajña is performed through actions. Know that karma arose from Brahman, and Brahman is created from the Eternal Imperishable. The all-pervading Brahman always abides in yajña."

Yogins who have succeeded in awakening the boundlessness of their consciousness have understood that this consciousness is a manifestation of the imperishable, all-pervading Time, that eternal and unchanging Brahman, manifesting in the limitlessness of the mind. The physical body is the support of the mind, and karma arises as a consequence of receiving various experiences through the physical body. The foundation of the body is food, which is produced by the moisture of rain, crowning the union of Earth and Sun.

*ēvaṁ pravartitaṁ cakraṁ nānuvartayatīha yaḥ |
aghāyurindriyārāmō mōghaṁ pārtha sa jīvati || 3-16 ||*

"O Pārtha! One who does not follow this established cycle and remains captivated by sensual pleasures, know that he lives in vain."

☝

**72**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

Ordinary people, who are unable to comprehend the nature of That Supreme Presence through the awakening of their dormant consciousness and do not even make an effort towards it, waste their life in vain. Due to their own limitation, the manifestation of that immeasurable Unconscious, which occurs through them, has no meaning.

*yastvātmaratirēva syādātmatṛptaśca mānavaḥ |
ātmanyēva ca saṁtuṣṭastasya kāryaṁ na vidyatē || 3-17 ||*

"But for one who finds joy, peace, and complete satisfaction in the Self alone, there remain no duties."

Great yogins, who have succeeded in knowing the ultimate, indestructible Supreme Essence, Time, through the awakening of the immeasurable consciousness of their mind by the practice of yoga, attain the goal of their life and abide in self-satisfaction. They have no need to perform any karma, and there is no karma that remains for them to perform.

*naiva tasya kṛtēnārthō nākṛtēnēha kaścana |
na cāsya sarvabhūtēṣu kaścidarthavyapāśrayaḥ || 3-18 ||*

"In this world, for him there is no purpose either in action or in inaction, nor does he have any dependence on other beings."

When sādhakas, awakening their consciousness through the practice of Kriyā Yoga, become established in samādhi, for them there remains no meaning in practicing this yoga, as they have already obtained its fruits. Established in the state of equanimity, they transcend such concepts as loss and gain; therefore, ceasing practice also holds no meaning for them.

☝
☝
☝

**73**
**Chapter 3**

*tasmādasaktaḥ satataṁ kāryaṁ karma samācara |
asaktō hyācarankarma paramāpnōti pūruṣaḥ || 3-19 ||*

"Therefore, carefully and unceasingly perform your karma without attachment; a dispassionate person thus attains the supreme goal."

For great people, nothing remains that is necessary to do for themselves, but since they are a source of inspiration for others, they do not renounce karma.

*karmaṇaiva hi saṁsiddhimāsthitā janakādayaḥ |
lōkasaṁgrahamēvāpi saṁpaśyankartumarhasi || 3-20 ||*

"It is indeed through karma that Janaka and others attained ultimate perfection. Therefore, for the welfare of all, act!"

Such eminent sthita-prajña as Janaka attained self-mastery through the awakening of their full consciousness by the practice of yoga, after which they had no duties left to perform.
