However, they did not abandon karma, in order to inspire by their example the beginning sādhakas and ordinary people.

*yadyadācarati śrēṣṭhastattadēvētarō janaḥ |
sa yatpramāṇaṁ kurutē lōkastadanuvartatē || 3-21 ||*

"People around act, inspired by the example of great personalities. All follow the path that the great have trodden."

We are all inspired by great people and try to follow their example. The sthita-prajña, for whom no duties remain, continue to perform

☝
☝
☝

**74**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

a particular karma for the encouragement of their followers, so that those, inspired by them, may themselves become capable of achieving great accomplishments.

*na mē pārthāsti kartavyaṁ triṣu lōkēṣu kiṁcana |
nānavāptamavāptavyaṁ varta ēva ca karmaṇi || 3-22 ||*

"O Pārtha! In all three worlds, there is nothing that I need to do, nor is there any goal I have not attained, yet I continue to act."

*yadi hyahaṁ na vartēyaṁ jātu karmaṇyatandritaḥ |
mama vartmānuvartantē manuṣyāḥ pārtha sarvaśaḥ || 3-23 ||*

*utsīdēyurimē lōkā na kuryāṁ karma cēdaham |
saṁkarasya ca kartā syāmupahanyāmimāḥ prajāḥ || 3-24 ||*

"For, O Pārtha, should I ever cease from action, all of humanity would follow My example. If I were to stop acting, this entire world would be destroyed, and I would become the cause of universal decline and the corruption of people."

For the infinite consciousness of Time, there is no necessity to manifest Itself, nor is there any necessity to remain unmanifest. Since It manifests through the entire universe, there is nothing in the whole world but This manifested Consciousness. If That Primal Element were not to manifest Itself, it would lead to the destruction of the world, which could also occur if This Unmanifest Conscious Presence were to manifest Itself too incautiously.

☝

**75**
**Chapter 3**

*saktāḥ karmaṇyavidvāṁsō yathā kurvanti bhārata |
kuryādvidvāṁstathāsaktaścikīrṣurlōkasaṁgraham || 3-25 ||*

"O Bhārata! Just as the ignorant, attached to activity, act, so should the wise act, but without attachment, for the welfare of all humanity."

Those who have become niṣkāma and established in samādhi as a result of performing yogic practice do not abandon it, although they no longer have any need for it. They continue to practice in order to inspire others, who are not yet perfected but are devoted to yogic practice, in their desire to attain samādhi.

*na buddhibhēdaṁ janayēdajñānāṁ karmasaṅginām |
jōṣayētsarvakarmāṇi vidvānyuktaḥ samācaran || 3-26 ||*

"Wise men should not confuse the minds of those attached to karma; they should perform actions only for the attainment of perfection, inspiring others to do likewise."

If a sthita-prajña, who has known Time through the attainment of samādhi, were to abandon yogic practice because he no longer needs it, his followers, inspired by him, as well as aspiring beginning yogins, would likely follow his example. Upon seeing a sthita-prajña sitting in silence, inactive, doubts would most likely arise in their minds. Desiring to protect his disciples from this, the sage does not abandon yogic practice, even if it is completely useless for him, so that those who have entered the path of knowledge may preserve their firm faith in yoga, following his example.

⁵ "Free from desires"

☝
☝

**76**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*prakṛtēḥ kriyamāṇāni guṇaiḥ karmāṇi sarvaśaḥ |
ahaṁkāravimūḍhātmā kartāhamiti manyatē || 3-27 ||*

"All karma is performed by the guṇas of material nature, yet one deluded by egoism thinks, 'I am the doer.'"

It is the mind that gives rise to all karma, and the body is the instrument for its performance. Those who have not succeeded in understanding this, using their own mind, have also not been able to understand That unmanifest, boundless Presence within their own body. They consider the body and sense organs as primary and thereby merely confine their consciousness within physical limitations.

*tattvavittu mahābāhō guṇakarmavibhāgayōḥ |
guṇā guṇēṣu vartanta iti matvā na sajjatē || 3-28 ||*

"O Mahābāho! The knower of the truth of karma and the guṇas sees: the guṇas revolve among the guṇas, and therefore does not become attached."

But great people, who have realized that all actions originate in the mind, also realize That conscious Presence which abides beyond the body. Such great personalities understand that the mind plays with itself, using itself as a toy. Through such understanding, their consciousness rises above physical limitations, and they are no longer enticed by the performance of karma for the gratification of sensual desires.

☝
☝

77
Chapter 3
प्रकृतेर्गुणसंमूढाः सज्जन्ते गुणकर्मसु ।
तानकृत्स्नविदो मन्दान्कृत्स्नविन्न विचालयेत् ॥३- २९॥
prakṛtērguṇasaṁmūḍhāḥ sajjantē guṇakarmasu ।
tānakṛtsnavidō mandānkṛtsnavinna vicālayēt ॥ 3-29॥

Bewildered by karma, blinded by the guṇas, they remain trapped in ignorance. The wise should not disturb such limited people.

Great personalities who have already awakened all the possibilities of their mind give no advice to those people whose mental capacities are largely asleep, and to those who believe that the body and senses are of primary importance. Since an ordinary person, who does not even attempt to awaken his consciousness, cannot understand the instructions of great people, he will most likely remain bewildered.

मयि सर्वाणि कर्माणि संन्यस्याध्यात्मचेतसा ।
निराशीर्निर्ममो भूत्वा युध्यस्व विगतज्वरः ॥३- ३०॥
mayi sarvāṇi karmāṇi saṁnyasyādhyātmacētasā ।
nirāśīrnirmamō bhūtvā yudhyasva vigatajvaraḥ ॥ 3-30॥

With a pious mind, dedicate your actions to Me. Fight without fury, abandoning hope and possessiveness.

Upon attaining the experience of the mind’s limitlessness, all the natural activity of a great person also takes on the character of limitlessness. Whatever such a person does—all points to That Limitlessness. In that state, he transcends hope, possessiveness, fury, and other limited experiences. Knowing the essence of death, he unites with the unmanifest consciousness of Time. Such great people, through their immense awakened mind, dedicate all their actions to That primordial Supreme Truth.

☝
☝

78
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
ये मे मतमिदं नित्यमनुतिष्ठन्ति मानवाः ।
श्रद्धावन्तोऽनसूयन्तो मुच्यन्ते तेऽपि कर्मभिः ॥३- ३१॥
yē mē matamidaṁ nityamanutiṣṭhanti mānavāḥ ।
śraddhāvantō’nasūyantō mucyantē tē’pi karmabhiḥ ॥ 3-31॥

The wise, who with faith and devotion follow these My instructions, are liberated from all their karma.

A great person who has attained limitlessness has no remaining duties that he must perform. Yet he does not cease to act, in order to inspire those who have yet to comprehend boundlessness. The perception of the sages who are aware of Time is free from distortion—they are able to contemplate the play of Time throughout all creation. Such great people remain devoted to Time and, through their actions, which are like the action of Time, are freed from the bonds of karma.

ये त्वेतदभ्यसूयन्तो नानुतिष्ठन्ति मे मतम् ।
सर्वज्ञानविमूढांस्तान्विद्धि नष्टानचेतसः ॥३- ३२॥
yē tvētadabhyasūyantō nānutiṣṭhanti mē matam ।
sarvajñānavimūḍhāṁstānviddhi naṣṭānacētasaḥ ॥ 3-32॥

But others, the ignorant, whose vision is clouded, do not follow these My instructions. Know such fools to be lost.

People devoid of ambition remain indifferent to the awakening of the countless possibilities of their own dormant mind. The life and death of such people have no meaning. They waste their lives in vain and only continue to destroy themselves.

सदृशं चेष्टते स्वस्याः प्रकृतेर्ज्ञानवानपि ।
प्रकृतिं यान्ति भूतानि निग्रहः किं करिष्यति ॥३- ३३॥
sadṛśaṁ cēṣṭatē svasyāḥ prakṛtērjñānavānapi ।
prakṛtiṁ yānti bhūtāni nigrahaḥ kiṁ kariṣyati ॥ 3-33॥

Like all beings, the wise also act in accordance with their own nature—what is the point in suppressing it?

☝
☝

79
Chapter 3
Most people have no experience of the limitlessness of the human mind, which is the principal force behind the body and all its organs of action. Consequently, they consider their own sense organs to be their enemies and attempt to forcibly suppress them. They do not realize that it is the mind that plays through the sense organs. Not understanding this, they inevitably fail in their endeavor to bring the sense organs under control.

But those who, through the practice of yoga, have been able to experience the limitlessness of the mind hidden behind the organs, remain established in it and fulfill all their desires.

इन्द्रियस्येन्द्रियस्यार्थे रागद्वेषौ व्यवस्थितौ ।
तयोर्न वशमागच्छेत्तौ ह्यस्य परिपन्थिनौ ॥३- ३४॥
indriyasyēndriyasyārthē rāgadvēṣau vyavasthitau ।
tayōrna vaśamāgacchēttau hyasya paripanthinau ॥ 3-34॥

The companions of each organ and sense object are attraction and aversion. One should not submit to them; both are enemies on this path of life.

Those for whom the sense organs are of primary importance limit themselves to their boundaries and, throughout their lives, do not rise above strong attraction and aversion. Limited, they are at war with themselves. Strong attraction and aversion are the greatest obstacles on the path to awakening one’s sleeping, immeasurable consciousness.

श्रेयान्स्वधर्मो विगुणः परधर्मात्स्वनुष्ठितात् ।
स्वधर्मे निधनं श्रेयः परधर्मो भयावहः ॥३- ३५॥
śrēyānsvadharmō viguṇaḥ paradharmātsvanuṣṭhitāt ।
svadharmē nidhanaṁ śrēyaḥ paradharmō bhayāvahaḥ ॥ 3-35॥

It is better to follow one’s own dharma, even imperfectly, than to expertly perform another’s. Better to die following one’s own dharma—another’s dharma is dangerous.

☝
☝

80
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
At the root of all fear lies the fear of losing what we love. It is our very love of life that is the cause of the fear of death. In reality, however, life and death are merely different manifestations of one single Presence. Just as its different manifestations can take the form of love and hatred, That Presence, manifesting as the feeling “I am,” has two sides, appearing as life and death.

We prefer to forget that in truth life and death exist in order to become one whole. Life possesses its own beauty, but death is equally poetically beautiful—only a few sādhakas have been able to glorify its beauty. The realization of how great life’s love for death is usually comes too late. But life, from the very beginning to the very end, does nothing but run with all its might towards death, to dissolve in its embrace.

It is precisely in the moment of the meeting of life and death that true beauty is born. Moments of union are always beautiful. Those who, ascending the steps of knowledge, have been able to understand life’s love for death and have become free from attachment to life, are called “jīvanmukta.” As a result of yogic practice, such great people have realized that the force sustaining life, or That unmanifest Presence which manifests through life, is death, or Time. The ancient ṛṣis said: “Dhārayet Sa Dharmah,” which means: “That which sustains is dharma.” Yogis understand this saying thus: because life manifests precisely through death, or Time, the force sustaining life is death, and, since it sustains life, knowing it is dharma. The thinkers of the past were able to understand this truth and therefore called the god of death Dharmarāja.

A sādhak absorbed in his dharma is one who is engaged in awakening the sleeping capacities of his mind in order to know death, or Time, manifesting through life. Such a

☝

81
Chapter 3
yogin devoted to practice, seeing in the moment of the meeting of life and death the beauty of their union, becomes supremely peaceful.

Those, however, who act contrary to dharma, continue to fear death throughout their lives, because they cannot understand that death is the foundation of life, and are unable to comprehend life’s love for death. Such people do not understand that life and death are merely two sides of one unmanifest Presence manifesting through life. Trying with all their might to cling to life, which is only one side of This Infinity, they continue to fear death their entire lives. Such people cannot understand that life is the means by which a great person, having attained the experience of the limitlessness of consciousness and having known the love of life and death, himself becomes limitless, transcending physical limitations at the moment of meeting death.

अर्जुन उवाच
अथ केन प्रयुक्तोऽयं पापं चरति पूरुषः ।
अनिच्छन्नपि वार्ष्णेय बलादिव नियोजितः ॥३- ३६॥
arjuna uvāca
atha kēna prayuktō’yaṁ pāpaṁ carati pūruṣaḥ ।
anicchannapi vārṣṇēya balādiva niyōjitaḥ ॥ 3-36॥

Arjuna said:
“O Vārṣṇeya⁶, but what impels a person to commit sins, even against his own will, as if driven by some force?”

“O Kṛṣṇa, what impels a person to commit sins, who pushes him, even when he himself does not wish it?”

⁶“Descendant of Vṛṣṇi”

☝

82
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
श्रीभगवानुवाच
काम एष क्रोध एष रजोगुणसमुद्भवः ।
महाशनो महापाप्मा विद्ध्येनमिह वैरिणम् ॥३- ३७॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
kāma ēṣa krōdha ēṣa rajōguṇasamudbhavaḥ ।
mahāśanō mahāpāpmā viddhyēnamiha vairiṇam ॥ 3-37॥

The Lord said:
“This force is desire and anger, born of rajoguṇa, the sources of all sins. They are insatiable here; know them as enemies in this world.

The guṇa of passion implies that the sense organs are given greater importance than the mind, as a result of which desire for sense objects is born. When an obstacle arises on the path of this desire for any reason, it manifests in the form of anger. Both these feelings (desire and anger) are the greatest obstacles on the path of awakening the limitless sleeping capacities of the mind, and they, because they keep a person in ignorance, are sin.

धूमेनाव्रियते वह्निर्यथादर्शो मलेन च ।
यथोल्बेनावृतो गर्भस्तथा तेनेदमावृतम् ॥३- ३८॥
आवृतं ज्ञानमेतेन ज्ञानिनो नित्यवैरिणा ।
कामरूपेण कौन्तेय दुष्पूरेणानलेन च ॥३- ३९॥
इन्द्रियाणि मनो बुद्धिरस्याधिष्ठानमुच्यते ।
एतैर्विमोहयत्येष ज्ञानमावृत्य देहिनम् ॥३- ४०॥
dhūmēnāvriyatē vanhiryathādarśō malēna ca ।
yathōlbēnāvṛtō garbhastathā tēnēdamāvṛtam ॥ 3-38॥
āvṛtaṁ jñānamētēna jñāninō nityavairiṇā ।
kāmarupēṇa kauntēya duṣpūrēṇānalēna ca ॥ 3-39॥
indriyāṇi manō buddhirasyādhiṣṭhānamucyatē ।
ētairvimōhayatyēṣa jñānamāvṛtya dēhinam ॥ 3-40॥

O Kaunteya! Just as fire is covered by smoke, a mirror by dust, as an embryo is concealed by the womb, so is this knowledge concealed by the eternal enemy of the wise—passionate desire, all-devouring, fire-like. Its abode is said to be

☝

83
Chapter 3
the sense organs, the conscious mind, and the intellect. Concealing knowledge through these, it deludes all embodied beings.

The limitless consciousness of the human mind remains hidden due to the dominance of the body and sense organs, because most of the mind’s capacities are asleep. Those people who practice yoga to awaken their mind can, as a result of their practice, realize that the mind itself perceives itself through the organs. The senses are merely instruments—desire is born precisely in the mind, and it encourages the striving of the sense organs towards their objects. Ordinary people with sleeping consciousness remain within the bounds of the sense organs and are enchanted by their objects throughout their lives, because they have no idea of the limitlessness of their own mind.

तस्मात्त्वमिन्द्रियाण्यादौ नियम्य भरतर्षभ ।
पाप्मानं प्रजहि ह्येनं ज्ञानविज्ञाननाशनम् ॥३- ४१॥
tasmāt tvamindriyāṇyādau niyamya bharatarṣabha ।
pāpmānaṁ prajahi hyēnaṁ jñānavijñānanāśanam ॥ 3-41॥

O best of the Bharatas! Therefore, having subdued the organs, restrain this sinner [passion], which destroys knowledge and wisdom.

Those who practice yoga to awaken all their sleeping capacities realize that the body and senses are merely the mind’s instruments for gaining experience, and the mind—a manifestation of That indestructible Supreme Essence—is itself Its embodiment. Such yogis transcend all limitations and become established in That Unmanifest Presence.

इन्द्रियाणि पराण्याहुरिन्द्रियेभ्यः परं मनः ।
मनसस्तु परा बुद्धिर्यो बुद्धेः परतस्तु सः ॥३- ४२॥
indriyāṇi parāṇyāhurindriyēbhyaḥ paraṁ manaḥ ।
manasastu parā buddhiryō buddhēḥ paratastu saḥ ॥ 3-42॥

The sense organs are great, but the conscious mind is higher than them; the intellect is higher than the mind; and higher than the intellect is He.

☝
☝

84  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

The conscious mind, being but a small part of the sleeping boundlessness of mind, abides above the sense organs. Above it is the intellect, which inspires the awakening of consciousness through the body. But consciousness itself, ever present in all its immensity, surpasses even the intellect. It is the limitless and indestructible Brahman, the unmanifest conscious Presence – Time, the Creator of the entire universe.  

एवं बुद्धेः परं बुद्ध्वा संस्तभ्यात्मानमात्मना ।  
जहि शत्रुं महाबाहो कामरूपं दुरासदम् ॥३- ४३॥  
ēvaṁ buddhēḥ paraṁ buddhvā saṁstabhyātmānamātmanā ।  
jahi śatruṁ mahābāhō kāmarūpaṁ durāsadam ॥ 3-43॥  

"O Mahābāho! Having known That which surpasses the intellect, and having established the self in the Self, slay desire – that invincible enemy."  

The sādhaka who practices yoga, attaining self-mastery, experiences his own boundlessness. In other words, having awakened his dormant capacities, he gains the experience of the limitlessness of his consciousness and becomes established in samādhi. Such a great one is called *sthitaprajña*.  

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे  
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे कर्मयोगो नाम तृतीयोऽध्यायः ॥ ३ ॥  
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē  
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē karmayōgō nāma tṛtīyō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 3॥  

Oṁ Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the third chapter, "Yoga of Action," of the Upaniṣad called Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.  

☝  
☝  

चतुर्थोऽध्यायः ज्ञानकर्मसंन्यासयोगः  
caturthō’dhyāyaḥ jñānakarmasaṁnyāsayōgaḥ  

**Chapter 4**  
**YOGA OF SELF-KNOWLEDGE**  

86  
श्रीभगवानुवाच  
इमं विवस्वते योगं प्रोक्तवानहमव्ययम् ।  
विवस्वान्मनवे प्राह मनुरिक्ष्वाकवेऽब्रवीत् ॥४-१॥  
śrībhagavānuvāca  
imaṁ vivasvatē yōgaṁ prōktavānahamavyayam ।  
vivasvānmanavē prāha manurikśvākavē’bravīt ॥ 4-1॥  

The Lord said:  
"I proclaimed this eternal yoga to Vivasvān; Vivasvān explained it to Manu, and Manu taught it to Ikṣvāku."  

Having described the fruits of this great yoga, Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa now explains its practical aspect from the very beginning.  

एवं परम्पराप्राप्तमिमं राजर्षयो विदुः ।  
स कालेनेह महता योगो नष्टः परन्तप ॥४-२॥  
ēvaṁ paramparāprāptamimaṁ rājarṣayō viduḥ ।  
sa kālēnēha mahatā yōgō naṣṭaḥ parantapa ॥ 4-2॥  

Thus the royal sages knew this yoga, which was transmitted from teacher to disciple. O Parantapa! Yoga was lost in the world for a long time.  

☝  
ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय  
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya  
Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya  

87  
**Chapter 4**  

स एवायं मया तेऽद्य योगः प्रोक्तः पुरातनः ।  
भक्तोऽसि मे सखा चेति रहस्यं ह्येतदुत्तमम् ॥४-३॥  
sa ēvāyaṁ mayā tē’dya yōgaḥ prōktaḥ purātanaḥ ।  
bhaktō’si mē sakhā cēti rahasyaṁ hyētaduttamam ॥ 4-3॥  

"I have revealed to you today that same ancient yoga, the supreme secret, for you are My devotee and My friend."  

अर्जुन उवाच  
अपरं भवतो जन्म परं जन्म विवस्वतः ।  
कथमेतद्विजानीयां त्वमादौ प्रोक्तवानिति ॥४-४॥  
arjuna uvāca  
aparaṁ bhavatō janma paraṁ janma vivasvataḥ ।  
kathamētadvijānīyāṁ tvamādau prōktavāniti ॥ 4-4॥  

Arjuna said:  
"You live now, whereas Vivasvān lived in the past. How can I believe that you proclaimed this to him?"  

श्रीभगवानुवाच  
बहूनि मे व्यतीतानि जन्मानि तव चार्जुन ।  
तान्यहं वेद सर्वाणि न त्वं वेत्थ परन्तप ॥४-५॥  
śrībhagavānuvāca  
bahūni mē vyatītāni janmāni tava cārjuna ।  
tānyahaṁ vēda sarvāṇi na tvaṁ vēttha parantapa ॥ 4-5॥  

The Lord said:  
"O Arjuna! Many births have passed for both you and Me. O Parantapa! You know none of them, but I know them all.  

अजोऽपि सन्नव्ययात्मा भूतानामीश्वरोऽपि सन् ।  
प्रकृतिं स्वामधिष्ठाय संभवाम्यात्ममायया ॥४-६॥  
ajō’pi sannavyayātmā bhūtānāmīśvarō’pi san ।  
prakṛtiṁ svāmadhiṣṭhāya sambhavāmyātmamāyayā ॥ 4-6॥  

Though I am indestructible, unborn, and the Supreme Lord of all beings, I manifest Myself through māyā, mastering My own nature."  

88  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

यदा यदा हि धर्मस्य ग्लानिर्भवति भारत ।  
अभ्युत्थानमधर्मस्य तदात्मानं सृजाम्यहम् ॥४-७॥  
yadā yadā hi dharmasya glānirbhavati bhārata ।  
abhyutthānamadharmasya tadātmānaṁ sṛjāmyaham ॥ 4-7॥  

"I manifest Myself whenever My law [dharma] declines and lawlessness [adharma] flourishes."  

In this world there are epochs when man, the best manifestation of the consciousness of Time, imprisons himself within physical boundaries and turns away from the ancient system of yoga, which awakens the dormant capacities of the mind for the knowledge of Time. Thus man gives rise to lawlessness (adharma) through his inability to practice yoga for the realization of this unmanifest conscious Presence. In such epochs, this unmanifest Parameśvara manifests Himself as a superhuman being, granting inspiration to ordinary people, so that by awakening their dormant boundless consciousness through yoga, they may become established in That unmanifest Time, the Light of all light, which manifests Its best creation – the consciousness of the human mind.  

परित्राणाय साधूनां विनाशाय च दुष्कृताम् ।  
धर्मसंस्थापनार्थाय सम्भवामि युगे युगे ॥४-८॥  
paritrāṇāya sādhūnāṁ vināśāya ca duṣkṛtām ।  
dharmasaṁsthāpanārthāya sambhavāmi yugē yugē ॥ 4-8॥  

"I come from age to age to protect the virtuous, destroy the wicked, and re-establish order."  

Those who follow the teaching of yoga, which such a great superhuman being bestows upon ordinary people, attain direct experience of Paramātman, the embodiment of Time. Through death they achieve liberation from the great bondage – the necessity of being born. Such sages who have known death, the *sthitaprajña*, are called *sādhu*. Those, however, who pay no heed to the boundless conscious Presence manifesting through the body, and who do not even suspect That unmanifest Supreme Spirit, Paramātman, live  

☝  
☝  

89  
**Chapter 4**  

unrighteously, caring only for the body. Such people remain bound to the wheel of saṁsāra. Death, which they so fear, destroys them again and again.  

जन्म कर्म च मे दिव्यमेवं यो वेत्ति तत्त्वतः ।  
त्यक्त्वा देहं पुनर्जन्म नैति मामेति सोऽर्जुन ॥४-९॥  
janma karma ca mē divyamēvaṁ yō vētti tattvataḥ ।  
tyaktvā dēhaṁ punarjanma naiti māmēti sō’rjuna ॥ 4-9॥  

"O Arjuna! My births and actions are divine. He who knows this in truth, after abandoning the body, attains Me and is not reborn."  

Time, the primordial Supreme Truth, manifests Itself in the form of the human body and through this leaves a hint of Itself – such are Its divine actions. The yogī who understands this hint of Time, knowing Its true nature, no longer needs to manifest in bodily form. He realizes That boundless Time, the primordial Supreme Essence, and by Its grace attains unity with It.  

वीतरागभयक्रोधा मन्मया मामुपाश्रिताः ।  
बहवो ज्ञानतपसा पूता मद्भावमागताः ॥४-१०॥  
vītarāgabhayakrōdhā manmayā mām upāśritāḥ ।  
bahavō jñānatapasā pūtā madbhāvamāgatāḥ ॥ 4-10॥  

"Free from passion, fear, and anger, absorbed in Me, taking refuge in Me, and purified by the fire of knowledge, many have attained My state."  

Great yogīs who have found refuge in Time Itself rise above passion, fear, and anger, and by awakening their boundless consciousness through the practice of yoga, merge with That unmanifest radiant Time.  

☝  
☝  

90  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

ये यथा मां प्रपद्यन्ते तांस्तथैव भजाम्यहम् ।  
मम वर्त्मानुवर्तन्ते मनुष्याः पार्थ सर्वशः ॥४-११॥  
yē yathā māṁ prapadyantē tāṁstathaiva bhajāmyaham ।  
mama vartmānuvartantē manuṣyāḥ pārtha sarvaśaḥ ॥ 4-11॥  

"As they approach Me, so do I receive them – all paths lead to Me, O Pārtha!"  

Yogīs who have realized that this entire world manifests Time Itself are filled with devotion to Time. Realizing Its infinity, such great ones find refuge only in It and always conduct themselves accordingly. Such sages know that whether people try to satisfy sensual desires, confining themselves to physical limits, or strive to know the true nature of Time by awakening their sleeping consciousness and overcoming physical limitations, all follow the current of Time – both meet death when their life's path ends. Those who have known the true nature of death, passing through death, attain unity with Time. Those who do not know Time remain in fear of death and, after meeting it, are reborn again.  

काङ्क्षन्तः कर्मणां सिद्धिं यजन्त इह देवताः ।  
क्षिप्रं हि मानुषे लोके सिद्धिर्भवति कर्मजा ॥४-१२॥  
kāṅkśantaḥ karmaṇāṁ siddhiṁ yajanta iha dēvatāḥ ।  
kśipraṁ hi mānuṣē lōkē siddhirbhavati karmajā ॥ 4-12॥  

"Desiring success in actions, they worship the gods here. The fruits of karma quickly ripen in this world of mortals."  

The intellect of those who cannot grasp the fundamental element of the universe remains limited by physical boundaries. Such people act, driven by the desire for results from their karma. The actions of such people, like the premature fruits of those actions, are limited. People attached to obtaining pleasures and satisfying the senses worship the gods to achieve their goals. Those who strive to awaken the dormant capacities of the mind and become established in the unmanifest  

☝  
☝  

91  
**Chapter 4**  

Consciousness of Time perform the practice of yoga. Karma performed by the embodied one yields quick results – such is the peculiarity of this body and the world of mortals.  

चातुर्वर्ण्यं मया सृष्टं गुणकर्मविभागशः ।  
तस्य कर्तारमपि मां विद्ध्यकर्तारमव्ययम् ॥४-१३॥  
cāturvarṇyaṁ mayā sṛṣṭaṁ guṇakarmavibhāgaśaḥ ।  
tasya kartāramapi māṁ viddhyakartāramavyayam ॥ 4-13॥  

"Dividing [people] according to nature and actions, I created the four varṇas. Know Me, their creator, to be free from karma."  

That primordial Truth, by whatever name It is called – indestructible Brahman, Parameśvara, Īśvara, or Time – assuming the form of man, who is Its best creation, does so by using the bodies of people of four orders, corresponding to their nature, actions, and disposition.  

Consciousness evolves from the gross to the subtle. The Śūdras (the serving class) are at the first stage of this evolution, when the soul (mind or self) gains experience of various perceptions, chiefly related to the body, and prepares for the next stage of development. At the next stage, the embodied one receives intense sensory experience (especially connected with the accumulation of wealth) concerning the sustenance of the body, for instance, in agriculture, animal husbandry, trade, and so on. This is the fundamental activity for maintaining the gross body. The Vaiśyas (the mercantile class) are at the second stage of the development of consciousness. When all experience of caring for the body has been obtained, consciousness reaches the threshold of transcending physical boundaries. Then one passes into the varṇa of the Kṣatriyas (the warrior class). It is in war that all experiences related to self-sacrifice reach their climax. When the pious feeling of encountering death is experienced, the human mind, rising above worldly sensations, strives to gain the experience of the Presence beyond physical limitations and the Sense of all senses, the Consciousness of all consciousness, Time, Paramātman.  

☝

92  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

It can be said that the embodied one moves toward his final liberation when he arrives at the fourth stage of evolution. At this stage, he is called a brāhmaṇa.

Today we have ruined all the beauty of this great system – the system of the four varṇas – by resorting to an extremely limited and narrow point of view. The scriptures say that these four estates, i.e., brāhmaṇas, kṣatriyas, vaiśyas, and śūdras, are the four principal parts of the body of Puruṣa. In other words, they represent the four principal forms of manifestation of that Immeasurable Element. Without any one of these forms, the manifestation of that Immeasurable Truth would be incomplete.

In India, the continuity of the transmission of knowledge from teacher to disciple has been preserved. It is precisely this continuity that was wrongfully used to confine the varṇa system to the territory of India. This was done by those false scholars who had not attained self-realization but passed themselves off as realized masters, imitating the wise. These immature scholars gave rise to a host of absurdities in Indian society in the name of the social system.

Now this is in the past; times have changed. Today all people must step beyond so-called political barriers and recognize themselves as citizens of the world. We live in a cosmic age, when humanity is gradually comprehending the phenomenon of the global unity of human civilization beyond the framework of national distinctions. If we look at what Lord Kṛṣṇa said on a global scale, we will easily see that His words pertain to all of humanity. Those who could not understand this confined this system to the territory of India. If, however, without limiting ourselves to India, we consider our entire planet, it turns out that the human race is divided into four colors: black, yellow, white, and brown. No other color occurs on Earth with equal frequency.

The human race which, according to Indian wisdom, manifested from the feet of Virāṭ Puruṣa¹ – these are the śūdras. The representatives of the black race of the Earth belong to this category. This

93  
Chapter 4

can easily be understood by observing their way of life, habits, type of thinking, culture, etc.

Agriculture, animal husbandry, and trade are the activities natural to the vaiśyas. Taking these characteristics into account, one can understand that the yellow-colored Mongoloid race constitutes the vaiśyas. On the entire Earth, no one is as devoted to agriculture and animal husbandry as the Mongoloid race. They are the vaiśyas of the Earth, having emerged from the belly of Puruṣa.

From the arms of Virāṭ Puruṣa the kṣatriyas were created. The traits natural to kṣatriyas are fearlessness, brilliance of character, courage, tact, steadfastness in battle, selflessness, the ability to lead people, as well as to manufacture and use weapons. These qualities are naturally endowed upon the white race, whose representatives are the kṣatriyas of the Earth. Looking at history, one can see that the greatest wars on this globe were waged by the armies of the white race, and they also governed most of the territories on Earth.

Now let us speak of the brāhmaṇas, who arose from the mouth of Puruṣa. Their natural qualities are tranquility, self-control, purity, asceticism, forgiveness, unpretentiousness of mind, senses, and body, piety, knowledge of sacred texts and the ability to compose them, capacity for perception of the Supreme Spirit and the dissemination of virtue, etc. Taking this into account, we discover that a particular race living between India and Israel (whose representatives, in physical constitution, resemble Europeans, but whose skin color is not white) – these are the brāhmaṇas of the Earth. All the religions of the world were preached by people of this race; all messiahs and Divine incarnations appeared among them. Faith in God and spiritual wisdom are their innate characteristics. Regardless of their creed – whether they are followers of sanātana dharma or Islām, Pārsīs or Buddhists, Jews or Christians – the innate devotion to the Supreme

¹ “The Cosmic Primordial Man”

94  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

Entity, which is clearly present in them, is the natural property of brāhmaṇas.

Now it is necessary to realize that the varṇa system is not a parochial concept of Indian philosophy. If one contemplates the division into varṇas globally, one can understand that it was not created by man – this division is inherent in the very cosmos itself.

**na māṁ karmāṇi limpanti na mē karmaphalē spṛhā ।  
iti māṁ yō’bhijānāti karmabhirna sa badhyatē ॥ 4-14॥**

I have no desire for the fruits of actions; karma is unable to stain Me. Whoever knows Me thus is not entangled by karma.

Those who have understood these hints and awakened the boundless consciousness of their mind by transcending physical limitations are able to know the true nature of unmanifest Time. Freeing themselves from all desires, they attain liberation from all bonds.

**ēvaṁ jñātvā kṛtaṁ karma pūrvairapi mumukśubhiḥ ।  
kuru karmaiva tasmāttvaṁ pūrvaiḥ pūrvataraṁ kṛtam ॥ 4-15॥**

Even the ancient seekers performed karma, realizing this. Like them, you too must act.

Many people who have studied the stories of the sages of antiquity and, on this basis, proclaimed themselves sages, quite often say that Brahman is real and the material world is an illusion. By calling the entire visible world an illusion, they equate themselves with the ancient sages, simply ignoring the fact that it is practically impossible to grasp the essence of their statements without attaining the same level of consciousness on which those great ones who composed these descriptions abided. People

95  
Chapter 4

who pass themselves off as scholars, reading such statements in the sacred texts, do not know that the authors of these statements comprehended the human mind as the support of all knowledge. It is the mind that is capable of knowing the truth of the consciousness of Time after awakening its boundlessness through the performance of yogic practice with the help of the body. It is considered that obtaining a human body is difficult even for the gods. Having plowed this great field through the practice of yoga and sown it with the seeds of knowledge, one can obtain the fruit of the knowledge of unmanifest Time, which manifests this universe.

When a yogī succeeds in fully awakening his consciousness, having risen above physical limitations through the practice of yoga, he acquires the ability to contemplate the Truth which creates, sustains, and then destroys everything. Whatever is said by such a great person who understands this mystery, his statements are merely a hint for the ignorant. Those who mistakenly consider themselves sages, seeing such hints in the sacred scriptures, are in reality throughout their lives engaged only in gratifying their own senses. They juggle such concepts as “Prakṛti,” “Puruṣa,” “Māyā,” “Brahman,” “Ātman,” and others, merely wasting themselves in vain. To become knowledgeable, it is necessary, understanding the hints of the wise, to develop one’s capacities and, through self-knowledge, to plunge into the boundless ocean of consciousness, gaining experience of that Truth which manifests itself through the entire visible world.

**kiṁ karma kimakarmēti kavayō’pyatra mōhitāḥ ।  
tattē karma pravakśyāmi yajjñātvā mōkśyasē’śubhāt ॥ 4-16॥  
karmaṇō hyapi bōddhavyaṁ bōddhavyaṁ ca vikarmaṇaḥ ।  
akarmaṇaśca bōddhavyaṁ gahanā karmaṇō gatiḥ ॥ 4-17॥**

What is action? What is inaction? This question confounds even the wise. I will tell you about karma;

96  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

this knowledge will grant you liberation. One should know the essence of karma, the truth of vikarma, and also the truth of akarma, for the consequences of actions are inscrutable.

What is yogic practice and what is its result, called akarma? This question still troubles many scholars. Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa, through Arjuna, explains that very yogic practice, the performance of which leads to liberation from the binding fetters of birth. It is necessary to know the nature of this yoga-karma. It is also necessary to know its result, called akarma – the state beyond karma, which is also termed samādhi. Furthermore, one must understand vikarma – actions that prevent a person from performing this great yogic practice. The results of this path, which liberates consciousness from physical bonds through the practice of yoga, are not obvious; therefore this path is described as inscrutable.

**karmaṇyakarma yaḥ paśyēdakarmaṇi ca karma yaḥ ।  
sa buddhimānmanuṣyēṣu sa yuktaḥ kṛtsnakarmakṛt ॥ 4-18॥**

Who sees akarma in karma and karma in akarma, he is a sage among men. Such a yogī is considered to have attained perfection in action.

A sādhaka, burning with the desire to attain the result of yoga – samādhi – performs this practice in order to awaken his sleeping consciousness. As a result, he becomes niṣkāma and is established in akarma, which is the consequence of karma. Having become established in akarma, he also understands that his state of niṣkāma is the result of the yogic practice performed in the past. This great person perceives karma in akarma and akarma in karma. Such sthitaprajña, having known karma and akarma, become Pūrṇa-kāma².

² “One who has fulfilled all desires”

97  
Chapter 4

**yasya sarvē samārambhāḥ kāmasaṁkalpavarjitāḥ ।  
jñānāgnidagdhakarmāṇaṁ tamāhuḥ paṇḍitaṁ budhāḥ ॥ 4-19॥**

One whose undertakings are devoid of desires and intentions, whose karma is burned in the fire of knowledge, is called a knower by the wise.

He who, through the performance of yogic practice, has obtained its results, has become niṣkāma and has transcended desires and intentions. Such a great person, who, being niṣkāma, has attained samādhi and become established in akarma, is called a sage, a sthitaprajña.

**tyaktvā karmaphalāsaṅgaṁ nityatṛptō nirāśrayaḥ ।  
karmaṇyabhipravṛttō’pi naiva kiṁcitkarōti saḥ ॥ 4-20॥**

Without support, always content and detached from the pursuit of the fruits of karma, he, even while acting, abides in inaction.

Having obtained the experience of the vastness of their mind, such great people know the true nature of the primordial, eternal Time that manifests consciousness. Established in themselves and having known themselves, they realize Time and always remain devoted to It. They do nothing even when they do something; in the same way, they do everything even when they do nothing.

**nirāśīryatacittātmā tyaktasarvaparigrahaḥ ।  
śārīraṁ kēvalaṁ karma kurvannāpnōti kilbiṣam ॥ 4-21॥**

He who has abandoned hope, has mastered himself, and has renounced all possessions, commits no sin while merely performing actions for the maintenance of the body.

**98**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

Great beings who have realized their limitations and transcended them through the awakening of their dormant consciousness by the practice of yoga, fulfill all their desires. For such people, life loses its allure, since all its goals have already been attained. Although such great *sthitaprajña* appear to perform actions through the body throughout their lives, they are truly beyond all limitations.

*yadṛcchālābhasantuṣṭō dvandvātītō vimatsaraḥ |
samaḥ siddhāvasiddhau ca kṛtvāpi na nibadhyatē || 4-22 ||*

Content with what comes of itself, free from duality and envy, unchanging in success and failure, he is not bound by the karma he performs.

The *sthitaprajña* established in samadhi regards gain and loss, joy and sorrow, envy, success and failure equally. For him, all these states are merely manifestations of the one Consciousness and therefore equal to one another.

*gatasaṅgasya muktasya jñānāvasthitacētasaḥ |
yajñāyācarataḥ karma samagraṁ pravilīyatē || 4-23 ||*

Having abandoned attachment, with consciousness established in wisdom, these liberated people perform *yajña*, whereby all their karma is completely dissolved.

This *yajña* is performed in a state of complete impartiality by kindling the fire of yoga through the physical body and awakening pure consciousness. As a result, all karma, because it originates in the mind, dissolves within it as well. This yogic wisdom is now expounded by Lord Shri Krishna.

☝
☝
☝

**99**
**Chapter 4**

*brahmārpaṇaṁ brahma havirbrahmāgnau brahmaṇā hutam |
brahmaiva tēna gantavyaṁ brahmakarmasamādhinā || 4-24 ||*

The offering is Brahman, Brahman is the oblation offered by Brahman into the fire of Brahman; Brahman alone is to be attained by him who is absorbed in the action of Brahman.

The human mind, being a manifestation of that eternal Brahman, is itself Brahman. Those who have kindled the fire of yoga in their body and offered their own body as a sacrifice into this fire, while still in the body, know that Boundlessness and, overcoming physical limitations through death, themselves attain Boundlessness. They realize that this body, the fire of yoga burning within it, the sleeping consciousness, the awakened consciousness – all are but forms of Brahman, manifestations of Time.

*daivamēvāparē yajñaṁ yōginaḥ paryupāsatē |
brahmāgnāvaparē yajñaṁ yajñēnaivōpajuhvati || 4-25 ||*

These yogis worship only *yajña* and through it sacrifice the offering of *yajña* itself into the fire of Brahman.

Devotees of yoga, through their practice, come to know the immeasurability of their mind, as well as the true role of the senses, which are merely instruments of the mind for obtaining experience. Pious people who continue to satisfy their mind, the form of Brahman, also comprehend this. When such yogis awaken their entire consciousness, thereby attaining samadhi and becoming free from their desires, they offer themselves as an oblation into the fire of yogic practice performed through their body, and attain unity with the primordial Brahman.

☝
☝

**100**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*śrōtrādīnīndriyāṇyanyē saṁyamāgniṣu juhvati |
śabdādīnviṣayānanya indriyāgniṣu juhvati || 4-26 ||
sarvāṇīndriyakarmāṇi prāṇakarmāṇi cāparē |
ātmasaṁyamayōgāgnau juvhati jñānadīpitē || 4-27 ||*

Some offer hearing and the other senses into the fire of self-control, while others offer sound and other objects of perception into the fire of the senses.

Into the fire of yoga, kindled by wisdom, yogis sacrifice all their worldly actions along with all their spiritual deeds.

The *sādhaka*, striving for the cherished result – samadhi, diligently performs the practice of yoga. In this attempt to know the interrelation of mind and senses, he controls his senses by means of the mind and thus realizes that it is indeed the mind that perceives sound and other sense objects through the organs. Having realized this, the yogin rises above the influence of the sense organs and moves further. He understands that the interrelation of mind and senses is sustained by *prāṇa*, which is expressed in the form of breath. Controlling the breath, the yogin masters *prāṇa* and, offering the objects of the senses as oblations into the fire of yoga kindled by means of *prāṇāyāma*, continues to advance towards the Infinite.

*dravyayajñāstapōyajñā yōgayajñāstathāparē |
svādhyāyajñānayajñāśca yatayaḥ saṁśitavratāḥ || 4-28 ||*

Other steadfast ones perform *yajña* for wealth, or *yajña* for austerity, or the *yajña* of yoga, or, firmly observing vows, they perform *jñāna-yajña* through self-knowledge.

☝

**101**
**Chapter 4**

Yogis engage in self-knowledge according to the level of their consciousness, studying their own essence. Their *tapas* is the *yajña* of *prāṇāyāma*, by which they kindle the fire of yoga in their body. Sacrificing themselves to this fire, knowing themselves, they abide in self-satisfaction. Whether such people are engaged in accumulating wealth, or performing austerities, or practicing yoga, or observing vows, they are truly only studying the various facets of their own consciousness. Those engaged in self-knowledge understand that in the process of performing any activity, a person merely perceives different aspects of his own personality.

*apānē juvhati prāṇaṁ prāṇē’pānaṁ tathāparē |
prāṇāpānagatī ruddhvā prāṇāyāmaparāyaṇāḥ || 4-29 ||
aparē niyatāhārāḥ prāṇānprāṇēṣu juhvati |
sarvē’pyētē yajñavidō yajñakśapitakalmaṣāḥ || 4-30 ||*

Earnest in the practice of *prāṇāyāma*, restraining the currents of *prāṇa* and *apāna*, they offer *prāṇa* into *apāna* and *apāna* into *prāṇa*. Purified of impurities by this sacrifice, they all become knowers of *yajña*.

Next is described the path followed by yogis who wish to awaken their sleeping consciousness through *prāṇāyāma*. These techniques are transmitted only from the mouth of the Guru. The first stage of this yoga, which the beginning *sādhaka* practices to release his consciousness from physical limits, is known as Brahma-granthi-bheda or Jihva-granthi-bheda³. It includes mastering *khecarī mudrā* and performing a special *prāṇāyāma* in which the natural flows of *prāṇa* and *apāna* are restrained,

³ "Piercing the knot of Brahma" or "Piercing the tongue knot"

☝
☝

**102**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

and *prāṇa* is offered into *apāna*, and *apāna* into *prāṇa* to bring them into balance. At this stage, when the yogin is able to perform *khecarī mudrā* (his rolled-back tongue passes into the throat and straightens towards *bhrūmadhya*) and simultaneously balance *prāṇa* and *apāna*, he rises above physical limitations and begins to approach establishment in Boundlessness. Now he is ready for the second stage of this ancient yoga.

The second stage is called Hridaya-granthi-bheda or Vishnu-granthi-bheda⁴. It includes two unusual *prāṇāyāmas*. During the first *prāṇāyāma*, *khecarī mudrā* is performed, *apāna* is raised and retained at the level of the heart, while *prāṇa* from the heart descends to the place of *apāna* and is retained there. Simultaneously, special movements of the head and neck are performed. In the second *prāṇāyāma* of this same stage, the yogin learns to still *prāṇa* and *apāna*, also performing special actions with the head and neck. The yogin who succeeds at this stage can receive the direct *darśana* of Lord Vasudeva, so called because He dwells in the heart of every being and sustains the entire material world. Then the yogin becomes established in the consciousness of the all-pervading Void, the embodiment of Vishnu Himself. Having achieved success in the stage of Hridaya-granthi-bheda, the yogin may proceed to the practice of Rudra-granthi-bheda or Muladhara-granthi-bheda⁵. This stage is so named because it enables one, through death, to directly perceive the primordial Truth – Time, which is the main Support of all supports and therefore called "mūl-ādhāra".

Success in this practice is attained only by those yogis who have passed through Hridaya-granthi and, established in the consciousness of the Void, are able to easily stop their heartbeat. In this final stage of yoga, which grants direct perception of the unmanifest Time, *prāṇa* is offered into *prāṇa* during the performance of *yonī mudrā*. This *prāṇāyāma* is called

⁴ "Piercing the heart knot" or "Piercing the knot of Vishnu"
⁵ "Piercing the knot of Rudra" or "Piercing the root knot"

**103**
**Chapter 4**

*Oṁkār kriyā*. As a result of performing this practice, the yogin receives the direct *darśana* of Time, the primordial Supreme Essence, and thus knows His true nature. *Oṁkār kriyā* enables the yogin to leave the body at the end of life by means of yogic power.

*yajñaśiṣṭāmṛtabhujō yānti brahma sanātanam |
nāyaṁ lōkō’styayajñasya kutō’nyaḥ kurusattama || 4-31 ||*

O Kurushreshtha⁶! Those who partake of the *amṛta* – the result of *yajña* – attain the Eternal Brahman. For those who do not sacrifice, there is not even this world, what to speak of other worlds beyond this?

Yogis fully awaken their consciousness by performing this great yogic practice and realize the true nature of death. Overcoming physical boundaries, they become established in the Eternal Brahman. Those who cannot do this remain in confusion, their consciousness is limited, and they only waste their lives in this world. When death comes, great terror seizes them, for they have not known its essence.

*ēvaṁ bahuvidhā yajñā vitatā brahmaṇō mukhē |
karmajānviddhi tānsarvānēvaṁ jñātvā vimōkśyasē || 4-32 ||*

Many such *yajñas* have been spread forth from the mouth of Brahman. Know them all as actions to be performed. Having realized this, you shall be liberated.

The three main stages of this ancient yoga, which successively bestow knowledge, have been expounded by great beings who have known Brahman. They are practiced by seekers of truth, firmly resolved

⁶ "Best of the Kuru dynasty"

☝
☝

**104**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

to attain samadhi, having received instruction from great beings who have known Brahman. Practicing this ancient yoga, they become *sthitaprajña*, know the essence of death, and thus achieve the overcoming of the great bond – the necessity of being born – liberating their consciousness from the limitations of the physical body.

*śrēyāndravyamayādyajñājjñānayajñaḥ parantapa |
sarvaṁ karmākhilaṁ pārtha jñānē parisamāpyatē || 4-33 ||*

O Parantapa! The *jñāna-yajña* surpasses the *yajña* for material abundance. O Partha! All karma ultimately culminates in wisdom.

Actions limited by the body and sense organs, not directed towards the knowledge of the Paramātman, Time, which manifests them, lead to the confinement of consciousness to the body alone. Better than such actions is that karma which, through the overcoming of physical limitations, leads to the knowledge of that unmanifest Presence. The result of such actions is wisdom, which establishes the yogin in Boundlessness, freeing him from physical and mental limitations.

*tadviddhi praṇipātēna paripraśnēna sēvayā |
upadēkśyanti tē jñānaṁ jñāninastattvadarśinaḥ || 4-34 ||*

Know that by prostrating yourself, by questioning, and by service, the wise ones, the seers of truth, will impart that knowledge to you.

One should strive to receive instruction in this ancient kriyā yoga by honoring the great sages who have known the truth, serving them, and questioning them again and again. The knowers of yogic practice, taking into account the qualities of the inquirer, bestow upon him instruction in this teaching. When an ordinary person bows before a sage, offering him reverence, this represents

☝
☝

**105**
**Chapter 4**

is an expression of respect not to any particular person, but to that ancient knowledge which is continuously transmitted from Guru to disciple. The person is merely a means of expressing this wisdom.

यज्ज्ञात्वा न पुनर्मोहमेवं यास्यसि पाण्डव ।
येन भूतान्यशेषेण द्रक्ष्यस्यात्मन्यथो मयि ॥४-३५॥
yajjñātvā na punarmōhamēvaṁ yāsyasi pāṇḍava ।
yēna bhūtānyaśēṣēṇa drakśyasyātmanyathō mayi ॥ 4-35॥

O Pāṇḍava! Having known this, you will never again fall into confusion. By the power of this knowledge, you will see yourself again in all beings.

Having received initiation into this yoga and then practicing it, a person never again falls into confusion. Established in samādhi through the awakening of all his sleeping consciousness, he comes to know that Unmanifest Element which creates this entire world, and sees no difference between himself and all other beings. Observing everywhere only that Unmanifest Truth, he sees himself and all other beings abiding in that One Truth.

अपि चेदसि पापेभ्यः सर्वेभ्यः पापकृत्तमः ।
सर्वं ज्ञानप्लवेनैव वृजिनं सन्तरिष्यसि ॥४-३६॥
api cēdasi pāpēbhyaḥ sarvēbhyaḥ pāpakṛttamaḥ ।
sarvaṁ jñānaplavēnaiva vṛjinaṁ santariṣyasi ॥ 4-36॥

Even if you are the greatest of sinners, through knowledge you will be purified of all sins.

Even if a person was previously limited by physical boundaries and engaged only in the satisfaction of his own senses, he is capable of awakening his sleeping consciousness, having firmly resolved to free it from physical limitations and attain samādhi, by practicing this ancient yoga. By focusing his awakened consciousness on the truth of Time, he can come to know His true nature. Thus he is freed from all sins connected with the limitation of the mind.

यथैधांसि समिद्धोऽग्निर्भस्मसात्कुरुतेऽर्जुन ।
ज्ञानाग्निः सर्वकर्माणि भस्मसात्कुरुते तथा ॥४-३७॥
yathaidhāṁsi samiddhō’gnirbhasmasātkurutē’rjuna ।
jñānāgniḥ sarvakarmāṇi bhasmasātkurutē tathā ॥ 4-37॥

O Arjuna! As a blazing fire turns firewood to ashes, so does the fire of wisdom turn all karma to ashes.

Sādhakas who have kindled the fire of yoga in their body and offered all their desires as oblation into it, awaken their limitless consciousness and transcend physical limits. As a result of yogic practice, they become established in the state of akarma and rise above all desires.

न हि ज्ञानेन सदृशं पवित्रमिह विद्यते ।
तत्स्वयं योगसंसिद्धः कालेनात्मनि विन्दति ॥४-३८॥
na hi jñānēna sadṛśaṁ pavitramiha vidyatē ।
tatsvayaṁ yōgasaṁsiddhaḥ kālēnātmani vindati ॥ 4-38॥

Truly, nothing in this world purifies like knowledge. One who has attained perfection through yoga finds this wisdom within himself in due time.

In this world, nothing purifies like knowledge. The yogin attains this wisdom by kindling the fire of yoga in his body and coming to know the secret of life and death through the awakening of his full consciousness.

श्रद्धावाँल्लभते ज्ञानं तत्परः संयतेन्द्रियः ।
ज्ञानं लब्ध्वा परां शान्तिमचिरेणाधिगच्छति ॥४-३९॥
śraddhāvāṁllabhatē jñānaṁ tatparaḥ saṁyatēndriyaḥ ।
jñānaṁ labdhvā parāṁ śāntimacirēṇādhigacchati ॥ 4-39॥

One who has mastered his organs of sense, who is devoted and thirsts for knowledge, soon attains supreme peace.

The sādhaka devoted to this teaching of yoga is always filled with resolve in his practice. Experiencing the vastness of the mind, he is able to know the unmanifest truth of Time which lies beyond it. Such a jitendriya¹ attains tranquility when all his doubts are dispelled.

¹ "One who has subdued the organs of sense"

अज्ञश्चाश्रद्दधानश्च संशयात्मा विनश्यति ।
नायं लोकोऽस्ति न परो न सुखं संशयात्मनः ॥४-४०॥
ajñaścāśraddadhānaśca saṁśayātmā vinaśyati ।
nāyaṁ lōkō’sti na parō na sukhaṁ saṁśayātmanaḥ ॥ 4-40॥

The ignorant, the faithless, and the doubting person perishes. For one who is in doubt, there is neither this world nor the next, nor happiness.

People who place the body and sense organs above all else remain in fear of death throughout their lives due to the limitation of their intellect. Even upon hearing the words of the wise, captivated by the objects of the senses, they begin to doubt. They can neither attain the benefit of yogic practice nor fully enjoy the objects of the senses. Living a life full of doubt, such people waste themselves in vain.

योगसंन्यस्तकर्माणं ज्ञानसंछिन्नसंशयम् ।
आत्मवन्तं न कर्माणि निबध्नन्ति धनंजय ॥४-४१॥
yōgasaṁnyastakarmāṇaṁ jñānasaṁchinnasaṁśayam ।
ātmavantaṁ na karmāṇi nibadhnanti dhanaṁjaya ॥ 4-41॥

O Dhanañjaya! Actions do not bind a self-realized person, whose every karma has been burned in the fire of yoga and whose doubts have been destroyed by knowledge.

Nothing binds those great persons who are established in the state of akarma, who have become free from desires by performing yogic practice, who have attained the knowledge of the Limitless and therefore have been freed from all doubts regarding life and death. Such great persons surrender to the mercy of Time and attain oneness with Him.

तस्मादज्ञानसम्भूतं हृत्स्थं ज्ञानासिनात्मनः ।
छित्त्वैनं संशयं योगमातिष्ठोत्तिष्ठ भारत ॥४-४२॥
tasmādajñānasambhūtaṁ hṛtsthaṁ jñānāsinātmanaḥ ।
chittvainaṁ saṁśayaṁ yōgamātiṣṭhōttiṣṭha bhārata ॥ 4-42॥

O Bhārata, arise! Establishing yourself in yoga, cut asunder with the sword of wisdom this doubt born of ignorance in the mind."

Having in mind all who live in doubt, Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa says to Arjuna: "Do not consider yourself limited by the body; cut asunder all the doubts of your mind with the sword of wisdom and practice this ancient yoga to attain knowledge."

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे ज्ञानकर्मसंन्यासयोगो नाम चतुर्थोऽध्यायः ॥ ४ ॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē jñānakarmasaṁnyāsayōgō nāma caturthō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 4॥

  Oṁ Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the fourth chapter, entitled "The Yoga of Self-Knowledge," of the Upaniṣad Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

पञ्चमोऽध्यायः कर्मसंन्यासयोगः
pañcamō’dhyāyaḥ karmasaṁnyāsayōgaḥ
**Chapter 5**
**THE YOGA OF RENUNCIATION**

**110**
अर्जुन उवाच
संन्यासं कर्मणां कृष्ण पुनर्योगं च शंससि ।
यच्छ्रेय एतयोरेकं तन्मे ब्रूहि सुनिश्चितम् ॥५- १॥
arjuna uvāca
saṁnyāsaṁ karmaṇāṁ kṛṣṇa punaryōgaṁ ca śansasi ।
yacchrēya ētayōrēkaṁ tanmē brūhi suniścitam ॥ 5-1॥

Arjuna said:
"First you extol renunciation of actions, and then you praise yoga. O Kṛṣṇa, tell me decisively which of the two is better?"

After praising the renunciation of karma (death or samādhi), Lord Kṛṣṇa extols yoga, therefore Arjuna asks: "O Kṛṣṇa, explain to me the better of these two paths."

श्रीभगवानुवाच
संन्यासः कर्मयोगश्च निःश्रेयसकरावुभौ ।
तयोस्तु कर्मसंन्यासात्कर्मयोगो विशिष्यते ॥५- २॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
saṁnyāsaḥ karmayōgaśca niḥśrēyasakarāvubhau ।
tayōstu karmasaṁnyāsātkarmayōgō viśiṣyatē ॥ 5-2॥

The Lord said:
"Renunciation, as well as the practice of yoga, are both conducive to supreme good, but of the two, the practice of yoga is superior to the renunciation of action.

ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya
  Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya

**111**
**Chapter 5**

The ancient yoga and the knowledge of death attained through the achievement of samādhi by its practice – both paths are excellent. Samādhi is perfect because it gives the experience of limitlessness through death. No one can attain samādhi, even by desiring it very strongly, if he does not practice yoga. The practice of yoga is the ladder that helps one attain samādhi, therefore it has special significance here.

ज्ञेयः स नित्यसंन्यासी यो न द्वेष्टि न काङ्क्षति ।
निर्द्वन्द्वो हि महाबाहो सुखं बन्धात्प्रमुच्यते ॥५- ३॥
jñēyaḥ sa nityasannyāsī yō na dvēṣṭi na kāṅkśati ।
nirdvandvō hi mahābāhō sukhaṁ bandhātpramucyatē ॥ 5-3॥

O Mahābāho! One who neither hates anyone nor desires anything is worthy of being considered eternally renounced. The balanced person is easily freed from bondage.

Great persons who have been able to know the limitlessness beyond death, established in samādhi through this great yogic practice, realize that this entire world is a manifestation of the eternal Brahman. For them, no difference remains between worldly pleasures and samādhi.

सांख्ययोगौ पृथग्बालाः प्रवदन्ति न पण्डिताः ।
एकमप्यास्थितः सम्यगुभयोर्विन्दते फलम् ॥५- ४॥
sāṁkhyayōgau pṛthagbālāḥ pravadanti na paṇḍitāḥ ।
ēkamapyāsthitaḥ samyagubhayōrvindatē phalam ॥ 5-4॥

Only the immature in mind think that yoga and wisdom [sāṅkhya] are different, but not those who have realized the truth, for being properly established in either one, one obtains the fruits of both.

Only ordinary people consider the practice of yoga and its result – samādhi – separately. They do not know that only those who practice yoga can attain its fruits.

**112**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

यत्सांख्यैः प्राप्यते स्थानं तद्योगैरपि गम्यते ।
एकं सांख्यं च योगं च यः पश्यति स पश्यति ॥५- ५॥
yatsāṁkhyaiḥ prāpyatē sthānaṁ tadyōgairapi gamyatē ।
ēkaṁ sāṁkhyaṁ ca yōgaṁ ca yaḥ paśyati sa paśyati ॥ 5-5॥

The state attained by the wise is also reached by yogins. He who sees wisdom and yoga as one, he alone truly sees.

That same death-transcending infinity which yogins experience in the state of samādhi is also experienced by sādhakas diligent in yoga who have not yet attained samādhi, but who, through their practice, have acquired sufficient yogic power within themselves to end their life at will. Such sādhakas, when their time comes, end their life by resorting to yogic power. Through death they attain the same infinity which yogins established in samādhi attain during their lifetime.

संन्यासस्तु महाबाहो दुःखमाप्तुमयोगतः ।
योगयुक्तो मुनिर्ब्रह्म नचिरेणाधिगच्छति ॥५- ६॥
saṁnyāsastu mahābāhō duḥkhamāptumayōgataḥ ।
yōgayuktō munirbrahma nacirēṇādhigacchati ॥ 5-6॥

O Mahābāho! Renunciation is difficult to attain without yoga, but the pious one devoted to it quickly attains Brahman.

The state of sannyāsa, that is, the knowledge of death, cannot be attained without intense practice of yoga. Those who, by the power of yogic practice, rise above physical limitations, become established in Brahman with all the vastness of their mind.

**113**
**Chapter 5**

योगयुक्तो विशुद्धात्मा विजितात्मा जितेन्द्रियः ।
सर्वभूतात्मभूतात्मा कुर्वन्नपि न लिप्यते ॥५- ७॥
yōgayuktō viśuddhātmā vijitātmā jitēndriyaḥ ।
sarvabhūtātmabhūtātmā kurvannapi na lipyatē ॥ 5-7॥

Pure in spirit, perfected in yoga, having conquered the passions, the soul of all souls, he performs actions without being bound by them.

When the yogin, by awakening all the capacities of his mind through the practice of yoga, himself becomes limitless and understands that the entire surrounding world is a manifestation of the immeasurable, unending Time, he performs karma solely to inspire others and remains above those actions.

नैव किंचित्करोमीति युक्तो मन्येत तत्त्ववित् ।
पश्यञ्श्रृण्वन्स्पृशञ्जिघ्रन्नश्नन्‌गच्छन्स्वपञ्श्वसन् ॥५- ८॥
प्रलपन्विसृजन्गृह्णन्नुन्मिषन्निमिषन्नपि ।
इन्द्रियाणीन्द्रियार्थेषु वर्तन्त इति धारयन् ॥५- ९॥
naiva kiṁcitkarōmīti yuktō manyēta tattvavit ।
paśyañśṛṇvanspṛśañjighrannaśnan‌gacchansvapañśvasan ॥ 5-8॥
pralapanvisṛjangṛhṇannunmiṣannimiṣannapi ।
indriyāṇīndriyārthēṣu vartanta iti dhārayan ॥ 5-9॥

When the knower of truth sees or touches, smells, goes, sleeps, breathes, gives, speaks, opens and closes his eyes, he realizes that it is the senses performing their respective functions, while he himself does nothing.

The great person does not see, even when seeing; does not smell, even when smelling; does not touch, even when touching; does not eat, even when taking food; remains motionless, even when moving; does not breathe, even when breathing. Established in the measurelessness that abides beyond the senses, he uses his senses through the mind, yet nevertheless does nothing, even when doing something.

114  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

brahmaṇyādhāya karmāṇi saṅgaṁ tyaktvā karoti yaḥ ।  
lipyatē na sa pāpēna padmapatramivāmbhasā ॥ 5-10॥  

Just as water does not wet the lotus leaf, so too is he who dedicates all his actions, performed without attachment, to Brahman, not stained by sin.  

The yogi understands that the foundation of the body, organs, and mind is the boundless mind, manifesting through the body. Self-satisfied in this knowledge and contemplating the entire visible world as a manifestation of the indestructible Brahman, he exists while not existing. Freed even from his own desire to know the unmanifest infinite, already established in it, such a great man never again commits the sin of ignorance and limitation.  

kāyēna manasā buddhyā kēvalairindriyairapi ।  
yōginaḥ karma kurvanti saṅgaṁ tyaktvātmaśuddhayē ॥ 5-11॥  

Having cast off attachment, yogis perform actions by means of the body, conscious mind, intellect, and senses solely for self-purification.  

When the yogi comprehends the connection of the body, conscious mind, intellect, and senses with consciousness, his attachment to the body and senses vanishes. Then he performs karma to awaken the full boundlessness of his consciousness, kindling the fire of yoga through the body, conscious mind, intellect, and senses.  

☝  
☝  

115  
Chapter 5  

yuktaḥ karmaphalaṁ tyaktvā śāntimāpnōti naiṣṭhikīm ।  
ayuktaḥ kāmakārēṇa phalē saktō nibadhyatē ॥ 5-12॥  

Those devotedly following yoga attain the highest peace, having renounced the fruits of karma. The impious are cast into bondage by the desire to obtain the results of their actions.  

Yogis act without attachment to the results of their activity. Their consciousness is free from physical limitations; all their actions are dedicated to the unmanifest Time and directed toward It. An ordinary man, indifferent to awakening the infinite capacities of his mind, remains confined by physical limits and bound to karma.  

sarvakarmāṇi manasā saṁnyasyāstē sukhaṁ vaśī ।  
navadvārē purē dēhī naiva kurvanna kārayan ॥ 5-13॥  

The embodied one, having attained self-mastery and mentally renounced all karma, dwells happily in the city of nine gates, whether acting or not acting.  

A great man, having after the awakening of his boundless consciousness attained the state of *sthitaprajña*, appears limited by physical boundaries until the end of his life, even while containing all infinity within himself.  

na kartṛtvaṁ na karmāṇi lōkasya sṛjati prabhuḥ ।  
na karmaphalasaṁyōgaṁ svabhāvastu pravartatē ॥ 5-14॥  

The Lord of the World is not implicated in karma, nor in its fruits, nor even in their conjunction. The entire world is set in motion only by its own nature.  

☝  
☝  

116  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

Manifested by indestructible Time, the boundless mind itself naturally presents all karma and its result. Unmanifest Time manifests this entire universe through the mind, yet remains outside it and, even while doing everything, does nothing.  

nādattē kasyacitpāpaṁ na caiva sukṛtaṁ vibhuḥ ।  
ajñānēnāvṛtaṁ jñānaṁ tēna muhyanti jantavaḥ ॥ 5-15॥  

Vibhu does not accept either sins or righteous deeds. All beings are bewildered by ignorance, which veils wisdom.  

The all-pervading, indestructible Supreme Being, Time, remains outside the karma and its fruits presented by the mind. Most people, because a significant part of their consciousness is asleep, abide in delusion, since their consciousness is limited only to activity and its results.  

jñānēna tu tadajñānaṁ yēṣāṁ nāśitamātmanaḥ ।  
tēṣāmādityavajjñānaṁ prakāśayati tatparam ॥ 5-16॥  

The wisdom of those whose ignorance has been destroyed by knowledge shines like the Supreme Truth, in color resembling the Sun.  

When the yogi, striving to awaken his dormant boundless consciousness, overcomes ignorance by awakening his sleeping capacities, he receives the direct *darśana* of the Light of all lights, the unmanifest Time, which shines like the Sun.  

☝  
☝  
☝  

117  
Chapter 5  

tad‌buddhayastadātmānastanniṣṭhāstatparāyaṇāḥ ।  
gacchantyapunarāvṛttiṁ jñānanirdhūtakalmaṣāḥ ॥ 5-17॥  

Those whose intellect is in Him, who themselves are in Him, who are devoted to Him and firmly adhere to Him, purified by knowledge, attain the state from which there is no return.  

Knowing Kāla-Brahman, the Light of all lights, brilliant like the Sun, yogis direct all their consciousness into Him. Remaining devoted to Time, through death they unite their consciousness, purified in the fire of knowledge, with the boundless, unbearably radiant Time. After their death, they never die again, for they are never born.  

vidyāvinayasaṁpannē brāhmaṇē gavi hastini ।  
śuni caiva śvapākē ca paṇḍitāḥ samadarśinaḥ ॥ 5-18॥  

They look equally upon a brāhmaṇa endowed with humility and wisdom, a cow, an elephant, a dog, and an outcaste.  

Great men, having known the true nature of radiant Time through the awakening of their measureless consciousness by the practice of this ancient yoga, have understood that this entire visible world is manifested by Time Itself. For such great *sthitaprajña*, all are equal: those who have attained samādhi, the realized, the wise, the ignorant, or anyone else, since all beings are manifestations of Time—the primordial Supreme Being.  

☝  
☝  

118  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

ihaiva tairjitaḥ sargō yēṣāṁ sāmyē sthitaṁ manaḥ ।  
nirdōṣaṁ hi samaṁ brahma tasmādbrahmaṇi tē sthitāḥ ॥ 5-19॥  

Those whose mind is established in equanimity have conquered the bonds of birth and death. Their mind, faultless and balanced, is established in the Supreme Being.  

Those who kindle the fire of yoga in their body and offer themselves as an oblation to this fire, during life come to know the boundless conscious Truth, Time, abiding far beyond physical limits. Possessing consciousness expanded to infinity, they have, as it were, conquered this entire world, uniting with the Time that manifests it. Yogis who have known the truth of Time and attained unity with It become like the Soul of the entire world.  

na prahṛṣyētpriyaṁ prāpya nōdvijētprāpya cāpriyam ।  
sthirabuddhirasaṁmūḍhō brahmavidbrahmaṇi sthitaḥ ॥ 5-20॥  

He who neither rejoices at gain nor grieves at loss, who is free from delusion and possesses a steadfast intellect—that sage who has known Brahman is established in Brahman.  

The yogi who has awakened his boundless consciousness through the practice of this ancient yoga appears limited by the body, though in truth he is one with the unmanifest, indestructible Supreme Being that manifests the world. Such a great man does not rejoice at the acquisition of sense objects. Unlike ordinary people, who have not comprehended death and therefore fear it, he, having already known the true nature of death, feels no fear of it at the end of his life. Such a great soul, with all the measureless consciousness of his boundless mind, abides in unity with that indestructible Supreme Being, Time.  

☝  
☝  

119  
Chapter 5  

bāhyasparśēṣvasaktātmā vindatyātmani yat sukham ।  
sa brahmayōgayuktātmā sukhamakśayamaśnutē ॥ 5-21॥  

A man unattached to the gratification of the senses through external objects finds joy born in the heart through contemplation of the Ātman. Such a man, established through yoga in unity with That Primordial, ever abides in imperishable bliss.  

The practitioner of yoga for the awakening of the boundless consciousness of his mind knows that it is the mind that satisfies itself through the senses. The yogi who has known this becomes free from the attraction of the senses and successfully awakens the consciousness of his mind in its fullness. He then concentrates this boundless consciousness on the unmanifest Time, the Supreme Being, and thus knows Its true nature. Uniting with Him, the yogi is established in eternal universal happiness.  

yē hi saṁsparśajā bhōgā duḥkhayōnaya ēva tē ।  
ādyantavantaḥ kauntēya na tēṣu ramatē budhaḥ ॥ 5-22॥  

Those pleasures born of contact with matter indeed lead to sorrow, for what has a beginning also has an end. O Kaunteya, the wise take no delight in them.  

Ordinary people consider the feelings and desires arising within them to be paramount, since a large part of their mind’s capacities is asleep. They are extremely tormented by the fear of losing their body when death comes to them. Whereas those who, through the practice of yoga, have known death, are never again confined within physical boundaries.  

☝  
☝  

120  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

śaknōtīhaiva yaḥ sōḍhuṁ prākśarīravimōkśaṇāt ।  
kāmakrōdhōdbhavaṁ vēgaṁ sa yuktaḥ sa sukhī naraḥ ॥ 5-23॥  

He who is able to withstand the impetuous onslaught of lust and anger before leaving the body—he alone is established in yoga, and he alone is happy.  

Those who practice this ancient yoga properly come to know the relationship between the mind and the senses through the awakening of their consciousness, even before leaving the body. They know their mind through the mind itself and rise above the desire for sensory pleasures through the sense organs. Freed from such desire, they also become free from anger. Those devoted to this ancient yoga who have gained such experience are called yogis.  

yō’ntaḥsukhō’ntarārāmastathāntarjyōtirēva yaḥ ।  
sa yōgī brahmanirvāṇaṁ brahmabhūtō’dhigacchati ॥ 5-24॥  

The yogi who has found the source of happiness and delight within himself and directly perceives That Light within himself becomes an embodiment of the Supreme Being and attains Brahma-Nirvāṇa.  

He who possesses intuition regarding his boundless capacities and kindles the fire of yoga in his body to awaken them directly perceives within himself the flame of the dazzling Light of all lights, the Supreme Being, Time, having awakened his infinite consciousness. Such a yogi transcends the limitations of life by uniting his consciousness with the consciousness of the infinite, indestructible, Supreme Time and himself becomes infinite.  

☝  
☝

**121**
**Chapter 5**

लभन्ते ब्रह्मनिर्वाणमृषयः क्षीणकल्मषाः ।
छिन्नद्वैधा यतात्मानः सर्वभूतहिते रताः ॥५- २५॥
labhantē brahmanirvāṇamṛṣayaḥ kśīṇakalmaṣāḥ ।
chinnadvaidhā yatātmānaḥ sarvabhūtahitē ratāḥ ॥ 5-25॥

The sage who has washed away all his sins, freed from all contradictions and established in himself, rejoicing in the welfare of all beings, attains Brahma-Nirvana.

After the direct perception of this most brilliant flame, the sin of the limitation of consciousness disappears, and the yogi, established in himself, unites with that indestructible Supreme Essence, realizing Time within himself.

कामक्रोधवियुक्तानां यतीनां यतचेतसाम् ।
अभितो ब्रह्मनिर्वाणं वर्तते विदितात्मनाम् ॥५- २६॥
kāmakrōdhaviyuktānāṁ yatīnāṁ yatacētasām ।
abhitō brahmanirvāṇaṁ vartatē viditātmanām ॥ 5-26॥

The ascetic who has subdued his mind, free from lust and anger, who has known his own essence, self-possessed, approaches the attainment of Brahma-Nirvana.

The great *sthitaprajña* have awakened their sleeping consciousness through the practice of ancient yoga, freeing it from physical limitations. Such people enjoy their own freedom in a state of boundless consciousness, perceiving the unmanifest Supreme Truth, embodied in all this universe. Whatever they do, all their actions point to the unmanifest Time.

☝
☝

**122**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

स्पर्शान्कृत्वा बहिर्बाह्यांश्चक्षुश्चैवान्तरे भ्रुवोः ।
प्राणापानौ समौ कृत्वा नासाभ्यन्तरचारिणौ ॥५- २७॥
यतेन्द्रियमनोबुद्धिर्मुनिर्मोक्षपरायणः ।
विगतेच्छाभयक्रोधो यः सदा मुक्त एव सः ॥५- २८॥
भोक्तारं यज्ञतपसां सर्वलोकमहेश्वरम् ।
सुहृदं सर्वभूतानां ज्ञात्वा मां शान्तिमृच्छति ॥५- २९॥
sparśānkṛtvā bahirbāhyānścakśuścaivāntarē bhruvōḥ ।
prāṇāpānau samau kṛtvā nāsābhyantaracāriṇau ॥ 5-27॥
yatēndriyamanōbuddhirmunirmōkśaparāyaṇaḥ ।
vigatēcchābhayakrōdhō yaḥ sadā mukta ēva saḥ ॥ 5-28॥
bhōktāraṁ yajñatapasāṁ sarvalōkamahēśvaram ।
suhṛdaṁ sarvabhūtānāṁ jñātvā māṁ śāntimṛcchati ॥ 5-29॥

"Having withdrawn the organs of sense from their objects, having fixed the eyes and gaze in *bhrumadhya*, having brought into equilibrium the movement of *prana* and *apana* in the nostrils, such a *sadhaka*, striving for liberation, gaining control over the sense organs, the conscious mind and the intellect, is freed from desire, fear and anger. He is liberated forever and attains peace by knowing Me as the Supreme Lord, who accepts *yajna*, austerities, and dwells in the heart of every being."

Sitting motionless, having performed *khechari mudra*, having fixed the eyes and gaze in *bhrumadhya*, having balanced *prana* and *apana* with the help of special *pranayama*, the yogi, thus establishing himself in the practice of yoga, knows his conscious mind and the intellect that abides beyond the organs. Expanding infinitely, his consciousness overcomes physical limitations and begins to touch the boundaries of the farthest frontiers of the measureless mind. This great man is freed from physical limitations by virtue of the boundlessness of his consciousness. Such a yogi offers himself as an oblation to Time through kindling the fire of yoga in his body and advances far on the path to attaining its results. He attains complete peace, knowing the Creator of the world, who dwells in the heart of every being and is therefore known as Vasudeva.

☝

**123**
**Chapter 5**

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे कर्मसंन्यासयोगो नाम पञ्चमोऽध्यायः ॥ ५ ॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē karmasannyāsayōgō nāma pañcamō’dhyāyaḥ

Om Tat Sat
Thus ends the dialogue of Krishna and Arjuna in the fifth chapter, "The Yoga of Renunciation of Action," of the Upanishad "Shrimad Bhagavad Gita," which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

षष्ठोऽध्यायः आत्मसंयमयोगः
ṣaṣṭhō’dhyāyaḥ ātmasaṁyamayōgaḥ
**Chapter 6**
**THE YOGA OF SELF-CONTEMPLATION**

**126**

श्रीभगवानुवाच
अनाश्रितः कर्मफलं कार्यं कर्म करोति यः ।
स संन्यासी च योगी च न निरग्निर्न चाक्रियः ॥६- १॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
anāśritaḥ karmaphalaṁ kāryaṁ karma karōti yaḥ ।
sa saṁnyāsī ca yōgī ca na niragnirna cākriyaḥ ॥ 6-1॥

The Lord said:
"He who performs the action that is to be done, without relying on the fruit of action, he is a *sannyasi* and a yogi, not he who is without fire and without action."

The great man, freed from desires and thereby established in *samadhi*, does not abandon activity, in order to inspire followers of yoga and ordinary people. Since he has already known death, he is called a *sannyasi*.

Ordinary people who do not kindle the fire of yoga and remain in passive inaction possess a consciousness limited only to the body. They are incapable of knowing the true nature of death and consequently cannot become *sannyasis*.

Ordinary people think that *sannyasa* is the renunciation of family life and the donning of saffron robes, reducing this exalted state of *sannyasa* to mere ritual. Why do they not understand that it is impossible to realize death by simply performing the ritual of one's own funeral during the acceptance of so-called *sannyasa*? In order to know the true nature of death during life, it is absolutely necessary to practice this ancient yoga. Only through the practice of yoga can one awaken one's consciousness and merge with that unmanifest Time, the primordial Parameshvara, through knowing His true nature. Only one who has attained this state can be called a *sannyasi* in the true sense.

☝
ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya
Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**127**
**Chapter 6**

यं संन्यासमिति प्राहुर्योगं तं विद्धि पाण्डव ।
न ह्यसंन्यस्तसंकल्पो योगी भवति कश्चन ॥६- २॥
yaṁ saṁnyāsamiti prāhuryōgaṁ taṁ viddhi pāṇḍava ।
na hyasannyastasaṅkalpō yōgī bhavati kaścana ॥ 6-2॥

O Pandava! Know that which is called *sannyasa* as yoga – for no one becomes a yogi without having abandoned sensual desires.

Considering themselves limited by the body, ordinary people not only do not try to know death, but also do not strive to awaken the boundless dormant capacities of their mind by kindling the fire of yoga in their body. Those who have dedicated themselves to yoga in order to awaken all the capacities of their mind for knowing death perform yogic practice and, becoming dispassionate, as a result know death, after which they begin to be called *sannyasis*. Such great *sthitaprajña* become established in *samadhi* (*akarma*), and see no difference between yogic practice (*karma*) and its result – *akarma*.

आरुरुक्षोर्मुनेर्योगं कर्म कारणमुच्यते ।
योगारूढस्य तस्यैव शमः कारणमुच्यते ॥६- ३॥
ārurukśōrmunēryōgaṁ karma kāraṇamucyatē ।
yōgārūḍhasya tasyaiva śamaḥ kāraṇamucyatē ॥ 6-3॥

Action is said to be the means for the sage who wishes to attain perfection in yoga. Inaction, however, is said to be the means for one who is established in this yoga.

☝

**128**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

The practice of yoga is the only way to attain *samadhi*, its reward. After attaining *samadhi*, the yogi knows death and, through rising above physical limitations, becomes established in the unmanifest Time, the embodiment of infinite Consciousness. Through this, all desires of such a yogi are fulfilled, and he attains supreme peace.

यदा हि नेन्द्रियार्थेषु न कर्मस्वनुषज्जते ।
सर्वसंकल्पसंन्यासी योगारूढस्तदोच्यते ॥६- ४॥
yadā hi nēndriyārthēṣu na karmasvanuṣajjatē ।
sarvasaṁkalpasannyāsī yōgārūḍhastadōcyatē ॥ 6-4॥

A person becomes established in yoga when, having renounced all desires, he is freed from attachment both to sense objects and to the activities for their attainment.

Of the great man who has awakened all the capacities of his mind and known death, it is said that he is established in yoga. Established in the consciousness of the boundless mind, which is beyond the senses, the great man is attached neither to the senses nor to their objects. His main desire – to awaken his consciousness – has already been fulfilled; he never again has other limited desires.

उद्धरेदात्मनात्मानं नात्मानमवसादयेत् ।
आत्मैव ह्यात्मनो बन्धुरात्मैव रिपुरात्मनः ॥६- ५॥
बन्धुरात्मात्मनस्तस्य येनात्मैवात्मना जितः ।
अनात्मनस्तु शत्रुत्वे वर्तेतात्मैव शत्रुवत् ॥६- ६॥
uddharēdātmanātmānaṁ nātmānamavasādayēt ।
ātmaiva hyātmanō bandhurātmaiva ripurātmanaḥ ॥ 6-5॥
bandhurātmātmanastasya yēnātmaivātmanā jitaḥ ।
