anātmanastu śatrutvē vartētātmaiva śatruvat ॥ 6-6॥

One should strive to elevate oneself; one should not bring about one's own downfall, for each person is his own friend and his own enemy.

He who has subdued himself becomes his own friend, but he who does not control himself is his own worst enemy. He who experiences, through kindling the fire of yoga, the boundlessness of his mind, realizes that he himself is the instrument for self-knowledge. He, however, who has not attained self-realization, only tightens his limitations. Great self-realized people are friends to themselves. The ordinary person, who has no desire to awaken the sleeping capacities of his mind, is hostile towards himself.

☝
☝
☝

**129**
**Chapter 6**

जितात्मनः प्रशान्तस्य परमात्मा समाहितः ।
शीतोष्णसुखदुःखेषु तथा मानापमानयोः ॥६- ७॥
jitātmanaḥ praśāntasya paramātmā samāhitaḥ ।
śītōṣṇasukhaduḥkhēṣu tathā mānāpamānayōḥ ॥ 6-7॥

Happiness and sorrow, heat and cold, fame and disgrace – all are the same for those who have conquered themselves and remain immersed in the silent Paramatma.

The great man, who has by his own efforts known all his capacities, experiences the measurelessness of his mind and becomes fully established in That Soul of the soul, Paramatma, the unmanifest Presence beyond that measurelessness. Such a great man sees fame and disgrace, joy and sorrow, heat, cold, and everything else as the manifold manifestations of That one Consciousness and attains the goal of his life's path.

ज्ञानविज्ञानतृप्तात्मा कूटस्थो विजितेन्द्रियः ।
युक्त इत्युच्यते योगी समलोष्टाश्मकाञ्चनः ॥६- ८॥
jñānavijñānatṛptātmā kūṭasthō vijitēndriyaḥ ।
yukta ityucyatē yōgī samalōṣṭāśmakāñcanaḥ ॥ 6-8॥

He who has absorbed the knowledge of both the gross and the subtle, who is unchanging, has conquered the passions, and regards a stone and gold equally, is called a perfected yogi.

The great man, who knows of the boundlessness hidden within his body, also considers his body divine. He understands that the body itself is that field, by plowing which with the plow of practice and sowing it with the seeds of knowledge, one can reap the harvest of infinity. Such a great soul is completely freed from intentions. Knowing the body and That unmanifest presence beyond it, such a yogi remains immersed in himself. He becomes imperturbable, knowing the entire universe as a manifestation of the unmanifest Time.

☝
☝

**130**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

सुहृन्मित्रार्युदासीनमध्यस्थद्वेष्यबन्धुषु ।
साधुष्वपि च पापेषु समबुद्धिर्विशिष्यते ॥६- ९॥
suhṛnmitrāryudāsīnamadhyasthadvēṣyabandhuṣu ।
sādhuṣvapi ca pāpēṣu samabuddhirviśiṣyatē ॥ 6-9॥

He who is equal-minded towards the well-wishers, friends, enemies, the indifferent, the mediators and the despicable, as well as towards brothers, sages and sinners, that man is great.

When, through the practice of the first stage (*Brahma-granthi-bheda*) of yoga, consciousness is freed from physical limitations, the yogi begins to perceive Vasudeva, so called because He dwells in the heart of every being. Observing Vasudeva in the hearts of all beings, he sees their true essence and therefore treats them equally.

योगी युञ्जीत सततमात्मानं रहसि स्थितः ।
एकाकी यतचित्तात्मा निराशीरपरिग्रहः ॥६- १०॥
yōgī yuñjīta satatamātmānaṁ rahasi sthitaḥ ।
ēkākī yatacittātmā nirāśīraparigrahaḥ ॥ 6-10॥

Abiding in solitude, having renounced the sense of ownership, established in self-control, let the yogi regularly perform his practice.

Having overcome the limitations of the physical body, or, in the language of yoga, having mastered the practice of *Brahma-granthi-bheda*, the yogi performs the practice of *Hridaya-granthi-bheda*, or *Vishnu-granthi-bheda*, for knowing the true nature of Vasudeva, who dwells in the heart. Now Lord Shri Krishna speaks of this great *sadhana*.

☝
☝

**131**
**Chapter 6**

śucau dēśē pratiṣṭhāpya sthiramāsanamātmanaḥ ।
nātyucchritaṁ nātinīcaṁ cailājinakuśōttaram ॥ 6-11॥

tatraikāgraṁ manaḥ kṛtvā yatacittēndriyakriyaḥ ।
upaviśyāsanē yuñjyādyōgamātmaviśuddhayē ॥ 6-12॥

Dwelling in a sacred place, neither high in the mountains nor in a lowland, having seated himself on a covering of grass, deerskin, and cloth, concentrating and properly controlling his body and mind, let the yogin perform the practice.

When the yogin is ready to approach the level of Hridaya-granthi-bheda, he is rewarded by the Guru with instructions in this secret practice. Such a yogin should dwell in solitude in a sacred place, situated neither too high in the mountains nor too close to sea level. Having prepared the place for practice – spreading a grass mat, covering it with a deerskin and a silk cloth, and seating himself on this asana, he should perform this special technique of yoga in order to know, in all Her infinity, That abiding in the heart, the immeasurability of Time, named Vasudeva.

samaṁ kāyaśirōgrīvaṁ dhārayannacalaṁ sthiraḥ ।
samprēkśya nāsikāgraṁ svaṁ diśaścānavalōkayan ॥ 6-13॥

Holding the body, head, and neck straight and motionless, fixing the gaze on the point before the nose and not looking to the sides,

He whose consciousness is established beyond physical limits should hold the body in balance and perform special actions with the head and neck. Having attained motionlessness through these actions, he should direct his gaze to the empty space directly before the nose. Performing this practice and thus

**132**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

establishing himself in the consciousness of the Void, which not only contains within itself all physical matter but is also the true support of its movement, the yogin fully knows Her. This Void was named by the sages in honor of Lord Vishnu, the protector of the entire world.

praśāntātmā vigatabhīrbrahmacārivratē sthitaḥ ।
manaḥ saṁyamya maccittō yukta āsīta matparaḥ ॥ 6-14॥

Established in brahmacharya, remaining fearless and tranquil, a person should concentrate his mind on Me and remain unwavering, having chosen Me as the supreme goal.

He who, through his practice, strives to know the Conscious Void has already attained fearlessness and calmed the mind by overcoming physical boundaries. Of such a great person it is said that he is established in brahmacharya, even if he is only making efforts to comprehend the consciousness of the Void.

Many thinkers have explained the natural attraction of man to woman and woman to man in a somewhat perverted manner. In the name of so-called abstinence, they extremely condemned women and even called them the gates of hell. An unnatural vow of celibacy was forcibly imposed upon yogins, which led not only to the complete disorder of their personality but also did not contribute to the attainment of true abstinence.

If one reflects on this in more detail, new facets of this question can be seen. I believe that, with rare exceptions, it is impossible to become established in abstinence without the company of a woman. When the main cause of attraction to a woman becomes understood, a man overcomes it. The same is true for the attraction that a woman feels towards a

**133**
**Chapter 6**

man. Let us first consider the former. It would be surprising not to feel attraction to the body which was once the sole support of our life before and after birth. Although some philosophers have given horrifying descriptions of life in the mother's womb – is the life of the fetus truly so terrible? Based on the data of modern science, a completely different vision can be formed.

In the maternal womb we remained completely carefree. The female body sustained our life. We were not afraid of being struck, we had neither worries about food nor anxieties about heat or cold, there was not even a need to breathe. We were completely satisfied, and the foundation of this satisfaction was the female body, which we called "mother." After the pangs of birth, if they can even be called pangs, when we were helpless, the sole support of our life was a woman. It was in her breast that the sap of our life flowed. It was the female body that was its center. Can we consider attraction to the female body abnormal? Is it worth describing the woman, through whom we came into being, as the gates of hell? I believe this would be a profound delusion. Perhaps only those philosophers who could not understand the naturalness of a man's attraction to a woman called this attraction abnormal. Those who are familiar with Indian wisdom and have practiced this ancient yoga, desiring to attain samadhi, understand that liberation is attained only through knowledge. The yogin becomes free from attraction to everything that has been known by him. Those who were able to understand life, having ascended the ladder of knowledge, became free from the allure of life and were called "jivanmukta."

Now let us dwell on the natural attraction of woman to man. The female body is created for motherhood, and it is precisely it that fulfills the noble mission of manifesting consciousness through the physical body. We all know that a woman cannot become a mother without union with a man, just as a man cannot become a father without union with a woman. Without motherhood

**134**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

femininity is barren – this is the foundation of a woman's attraction to a man.

When the traditions of this ancient yoga were almost interrupted in the world, and thinkers failed in their investigation of natural attractions, they mistakenly considered this mutual attraction abnormal. Perhaps they could not understand that love-passion is the foundation of the continuity of life. Love-passion was separated from motherhood and fatherhood to such a degree that motherhood was revered, but the woman seeking love was condemned; fatherhood was extolled, but the man suffering from hopeless love was censured. People forgot that motherhood and fatherhood arise from love. The sages of antiquity were aware of the divinity of love and paid it due respect. Only in the Middle Ages was the divinity of love distorted.

No one can attain brahmacharya by revering motherhood while at the same time condemning a woman's falling in love. In the same way, no woman can become established in brahmacharya by condemning a man while noisily acclaiming fatherhood. Only those yogins and yoginis who succeeded in knowing the fundamental cause of attraction between man and woman and freed themselves from this attraction through knowledge attained brahmacharya. They experienced the divine power of love and, by retaining the seed (menstrual discharge), attained the state of "urdhvaretas."

Undoubtedly, abstinence is a great power. When Arjuna asked Lord Shri Krishna: "What is Brahman?", the answer immediately followed: "Aksharam Brahma Paramam" – that which does not perish is Brahman. Engaging in diligent practice of yoga, the ancient sages realized this truth and came to the conclusion that only those yogins who are able to avoid the loss of this vital fluid can attain brahmacharya. Having themselves become indestructible, they were able to know That unmanifest, indestructible Brahman.

**135**
**Chapter 6**

yuñjannēvaṁ sadātmānaṁ yōgī niyatamānasaḥ ।
śāntiṁ nirvāṇaparamāṁ matsansthāmadhigacchati ॥ 6-15॥

Surrendered to Me and established in Me, such a yogin of controlled mind attains the peace that is beyond death.

Having already freed himself from physical limitations, the yogin performing the practice of Hridaya-granthi-bheda completely controls his mind. Even while alive, he experiences the state beyond death and, established in the consciousness of the Void which supports all matter and its movement, becomes peaceful.

nātyaśnatastu yōgō'sti na caikāntamanaśnataḥ ।
na cāti svapnaśīlasya jāgratō naiva cārjuna ॥ 6-16॥

O Arjuna! This yoga is not for those who eat excessively or abstain from food, nor for those who sleep too much or remain wakeful.

Only he is suitable and ready for this practice who has known the interrelation of mind and body, and can also control his imagination. Although such a person has not yet fully awakened his mental faculties, having completed the practice of Brahma-granthi-bheda, he has advanced sufficiently far in the awakening of his mind.

**136**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

yuktāhāravihārasya yuktacēṣṭasya karmasu ।
yuktasvapnāvabōdhasya yōgō bhavati duḥkhahā ॥ 6-17॥

This sorrow-dispelling yoga is for those possessing proper knowledge who have regulated eating, wakefulness and sleep, activity and inactivity.

Only he succeeds in the practice of the second stage of this yoga, which allows one to become established in the consciousness of the Void, who has fully dedicated himself to this practice, having subdued and focused all actions and efforts of his body. He has realized the truth of boundlessness beyond the body, which ordinary people consider a product of imagination. Only such a great person is capable of realizing the true nature of the consciousness of this Conscious Void and becoming established in it.

yadā viniyataṁ cittamātmanyēvāvatiṣṭhatē ।
niḥspṛhaḥ sarvakāmēbhyō yukta ityucyatē tadā ॥ 6-18॥

He who, completely controlling his mind, becomes established in the Self and therefore freed from the oppression of all desires, is called "yoga-yukta."

When the yogin knows the true nature of the consciousness of the Void, he acquires the corresponding capacities for knowing the consciousness of Time which fills this Void. In such a state, when all his desires are fulfilled, he attains perfection in yoga.

**137**
**Chapter 6**

yathā dīpō nivātasthō nēṅgatē sōpamā smṛtā ।
yōginō yatacittasya yuñjatō yōgamātmanaḥ ॥ 6-19॥

yatrōparamatē cittaṁ niruddhaṁ yōgasēvayā ।
yatra caivātmanātmānaṁ paśyannātmani tuṣyati ॥ 6-20॥

sukhamātyantikaṁ yattad buddhigrāhyamatīndriyam ।
vētti yatra na caivāyaṁ sthitaścalati tattvataḥ ॥ 6-21॥

The concentrated mind of a self-realized yogin is like a lamp that does not flicker in a windless place. When, subdued by the practice of yoga, the mind becomes dispassionate, then, contemplating the Self, the yogin abides satisfied in the Self. When he experiences that boundless bliss, beyond the senses, which is graspable by the intellect, then, established in that state, the yogin does not deviate from the truth.

The great yogin, having successfully completed the practice of Hridaya-granthi-bheda – the second stage of this ancient yoga, becomes established in the consciousness of the Void. In the state of samadhi, when he stops the breath, his eyes are motionless, his heart does not beat, and to those around him he appears dead, he directly perceives Vasudeva, That boundless embodiment of Time, and abides in self-satisfaction. Having received this experience and emerged from the state of samadhi, he performs actions only to inspire other yogins and ordinary people. Although he appears limited by the body, in reality he has attained omnipotence.

138  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

*yaṁ labdhvā cāparaṁ lābhaṁ manyatē nādhikaṁ tataḥ |  
yasminsthitō na duḥkhēna guruṇāpi vicālyatē || 6-22 ||*  

There is no attainment higher than this. One who has experienced this state cannot be disturbed even by great sorrow.  

By practicing this ancient yoga, a person receives the direct darśan of Lord Vāsudeva, who dwells in every heart. After this, there remains nothing better in this world than the realization of Him. Events that are extremely painful for ordinary people are insignificant for such great souls. They see Vāsudeva everywhere and abide always in bliss.  

*taṁ vidyād duḥkhasaṁyōgaviyōgaṁ yōgasan̄jñitam |  
sa niścayēna yōktavyō yōgō’nirviṇṇacētasā || 6-23 ||*  

That which liberates from sorrow is called yoga. Practice it with great enthusiasm and resolve.  

An ordinary person learns with disappointment that a large part of his mental faculties lie asleep. Striving to awaken them, he, by good fortune, receives instruction in this secret ancient science from a great man who has realized Brahman. Then, having received instruction, he persistently practices this ancient yoga, filled with determination to awaken all his faculties.  

☝  
☝  

139  
Chapter 6  

*saṁkalpaprabhavān kāmāṁstyaktvā sarvānaśēṣataḥ |  
manasaivēndriyagrāmaṁ viniyamya samantataḥ || 6-24 ||  
śanaiḥ śanairuparamēd buddhyā dhṛtigṛhītayā |  
ātmasansthaṁ manaḥ kṛtvā na kiṁcidapi cintayēt || 6-25 ||*  

Having abandoned all desires born of imagination, and having completely subdued the entire group of senses by means of the mind, gradually attaining vairāgya, one should fix the mind upon the Self and, trusting in one’s own strength, think of nothing else.  

Imagination is the most powerful force in this world. Those endowed with a rich imagination and able to control it through yoga can achieve anything whatsoever. Only such people are capable of realizing the boundless potential of their mind. By controlling all their sense organs through the mind—that is, by controlling the mental image of their objects—they are able to concentrate their limitless imagination upon that Primal Truth and thus know It.  

A yogī practicing this ancient yoga experiences the boundless power of his intellect when, through it, he cognizes the relationship between the mind and the senses. He is able to understand: that which is ordinarily considered a thoughtless state, or “nirvikār,” is founded upon pure thought, beyond word and visual image, which serve as supports for ordinary thinking. Only such a yogī, established in pure thought, can know the true nature of the consciousness of that Primal Void.  

☝  

140  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

*yatō yatō niścarati manaścañcalamasthiram |  
tatastatō niyamyaitadātmanyēva vaśaṁ nayēt || 6-26 ||*  

Wherever this restless and unsteady mind wanders, one should, curbing it, bring it back under control.  

People whose greater part of consciousness is asleep consider the boundless consciousness of the mind to be merely a product of imagination, because they use only a small portion of their infinite consciousness. Due to a lack of purpose, their limited consciousness continues to hold them captive to mere mental images of objects accessible to sensory perception.  

At the same time, those who possess a glimpse of the boundless sleeping consciousness of their mind, full of enthusiasm, practice yoga to fully awaken their consciousness. Such great souls, gradually advancing toward boundlessness, transcend all physical limitations.  

*praśāntamanasaṁ hyēnaṁ yōginaṁ sukhamuttamam |  
upaiti śāntarajasaṁ brahmabhūtamakalmaṣam || 6-27 ||*  

Supreme happiness comes to that yogī whose mind is exceedingly calm, who is free from passion, who is pure and one with Brahman.  

Those great souls who are able to overcome the limitations of their consciousness through the practice of this ancient yoga, having received instruction in it, become filled with rapture as they awaken their mental faculties and become established in the consciousness of the Void, the unshakable, transcendent Brahman.  

☝  
☝  

141  
Chapter 6  

*yuñjannēvaṁ sadātmānaṁ yōgī vigatakalmaṣaḥ |  
sukhēna brahmasaṁsparśamatyantaṁ sukhamaśnutē || 6-28 ||*  

The sinless yogī, constantly engaged in self-perfection, attains infinite bliss in proximity to Brahman.  

Freed from the sin of limitation, the yogī, in the process of practice, awakens his boundless consciousness. Thus, established in the Conscious Void, he finds satisfaction and happiness from receiving the direct darśan of Vāsudeva.  

*sarvabhūtasthamātmānaṁ sarvabhūtāni cātmani |  
īkśatē yōgayuktātmā sarvatra samadarśanaḥ || 6-29 ||*  

The perfected yogī, who sees himself in all beings and all beings within himself, looks upon everything impartially.  

The great man who has known the true nature of Vāsudeva, pervading the Conscious Void, sees Him in his own heart and in the hearts of all beings. Such a sage, thus established in the consciousness of the Void, knows himself as an embodiment of Vāsudeva, whose color is like the sky, and sees in this entire universe and all living beings only His divine manifestations.  

*yō māṁ paśyati sarvatra sarvaṁ ca mayi paśyati |  
tasyāhaṁ na praṇaśyāmi sa ca mē na praṇaśyati || 6-30 ||*  

He who always beholds Me and also beholds in Me that measureless Time never abandons Me, and I do not forsake him either.  

☝  
☝  

142  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

After passing through Hṛdaya-granthi, the yogī contemplates the Conscious Void everywhere and always receives the darśan of Vāsudeva. Vāsudeva Himself bestows grace upon the yogī established in the consciousness of the Void and inspires him to know Its true nature, the consciousness of Time, by which the consciousness of the Void is permeated.  

*sarvabhūtasthitaṁ yō māṁ bhajatyēkatvamāsthitaḥ |  
sarvathā vartamānō’pi sa yōgī mayi vartatē || 6-31 ||*  

Established in oneness with Me, the eternal, who abides in all beings, such a yogī finds refuge and always abides only in Me.  

The great man who, through his practice of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda, has realized that all matter is upheld by the Conscious Void, and that the primal consciousness of this Void is Vāsudeva, observes everywhere in this visible world only the manifestations of the consciousness of the Void.  

*ātmaupamyēna sarvatra samaṁ paśyati yō’rjuna |  
sukhaṁ vā yadi vā duḥkhaṁ sa yōgī paramō mataḥ || 6-32 ||*  

“O Arjuna! He who sees other beings as equal to himself, and remains unperturbed by joy or sorrow—that yogī is considered the best among yogīs.”  

The yogī, established in the consciousness of the Void and having begun to know Its true nature, directs his gaze upon the Void and concentrates it upon That which is not accessible to ordinary sight. He directly perceives the protector of the entire world, Vāsudeva, Lord Viṣṇu.  

☝  
☝  
☝  

143  
Chapter 6  

*arjuna uvāca*  
*yō’yaṁ yōgastvayā prōktaḥ sāmyēna madhusūdana |  
ētasyāhaṁ na paśyāmi cañcalatvātsthitiṁ sthirām || 6-33 ||  
cañcalaṁ hi manaḥ kṛṣṇa pramāthi balavad dṛḍham |  
tasyāhaṁ nigrahaṁ manyē vāyōriva suduṣkaram || 6-34 ||*  

Arjuna said:  
“O Madhusūdana, due to the unsteadiness of the mind, I cannot grasp that unchanging state of yoga which you have described. For, O Kṛṣṇa, the conscious mind is stubborn, restless, and powerful; to control it is as difficult as trying to tame the wind.”  

Ordinary people do not even suspect the sleeping potential of their mind and therefore have no aspiration to awaken it. They cannot even imagine the result of this ancient yoga, and thus the yoga itself seems impossible to them. That small part of their consciousness which is not asleep is limited by physical boundaries, as a result of which they cannot even conceive of a state beyond the body and the sense organs. They do not understand that the boundless consciousness of the mind can be awakened through the practice of yoga.  

*śrībhagavānuvāca*  
*asaṁśayaṁ mahābāhō manō durnigrahaṁ calam |  
abhyāsēna tu kauntēya vairāgyēṇa ca gṛhyatē || 6-35 ||*  

The Lord said:  
“O Mahābāho! Undoubtedly, this mind is restless and powerful. But it can be tamed through practice and vairāgya.”  

☝  

144  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  

He who dedicates himself to awakening the sleeping consciousness of his mind encounters difficulties at the beginning of the path due to the limitation of consciousness by physical boundaries. But if such a yogī continues to practice resolutely and regularly, as a result he successfully passes the first stage of this ancient yoga, called Brahma-granthi-bheda, and develops aversion to sense objects. Thus, rising above physical limitations, he begins to experience the boundlessness of consciousness.  

When, through practice, the sādhaka reaches successive boundaries of consciousness, this frees him from what previously seemed attractive. Continuing to move forward, he transcends these. Yogīs know that one of the results of yoga is vairāgya, that is, the state of dispassion. It can be said that when the mind is fully satisfied with the study of something, that satisfaction leads to a feeling of satiety (boredom), as a result of which the very desire for what once seemed so attractive disappears.  

*asaṁyatātmanā yōgō duṣprāpa iti mē matiḥ |  
vaśyātmanā tu yatatā śakyō’vāptumupāyataḥ || 6-36 ||*  

“It is my conviction that this yoga is unattainable for those whose conscious mind is undisciplined, but those who have mastered themselves and are diligent can become established in it.”  

Mediocre people do not strive to awaken the sleeping faculties of their mind and make no effort toward self-knowledge, and therefore they never attain the state of yoga. Whereas he who has realized that the greater part of his mind’s boundless consciousness is asleep seeks initiation into the practice of this ancient yoga, desiring to awaken his consciousness, and as a result obtains the grace and instruction of the great authorities of this discipline.  

☝  
☝  

145  
Chapter 6  

*arjuna uvāca*  
*ayatiḥ śraddhayōpētō yōgāccalitamānasaḥ |  
aprāpya yōgasaṁsiddhiṁ kāṁ gatiṁ kṛṣṇa gacchati || 6-37 ||  
kaccinnōbhayavibhraṣṭaśchinnābhramiva naśyati |  
apratiṣṭhō mahābāhō vimūḍhō brahmaṇaḥ pathi || 6-38 ||  
ētanmē sanśayaṁ kṛṣṇa chēttumarhasyaśēṣataḥ |  
tvadanyaḥ sanśayasyāsya chēttā na hyupapadyatē || 6-39 ||*  

Arjuna said:  
“O Kṛṣṇa! What is the fate of a person who possesses firm faith but falls away from practice and does not attain perfection in yoga? O Mahābāho! Does not he who strays from the path to Brahman without attaining perfection perish like a cloud scattered by the wind? O Kṛṣṇa! Only you are able to completely dispel my doubts, for besides you there is no one here who can help me.”  

This question arises in the minds of most beginning yogīs: what happens to those who, step by step, in accordance with the instructions received, practice this ancient teaching of yoga, but for some reason die before attaining the result of practice—samādhi?  

☝

146
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
śrībhagavānuvāca
pārtha naivēha nāmutra vināśastasya vidyatē ।
na hi kalyāṇakṛtkaścid‌durgatiṁ tāta gacchati ॥ 6-40॥

The Lord said:
“O Pārtha! He does not perish either in this world or beyond it;
misfortune does not befall anyone who does good, O My friend!
If the life of a yogī, who is performing the practice of this ancient yoga according to his level, is cut short for some reason before he attains samādhi through the awakening of his dormant infinite consciousness, even then calamity will not overtake him.

prāpya puṇyakṛtāṁ lōkānuṣitvā śāśvatīḥ samāḥ ।
śucīnāṁ śrīmatāṁ gēhē yōgabhṛṣṭō’bhijāyatē ॥ 6-41॥
athavā yōgināmēva kulē bhavati dhīmatām ।
ētaddhi durlabhataraṁ lōkē janma yadīdṛśam ॥ 6-42॥

Tempered in the fire of yoga, by his righteous deeds he attains the subtle worlds, abides there, and is reborn in a pious and prosperous family. Or he obtains embodiment in a family of wise yogīs—but such a birth is extremely difficult to merit in this world.
A yogī whose life ends for some reason before the full awakening of his infinite consciousness transcends physical limitations through death by virtue of his practice of yoga. For a long time he experiences the primordial infinite consciousness of the Void in the subtle worlds and is born again into a lineage of great people through the body of a virtuous woman.

☝

147
Chapter 6
Those same yogīs whose life ceases for some reason after completing the level of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda of this ancient yoga receive a profound experience of that most intense, unbearably radiant, infinite consciousness of Time and are born from a mother who is a yoginī into a lineage of yogīs. To be born into such a family is a great fortune compared to an ordinary birth. It is considered to happen very rarely.

tatra taṁ buddhisaṁyōgaṁ labhatē paurvadēhikam ।
yatatē ca tatō bhūyaḥ saṁsiddhau kurunandana ॥ 6-43॥

O Kurunandana! He attains the wisdom acquired in a past incarnation and with its help again strives toward perfection.
Through the steadfast practice accomplished in a previous life, after obtaining a new body such great people diligently continue the practice of yoga in order to know the true nature of the Unmanifest.

pūrvābhyāsēna tēnaiva hriyatē hyavaśō’pi saḥ ।
jijñāsurapi yōgasya śabdabrahmātivartatē ॥ 6-44॥

He who has attained liberation through practice perfected in the past, the seeker of knowledge, the yogī, transcends Śabda Brahman¹.
Having completed the practice of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda in a previous body and thus having passed through the sound of Anāhata Nāda, which fills the consciousness of the Void, the yogī continues with the next practice—Rudra-granthi-bheda. Then he applies
¹Vedic rites and rituals

☝

148
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
great effort to complete this third stage of yoga, also known as Mūlādhāra-granthi-bheda, for the realization of Time, called “Mūlādhāra”—the foundation of all foundations.

prayatnādyatamānastu yōgī saṁśuddhakilbiṣaḥ ।
anēkajanmasaṁsiddhastatō yāti parāṁ gatim ॥ 6-45॥

The yogī who practices diligently becomes flawless and, after a succession of incarnations, is ready to attain that ultimate goal.
Having overcome the fear of death through his yogic practice performed over several lives, the yogī, who has repeatedly transcended physical boundaries through death, becomes established in the Conscious Void. He diligently performs the practice of yoga to know the true nature of the consciousness of Time, which abides beyond the Void, and, having known It, becomes one with It.

tapasvibhyō’dhikō yōgī jñānibhyō’pi matō’dhikaḥ ।
karmibhyaścādhikō yōgī tasmādyōgī bhavārjuna ॥ 6-46॥

The yogī is higher than the ascetic, nobler than the sage, and better than one who acts for the sake of fruits. Therefore, O Arjuna, be a yogī!
The yogī who diligently performs the practice of Rudra-granthi-bheda in order to know the consciousness of Time, which, pervading the Void and this entire visible world, remains beyond them, stands on a higher level than those who perform the initial techniques of yoga to know their physical limitations. He surpasses even those who have already realized their physical limits. He is also on a higher level than yogīs who perform the practice of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda and have realized themselves.

☝

149
Chapter 6
Great effort must be applied to successfully pass through all stages of this yoga and to merit the opportunity, at this final stage, to know the true nature of the consciousness of Time.

yōgināmapi sarvēṣāṁ madgatēnāntarātmanā ।
śraddhāvān bhajatē yō māṁ sa mē yuktatamō mataḥ ॥ 6-47॥

“Among all yogīs, he who has dedicated his mind to Me and through this has attained Me is considered by Me to be the greatest.”
The greatest among all yogīs is he who has transcended all physical boundaries, become established in the consciousness of the Void through the awakening of the infinite consciousness of his mind, and thus begun to know the consciousness of Time, which pervades the consciousness of the Void. Such a great person is revered by the primordial Supreme Being, the Light of all light, the unmanifest Time itself.

ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē ātmasaṁyamayōgō nāma ṣaṣṭhō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 6॥

Oṁ Tat Sat
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the sixth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Self-Restraint,” of the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which treats the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

☝

saptamō’dhyāyaḥ jñānavijñānayōgaḥ

Chapter 7
THE YOGA OF KNOWLEDGE AND REALIZATION

152
śrībhagavānuvāca
mayyāsaktamanāḥ pārtha yōgaṁ yuñjanmadāśrayaḥ ।
asaṁśayaṁ samagraṁ māṁ yathā jñāsyasi tacchṛṇu ॥ 7-1॥

The Lord said:
“O Pārtha! With your mind fixed on Me, surrendered to Me, having attained perfection in yoga, strive for the complete realization of Me—and you shall know Me, without doubt.
The yogī who has attained the result of the practice of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda directly contemplates Lord Viṣṇu, who sustains the entire universe, and begins to know the true nature of the consciousness of the Conscious Void. When he attains such a state, the Guru introduces him to the consciousness of Time, which fills the consciousness of the Void. Thereafter, such a yogī is ready to master the final stage of this ancient yoga, called Rudra-granthi-bheda or Mūlādhāra-granthi-bheda.

☝
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya
Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya

153
Chapter 7
jñānaṁ tē’haṁ savijñānamidaṁ vakśyāmyaśēṣataḥ ।
yajjñātvā nēha bhūyō’nyajjñātavyamavaśiṣyatē ॥ 7-2॥

I shall impart to you this knowledge together with the means of its attainment. For one who has known this, there remains nothing else in the whole world worth knowing.
In this world, nothing remains worth knowing after receiving instruction in this great secret practice.

manuṣyāṇāṁ sahasrēṣu kaścidyatati siddhayē ।
yatatāmapi siddhānāṁ kaścinmāṁ vētti tattvataḥ ॥ 7-3॥

Among thousands of men, scarcely one strives for perfection, and among those striving, scarcely one truly knows Me as I am.
An ordinary person does not sense the boundlessness of the dormant consciousness of his own mind and, as a result, does not even have an idea that it can be awakened. Among the multitude of such people, only a few, inspired by great sages, firmly resolve to awaken their dormant infinite consciousness, receive instruction from a great man who has realized Brahman (brahmajñānī) in this ancient yogic sādhanā, and begin diligent practice. And among those practicing yoga, thirsting for its result—samādhi—scarcely one is able to complete all stages of this ancient yoga within his lifetime and know the nature of the Light of all light, the dazzlingly radiant Time.

☝

154
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
bhūmirāpō’nalō vāyuḥ khaṁ manō buddhirēva ca ।
ahaṁkāra itīyaṁ mē bhinnā prakṛtiraṣṭadhā ॥ 7-4॥

Earth, water, fire, air, space, the conscious mind, intellect, and ego—such is My eightfold nature.
Time, Paramātman, manifests in the form of this entire visible world through earth, water, fire, air, and space (the five elements). Through these elements, as well as the conscious mind, intellect, and the boundless capacities of the mind, It embodies itself in the form of the human body—Its best expression.

aparēyamitastvanyāṁ prakṛtiṁ viddhi mē parām ।
jīvabhūtāṁ mahābāhō yayēdaṁ dhāryatē jagat ॥ 7-5॥

This is My mundane Nature, but, Mahābāho, I am higher than It and even higher than the Soul of all beings. By My presence I sustain everything, and at the same time, being subtle and inconceivable, I abide beyond it.
The eight separate dimensions of the consciousness of Time, which abide far beyond the limited intellect of ordinary people, are reflected in Its manifestations. Only those yogīs who have already advanced sufficiently on the path of realizing the truth of the unmanifest Time are able to know that it is the consciousness of Time that fills the consciousness of the Void and that It alone manifests this entire visible world. It is Time that was unmanifest before the creation of the world, is unmanifest during the existence of this world, and will remain unmanifest even after its dissolution.

☝

155
Chapter 7
ētadyōnīni bhūtāni sarvāṇītyupadhāraya ।
ahaṁ kṛtsnasya jagataḥ prabhavaḥ pralayastathā ॥ 7-6॥

Know: all beings arise from the two states of My being, and I am the beginning and the end of the entire universe.
This entire visible world arises from the womb of Time. Time itself sustains its existence, and Time itself is the cause of its destruction.

mattaḥ parataraṁ nānyatkiṁcidasti dhanaṁjaya ।
mayi sarvamidaṁ prōtaṁ sūtrē maṇigaṇā iva ॥ 7-7॥

O Dhanañjaya! There is nothing higher than Me. I pervade everything, like a string that threads a necklace of pearls.
There is nothing moving or unmoving in this world besides the all-pervading Conscious Void, revered as Viṣṇu, and the consciousness of Time that fills It. Only the unmanifest Time, the primordial Supreme Being, or one who has united with Time by knowing Its true nature, knows where the consciousness of the Void transitions into the consciousness of Time and where that boundary lies beyond which the consciousness of Time becomes perceptible in the form of the Void. Who else could know this?

rasō’hamapsu kauntēya prabhāsmi śaśisūryayōḥ ।
praṇavaḥ sarvavēdēṣu śabdaḥ khē pauruṣaṁ nṛṣu ॥ 7-8॥

O Kaunteya! I am the fluidity in water, I am the light of the sun and the moon. I am “Oṁ” in the Vedas, sound in space, and the life force in men.

☝

**156**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

That boundless Unmanifest Element manifests through water, as fluidity is its principal quality. Although It is perceived by gross vision as light, Its nature is the supreme, transcendent Light, accessible only to the direct perception of yogis. It itself is the human nature in humans. It is also the great Omkar, the supreme sound perceived by those established in the consciousness of measureless Emptiness.

पुण्यो गन्धः पृथिव्यां च तेजश्चास्मि विभावसौ ।
जीवनं सर्वभूतेषु तपश्चास्मि तपस्विषु ॥७- ९॥
puṇyō gandhaḥ pṛthivyāṁ ca tējaścāsmi vibhāvasau ।
jīvanaṁ sarvabhūtēṣu tapaścāsmi tapasviṣu ॥ 7-9॥

I am the sacred fragrance of the earth and the heat of fire. I am the life of all beings and the austerity of ascetics.

Being the basis for the union of all elements, the body is like the earth, and all the sense organs are like fragrance—the principal quality of earth. Time itself is the heat of the fire of yoga, which the yogin kindles in his own body for the sake of knowing the unmanifest consciousness of Time. The support of all life, the Life of every life—is Time itself.

बीजं मां सर्वभूतानां विद्धि पार्थ सनातनम् ।
बुद्धिर्बुद्धिमतामस्मि तेजस्तेजस्विनामहम् ॥७- १०॥
bījaṁ māṁ sarvabhūtānāṁ viddhi pārtha sanātanam ।
buddhirbuddhimatāmasmi tējastējasvināmaham ॥ 7-10॥

O Partha! Know Me as the eternal seed of all living beings. I am the wisdom of the wise and the splendor of the glorious.

Time manifests the entire world. It existed before its manifestation, exists during its manifestation, and will exist always, even after the destruction of the universe. It is the exceptional intellect of the wise and the brilliance of the outstanding, for the mind and abilities develop only with the passage of time.

☝
☝
☝

**157**
**Chapter 7**

बलं बलवतां चाहं कामरागविवर्जितम् ।
धर्माविरुद्धो भूतेषु कामोऽस्मि भरतर्षभ ॥७- ११॥
balaṁ balavatāṁ cāhaṁ kāmarāgavivarjitam ।
dharmāviruddhō bhūtēṣu kāmō’smi bharatarṣabha ॥ 7-11॥

O best of the Bharatas! I am the strength of the strong, free from desire and attachment. In all beings, I am the passion that is in accord with dharma.

Time itself is the yogic power of sadhakas who, desiring to know it, perform the practice of the final stage of this ancient yoga, concentrating all their awakened boundless consciousness on the consciousness of Time. That same Time inspires everyone towards self-knowledge.

ये चैव सात्त्विका भावा राजसास्तामसाश्च ये ।
मत्त एवेति तान्विद्धि न त्वहं तेषु ते मयि ॥७- १२॥
yē caiva sāttvikā bhāvā rājasāstāmasāśca yē ।
matta ēvēti tānviddhi na tvahaṁ tēṣu tē mayi ॥ 7-12॥

Know also that all the gunas—sattva, rajas, and tamas—originate from Me, but I am not in them, nor are they in Me.

Sattvaguna, which inspires one to know Time through awakening one's consciousness; rajoguna, which is the cause of the interconnection of the mind and senses; tamoguna, which leads to complete limitation by sense objects—all of them originated from Time itself. The manifestation of the three gunas is but a small part of the great consciousness of Time; therefore, even while present within them, the infinite consciousness of Time always remains beyond them.

☝
☝

**158**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

त्रिभिर्गुणमयैर्भावैरेभिः सर्वमिदं जगत् ।
मोहितं नाभिजानाति मामेभ्यः परमव्ययम् ॥७- १३॥
tribhirguṇamayairbhāvairēbhiḥ sarvamidaṁ jagat ।
mōhitaṁ nābhijānāti māmēbhyaḥ paramavyayam ॥ 7-13॥

The entire world is deluded by the gunas. Thrown into confusion, they do not know Me, who is transcendent to the world.

All creatures are enchanted by the manifestation of these three gunas. Captivated by the gunas, they do not seek liberation in this ancient teaching of yoga for awakening the boundless consciousness of their mind. Not practicing yoga, they are unable to know the Consciousness of every consciousness, the consciousness of Time.

दैवी ह्येषा गुणमयी मम माया दुरत्यया ।
मामेव ये प्रपद्यन्ते मायामेतां तरन्ति ते ॥७- १४॥
daivī hyēṣā guṇamayī mama māyā duratyayā ।
māmēva yē prapadyantē māyāmētāṁ taranti tē ॥ 7-14॥

It is difficult to overcome that illusion of the gunas—only those who have wholly dedicated themselves to Me can transcend it.

For an ordinary person who does not strive to go beyond physical limitations, there is no possibility whatsoever of experiencing one's own boundlessness. Those who purposefully perform the practice of yoga in order to know the truth of boundless Time pass beyond all limits and, taking refuge in Time itself, become the Conscious of Time.

न मां दुष्कृतिनो मूढाः प्रपद्यन्ते नराधमाः ।
माययापहृतज्ञाना आसुरं भावमाश्रिताः ॥७- १५॥
na māṁ duṣkṛtinō mūḍhāḥ prapadyantē narādhamāḥ ।
māyayāpahṛtajñānā āsuraṁ bhāvamāśritāḥ ॥ 7-15॥

People whose knowledge is captive to illusion, the lowest of men possessing a demonic nature, as well as fools immersed in sinful deeds, do not surrender to Me.

☝
☝

**159**
**Chapter 7**

Ordinary people, who limit their mind to the body and are attached to sense objects, do not strive to awaken themselves and therefore are unable to feel the boundlessness of their own sleeping consciousness. They cannot even conceive of the Consciousness of all consciousness, the consciousness of Time, which is transcendent even to the consciousness of Emptiness.

चतुर्विधा भजन्ते मां जनाः सुकृतिनोऽर्जुन ।
आर्तो जिज्ञासुरर्थार्थी ज्ञानी च भरतर्षभ ॥७- १६॥
तेषां ज्ञानी नित्ययुक्त एकभक्तिर्विशिष्यते ।
प्रियो हि ज्ञानिनोऽत्यर्थमहं स च मम प्रियः ॥७- १७॥
caturvidhā bhajantē māṁ janāḥ sukṛtinō’rjuna ।
ārtō jijñāsurarthārthī jñānī ca bharatarṣabha ॥ 7-16॥
tēṣāṁ jñānī nityayukta ēkabhaktirviśiṣyatē ।
priyō hi jñāninō’tyarthamahaṁ sa ca mama priyaḥ ॥ 7-17॥

O Arjuna! Four types of righteous ones worship Me: the seeker of wealth, the afflicted, the seeker of knowledge, and the knower, O Bharata. The ever-devoted knower is the best among them, for I am very dear to him, and he is dear to Me as well.

Having glimpsed the boundlessness of consciousness, a person becomes filled with the desire to awaken it, and, following this desire, seeks the opportunity to receive instruction in this ancient yogic practice. His search culminates in success: he receives these instructions from a great sage who has known Brahman, and he begins the practice of yoga. Awakening his sleeping consciousness, the yogin concentrates it on the consciousness of Time, and thus acquiring supreme knowledge, takes refuge in Time itself. Such a great yogin, having successfully completed all stages of this ancient practice, stands out among other sadhakas. Having known the true nature of Time and having united with It, such a sage becomes dear to himself.

☝
☝

**160**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

उदाराः सर्व एवैते ज्ञानी त्वात्मैव मे मतम् ।
आस्थितः स हि युक्तात्मा मामेवानुत्तमां गतिम् ॥७- १८॥
udārāḥ sarva ēvaitē jñānī tvātmaiva mē matam ।
āsthitaḥ sa hi yuktātmā māmēvānuttamāṁ gatim ॥ 7-18॥

All of them are noble, and yet the knower is My very Self—such is My opinion. He who is devoted, like him, attains Me, the Supreme Goal.

Faithful to their vows, immersed in practice, such yogis stand out among ordinary people. And those among them who, after passing through all stages of this yoga, are able to unite their consciousness with the consciousness of Time, dissolve in It, knowing Its true nature.

बहूनां जन्मनामन्ते ज्ञानवान्मां प्रपद्यते ।
वासुदेवः सर्वमिति स महात्मा सुदुर्लभः ॥७- १९॥
bahūnāṁ janmanāmantē jñānavānmāṁ prapadyatē ।
vāsudēvaḥ sarvamiti sa mahātmā sudurlabhaḥ ॥ 7-19॥

After passing through many births and deaths, having known Me, such a great sage worships Me as Vasudeva and sees Me in everything. Such a great soul is difficult to find.

Even among sages, it is difficult to encounter such a great person who, performing the practice of yoga over many of his lives, finally comprehends the consciousness of Emptiness, Vasudeva, who lives in the heart of every being, and then, by yogic power, knows the consciousness of Time that fills Emptiness.

कामैस्तैस्तैर्हृतज्ञानाः प्रपद्यन्तेऽन्यदेवताः ।
तं तं नियममास्थाय प्रकृत्या नियताः स्वया ॥७- २०॥
kāmaistaistairhṛtajñānāḥ prapadyantē’nyadēvatāḥ ।
taṁ taṁ niyamamāsthāya prakṛtyā niyatāḥ svayā ॥ 7-20॥

Overwhelmed by manifold desires, people worship various gods, following the vows determined by their own nature.

☝
☝

**161**
**Chapter 7**

Ordinary people possess an intellect confined within physical boundaries and are unable to feel the unmanifest boundlessness of their own consciousness. Due to this limitation, they remain preoccupied only with the body. Driven by greed, they choose some deity according to their preference and begin to worship it.

यो यो यां यां तनुं भक्तः श्रद्धयार्चितुमिच्छति ।
तस्य तस्याचलां श्रद्धां तामेव विदधाम्यहम् ॥७- २१॥
yō yō yāṁ yāṁ tanuṁ bhaktaḥ śraddhayārcitumicchati ।
tasya tasyācalāṁ śraddhāṁ tāmēva vidadhāmyaham ॥ 7-21॥

In whatever form a devotee wishes to worship with faith, I make that faith of his unwavering.

Having read about deities in sacred scriptures or heard attractive stories about ritual actions, an ordinary person bestows faith upon the deity he has chosen and begins his worship, and Time itself strengthens his faith. Over time, the faith of a person hoping for a result becomes more and more firm.

स तया श्रद्धया युक्तस्तस्याराधनमीहते ।
लभते च ततः कामान्मयैव विहितान्हि तान् ॥७- २२॥
sa tayā śraddhayā yuktastasyārādhanamīhatē ।
labhatē ca tataḥ kāmānmayaiva vihitānhi tān ॥ 7-22॥

Endowed with that faith, they strive for the worship of that deity, and from it they obtain the desired boons, which are ordained by Me.

Thus acquiring the grace of the chosen deity, an ordinary person, instead of awakening the boundless consciousness of his mind, worships an extremely insignificant part of that boundless Time. Whatever desire he may be captivated by, performing such worship, that desire is fulfilled, for through worship it became the meaning of all his actions.

☝
☝
☝

**162**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

अन्तवत्तु फलं तेषां तद्भवत्यल्पमेधसाम् ।
देवान्देवयजो यान्ति मद्भक्ता यान्ति मामपि ॥७- २३॥
antavattu phalaṁ tēṣāṁ tadbhavatyalpamēdhasām ।
dēvāndēvayajō yānti madbhaktā yānti māmapi ॥ 7-23॥

But fleeting is that gain of ordinary people. Worshippers of gods go to the gods, whereas My devotees come to Me.

Ordinary people, remaining locked within their physical limits, consider their senses supreme and deify them, merely sustaining their limitation by sense objects. But the sadhakas devoted to practice, who diligently practice yoga for the awakening of the sleeping boundlessness of their mind in order to know Time, attain union with Time itself. Those who worship deities representing but a minuscule part of that unmanifest Time, at the end of their life remember only them and therefore attain the worlds of those deities. Such people take birth again and again.

अव्यक्तं व्यक्तिमापन्नं मन्यन्ते मामबुद्धयः ।
परं भावमजानन्तो ममाव्ययमनुत्तमम् ॥७- २४॥
avyaktaṁ vyaktimāpannaṁ manyantē māmabuddhayaḥ ।
paraṁ bhāvamajānantō mamāvyayamanuttamam ॥ 7-24॥

The unintelligent, not knowing My supreme Nature, think of Me, the unmanifest, as having become manifest.

Fools, whose intellect is limited by the body and senses, are unable even to think of the unmanifest Presence that manifests the body. Confined within physical limits, they give preference only to the body and, even upon the completion of many of their births, cannot grasp even a glimpse of the consciousness of Time that fills the consciousness of Emptiness.

☝
☝

**163**
**Chapter 7**

_nāhaṁ prakāśaḥ sarvasya yōgamāyāsamāvṛtaḥ_
_mūḍhō’yaṁ nābhijānāti lōkō māmajamavyayam_

Veiled by the covering of Maya, I do not reveal Myself to all. This ignorant world is unable to know Me, the unborn and imperishable.

Those who do not practice yoga to awaken their sleeping consciousness continue to abide within physical limitations. For this reason, they cannot know the boundlessness of the consciousness of Time, the Light of all lights, which has no beginning, is imperishable, and unmanifest.

_vēdāhaṁ samatītāni vartamānāni cārjuna_
_bhaviṣyāṇi ca bhūtāni māṁ tu vēda na kaścana_

O Arjuna! I know the past, present, and future of all living beings, but no one knows Me.

The present was the future of the past and, with the passage of time, will become the past of the future. Those who have awakened themselves through yoga can realize that Time itself is motionless, although it appears to move. Consciousness fixes only that moment of time upon which it is directed, and since the focus of consciousness continues to shift unceasingly, time appears to move. Yogis who have known this are able to understand that past, present, and future always abide fused into one in that boundless consciousness of Time.

☝
☝

**164**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

_icchādvēṣasamutthēna dvandvamōhēna bhārata_
_sarvabhūtāni sammōhaṁ sargē yānti parantapa_

O Bharata! The illusion of duality, arising from attraction and aversion, deludes all beings in this world.

Fools, possessing consciousness confined within physical limits, know nothing of their hidden boundlessness and are therefore unhappy. They continue to crave only the gratification of the senses and consider happiness to be the fulfillment of desire, and sorrow—an obstacle on its path. Such people continue to abide limited by this duality.

_yēṣāṁ tvantagataṁ pāpaṁ janānāṁ puṇyakarmaṇām_
_tē dvandvamōhanirmuktā bhajantē māṁ dṛḍhavratāḥ_

But the wise, purified from sins by sacred actions, freed from this illusion, steadfast in the fulfillment of vows, worship only Me.

Faithful to their vows, yogis diligently perform the practice of this ancient discipline to awaken the entire boundlessness of the mind and transcend physical limits. Through this, such great people rise above the illusory duality of happiness and sorrow. Knowing the nature of death, they unite with the consciousness of Time that fills the Conscious Void.

☝
☝

**165**
**Chapter 7**

_jarāmaraṇamōkśāya māmāśritya yatanti yē_
_tē brahma tadviduḥ kṛtsnamadhyātmaṁ karma cākhilam_

Those who strive for freedom from old age and death, having taken refuge in Me, realize Brahman, fully know spiritual wisdom and karma.

Great people who practice yoga for liberation from the bonds of birth and succeed in awakening their boundless consciousness fully realize the entire importance of the body, which is the support of the consciousness of the mind. Such great yogis, carefully protecting their body, pass through all stages of this ancient practice during their lifetime, striving to know the consciousness of Time that pervades the Conscious Void. To protect the body from aging and death on the path to achieving the final result of their practice, they find support in Time itself and resort to methods of rejuvenating the body and prolonging life. Those who surrender to Time thus strive to remain beyond the power of aging and death until their practice is complete. They are able to fully know the consciousness of Time, the imperishable Brahman, as well as Its manifestation—the boundlessness of their own mind—and the path of yoga leading to the attainment of this boundlessness.

_sādhibhūtādhidaivaṁ māṁ sādhiyajñaṁ ca yē viduḥ_
_prayāṇakālē’pi ca māṁ tē viduryuktacētasaḥ_

Perfect yogis, who know Me as the Supreme Spirit, the Supreme Lord, and the Supreme Yajna, realize Me even at the moment of death.

Such great yogis, having attained ultimate perfection, using the body, awaken the boundlessness of the mind. They are able

☝
☝

**166**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

to know the true nature of the unmanifest Consciousness that manifests this boundlessness—the consciousness of Time that pervades the Conscious Void. Through death, knowing the consciousness of Time, such yogis abandon their body and themselves become conscious of Time.

_ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē_
_śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē jñānavijñānayōgō nāma saptamō’dhyāyaḥ_

Om Tat Sat
Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the seventh chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Knowledge and Realization,” of the Upanishad “Shrimad Bhagavad Gita,” which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

**Chapter 8**
**THE YOGA OF THE ETERNAL BRAHMAN**

**168**

_arjuna uvāca_
_kiṁ tadbrahma kimadhyātmaṁ kiṁ karma puruṣōttama_
_adhibhūtaṁ ca kiṁ prōktamadhidaivaṁ kimucyatē_

Arjuna said:
“O Purushottama! What is Brahman? What is the Supreme Essence [Adhyatma]? What is karma? What is called the Supreme Spirit [Adhibhuta]? Who is the Supreme Lord [Adhideva]?

_adhiyajñaḥ kathaṁ kō’tra dēhē’sminmadhusūdana_
_prayāṇakālē ca kathaṁ jñēyō’si niyatātmabhiḥ_

O Madhusudana! What is the Supreme Yajna [Adhiyajna]? How does This abide in the body? And how, at the time of their death, do the self-controlled know You?”

_ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya_
Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**169**
**Chapter 8**

_śrībhagavānuvāca_
_akśaraṁ brahma paramaṁ svabhāvō’dhyātmamucyatē_
_bhūtabhāvōdbhavakarō visargaḥ karmasaṁjñitaḥ_

The Lord said:
“Brahman is that Primordial and Imperishable; His Nature [Svabhava] is called the Supreme Essence; and renunciation of the principal cause of existence is termed karma.

The unmanifest infinite Time is that primordial imperishable Brahman. The conscious human mind, representing His best manifestation, is called Atman. The ancient yoga that leads to the renunciation of actions performed only for the gratification of the senses, which do not release ordinary people from physical limits, allows one to awaken the boundless consciousness of the mind in its full entirety. Called Kriya Yoga, it is defined as ‘karma.’

_adhibhūtaṁ kśarō bhāvaḥ puruṣaścādhidaivatam_
_adhiyajñō’hamēvātra dēhē dēhabhṛtāṁ vara_

The Supreme Spirit is considered to be the transient presence itself; Purusha is the Supreme Lord; and, O best among the embodied, the Supreme Yajna in this body is I.

The body is the support of the boundless consciousness of the mind, and even though it is impermanent and mortal, it is called Adhibhuta. The conscious mind, a small part of the immeasurable mind, enjoying through the organs and controlling them, like Lord Indra, is the Purusha among the organs and is known as Adhideva. Time, Paramatma (also called Vasudeva,

☝
☝

**170**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

because It dwells in the heart of every being), which manifests both the body and the mind, intellect, and full consciousness, abiding in the body, is called Adhiyajna.

_antakālē ca māmēva smaranmuktvā kalēvaram_
_yaḥ prayāti sa madbhāvaṁ yāti nāstyatra sanśayaḥ_

Without doubt, he who at the moment of his death remembers only Me, freed from the bonds of the body, attains My nature.

Now the difference between the death of an ordinary person and the death of a *sthitaprajna* is explained. After death, a person unites with that idea which arises in his mind in the last moments of life (during the release from physical limits), regardless of the limitation or immensity of that idea. Giving preference to the body throughout life, ordinary people even at the moment of death experience strong physical attachment and therefore, after death, are forced to be born again. At the same time, those great people who leave the body, awakening their boundless consciousness and thus knowing the true nature of Time that fills the Conscious Void, unite with that Primordial Consciousness.

_yaṁ yaṁ vāpi smaranbhāvaṁ tyajatyantē kalēvaram_
_taṁ tamēvaiti kauntēya sadā tadbhāvabhāvitaḥ_

Whatever state of being a person remembers at the last moment of his life, absorbed in thoughts of it, he attains only that.

After death, a person becomes a hostage to those feelings and experiences which he revives in memory while leaving the body. At the time of death, the thought that predominates in the mind is the one that was dominant for the person throughout his entire life. If life was spent satisfying the sense organs and the limited mind, then because of this, even after overcoming physical boundaries through death, a person is again forced to don the yoke of physical limits.

☝
☝

**171**
**Chapter 8**

_tasmātsarvēṣu kālēṣu māmanusmara yudhya ca_
_mayyarpitamanōbuddhirmāmēvaiṣyasyasanśayam_

Therefore, while fighting, remember Me constantly! Having wholly dedicated your mind and intellect to Me, you will undoubtedly attain Me.

Great people who have succeeded in awakening the entire boundlessness of their consciousness, passing through death, begin to know the true nature of primordial Time. Such yogis see the entire universe as a manifestation of the consciousness of Time. They always think only of this primordial eternal Presence, and when their life's path ends, such Time-conscious sages attain unity with that Light of all lights, the unbearably radiant Time.

_abhyāsayōgayuktēna cētasā nānyagāminā_
_paramaṁ puruṣaṁ divyaṁ yāti pārthānucintayan_

O Partha! A person attains the primordial divine Purusha through self-contemplation, using his mind, perfected by the practice of yoga and not straying to anything else.

Great people, knowing the Conscious Void through their steadfast practice of yoga, continue with great diligence to strive for the realization of Time which fills It. Acquiring yogic power, they directly perceive the radiant form of that unmanifest Time and become omniscient.

☝
☝

172
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
कविं पुराणमनुशासितारमणोरणीयांसमनुस्मरेद्यः ।
सर्वस्य धातारमचिन्त्यरूप मादित्यवर्णं तमसः परस्तात् ॥८- ९॥
kaviṁ purāṇamanuśāsitāramaṇōraṇīyāṁsamanusmarēdyaḥ ।
sarvasya dhātāramacintyarūpa mādityavarṇaṁ tamasaḥ parastāt ॥ 8-9॥

The all-knowing one experiences that primordial State of Being, sovereign, subtle, and even super-subtle, yet encompassing all, inconceivable, in color like the Sun, and beyond darkness.

That unbearable Radiance of all radiance, the Flame of all flame, in color like the Sun, subtle and even super-subtle, the support of all – the sole cause through which this universe manifests. It is impossible to imagine this splendor without the experience of its direct perception. Great yogis are able to behold with their own eyes this unbearable radiance of Time.

प्रयाणकाले मनसाचलेन भक्त्या युक्तो योगबलेन चैव ।
भ्रुवोर्मध्ये प्राणमावेश्य सम्यक् स तं परं पुरुषमुपैति दिव्यम् ॥८- १०॥
prayāṇakālē manasācalēna bhaktyā yuktō yōgabalēna caiva ।
bhruvōrmadhyē prāṇamāvēśya samyak sa taṁ paraṁ puruṣamupaiti divyam ॥ 8-10॥

He who, at the moment of death, with a calm mind and full devotion, by the power of yoga properly places prāṇa between the eyebrows, attains that divine primordial Puruṣa.

When the final moment of a yogi’s life approaches, who has obtained the experience of that Ultimate Radiance, he concentrates on that Radiance, surrendering to Time, by the power of yoga raises prāṇa upward through suṣumṇā, places it between the eyebrows, and leaves his body, uniting with that great Radiance.

This yogic power is attained through valiant practice of the techniques of Rudra-granthi-bheda. The performance of these techniques grants the ability to directly perceive the unbearable brilliance of Time, the Foundation of all foundations. Yogis call this particular kriyā “oṁkār kriyā.” If at the time of death oṁkār kriyā is repeated 20,736
2“The Gate of Brahman”
☝
☝

173
Chapter 8
(twenty thousand seven hundred thirty-six) times in one breath, the Brahmarandhra² is pierced and the yogi merges with that Boundless Radiance.

यदक्षरं वेदविदो वदन्ति विशन्ति यद्यतयो वीतरागाः ।
यदिच्छन्तो ब्रह्मचर्यं चरन्ति तत्ते पदं संग्रहेण प्रवक्ष्ये ॥८- ११॥
yadakśaraṁ vēdavidō vadanti viśanti yadyatayō vītarāgāḥ ।
yadicchantō brahmacaryaṁ caranti tattē padaṁ saṁgrahēṇa pravakśyē ॥ 8-11॥

That which the wise call the Imperishable, that which dispassionate ascetics attain, and for the sake of which seekers observe brahmacarya – that goal I shall now describe to you briefly.

That Truth of boundless Time, which the great sages describe as imperishable, is attained only through the direct contemplation of its unbearable Radiance. Sādhakas strive with all their might to obtain the practices of the final stage of this ancient yoga, valiantly performing the techniques of the Jihvā-granthi-bheda and Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda levels. This mystical teaching of yoga is now explained by Lord Kṛṣṇa.

सर्वद्वाराणि संयम्य मनो हृदि निरुध्य च ।
मूर्ध्न्याधायात्मनः प्राणमास्थितो योगधारणाम् ॥८- १२॥
ओमित्येकाक्षरं ब्रह्म व्याहरन्मामनुस्मरन् ।
यः प्रयाति त्यजन्देहं स याति परमां गतिम् ॥८- १३॥
sarvadvārāṇi sanyamya manō hṛdi nirudhya ca ।
mūrdhnyādhāyātmanaḥ prāṇamāsthitō yōgadhāraṇām ॥ 8-12॥
ōmityēkākśaraṁ brahma vyāharanmāmanusmaran ।
yaḥ prayāti tyajandēhaṁ sa yāti paramāṁ gatim ॥ 8-13॥

He who closes all the gates of the body, restrains his mind in the heart, raises prāṇa to the head, abides in deep concentration, reciting the single-syllable mantra “Om,” and, leaving his body, calls upon Me, attains that Supreme Goal.

The yogi, closing the nine gates of the body while performing yoni mudrā (this refers to a person whose heart has become suṣumṇā due to his ability to stop the heartbeat after
☝
☝

174
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
passing through Hṛdaya-granthi), directing the mind together with prāṇa into suṣumṇā and placing prāṇa in the center between the eyebrows (bhrūmadhya), directly contemplates the unbearable brilliance of Time. Established in this state, the yogi performs 20,736 (twenty thousand seven hundred thirty-six) oṁkār kriyās in one breath and leaves the body, attaining the supreme Goal through union with the unbearable radiance of Time.

अनन्यचेताः सततं यो मां स्मरति नित्यशः ।
तस्याहं सुलभः पार्थ नित्ययुक्तस्य योगिनः ॥८- १४॥
ananyacētāḥ satataṁ yō māṁ smarati nityaśaḥ ।
tasyāhaṁ sulabhaḥ pārtha nityayuktasya yōginaḥ ॥ 8-14॥

O Pārtha! I am easily attainable for the ever-devoted yogi who constantly calls upon Me, thinking of nothing else.

For sādhakas who have dedicated their entire lives to the practice of yoga, it is easier to directly realize the unbearable radiance of Time through this final stage of practice.

मामुपेत्य पुनर्जन्म दुःखालयमशाश्वतम् ।
नाप्नुवन्ति महात्मानः संसिद्धिं परमां गताः ॥८- १५॥
māmupētya punarjanma duḥkhālayamaśāśvatam ।
nāpnuvanti mahātmānaḥ saṁsiddhiṁ paramāṁ gatāḥ ॥ 8-15॥

Great souls who have attained ultimate perfection, having reached Me, do not accept the bonds of new birth in this transient and sorrow-filled world.

Great men who are conscious of Time, having attained the results of yoga, become established in the boundless magnificence of Time and never again fall into the bonds of physical limitations.
☝
☝

175
Chapter 8
आब्रह्मभुवनाल्लोकाः पुनरावर्तिनोऽर्जुन ।
मामुपेत्य तु कौन्तेय पुनर्जन्म न विद्यते ॥८- १६॥
ābrahmabhuvanāllōkāḥ punarāvartinō’rjuna ।
māmupētya tu kauntēya punarjanma na vidyatē ॥ 8-16॥

O Arjuna! Beings in all worlds, including Brahma-Loka, return again and again, but no one is born here again after attaining Me, O Kaunteya!

All beings in this universe are reborn again and again until they come to know the true nature of the imperishable Supreme Time. Once they have known it, they are no longer born and do not limit themselves with physical boundaries.

Next, for ordinary people who do not practice yoga and have not known the dazzling radiance of Time, certain states that follow shortly after death are explained. If an ordinary person, knowing these states, is able to maintain fearlessness during death and for some time afterward, then even he can become free from the necessity of rebirth.

When breathing slows at the moment of death, a feeling of lightness appears simultaneously with the fear of death. After the heartbeat ceases, a person experiences a strong sensation of dizziness and hears a whistle, roar, or ringing of bells. Simultaneously, the consciousness of the dying person leaves his body. The dizziness may last from a few moments to three or four days on the physical time scale, depending on the level of individual mental development. When consciousness leaves the physical body, the person receives a fleeting experience of the great radiance of Time. Having no such experience in the past, ordinary people feel terror at this moment.

This fleeting experience is like an unexpected emergence into dazzling sunlight after a very long confinement in a dark room. If the person remains unperturbed and remembers that this is that same great Radiance which manifests
☝

176
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
him and also this universe, then he has a chance to merge with It.

If, however, he is frightened by the darśana of this terrible Radiance and tries to hide, the Radiance immediately disappears and the person finds himself outside the body. Having lost the support of the body, his consciousness experiences a feeling of emptiness. At this moment, the person does not understand that death has overtaken him. When he sees his relatives, he even tries to communicate with them, but no one can hear him or feel his presence. All his attempts fail. Later, when the person observes the funeral ceremony being performed over his body, he gradually begins to realize that he has died.

At this moment, or sometimes a little later, he again sees that ultimate Radiance. This time it resembles a pure light that alternately brightens and dims, and has the form of a large, bright golden circle with a dark blue center. This is the direct darśana of Conscious Emptiness. Simultaneously, the deceased also hears a deafening sound of Anāhata Nāda emanating from the center of the circle, like the simultaneous thunderclap from thousands of clouds. If an ordinary person can maintain fearlessness while experiencing this, and realize that this is his true form, as well as that same Radiance which manifests his own consciousness, then he too can merge with It and be freed from the painful obligation of rebirth.

Those who are frightened by this experience go to heaven or hell, depending on the level of their consciousness. Remaining in the bonds of limitation, they are forced to be reborn again and again.

The yogi obtains this experience while still alive and therefore becomes fearless. Through death, he unites with the Light of all light, the unbearable radiance of Time.

177
Chapter 8
सहस्रयुगपर्यन्तमहर्यद्ब्रह्मणो विदुः ।
रात्रिं युगसहस्रान्तां तेऽहोरात्रविदो जनाः ॥८- १७॥
sahasrayugaparyantamaharyadbrahmaṇō viduḥ ।
rātriṁ yugasahasrāntāṁ tē’hōrātravidō janāḥ ॥ 8-17॥

Those who know that one cosmic day⁴ lasts a thousand yugas and that one cosmic night⁴ also lasts a thousand yugas, truly know Day and Night.

Matter, which is the true support for the manifestation of the entire universe, as well as its body, is called by the name Brahmā for its absolute boundlessness. Now Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa speaks of its temporal duration. One day of physical matter constitutes 4,320,000,000 (four billion three hundred twenty million) solar years of humanity, and its night lasts the same. When the yogi’s consciousness overcomes physical boundaries and becomes boundless, first passing beyond the limits of the Earth and then the Solar System, he begins to perceive Time. Such great men possess an understanding of the temporal interval between the manifestation of matter and its subsequent dissolution.

अव्यक्ताद्व्यक्तयः सर्वाः प्रभवन्त्यहरागमे ।
रात्र्यागमे प्रलीयन्ते तत्रैवाव्यक्तसंज्ञके ॥८- १८॥
avyaktādvyaktayaḥ sarvāḥ prabhavantyaharāgamē ।
rātryāgamē pralīyantē tatraivāvyaktasaṁjñakē ॥ 8-18॥

All beings arise from the Unmanifest at the dawn of Day and dissolve into that which is called the Unmanifest with the onset of Night.

When this entire visible world manifests through matter from the womb of unmanifest Time, that moment is considered the beginning of the Day of Brahmā, or matter. When matter, dissolving with the passage of time, sinks into Conscious Emptiness, this is considered the beginning of the Night of Brahmā.
⁴Day of Brahmā, Night of Brahmā
☝
☝

178
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
भूतग्रामः स एवायं भूत्वा भूत्वा प्रलीयते ।
रात्र्यागमेऽवशः पार्थ प्रभवत्यहरागमे ॥८- १९॥
bhūtagrāmaḥ sa ēvāyaṁ bhūtvā bhūtvā pralīyatē ।
rātryāgamē’vaśaḥ pārtha prabhavatyaharāgamē ॥ 8-19॥

O Pārtha! This entire multitude of beings, being born again and again, helplessly dissolves with the onset of Night and is created anew at the dawn of Day.

Boundless conscious Matter, which supports the entire universe, having completely dissolved into the womb of Time, once again manifests from His womb together with its full consciousness. The moment of the birth of conscious Matter is mentioned as the beginning of that endless Day.

This knowledge naturally comes to yogis awakening their intellect when they begin to comprehend the boundlessness of Time, concentrating their consciousness on the consciousness of Time. After the passing of a hundred endless years, measured by these endless Days of Matter, the life of this infinite conscious Matter ends, and It sinks into the womb of Time only to be born again in due time.

परस्तस्मात्तु भावोऽन्योऽव्यक्तोऽव्यक्तात्सनातनः ।
यः स सर्वेषु भूतेषु नश्यत्सु न विनश्यति ॥८- २०॥
parastasmāttu bhāvō’nyō’vyaktō’vyaktātsanātanaḥ ।
yaḥ sa sarvēṣu bhūtēṣu naśyatsu na vinaśyati ॥ 8-20॥

But beyond that Unmanifest there remains My Eternal Presence, which does not perish even when all creatures are destroyed.

Unmanifest Time, that imperishable Brahman, abides beyond the Conscious Emptiness into which Matter ultimately sinks. It truly remains unmanifest even after all Matter and Conscious Emptiness have merged.
☝
☝

179
Chapter 8
अव्यक्तोऽक्षर इत्युक्तस्तमाहुः परमां गतिम् ।
यं प्राप्य न निवर्तन्ते तद्धाम परमं मम ॥८- २१॥
avyaktō’kśara ityuktastamāhuḥ paramāṁ gatim ।
yaṁ prāpya na nivartantē taddhāma paramaṁ mama ॥ 8-21॥

That which is described as unmanifest and imperishable is also called the Supreme Goal, which is My Highest Abode. None who attain it ever return.

The great man, having passed through death, directly perceives that Unbearable Radiance of primordial Time and unites with It. After this, such a yogin never again takes a new birth.

पुरुषः स परः पार्थ भक्त्या लभ्यस्त्वनन्यया ।
यस्यान्तःस्थानि भूतानि येन सर्वमिदं ततम् ॥८- २२॥
puruṣaḥ sa paraḥ pārtha bhaktyā labhyastvananyayā ।
yasyāntaḥsthāni bhūtāni yēna sarvamidaṁ tatam ॥ 8-22॥

O Partha! That Primordial Purusha, who manifests the entire world and contains all beings within Himself, is attained through undivided devotion to Him.

The unmanifest truth of Time, which manifests the entire visible world from its womb, is attained through undivided faith in the consciousness of Time. This faith arises with the experience of perceiving Him through diligent practice of yoga.

यत्र काले त्वनावृत्तिमावृत्तिं चैव योगिनः ।
प्रयाता यान्ति तं कालं वक्ष्यामि भरतर्षभ ॥८- २३॥
yatra kālē tvanāvṛttimāvṛttiṁ caiva yōginaḥ ।
prayātā yānti taṁ kālaṁ vakśyāmi bharatarṣabha ॥ 8-23॥

O best of the Bharatas! Now I shall tell you of that time when yogins depart from their bodies, never to return, or to be born again.

☝
☝

180
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

Now Lord Shri Krishna explains the conditions under which, upon leaving the body, the yogin bound by physical limitations either takes a subsequent birth or is no longer born again.

अग्निर्ज्योतिरहः शुक्लः षण्मासा उत्तरायणम् ।
तत्र प्रयाता गच्छन्ति ब्रह्म ब्रह्मविदो जनाः ॥८- २४॥
agnirjyōtirahaḥ śuklaḥ ṣaṇmāsā uttarāyaṇam ।
tatra prayātā gacchanti brahma brahmavidō janāḥ ॥ 8-24॥

Those who know Brahman [the Absolute], departing from the body on the path marked by fire, light, day, the waxing moon, and the half-year of the Sun’s northern course, attain Brahman.

Those who are able to attain the consciousness of Emptiness through the awakening of their dormant consciousness can directly perceive the unmanifest Time, the primordial Soul, the Light of all lights, whose color is like the Sun. At the end of their lives, such yogins leave their bodies with yogic power during those six months when the planet is full of divine sentiments and when, from Earth, the Sun appears to move northward. They merge into the Light of all lights, the infinite radiance of Time, and never return.

धूमो रात्रिस्तथा कृष्णः षण्मासा दक्षिणायनम् ।
तत्र चान्द्रमसं ज्योतिर्योगी प्राप्य निवर्तते ॥८- २५॥
dhūmō rātristathā kṛṣṇaḥ ṣaṇmāsā dakśiṇāyanam ।
tatra cāndramasaṁ jyōtiryōgī prāpya nivartatē ॥ 8-25॥

But he who departs from the body on the path marked by smoke, night, the waning moon, and the half-year of the Sun’s southern course, having attained the light of the moon, returns again.

Yogins who leave the body before attaining the consciousness of Emptiness through yogic practice are able to see only a partial glimpse of that Light of all lights, the unbearable radiance of Time. This glimpse is like the light of the moon compared to the brilliance of the Sun. Such yogins usually depart when, from Earth, the Sun appears to move southward. After rebirth, they resume their practice.

☝
☝
☝

181
Chapter 8

शुक्लकृष्णे गती ह्येते जगतः शाश्वते मते ।
एकया यात्यनावृत्तिमन्ययावर्तते पुनः ॥८- २६॥
śuklakṛṣṇē gatī hyētē jagataḥ śāśvatē matē ।
ēkayā yātyanāvṛttimanyayāvartatē punaḥ ॥ 8-26॥

These two paths, the bright and the dark, are considered eternal in this world. By one, one goes to that place from which there is no return; by the other, one returns again.

The great sages have determined two paths for men. The first is the bright path of direct realization of the radiant form of the unmanifest, imperishable, absolute Time, which opens through the awakening of the entire boundlessness of one’s own mind. Those who follow this path have no need to return.

The second path is covered in the darkness of ignorance; it is followed by those who do not realize Time, the primordial Supreme Essence, due to their inability to awaken the dormant powers of the mind. Those who walk this path are forced to take birth again and again.

नैते सृती पार्थ जानन्योगी मुह्यति कश्चन ।
तस्मात्सर्वेषु कालेषु योगयुक्तो भवार्जुन ॥८- २७॥
naitē sṛtī pārtha jānanyōgī muhyati kaścana ।
tasmātsarvēṣu kālēṣu yōgayuktō bhavārjuna ॥ 8-27॥

O Partha! No yogin who knows these paths is ever deluded again. Therefore, O Arjuna, be devoted to yoga at all times.

The yogin who is unable to know the Unmanifest because most of his consciousness is asleep, undertakes the practice of yoga to awaken his dormant consciousness. As a reward for his valiant practice, he attains the Truth of the consciousness of Time. Having known Time, he dissolves into His radiance.

☝

182
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

वेदेषु यज्ञेषु तपःसु चैव दानेषु यत् पुण्यफलं प्रदिष्टम् ।
अत्येति तत्सर्वमिदं विदित्वा योगी परं स्थानमुपैति चाद्यम् ॥८- २८॥
vēdēṣu yajñēṣu tapaḥsu caiva dānēṣu yat puṇyaphalaṁ pradiṣṭam ।
atyēti tatsarvamidaṁ viditvā yōgī paraṁ sthānamupaiti cādyam ॥ 8-28॥

The practitioner of yoga obtains all the fruits of studying the Vedas, performing austerities and yajnas, and giving gifts, and, having surpassed this, proceeds to the Supreme Goal.

Such great men, having become conscious of Time and known His true nature, cross the boundaries of death and, through death itself, uniting with the splendor of Mahakala, the great radiant Time, enjoy immortality.

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे अक्षरब्रह्मयोगो नामाष्टमोऽध्यायः ॥८॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē akśarabrahmayōgō nāmāṣṭamō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 8॥

  Om Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the eighth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of the Imperishable Brahman,” of the Upanishad of the Shrimad Bhagavad Gita, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

☝

 नवमोऽध्यायः राजविद्याराजगुह्ययोगः
navamō’dhyāyaḥ rājavidyārājaguhyayōgaḥ
Chapter 9
THE YOGA OF THE ROYAL KNOWLEDGE
AND THE ROYAL SECRET

184
श्रीभगवानुवाच
इदं तु ते गुह्यतमं प्रवक्ष्याम्यनसूयवे ।
ज्ञानं विज्ञानसहितं यज्ज्ञात्वा मोक्ष्यसेऽशुभात् ॥९- १॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
idaṁ tu tē guhyatamaṁ pravakśyāmyanasūyavē ।
jñānaṁ vijñānasahitaṁ yajjñātvā mōkśyasē’śubhāt ॥ 9-1॥

The Lord said:
“Now, to you who are free from malice, I shall reveal this knowledge, together with the most secret means of its attainment. Knowing this, you will be liberated from the inauspicious.

The sadhaka who achieves success in the initial stages of this ancient yoga proceeds to the final step of practice, striving to realize the true nature of the Source of all sources, Time. Now Lord Krishna speaks of the experience attained by the yogin who is devoted to Time and has surrendered himself to Him.

राजविद्या राजगुह्यं पवित्रमिदमुत्तमम् ।
प्रत्यक्षावगमं धर्म्यं सुसुखं कर्तुमव्ययम् ॥९- २॥
rājavidyā rājaguhyaṁ pavitramidamuttamam ।
pratyakśāvagamaṁ dharmyaṁ susukhaṁ kartumavyayam ॥ 9-2॥

This most secret and supreme knowledge is sacred, full of virtue,

☝
ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya 
  Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya  

185
Chapter 9

and is attained through direct experience. It exists eternally and, through practice, bestows joy.

This ancient yoga grants its followers its direct result – samadhi. Through samadhi, it allows one to realize the true nature of Time, and therefore it is considered secret and bliss-bestowing. Its line of transmission is never broken in this world.

अश्रद्दधानाः पुरुषा धर्मस्यास्य परन्तप ।
अप्राप्य मां निवर्तन्ते मृत्युसंसारवर्त्मनि ॥९- ३॥
aśraddadhānāḥ puruṣā dharmasyāsya parantapa ।
aprāpya māṁ nivartantē mṛtyusansāravartmani ॥ 9-3॥

O Parantapa! Those who have no faith in this dharma do not attain Me and continue to return again and again to this world of mortals.

Ordinary people, who have not received even a glimpse of the unmanifest, boundless Consciousness abiding within themselves, possess no faith either in this ancient science of yoga or in its results. Having failed to know through yoga that great radiance of Time, they are reborn again and again, living a miserable life in fear of death. Those, however, who have succeeded in awakening their consciousness through the practice of yoga are able to contemplate the origin of the universe, its dissolution, and similar themes, and can comprehend the mystery of these processes.

मया ततमिदं सर्वं जगदव्यक्तमूर्तिना ।
मत्स्थानि सर्वभूतानि न चाहं तेष्ववस्थितः ॥९- ४॥
mayā tatamidaṁ sarvaṁ jagadavyaktamūrtinā ।
matsthāni sarvabhūtāni na cāhaṁ tēṣvavasthitaḥ ॥ 9-4॥

The entire universe is filled with My manifestations and pervaded by Me, the unmanifest. All elements [earth, water, fire, air, and space] abide in Me, yet I am not in them.

All the manifested universe is established in that unmanifest

☝
☝
☝

186
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

consciousness of Time, which fills the consciousness of Emptiness that contains all matter. That consciousness of Time abides unmanifest beyond the entire universe.

न च मत्स्थानि भूतानि पश्य मे योगमैश्वरम् ।
भूतभृन्न च भूतस्थो ममात्मा भूतभावनः ॥९- ५॥
na ca matsthāni bhūtāni paśya mē yōgamaiśvaram ।
bhūtabhṛnna ca bhūtasthō mamātmā bhūtabhāvanaḥ ॥ 9-5॥

And all created things are outside Me. Behold My divine yogic power! Though I am the Sustainer of all beings and the Creator of all creatures, I do not abide in them.

Great men who attain yogic power through their diligent practice are able to realize that the unmanifest primordial truth of Time manifests the entire universe from its womb and yet abides outside it. Time manifests matter, which is the primordial support of the universe, as well as the five primary foundations, the five great elements. It is present and, despite this, absent, remaining unmanifest beyond the consciousness of Emptiness which contains the universe.

यथाकाशस्थितो नित्यं वायुः सर्वत्रगो महान् ।
तथा सर्वाणि भूतानि मत्स्थानीत्युपधारय ॥९- ६॥
