yathākāśasthitō nityaṁ vāyuḥ sarvatragō mahān ।
tathā sarvāṇi bhūtāni matsthānītyupadhāraya ॥ 9-6॥

Know that just as the great wind, moving everywhere freely, abides in space, so do all creatures abide in Me.

Although the wind cannot be seen, it can be felt. That great Wind abides enclosed in space, which appears unmanifest. In the same way, this entire universe, being enclosed in Conscious Emptiness, abides in the unmanifest truth of Time.

☝
☝

187
Chapter 9

सर्वभूतानि कौन्तेय प्रकृतिं यान्ति मामिकाम् ।
कल्पक्षये पुनस्तानि कल्पादौ विसृजाम्यहम् ॥९- ७॥
sarvabhūtāni kauntēya prakṛtiṁ yānti māmikām ।
kalpakśayē punastāni kalpādau visṛjāmyaham ॥ 9-7॥

O Kaunteya! At the end of a kalpa, all beings attain My State, and at the beginning of a kalpa, I am the cause of the universe manifesting again.

Great men who have known the entire vastness of Matter and continue to be established in the consciousness of Emptiness that contains this Matter, learn that one Day of the consciousness of Matter comprises 4,320,000,000 (four billion three hundred twenty million) human years. The entire universe appears from Conscious Emptiness through the consciousness of Matter at the dawn of that Day, and at the end of that infinitely long Day, the universe dissolves into the consciousness of Emptiness and into the consciousness of Time which pervades Her. Yogins who possess an understanding of the duration of this infinite Day have called it a “kalpa.”

प्रकृतिं स्वामवष्टभ्य विसृजामि पुनः पुनः ।
भूतग्राममिमं कृत्स्नमवशं प्रकृतेर्वशात् ॥९- ८॥
prakṛtiṁ svāmavaṣṭabhya visṛjāmi punaḥ punaḥ ।
bhūtagrāmamimaṁ kṛtsnamavaśaṁ prakṛtērvaśāt ॥ 9-8॥

Inactive by My true nature and free from its compelling force, I am again and again the cause of the arising of all creatures.

To be the cause of the manifestation of the universe and yet remain uninvolved in its creation – this is the nature of Time, the primordial Soul, the unmanifest radiance of consciousness. Truly, It does nothing, even while creating and destroying the entire universe again and again.

☝
☝

188
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
na ca māṁ tāni karmāṇi nibadhnanti dhanañjaya ।
udāsīnavadāsīnamasaktaṁ teṣu karmasu ॥ 9-9॥
But these actions do not bind Me, O Dhanañjaya, who am devoid of attachment and appear indifferent.

For the sake of knowing the essence of Time, a person, performing yogic practice, becomes free from desires and is established in samādhi. Such great sthita-prajña, conscious of Time, are able to understand that That unmanifest, dazzlingly radiant Time, being the result of Itself, although it seems to manifest creation, reflecting in it, nevertheless abides outside it.

mayādhyakṣeṇa prakṛtiḥ sūyate sacarācaram ।
hetunānena kaunteya jagadviparivartate ॥ 9-10॥
O Kaunteya! My true nature gives birth to all that is moving and unmoving, therefore this entire world is subject to change.

It is for this reason that such actions of Time, the Supreme Being, as the conception of this universe by Itself from Itself, then its manifestation and subsequent absorption within Itself, are described as natural properties of the nature of Time. Only by virtue of this nature of Time is the entire universe perceived as being created and destroyed.

avajānanti māṁ mūḍhā mānuṣīṁ tanumāśritam ।
paraṁ bhāvamajānanto mama bhūtamaheśvaram ॥ 9-11॥
Fools, not knowing My primordial Presence, disregard Me, Maheśvara, the Supreme Lord of all beings, the true support of human life.

☝
☝

189
Chapter 9
Despite the fact that Time, the Supreme Lord, manifests Itself through the human body to give a hint of the existence of the unmanifest consciousness of Time, ordinary people are deeply mistaken, considering Him merely a human. They scarcely understand that Time Itself manifests in the form of Its incarnation, in order to point to Itself.

moghāśā moghakarmāṇo moghajñānā vicetasaḥ ।
rākṣasīmāsurīṁ caiva prakṛtiṁ mohinīṁ śritāḥ ॥ 9-12॥
Led astray, deceived by futile hopes, useless actions, and empty knowledge, they take refuge in a demonic nature and evil qualities, and their mind is scattered.

People whose consciousness does not leave physical limits, who prefer only sensual pleasures, live under the sway of demonic traits of ignorance. Due to their inability to awaken their consciousness, they cannot even conceive of the unmanifest, boundless Presence lying at the foundation of the manifestation of all life.

mahātmānastu māṁ pārtha daivīṁ prakṛtimāśritāḥ ।
bhajantyananyamanaso jñātvā bhūtādimavyayam ॥ 9-13॥
O Pārtha! But great souls, taking refuge in My divine nature, see in Me the inexhaustible source of creation, the Indestructible Essence, and strive towards Me, thinking of nothing else.

Great people, capable of understanding the divine boundlessness of the mind, which empowers the organs, become established in the consciousness of Time, in That unmanifest Presence which manifests

☝
☝
☝

190
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
the vast intellect and fills the consciousness of the Void. Whatever such Time-conscious sages do, all their actions point to That unmanifest Light of all light, the unbearable radiance of Time.

satataṁ kīrtayanto māṁ yatantaśca dṛḍhavratāḥ ।
namasyantaśca māṁ bhaktyā nityayuktā upāsate ॥ 9-14॥
They worship Me with devotion, glorifying Me, constantly keeping their vows, calling upon Me, and abiding in eternal union with Me.

Great people, performing yoni mudrā and offering prāṇa to prāṇa through oṁkār kriyā, come to know the dazzlingly radiant Time, the Light of all light, whose radiance is like the Sun. Such yogis become devoted to Him, live under His protection, glorify That Light of boundless Time, hear the sound of Anāhata Nāda emanating from That Radiance, and bow down in prostration before Time Itself. Having become conscious of Time, they worship only Time eternally.

jñānayajñena cāpyanye yajanto māmupāsate ।
ekatvena pṛthaktvena bahudhā viśvatomukham ॥ 9-15॥
Some worship Me with a feeling of unity, performing jñāna-yajña. Others worship Me, the Face of the universe, through various paths with a feeling of separateness.

The consciousness of yogis who have attained wisdom through the knowledge of the unmanifest, immeasurably radiant Time, has become one with the consciousness of Time. Such people see in this world only the play of Time.

☝
☝

191
Chapter 9
ahaṁ kraturahaṁ yajñaḥ svadhāhamahamauṣadham ।
mantro’hamahamevājyamahamagnirahaṁ hutam ॥ 9-16॥
I am the rite, I am the sacrifice, I am the offering to the ancestors, I am the medicine, I am the mantra, I am the clarified butter, I am the fire, and that which is offered in sacrifice.

People who have known Time are considered Time-conscious great souls. Such people see in all actions of this visible world, as well as in the unmanifest Conscious Void that lies beyond it, only the consciousness of Time. They are able to perceive Time as the doer, as everything that is done, and as the result of all actions. The body, the means supporting the body, the repetition of mantra, which liberates from ignorance, the fire, the clarified butter, the offering, the slain, the slayer — all this is only Time.

pitāhamasya jagato mātā dhātā pitāmahaḥ ।
vedyaṁ pavitramoṁkāra ṛksāma yajureva ca ॥ 9-17॥
I Myself am the father and mother, the protector and progenitor of this world. I am the sacred syllable “Oṁ,” which is to be known. I Myself are the Ṛgveda, Sāmaveda, and Yajurveda.

The unbearably radiant Time is the father, mother, protector, and progenitor of this world. That remembered heritage, called the Vedas, which the ancient sages preserved in words for posterity, and Oṁkār, the support of all words — all is Time Itself.

☝
☝

192
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
gatirbhartā prabhuḥ sākṣī nivāsaḥ śaraṇaṁ suhṛt ।
prabhavaḥ pralayaḥ sthānaṁ nidhānaṁ bījamavyayam ॥ 9-18॥
I am the destination, the caring and observing Lord, the abode of everyone, the dearest friend, the creation, maintenance, and dissolution of the universe. I am the imperishable seed.

Time moves and is yet motionless. Although motionless, It appears to move. Time is the Master, to whom all are subject; It alone is all creatures, their friends and enemies. Time Itself is the support of everyone, as well as its absence.

tapāmyahamahaṁ varṣaṁ nigṛhṇāmyutsṛjāmi ca ।
amṛtaṁ caiva mṛtyuśca sadasaccāhamarjuna ॥ 9-19॥
I give warmth, I hold back and pour forth the rains, and, O Arjuna, I am death, reality, and illusion.

Time Itself, taking the form of a woman, attracts Time in the form of a man and, igniting Itself in the fire of passion, pours Itself forth in the form of seed and menstruation, after which It is born as offspring. When death comes, It Itself dies. That which is beyond death, and all that is called immortal, real, unreal, and whatever else — all this is Time Itself.

☝
☝

193
Chapter 9
traividyā māṁ somapāḥ pūtapāpāyajñairiṣṭvā svargatiṁ prārthayante ।
te puṇyamāsādya surendralokamaśnanti divyāndivi devabhogān ॥ 9-20॥
te taṁ bhuktvā svargalokaṁ viśālaṁ kṣīṇe puṇye martyalokaṁ viśanti ।
evaṁ trayīdharmamanuprapannāgatāgataṁ kāmakāmā labhante ॥ 9-21॥
Those who drink the soma juice are purified from sins and worship Me through the three paths by yajña, praying for heaven. They attain the world of Indra and enjoy the celestial pleasures of the gods. Having enjoyed the vast heaven and exhausted their merits, they again enter the world of mortals. Thus, following the three laws and striving to satisfy sensual desires, they merely repeat the journey back and forth.

Those who were unable to make use of this knowledge apply effort in the practice of yoga, comprehending the three stages of this ancient teaching. Tempered by the fire of yoga, they gradually begin to acquire the knowledge of That Unmanifest, which manifests life, by passing through the first stage of this practice. If yogis die at this stage, having lived a long time in the subtle worlds of the gods, after death they are reborn again in this world to pass through the remaining stages of development. Such yogis need to accept several births to fully awaken their boundless consciousness through the practice of yoga and to know the consciousness of Time, with which the Conscious Void is filled.

Yogis who, through practice, have overcome physical boundaries can see the subtle world, transcendent to the world of mortals. Some of these great people have personally observed such subtle worlds as heaven or hell and described them in detail. Such great souls have already known that this gross world of mortals and the subtle worlds beyond it are manifestations of the supremely brilliant Time.

Those who do not abandon the constant thirst for pleasures in

☝

194
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
life and after it, take recourse to rituals established by the sacred scriptures and to so-called sacred acts, such as yajña, giving, and others, which yield limited results. As a result, after their death they abide in pleasure-oriented subtle worlds, such as heaven, and after that are reborn again on Earth.

ananyāścintayanto māṁ ye janāḥ paryupāsate ।
teṣāṁ nityābhiyuktānāṁ yogakṣemaṁ vahāmyaham ॥ 9-22॥
Those abiding in unity with Me worship Me, calling upon Me. I Myself ensure the well-being of those who are always devoted to yoga.

Yogis who have attained self-mastery see the play of Time everywhere. Time Itself, Paramātma, bestows upon them the fruits of the practice performed by such yogis for the sake of knowing Time.

ye’pyanyadevatābhaktā yajante śraddhayānvitāḥ ।
te’pi māmeva kaunteya yajantyavidhipūrvakam ॥ 9-23॥
O Kaunteya! And even those who are devotedly honor other gods also worship only Me, albeit indirectly.

People limited by physical boundaries, attached to pleasures, encounter knowledge of the deities of the subtle world and begin to worship them. Such people scarcely know that by honoring a deity, which is a manifestation of That Same Time, they only indirectly worship Time. Not knowing this, in their striving they are unable to obtain even a glimpse of That Light of all light, the unbearable radiance of Time.

☝
☝

195
Chapter 9

अहं हि सर्वयज्ञानां भोक्ता च प्रभुरेव च ।
न तु मामभिजानन्ति तत्त्वेनातश्च्यवन्ति ते ॥९- २४॥
ahaṁ hi sarvayajñānāṁ bhōktā ca prabhurēva ca ।
na tu māmabhijānanti tattvēnātaścyavanti tē ॥ 9-24॥

I Myself am the Supreme Lord, the receiver of all yajñas. But, not knowing My true nature, they inevitably fall.

All yajñas and the reward for them, as well as the cause that impels one to perform yajñas—all is the unmanifest Time itself. Ordinary people, not knowing this truth, do not go beyond their physical limitations or, at best, some subtle worlds beyond them. Therefore, they again and again undergo death and birth.

यान्ति देवव्रता देवान्पितॄन्यान्ति पितृव्रताः ।
भूतानि यान्ति भूतेज्या यान्ति मद्याजिनोऽपि माम् ॥९- २५॥
yānti dēvavratā dēvānpitṝnyānti pitṛvratāḥ ।
bhūtāni yānti bhūtējyā yānti madyājinō’pi mām ॥ 9-25॥

Worshippers of the devas attain the devas; worshippers of the ancestors attain the ancestors; worshippers of spirits attain the spirits. All those who worship Me attain Me.

Those who worship the devas according to their own or others' conception of the subtle worlds, and those who honour their deceased ancestors, as well as those tamasic ones who worship ghosts and spirits—all of them, due to the concentration of the mind, remain confined after death within the subtle worlds of their lifetime worship. Then such people are born again and again.

The yogis who directly perceive the unbearable radiance of Time surrender to Time itself and merge into That Same Radiance after their death. Such great people are no longer born.

☝
☝

196
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

पत्रं पुष्पं फलं तोयं यो मे भक्त्या प्रयच्छति ।
तदहं भक्त्युपहृतमश्नामि प्रयतात्मनः ॥९- २६॥
patraṁ puṣpaṁ phalaṁ tōyaṁ yō mē bhaktyā prayacchati ।
tadahaṁ bhaktyupahṛtamaśnāmi prayatātmanaḥ ॥ 9-26॥

Whoever, being self-controlled, offers Me with devotion a leaf, a flower, a fruit, or water, I partake of that sincerely perfected offering.

The devotee of Time, knowing the truth of Time, realises himself as Its manifestation and worships the Self through himself. Fruits, flowers, and whatever he may offer to others or receive himself—all ultimately goes to the Light of all lights, Time.

यत्करोषि यदश्नासि यज्जुहोषि ददासि यत् ।
यत्तपस्यसि कौन्तेय तत्कुरुष्व मदर्पणम् ॥९- २७॥
yatkarōṣi yadaśnāsi yajjuhōṣi dadāsi yat ।
yattapasyasi kauntēya tatkuruṣva madarpaṇam ॥ 9-27॥

O Kaunteya! Whatever you do, whatever you eat, whatever you offer into the fire, whatever you give as a gift, and whatever austerities you perform—do all as an offering to Me.

Whatever such great people, striving to know the true nature of Time, may do—whether they burn in the fire of yoga or bestow the knowledge of yoga upon seekers of truth—all is merely an offering of Time to Time itself.

शुभाशुभफलैरेवं मोक्ष्यसे कर्मबन्धनैः ।
संन्यासयोगयुक्तात्मा विमुक्तो मामुपैष्यसि ॥९- २८॥
śubhāśubhaphalairēvaṁ mōkśyasē karmabandhanaiḥ ।
sannyāsayōgayuktātmā vimuktō māmupaiṣyasi ॥ 9-28॥

Thus you will cast off the bonds of karma, which bear favourable and unfavourable fruits, and attain Sannyāsa-Yoga¹. Becoming perfect in this way, you will attain Me.

☝
☝

197
Chapter 9

Great people, established in samādhi—the result of yoga—know death. Constantly reflecting only on the immeasurably radiant Time, such yogis dissolve in Him.

समोऽहं सर्वभूतेषु न मे द्वेष्योऽस्ति न प्रियः ।
ये भजन्ति तु मां भक्त्या मयि ते तेषु चाप्यहम् ॥९- २९॥
samō’haṁ sarvabhūtēṣu na mē dvēṣyō’sti na priyaḥ ।
yē bhajanti tu māṁ bhaktyā mayi tē tēṣu cāpyaham ॥ 9-29॥

I am the same in all beings. There is none dear to Me, nor any hateful. But those who worship Me with love—they are in Me, and I am in them.

In Its radiant form, Time itself abides in all beings. No one possesses Its favour, and there is no one who is in Its disfavour. And yet, those who kindle the fire of yoga and sacrifice their body into this fire receive the direct darśana of this radiant form of Time. Such yogis always perceive the radiant form of Time, constantly and directly contemplating Him. They become exclusively devoted to Him and abide only in Him.

अपि चेत्सुदुराचारो भजते मामनन्यभाक् ।
साधुरेव स मन्तव्यः सम्यग्व्यवसितो हि सः ॥९- ३०॥
api cētsudurācārō bhajatē māmananyabhāk ।
sādhurēva sa mantavyaḥ samyagvyavasitō hi saḥ ॥ 9-30॥

If even the greatest of sinners worships Me with unparalleled devotion, he is to be considered righteous, for he has acquired the right resolve.

If an ordinary person, who has lived within physical limits, merely satisfying his sense organs, begins to practise yoga, sooner or later he catches a glimpse of the infinity of the mind, which, through the senses, enjoys everything. Such a person

¹ The knowledge of death
☝
☝
☝

198
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

must properly adhere to his unwavering determination to become established in samādhi. He should be considered a great soul, for, overcoming physical limits, he has already set out on his journey into Infinity.

क्षिप्रं भवति धर्मात्मा शश्वच्छान्तिं निगच्छति ।
कौन्तेय प्रति जानीहि न मे भक्तः प्रणश्यति ॥९- ३१॥
kśipraṁ bhavati dharmātmā śaśvacchāntiṁ nigacchati ।
kauntēya prati jānīhi na mē bhaktaḥ praṇaśyati ॥ 9-31॥

He quickly becomes righteous and attains eternal peace. O Kaunteya! Proclaim to all that My devotee never perishes.

Such a great person knows death and Time, which presides over the entire world, manifesting it, and therefore becomes a righteous soul aware of Time. He dissolves in the radiance of Time and thereby abides in eternal tranquillity. Such a great soul is not obliged to again confine itself within physical limits.

मां हि पार्थ व्यपाश्रित्य येऽपि स्युः पापयोनयः ।
स्त्रियो वैश्यास्तथा शूद्रास्तेऽपि यान्ति परां गतिम् ॥९- ३२॥
māṁ hi pārtha vyapāśritya yē’pi syuḥ pāpayōnayaḥ ।
striyō vaiśyāstathā śūdrāstē’pi yānti parāṁ gatim ॥ 9-32॥

O Pārtha! Even people of low birth, women, vaiśyas, and śūdras attain the supreme Goal, taking refuge in Me.

Women, by means of their body, manifest that unmanifest consciousness, sheltering it in the human body. Śūdras are not inclined to transcend physical boundaries. Vaiśyas are experts in everything that sustains the body. All of them, as well as all those born from sinful mixed marriages, can, through the practice of yoga for overcoming physical limits, obtain direct experience of that unbearably radiant form

☝
☝

199
Chapter 9

of Time. Surrendering to the mercy of Time, even they are capable of attaining the supreme Goal.

किं पुनर्ब्राह्मणाः पुण्या भक्ता राजर्षयस्तथा ।
अनित्यमसुखं लोकमिमं प्राप्य भजस्व माम् ॥९- ३३॥
kiṁ punarbrāhmaṇāḥ puṇyā bhaktā rājarṣayastathā ।
anityamasukhaṁ lōkamimaṁ prāpya bhajasva mām ॥ 9-33॥

How much more, then, the righteous brāhmaṇas, devoted royal sages—taking refuge in Me, they undoubtedly attain liberation from rebirth. Therefore, having obtained this impermanent human body in this world full of suffering, worship only Me.

Kṣatriyas, inclined to surpass physical limits by sacrificing their body, and brāhmaṇas, possessing an innate inclination to reflect upon the unmanifest presence beyond physical limitations, take recourse to this ancient teaching of yoga. By directly experiencing that light of the great radiance of Time, such people become one with Him. To achieve this, one must practise yoga to fully awaken one's mind and, overcoming the limits of the human body, become established in the consciousness of Time that fills the Conscious Void.

मन्मना भव मद्भक्तो मद्याजी मां नमस्कुरु ।
मामेवैष्यसि युक्त्वैवमात्मानं मत्परायणः ॥९- ३४॥
manmanā bhava madbhaktō madyājī māṁ namaskuru ।
māmēvaiṣyasi yuktvaivamātmānaṁ matparāyaṇaḥ ॥ 9-34॥

Fix your mind on Me, be devoted to Me, worship Me, bow down to Me. Thus, having achieved oneness with Me, striving towards Me, you will attain Me.”

Yogis who have overcome physical boundaries for the sake of knowing Time become established in the consciousness of Time that fills the Conscious Void and, directing their mind into Him, complete

☝
☝

200
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

the practice of Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda. They become devotees of Time and, through the performance of oṁkār kriyā in yoni mudrā, receive His direct darśana. Such yogis bow only before Time and, concentrating all the immeasurable consciousness of their mind on His unbearable radiance, penetrate into Time itself.

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे राजविद्याराजगुह्ययोगो नाम नवमोऽध्यायः ॥९॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē rājavidyārājaguhyayōgō nāma navamō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 9॥

  Oṁ Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the ninth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of the Secret Knowledge,” of the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

 दशमोऽध्यायः विभूतियोगः
daśamō’dhyāyaḥ vibhūtiyōgaḥ
Chapter 10
THE YOGA OF DIVINE
SPLENDOUR

202
श्रीभगवानुवाच
भूय एव महाबाहो शृणु मे परमं वचः ।
यत्तेऽहं प्रीयमाणाय वक्ष्यामि हितकाम्यया ॥१०- १॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
bhūya ēva mahābāhō śṛṇu mē paramaṁ vacaḥ ।
yattē’haṁ prīyamāṇāya vakśyāmi hitakāmyayā ॥ 10-1॥

The Lord said:
“O Mahābāho! Listen now to My supreme words, which I shall declare, wishing you well, for you are very dear to Me.

The great sthitaprajña, capable of concentrating all the immensity of their mind on the unbearably bright radiance of Time, penetrate into this radiance. To such great yogis, Time itself speaks of Itself.

न मे विदुः सुरगणाः प्रभवं न महर्षयः ।
अहमादिर्हि देवानां महर्षीणां च सर्वशः ॥१०- २॥
na mē viduḥ suragaṇāḥ prabhavaṁ na maharṣayaḥ ।
ahamādirhi dēvānāṁ maharṣīṇāṁ ca sarvaśaḥ ॥ 10-2॥

Neither the gods nor the great sages know My origin, for I Myself am the Origin of both the gods and the great sages.

The yogis who become established in the Conscious Void and concen-

☝
☝
ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya 
  Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya  

203
Chapter 10

trate all the boundlessness of their awakened mind on the consciousness of Time begin to perceive That Unmanifest. They can feel that all beings, gods, and sages of the gross as well as the subtle worlds are unable to fully comprehend the influence of Time simply because they are still in the process of knowing this primordial truth.

यो मामजमनादिं च वेत्ति लोकमहेश्वरम् ।
असंमूढः स मर्त्येषु सर्वपापैः प्रमुच्यते ॥१०- ३॥
yō māmajamanādiṁ ca vētti lōkamahēśvaram ।
asaṁmūḍhaḥ sa martyēṣu sarvapāpaiḥ pramucyatē ॥ 10-3॥

He who knows Me as Beginningless, Unborn, the Supreme Lord—such a sage among mortals is liberated from all sins.

Despite the limitations of the human body, those few who have been able to awaken all the immensity of their mind through the practice of this ancient yoga and then concentrate all the consciousness of that awakened mind on the brilliance of the unbearable radiance of Time—such great sages are able to understand that Time has neither beginning nor end. The unmanifest Time itself is That Great Lord, manifesting all these gross and subtle worlds or various dimensions.

बुद्धिर्ज्ञानमसंमोहः क्षमा सत्यं दमः शमः ।
सुखं दुःखं भवोऽभावो भयं चाभयमेव च ॥१०- ४॥
अहिंसा समता तुष्टिस्तपो दानं यशोऽयशः ।
भवन्ति भावा भूतानां मत्त एव पृथग्विधाः ॥१०- ५॥
buddhirjñānamasaṁmōhaḥ kśamā satyaṁ damaḥ śamaḥ ।
sukhaṁ duḥkhaṁ bhavō’bhāvō bhayaṁ cābhayamēva ca ॥ 10-4॥
ahiṁsā samatā tuṣṭistapō dānaṁ yaśō’yaśaḥ ।
bhavanti bhāvā bhūtānāṁ matta ēva pṛthagvidhāḥ ॥ 10-5॥

Intellect, knowledge, absence of delusion, forgiveness, truthfulness, restraint, tranquillity, joy and sorrow, birth and death, fear and fearlessness, non-violence, equanimity,

☝

204
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

Contentment, asceticism, compassion, success and failure—
all these various manifestations of the nature of living beings have originated from Me.

Unmanifest Time, the Foundation of all foundations, the chief Support of the universe, the Light of every light, manifests Itself in all that exists and has a name. Intellect, the knowledge of knowledge itself, forgiveness, the capacity to perceive the nature of the senses, happiness and sorrow, fear and fearlessness, violence and non-violence, equanimity, austerity in the form of the fire of yoga, the rewarding of the worthy with yogic practice and other sciences, success and failure, etc.—all these are manifestations of Time Itself.

महर्षयः सप्त पूर्वे चत्वारो मनवस्तथा ।
मद्भावा मानसा जाता येषां लोक इमाः प्रजाः ॥१०- ६॥
maharṣayaḥ sapta pūrvē catvārō manavastathā ।
madbhāvā mānasā jātā yēṣāṁ lōka imāḥ prajāḥ ॥ 10-6॥

The seven great sages, the four most ancient ones who came before them, and the Manus are born from the nature of My mind. From them have descended all who populate this world.

The seven sages, Sanat Kumāra and others who came even earlier, as well as the Manus, were created by but a single thought of That Thought of all thoughts. All people in this universe have descended from them.

एतां विभूतिं योगं च मम यो वेत्ति तत्त्वतः ।
सोऽविकम्पेन योगेन युज्यते नात्र संशयः ॥१०- ७॥
ētāṁ vibhūtiṁ yōgaṁ ca mama yō vētti tattvataḥ ।
sō’vikampēna yōgēna yujyatē nātra sanśayaḥ ॥ 10-7॥

He who truly knows My majesty and the power of this ancient practice attains an unshakable state of yoga. Of this there is no doubt.

Those great beings who have been able to offer their body as an oblation into the fire of yoga, kindled by fierce practice,
☝
☝
☝

205
Chapter 10
are capable, by all their yogic power, of concentrating their consciousness upon unmanifest Time, the Supreme Lord. By His grace they become united with Time and come to know His true nature.

अहं सर्वस्य प्रभवो मत्तः सर्वं प्रवर्तते ।
इति मत्वा भजन्ते मां बुधा भावसमन्विताः ॥१०- ८॥
ahaṁ sarvasya prabhavō mattaḥ sarvaṁ pravartatē ।
iti matvā bhajantē māṁ budhā bhāvasamanvitāḥ ॥ 10-8॥

The devoted sage worships Me, realizing that I am the true Creator of all and that everything occurs only through Me.

Great *sthitaprajña* beings, endowed with self-mastery, are able to understand that This Unmanifest Self is the cause of the creation of the entire visible world. Such people have realized that, manifesting Itself, It merely plays with Itself. Great beings who attain this experience surrender to Time and end their life’s journey, attaining the consciousness of Time.

मच्चित्ता मद्गतप्राणा बोधयन्तः परस्परम् ।
कथयन्तश्च मां नित्यं तुष्यन्ति च रमन्ति च ॥१०- ९॥
maccittā madgataprāṇā bōdhayantaḥ parasparam ।
kathayantaśca māṁ nityaṁ tuṣyanti ca ramanti ca ॥ 10-9॥

Those who have fixed their mind on Me and placed their life in Me, enlightening one another and speaking of Me always, attain contentment and are filled with bliss.

The yogis who, with inspiration, practice this ancient yoga to know that unmanifest presence which is the cause of life and death, successfully pass through the second stage, *Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda*, of this ancient yoga and become established in the consciousness of Emptiness.

After this, they begin the practice of the final stage of yoga, to know the consciousness of Time that fills this
☝
☝

206
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
Emptiness. Performing *yoni mudrā*, they sit motionless and, contemplating the great radiant form of Time, concentrate all their consciousness upon it. Then, by means of *oṁkār kriyā*, they raise their *prāṇa* into the *Prāṇa* of *prāṇas*—into Time. Having known Him, they become conscious of Time and abide in Time with rapture. Concentrating their awakened, boundless consciousness upon the unbearable radiance of Time, they abide in contentment, conversing with Themselves or with the radiant Time Itself.

तेषां सततयुक्तानां भजतां प्रीतिपूर्वकम् ।
ददामि बुद्धियोगं तं येन मामुपयान्ति ते ॥१०- १०॥
tēṣāṁ satatayuktānāṁ bhajatāṁ prītipūrvakam ।
dadāmi buddhiyōgaṁ taṁ yēna māmupayānti tē ॥ 10-10॥

To those ever-devoted to Me, who worship Me with love, I grant that *Buddhi-Yoga* by which they truly attain Me.

Those great beings who, out of their love for Time, have offered their life as an oblation into the boundless radiance of Time by means of *oṁkār kriyā*, are rewarded by Time Itself with the knowledge of Time.

तेषामेवानुकम्पार्थमहमज्ञानजं तमः ।
नाशयाम्यात्मभावस्थो ज्ञानदीपेन भास्वता ॥१०- ११॥
tēṣāmēvānukampārthamahamajñānajaṁ tamaḥ ।
nāśayāmyātmabhāvasthō jñānadīpēna bhāsvatā ॥ 10-11॥

Out of compassion for them, I Myself dispel the darkness of ignorance in their consciousness with the touch of radiant knowledge.”

Great beings, in order to know this highest Truth, offered their entire life as an oblation into the fire of yoga kindled by their practice. To such yogis, Time Itself, out of compassion for them, grants the direct *darśana* of His boundless, dazzlingly radiant form.
☝
☝

207
Chapter 10

अर्जुन उवाच
परं ब्रह्म परं धाम पवित्रं परमं भवान् ।
पुरुषं शाश्वतं दिव्यमादिदेवमजं विभुम् ॥१०- १२॥
आहुस्त्वामृषयः सर्वे देवर्षिर्नारदस्तथा ।
असितो देवलो व्यासः स्वयं चैव ब्रवीषि मे ॥१०- १३॥
arjuna uvāca
paraṁ brahma paraṁ dhāma pavitraṁ paramaṁ bhavān ।
puruṣaṁ śāśvataṁ divyamādidēvamajaṁ vibhum ॥ 10-12॥
āhustvāmṛṣayaḥ sarvē dēvarṣirnāradastathā ।
asitō dēvalō vyāsaḥ svayaṁ caiva bravīṣi mē ॥ 10-13॥

Arjuna said:
“You, the Most Radiant, are the supreme Brahman, the supreme Destination. All sages recognize You as the Eternal Divine Creator, the primordial God, Unborn and Omnipresent. This same truth has been told to me by Nārada, the sage among gods, by Asita, Devala, the great sage Vyāsa, and You Yourself now speak of it to me.

सर्वमेतदृतं मन्ये यन्मां वदसि केशव ।
न हि ते भगवन्व्यक्तिं विदुर्देवा न दानवाः ॥१०- १४॥
sarvamētadṛtaṁ manyē yanmāṁ vadasi kēśava ।
na hi tē bhagavanvyaktiṁ vidurdēvā na dānavāḥ ॥ 10-14॥

O Keśava, now I believe in the truth of all that You have told me. O Lord! Neither demons nor gods know Your essence.

स्वयमेवात्मनात्मानं वेत्थ त्वं पुरुषोत्तम ।
भूतभावन भूतेश देवदेव जगत्पते ॥१०- १५॥
svayamēvātmanātmānaṁ vēttha tvaṁ puruṣōttama ।
bhūtabhāvana bhūtēśa dēvadēva jagatpatē ॥ 10-15॥

O Lord of the Universe! O Source of all existence, God of gods, Lord of all beings, Puruṣottama! You Yourself know Yourself through Yourself alone.

208
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

वक्तुमर्हस्यशेषेण दिव्या ह्यात्मविभूतयः ।
याभिर्विभूतिभिर्लोकानिमांस्त्वं व्याप्य तिष्ठसि ॥१०- १६॥
vaktumarhasyasēṣēṇa divyā hyātmavibhūtayaḥ ।
yābhirvibhūtibhirlōkānimāṁstvaṁ vyāpya tiṣṭhasi ॥ 10-16॥

Only You are able to tell of Your divine manifestations, by which You pervade the entire universe.

कथं विद्यामहं योगिंस्त्वां सदा परिचिन्तयन् ।
केषु केषु च भावेषु चिन्त्योऽसि भगवन्मया ॥१०- १७॥
kathaṁ vidyāmahaṁ yōgiṁstvāṁ sadā paricintayan ।
kēṣu kēṣu ca bhāvēṣu cintyō’si bhagavanmayā ॥ 10-17॥

O Great Yogin! Constantly meditating upon You, how am I to know You? And in which of Your many forms am I to contemplate You?

विस्तरेणात्मनो योगं विभूतिं च जनार्दन ।
भूयः कथय तृप्तिर्हि शृण्वतो नास्ति मेऽमृतम् ॥१०- १८॥
vistarēṇātmanō yōgaṁ vibhūtiṁ ca janārdana ।
bhūyaḥ kathaya tṛptirhi śṛṇvatō nāsti mē’mṛtam ॥ 10-18॥

O Janārdana! Please tell me once again in detail of this Yoga of Yours and of Your glory, for I cannot be satiated with the nectar of these immortal words!”

A great
being, having concentrated all the boundlessness of his mind upon That infinite, indestructible, supreme Time, having known Him and become duly established in Him, asks questions of Time Itself. And this Flame of every flame, Support of all supports, Infinity of infinity itself, Time Itself, reveals Itself to such a *sādhaka*.
☝

209
Chapter 10

श्रीभगवानुवाच
हन्त ते कथयिष्यामि दिव्या ह्यात्मविभूतयः ।
प्राधान्यतः कुरुश्रेष्ठ नास्त्यन्तो विस्तरस्य मे ॥१०- १९॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
hanta tē kathayiṣyāmi divyā hyātmavibhūtayaḥ ।
prādhānyataḥ kuruśrēṣṭha nāstyantō vistarasya mē ॥ 10-19॥

The Lord said:
“O Kuruśreṣṭha! I shall tell you only of My most radiant manifestations, for there is no end to My glory.

Time, the primordial Lord, the Foundation of all foundations, the Light of every light, the Soul of the soul, the Emptiness of emptiness itself, the Consciousness of consciousness, now explains Itself. Who else can fully know Him, if He Himself does not reveal Himself? Time, having taken the form of Śrī Kṛṣṇa, bestows this knowledge upon all future humanity, pointing to Himself through Arjuna.

अहमात्मा गुडाकेश सर्वभूताशयस्थितः ।
अहमादिश्च मध्यं च भूतानामन्त एव च ॥१०- २०॥
ahamātmā guḍākēśa sarvabhūtāśayasthitaḥ ।
ahamādiśca madhyaṁ ca bhūtānāmanta ēva ca ॥ 10-20॥

O Guḍākeśa! I am the Ātman, the sense of ‘I’, that abides in the heart of every being. I am the birth, life, and death of all beings.

“O Conqueror of sleep! I am the essence of all elements that constitute the basis of matter in this universe: earth, water, fire, air, and space. I am the beginning, the middle, and the end, or the past, present, and future of all this.”

आदित्यानामहं विष्णुर्ज्योतिषां रविरंशुमान् ।
मरीचिर्मरुतामस्मि नक्षत्राणामहं शशी ॥१०- २१॥
ādityānāmahaṁ viṣṇurjyōtiṣāṁ raviranśumān ।
marīcirmarutāmasmi nakśatrāṇāmahaṁ śaśī ॥ 10-21॥

I am Viṣṇu among the Ādityas, the Sun among all sources of light, Marīci among the Maruts, and the Moon among the constellations.
☝
☝

210
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

वेदानां सामवेदोऽस्मि देवानामस्मि वासवः ।
इन्द्रियाणां मनश्चास्मि भूतानामस्मि चेतना ॥१०- २२॥
vēdānāṁ sāmavēdō’smi dēvānāmasmi vāsavaḥ ।
indriyāṇāṁ manaścāsmi bhūtānāmasmi cētanā ॥ 10-22॥

Among ancient knowledge I am the Sāmaveda, Indra among the gods, the conscious mind among the sense organs, and consciousness in all beings.

रुद्राणां शंकरश्चास्मि वित्तेशो यक्षरक्षसाम् ।
वसूनां पावकश्चास्मि मेरुः शिखरिणामहम् ॥१०- २३॥
rudrāṇāṁ śaṁkaraścāsmi vittēśō yakśarakśasām ।
vasūnāṁ pāvakaścāsmi mēruḥ śikhariṇāmaham ॥ 10-23॥

I am Śaṅkara among the Rudras, Kubera among the yakṣas and rākṣasas, fire among the Vasus. I am Meru among mountain peaks.

Lord Kṛṣṇa described Himself as Meru among mountain peaks. Mount Meru has been shrouded in mystery for too long. In my opinion, the polar aurora near the North Pole, which in appearance resembles mountain peaks, should be considered Meru. People have attempted to find Meru, supposing it might be a peak in one of the mountain ranges, but a peak matching the existing description has never been found. If we take all its descriptions into account, we find that the golden peak of Meru, where deities and certain superhuman beings reside, is perhaps that very splendor of the polar aurora (Aurora Borealis) observable near the North Pole, which may be the aura of our planet Earth. In the ancient sacred scriptures we also find that the day, as well as the night, of the gods lasts six months, which is true in the case of the North Pole.
☝

211
Chapter 10

पुरोधसां च मुख्यं मां विद्धि पार्थ बृहस्पतिम् ।
सेनानीनामहं स्कन्दः सरसामस्मि सागरः ॥१०- २४॥
purōdhasāṁ ca mukhyaṁ māṁ viddhi pārtha bṛhaspatim ।
sēnānīnāmahaṁ skandaḥ sarasāmasmi sāgaraḥ ॥ 10-24॥

Know Me as Bṛhaspati, the foremost among priests. I am Skanda among warriors and the ocean among bodies of water.

महर्षीणां भृगुरहं गिरामस्म्येकमक्षरम् ।
यज्ञानां जपयज्ञोऽस्मि स्थावराणां हिमालयः ॥१०- २५॥
maharṣīṇāṁ bhṛgurahaṁ girāmasmyēkamakśaram ।
yajñānāṁ japayajñō’smi sthāvarāṇāṁ himālayaḥ ॥ 10-25॥

I am Bhṛgu among the great sages, Oṁkār [the first syllable] among words, *japa-yajña* among sacrifices, and the Himālaya among that which is immovable.

“I am Bhṛgu among the great sages, I am the letter—the foundation of words, *japa-yajña* among sacrifices, and the Himālaya among that which is immovable.”

अश्वत्थः सर्ववृक्षाणां देवर्षीणां च नारदः ।
गन्धर्वाणां चित्ररथः सिद्धानां कपिलो मुनिः ॥१०- २६॥
aśvatthaḥ sarvavṛkśāṇāṁ dēvarṣīṇāṁ ca nāradaḥ ।
gandharvāṇāṁ citrarathaḥ siddhānāṁ kapilō muniḥ ॥ 10-26॥

I am the sacred Aśvattha tree among trees, Nārada among divine sages, Citraratha among celestial musicians, and Kapila among the siddhas.

उच्चैःश्रवसमश्वानां विद्धि माममृतोद्भवम् ।
ऐरावतं गजेन्द्राणां नराणां च नराधिपम् ॥१०- २७॥
uccaiḥśravasamaśvānāṁ viddhi māmamṛtōdbhavam ।
airāvataṁ gajēndrāṇāṁ narāṇāṁ ca narādhipam ॥ 10-27॥

Among horses I am Uccaiḥśravas, born of Amṛta; I am Airāvata among great elephants, and the king among men.
☝

212  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

*āyudhānāmahaṁ vajraṁ dhēnūnāmasmi kāmadhuk ।*  
*prajanaścāsmi kandarpaḥ sarpāṇāmasmi vāsukiḥ ॥ 10-28॥*  

I am the vajra among weapons, Kāmadhenu among cows; among those who beget offspring I am Kāmadeva, and Vāsuki among serpents.  

“I am the vajra among weapons, Kāmadhenu among cows. I am the passion of love that is the basis of procreation, and Vāsuki among serpents.”  

*anantaścāsmi nāgānāṁ varuṇō yādasāmaham ।*  
*pitṝṇāmaryamā cāsmi yamaḥ saṁyamatāmaham ॥ 10-29॥*  

Among the Nāgas I am Ananta [Śeṣanāga]; I am Varuṇa, the god of waters; Aryamā among the ancestors; and Yamarāja among those who rule living beings.  

*prahlādaścāsmi daityānāṁ kālaḥ kalayatāmaham ।*  
*mṛgāṇāṁ ca mṛgēndrō’haṁ vainatēyaśca pakśiṇām ॥ 10-30॥*  

I am Prahlāda among the Daityas; Time among measures; the lion among beasts; and the eagle among birds.  

“I am Prahlāda among demons; Time, perceived by beings who are aware of past, present, and future. I am Mṛgendra, the lord of beasts, and the eagle among birds.”  

☝  
☝  

213  
**Chapter 10**  

*pavanaḥ pavatāmasmi rāmaḥ śastrabhṛtāmaham ।*  
*jhaṣāṇāṁ makaraścāsmi srōtasāmasmi jāhnavī ॥ 10-31॥*  

Among purifying elements I am the wind; I am Rāma among warriors; the alligator among fish; and the Gaṅgā among rivers.  

“I am the air that fills the mortal body with life; among warriors I am Rāma; the alligator among fish; and among rivers I am the Gaṅgā.”  

*sargāṇāmādirantaśca madhyaṁ caivāhamarjuna ।*  
*adhyātmavidyā vidyānāṁ vādaḥ pravadatāmaham ॥ 10-32॥*  

O Arjuna! I am the beginning, the middle, and the end of creation. Among sciences I am the ancient science of yoga. I am the argument among those who debate.  

*akśarāṇāmakārō’smi dvandvaḥ sāmāsikasya ca ।*  
*ahamēvākśayaḥ kālō dhātāhaṁ viśvatōmukhaḥ ॥ 10-33॥*  

Among letters I am the letter “A”; I are the *dvandva¹* among compound words; I am eternal Time; and I am the Creator facing all directions.  

“I am the letter ‘A’ among letters; I am the conflict among those in a group; I Myself am eternal, indestructible Time, supporting all.”  

¹A copulative compound word  

☝  
☝  

214  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

*mṛtyuḥ sarvaharaścāhamudbhavaśca bhaviṣyatām ।*  
*kīrtiḥ śrīrvākca nārīṇāṁ smṛtirmēdhā dhṛtiḥ kśamā ॥ 10-34॥*  

I am death, which comes to all, and also the source of all that is to come in the future. In women I are glory, prosperity, speech, memory, intellect, fortitude, and compassion.  

*bṛhatsāma tathā sāmnāṁ gāyatrī chandasāmaham ।*  
*māsānāṁ mārgaśīrṣō’hamṛtūnāṁ kusumākaraḥ ॥ 10-35॥*  

I am the *Bṛhat-Sāma* among the Sāma Veda hymns and Gāyatrī among poetic meters. I am Mārgaśīrṣa among months and spring among seasons.  

*dyūtaṁ chalayatāmasmi tējastējasvināmaham ।*  
*jayō’smi vyavasāyō’smi sattvaṁ sattvavatāmaham ॥ 10-36॥*  

Among deceptions I am gambling; I am the splendor of all that shines with brilliance; and I am the victory of victors. I am the enterprise of merchants. I am the reality of the real.  

*vṛṣṇīnāṁ vāsudēvō’smi pāṇḍavānāṁ dhanaṁjayaḥ ।*  
*munīnāmapyahaṁ vyāsaḥ kavīnāmuśanā kaviḥ ॥ 10-37॥*  

Among the Vṛṣṇis I am Vāsudeva; among the Pāṇḍavas I am Dhanañjaya; among sages I am Vyāsa; and among poets I am Śukrācārya.  

215  
**Chapter 10**  

*daṇḍō damayatāmasmi nītirasmi jigīṣatām ।*  
*maunaṁ caivāsmi guhyānāṁ jñānaṁ jñānavatāmaham ॥ 10-38॥*  

I am the scepter of conquerors. I am the strategy of those who thirst for victory. I am the silence of secrets and the wisdom of the wise.  

*yaccāpi sarvabhūtānāṁ bījaṁ tadahamarjuna ।*  
*na tadasti vinā yatsyānmayā bhūtaṁ carācaram ॥ 10-39॥*  

And, O Arjuna! I am the seed from which all beings arise. There is no moving or unmoving creature in which I do not dwell.  

“I am the seed from which all beings have arisen. There is no moving or unmoving creature that was not created by Me. Everywhere there is only I, and I alone.”  

*nāntō’sti mama divyānāṁ vibhūtīnāṁ parantapa ।*  
*ēṣa tūddēśataḥ prōktō vibhūtērvistarō mayā ॥ 10-40॥*  

O Parantapa, there is no end to My divine, magnificent manifestations. I have briefly described the greatness of only the most beautiful among them.  

“I am Infinity. My divine, magnificent creations are countless. I have spoken of these excellent creations at your request.”  

☝  
☝  

216  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

*yadyadvibhūtimatsattvaṁ śrīmadūrjitamēva vā ।*  
*tattadēvāvagaccha tvaṁ mama tējōṁ’śasaṁbhavam ॥ 10-41॥*  

My unique radiance manifests in every particle of this creation that sparkles with splendor and is full of greatness.  

*athavā bahunaitēna kiṁ jñātēna tavārjuna ।*  
*viṣṭabhyāhamidaṁ kṛtsnamēkānśēna sthitō jagat ॥ 10-42॥*  

But why do you need to know all this, O Arjuna? I remain unwavering, supporting this entire world with but a small fraction of Myself.”  

The great sage who has succeeded in concentrating the entire vastness of his mind upon that unbearable radiance of Time and has united his consciousness with It is able to understand that this entire universe is but an insignificant manifestation of Time. Yet among all these creations, those that stand out with divine splendor, endowed with beauty and power, are a direct indication of that limitless Time.  

*ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē*  
*śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē vibhūtiyōgō nāma daśamō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 10॥*  

**Oṁ Tat Sat**  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the tenth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Divine Splendor,” of the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.  

☝  

*ēkādaśō’dhyāyaḥ viśvarūpadarśanayōgaḥ*  
**Chapter 11**  
**THE YOGA OF THE VISION OF THE UNIVERSAL FORM**  

218  

*arjuna uvāca*  
*madanugrahāya paramaṁ guhyamadhyātmasaṁjñitam ।*  
*yattvayōktaṁ vacastēna mōhō’yaṁ vigatō mama ॥ 11-1॥*  

Arjuna said:  
“By Your grace, through Your words concerning that supreme secret known as adhyātma, this delusion of mine has been destroyed.  

*bhavāpyayau hi bhūtānāṁ śrutau vistaraśō mayā ।*  
*tvattaḥ kamalapatrākśa māhātmyamapi cāvyayam ॥ 11-2॥*  

O Kamalapatrākṣa¹! I have heard from You the detailed account of the origin and dissolution of beings, as well as of Your imperishable greatness.  

¹“Lotus-eyed”  

*ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya*  
**Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya**  

219  
**Chapter 11**  

*ēvamētadyathāttha tvamātmānaṁ paramēśvara ।*  
*draṣṭumicchāmi tē rūpamaiśvaraṁ puruṣōttama ॥ 11-3॥*  

O Parameśvara! You are exactly as You describe Yourself. I wish to behold Your divine form, O Puruṣottama!  

*manyasē yadi tacchakyaṁ mayā draṣṭumiti prabhō ।*  
*yōgēśvara tatō mē tvaṁ darśayātmānamavyayam ॥ 11-4॥*  

O Prabho! If You deem me capable of beholding It, then, O Yogeśvara, I pray You, grant me darśana of Your indestructible, immortal Essence.”  

The great man who has concentrated the entire vastness of his mind upon the great radiance of Time and thus attained unity with It can hold converse with Time Itself, the Creator of all that exists. Following the knowledge of all Its wondrous manifestations, as well as of the entire universe as a whole, such a yogin yearns to receive the direct darśana of Its infinite, dazzling essence and implores the indestructible, unmanifest, supremely brilliant Time to manifest in that boundless form.  

*śrībhagavānuvāca*  
*paśya mē pārtha rūpāṇi śataśō’tha sahasraśaḥ ।*  
*nānāvidhāni divyāni nānāvarṇākṛtīni ca ॥ 11-5॥*  

The Lord said:  
“O Pārtha! Behold then hundreds and thousands of My divine forms, of various shapes, colors, and hues.  

☝  

220  
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**  

Time accepts the prayers of the great man who has kindled the fire of yoga within his body and offered himself to that fire. Time Itself reveals Its boundless form to such a yogin, offering him the vision of hundreds and thousands of divine images, of different hues and shapes.  

*paśyādityānvasūnrudrānaśvinau marutastathā ।*  
*bahūnyadṛṣṭapūrvāṇi paśyāścaryāṇi bhārata ॥ 11-6॥*  

O Bhārata! Behold the Ādityas, the Vasus, the Rudras, the Aśvins, and the Maruts. Witness wonders and great forms never seen before.  

*ihaikasthaṁ jagatkṛtsnaṁ paśyādya sacarācaram ।*  
*mama dēhē guḍākēśa yaccānyad draṣṭumicchasi ॥ 11-7॥*  

O Guḍākeśa! Behold now, within this body of Mine, the entire universe, all that is moving and unmoving, and whatever else you wish to see.  

Time, the primordial Lord, blesses that great soul with the direct darśana of all Its splendor and offers him the vision of the entire universe together with all gross and subtle worlds, as well as whatever else he may desire. All this is contained within Its unmanifest, sky-like body.  

*na tu māṁ śakyasē draṣṭumanēnaiva svacakśuṣā ।*  
*divyaṁ dadāmi tē cakśuḥ paśya mē yōgamaiśvaram ॥ 11-8॥*  

But you cannot behold Me with these your eyes. I shall grant you divine sight. Behold this radiant splendor of My yoga.”  

☝  
☝  

221  
**Chapter 11**  

Blessing such a great man, Time bestows upon the yogin divine vision and the direct darśana of Its infinite, radiant splendor.  

*sañjaya uvāca*  
*ēvamuktvā tatō rājanmahāyōgēśvarō hariḥ ।*  
*darśayāmāsa pārthāya paramaṁ rūpamaiśvaram ॥ 11-9॥*  

Sañjaya said:  
“Having spoken thus, O King, Mahāyogeśvara² Hari revealed to the son of Pṛthā His supreme universal form.  

The yogin, having concentrated all the boundless consciousness of his mind upon the flame of omnipotent Time, beholds with divine eyes, obtained by the grace of Time, His divine form, full of unsurpassed majesty.  

*anēkavaktranayanamanēkādbhutadarśanam ।*  
*anēkadivyābharaṇaṁ divyānēkōdyatāyudham ॥ 11-10॥*  

*divyamālyāmbaradharaṁ divyagandhānulēpanam ।*  
*sarvāścaryamayaṁ dēvamanantaṁ viśvatōmukham ॥ 11-11॥*  

With many mouths and eyes, with numerous wondrous aspects, adorned with countless divine ornaments and raising divine weapons, wearing divine garlands and garments, anointed with divine oils—thus did Arjuna see the Lord, dazzling, boundless, many-faced, and filled with marvels.  

²“Great Lord of Yoga”  

☝  
☝

222
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

That infinite form of Time possesses numerous mouths and eyes and is filled with wondrous appearances. All worlds are but His divine ornaments. Raising manifold divine weapons, He wears garlands of all planets and constellations. Space itself is like His garment. All natural phenomena are like fragrances applied to His body. With the greatest astonishment, the yogin gazes upon the eternal boundless Time by His own grace.

दिवि सूर्यसहस्रस्य भवेद्युगपदुत्थिता ।
यदि भाः सदृशी सा स्याद्भासस्तस्य महात्मनः ॥११- १२॥
divi sūryasahasrasya bhavēdyugapadutthitā ।
yadi bhāḥ sadṛśī sā syādbhāsastasya mahātmanaḥ ॥ 11-12॥

The light of a thousand suns, suddenly blazing forth all at once in the sky, can scarcely compare with the radiance of that Mahātma.

The radiance of that infinite Light of all lights, of the unbearably brilliant form of Time, is such that the brilliance of several thousand suns can scarcely compare even with a minor glimpse of It.

तत्रैकस्थं जगत्कृत्स्नं प्रविभक्तमनेकधा ।
अपश्यद्देवदेवस्य शरीरे पाण्डवस्तदा ॥११- १३॥
tatraikasthaṁ jagatkṛtsnaṁ pravibhaktamanēkadhā ।
apaśyaddēvadēvasya śarīrē pāṇḍavastadā ॥ 11-13॥

There, in the body of the Supreme Lord, the Pāṇḍava saw the entire universe, divided in manifold ways, gathered into one.

All separately manifested worlds appear at once in the body of that most brilliant Flame, of the unbearably shining Mahādeva.

☝
☝
☝

223
Chapter 11

ततः स विस्मयाविष्टो हृष्टरोमा धनंजयः ।
प्रणम्य शिरसा देवं कृताञ्जलिरभाषत ॥११- १४॥
tataḥ sa vismayāviṣṭō hṛṣṭarōmā dhanaṁjayaḥ ।
praṇamya śirasā dēvaṁ kṛtāñjalirabhāṣata ॥ 11-14॥

Then, agitated and seized with wonder, his hair standing on end, bowing his head and joining his palms before the Lord, Dhanañjaya spoke.

अर्जुन उवाच
पश्यामि देवांस्तव देव देहे सर्वांस्तथा भूतविशेषसंघान् ।
ब्रह्माणमीशं कमलासनस्थमृषींश्च सर्वानुरगांश्च दिव्यान् ॥११- १५॥
arjuna uvāca
paśyāmi dēvānstava dēva dēhē sarvānstathā bhūtaviśēṣasaṁghān ।
brahmāṇamīśaṁ kamalāsanasthamṛṣīṁśca sarvānuragānśca divyān ॥ 11-15॥

Arjuna said:
“O Lord! I see all the gods, as well as multitudes of various beings. I see Lord Brahmā seated on the lotus throne, all the sages, and the divine serpents—all are contained within Your body.

“Only by Your blessing am I able to behold in Your unmanifest body all the gods, the various forms of matter, and the very consciousness of matter embodied as Lord Brahmā, all the sages, and the vast divine serpents. All is manifested by this Your great radiance!”

अनेकबाहूदरवक्त्रनेत्रं पश्यामि त्वां सर्वतोऽनन्तरूपम् ।
नान्तं न मध्यं न पुनस्तवादिं पश्यामि विश्वेश्वर विश्वरूप ॥११- १६॥
anēkabāhūdaravaktranētraṁ paśyāmi tvāṁ sarvatō’nantarūpam ।
nāntaṁ na madhyaṁ na punastavādiṁ paśyāmi viśvēśvara viśvarūpa ॥ 11-16॥

I see You everywhere, with countless arms, bellies, mouths, and eyes. O Viśvarūpa!³ I cannot perceive Your beginning, nor Your middle, nor Your end.

³“Universal Form”
☝

224
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

किरीटिनं गदिनं चक्रिणं च तेजोराशिं सर्वतो दीप्तिमन्तम् ।
पश्यामि त्वां दुर्निरीक्ष्यं समन्ताद्दीप्तानलार्कद्युतिमप्रमेयम् ॥११- १७॥
kirīṭinaṁ gadinaṁ cakriṇaṁ ca tējōrāśiṁ sarvatō dīptimantam ।
paśyāmi tvāṁ durnirīkśyaṁ samantāddīptānalārkadyutimapramēyam ॥ 11-17॥

Everywhere I see only You, crowned with a diadem, with scepter and chakra, illumining all around with blinding radiance, like blazing fire. It is unbearable to behold this boundless, dazzling form.

“The great radiance, before which the light of a thousand suns is nothing—that great radiance is like Your crown. That very radiance is like Your scepter, and that same radiance is Your face, round as a disc. I see Your face, like an unbearably bright, luminous radiance, blazing like the terrifying fire of the Sun. It is bottomless, this blinding radiance of Time.”

त्वमक्षरं परमं वेदितव्यं त्वमस्य विश्वस्य परं निधानम् ।
त्वमव्ययः शाश्वतधर्मगोप्ता सनातनस्त्वं पुरुषो मतो मे ॥११- १८॥
tvamakśaraṁ paramaṁ vēditavyaṁ tvamasya viśvasya paraṁ nidhānam ।
tvamavyayaḥ śāśvatadharmagōptā sanātanastvaṁ puruṣō matō mē ॥ 11-18॥

You are that Supreme and Indestructible, to be known. You alone are the Supreme Refuge of this world. You alone are the Guardian of the eternal law. I have recognized You—You are that Imperishable Puruṣa, You are the Eternal Truth.

अनादिमध्यान्तमनन्तवीर्यमनन्तबाहुं शशिसूर्यनेत्रम् ।
पश्यामि त्वां दीप्तहुताशवक्त्रं स्वतेजसा विश्वमिदं तपन्तम् ॥११- १९॥
anādimadhyāntamanantavīryamanantabāhuṁ śaśisūryanētram ।
paśyāmi tvāṁ dīptahutāśavaktraṁ svatējasā viśvamidaṁ tapantam ॥ 11-19॥

You are without beginning, middle, or end; You are endowed with boundless, mighty, countless arms. The Sun and Moon are like Your eyes. Your face is the most brilliant flame; You heat the entire world with Your radiance.

☝

225
Chapter 11

The Supreme Essence, absolute eternal Time, transcends past, present, and future. It ever abides as triune. All directions are Its infinitely mighty arms. The Sun and Moon are Its eyes; Its radiant face shines like thousands of terrifying suns and heats this entire world with its radiance.

द्यावापृथिव्योरिदमन्तरं हि व्याप्तं त्वयैकेन दिशश्च सर्वाः ।
दृष्ट्वाद्भुतं रूपमुग्रं तवेदं लोकत्रयं प्रव्यथितं महात्मन् ॥११- २०॥
dyāvāpṛthivyōridamantaraṁ hi vyāptaṁ tvayaikēna diśaśca sarvāḥ ।
dṛṣṭvādbhutaṁ rūpamugraṁ tavēdaṁ lōkatrayaṁ pravyathitaṁ mahātman ॥ 11-20॥

O Mahātma! Truly You alone fill all of Heaven, Earth, and cosmic space. All three worlds tremble at the sight of such an astonishing, terrifying form.

Heaven, Earth, planets and stars, galaxies, all directions in space are filled only by Him alone. Even while being permeated by Time and being manifestations of Time, all are distressed, not knowing Time, observing His terrifying, destructive, wondrously beautiful form.

अमी हि त्वां सुरसंघा विशन्ति केचिद्भीताः प्राञ्जलयो गृणन्ति ।
स्वस्तीत्युक्त्वा महर्षिसिद्धसंघाः स्तुवन्ति त्वां स्तुतिभिः पुष्कलाभिः ॥११- २१॥
amī hi tvāṁ surasaṁghā viśanti kēcidbhītāḥ prāñjalayō gṛṇanti ।
svastītyuktvā maharṣisiddhasaṁghāḥ stuvanti tvāṁ stutibhiḥ puṣkalābhiḥ ॥ 11-21॥

Hosts of gods merge into You. Many of them, with joined palms, praise You in fear. Hosts of great sages and perfected yogins, greeting You, call out to You in their hymns of praise.

All beings and gods are manifested by Time and soon after, when their time comes to an end, are absorbed by Time itself. Perfect sages, who have gained some notion of Time, struck with terror by Him, praise Him in fear, finding refuge only in Time.

☝
☝
☝

226
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

रुद्रादित्या वसवो ये च साध्या विश्वेऽश्विनौ मरुतश्चोष्मपाश्च ।
गन्धर्वयक्षासुरसिद्धसंघा वीक्षन्ते त्वां विस्मिताश्चैव सर्वे ॥११- २२॥
rudrādityā vasavō yē ca sādhyā viśvē’śvinau marutaścōṣmapāśca ।
gandharvayakśāsurasiddhasaṁghā vīkśantē tvāṁ vismitāścaiva sarvē ॥ 11-22॥

Hosts of Rudras, Ādityas, Vasus, Sādhyas, Viśvadevas, as well as the Aśvins, Maruts, Manus, Gandharvas, Yakṣas, Rākṣasas, and Siddhas—all gaze upon You in astonishment.

That unmanifest Time, the Soul of the soul, the Support of all supports, whose radiance remains incomparable to any other radiance—that Time, the Creator of all, is Itself Its own eternal embodiment. It manifests Itself in the form of Śiva, in the form of Viṣṇu, in the form of the forefather Brahmā, the Sun, the Moon, Indra, Varuṇa, Vāyu, Yama, the past, present, and future—in the form of the entire universe. Great men, able to see Him by His blessing, are stunned by the sight of that unbearable, terrifying phenomenon and cannot turn their gaze from Him.

रूपं महत्ते बहुवक्त्रनेत्रं महाबाहो बहुबाहूरुपादम् ।
बहूदरं बहुदंष्ट्राकरालं दृष्ट्वा लोकाः प्रव्यथितास्तथाहम् ॥११- २३॥
rūpaṁ mahattē bahuvaktranētraṁ mahābāhō bahubāhūrupādam ।
bahūdaraṁ bahudaṁṣṭrākarālaṁ dṛṣṭvā lōkāḥ pravyathitāstathāham ॥ 11-23॥

O Mahābāho! At the sight of Your measureless form with numerous mouths and eyes, many arms, thighs, and feet, many bellies and terrifying fangs, all creatures tremble. Confusion has seized me as well.

Directly observing the blinding flame of Time, yogins see His terrifying face with dreadful fangs and unbearably blazing mouths. His eyes, His arms, legs, and bellies—all His organs simultaneously encompass the entire world. Great men who are conscious of Time are terrified at the sight of this radiant, terrifying, fear-inspiring manifestation.

☝
☝

227
Chapter 11

नभःस्पृशं दीप्तमनेकवर्णं व्यात्ताननं दीप्तविशालनेत्रम् ।
दृष्ट्वा हि त्वां प्रव्यथितान्तरात्मा धृतिं न विन्दामि शमं च विष्णो ॥११- २४॥
nabhaḥspṛśaṁ dīptamanēkavarṇaṁ vyāttānanaṁ dīptaviśālanētram ।
dṛṣṭvā hi tvāṁ pravyathitāntarātmā dhṛtiṁ na vindāmi śamaṁ ca viṣṇō ॥ 11-24॥

O Viṣṇu! At the sight of You, touching the heavens, radiant, multi-colored, with wide-open mouth and huge blazing eyes, my mind is seized with terror. Courage and peace have abandoned me.

Great men lose courage at the sight of fear-inspiring Time, possessed of all-pervading, terrifying radiance, huge countless fangs, and unbearable eyes like pillars of flame.

दंष्ट्राकरालानि च ते मुखानि दृष्ट्वैव कालानलसन्निभानि ।
दिशो न जाने न लभे च शर्म प्रसीद देवेश जगन्निवास ॥११- २५॥
daṁṣṭrākarālāni ca tē mukhāni dṛṣṭvaiva kālānalasannibhāni ।
diśō na jānē na labhē ca śarma prasīda dēvēśa jagannivāsa ॥ 11-25॥

I do not recognize the directions and lose my composure at the sight of Your most terrible face, which is like the all-encompassing fire of cosmic destruction. O Lord of all gods, be gracious!

Frightened by the sight of the terrifying faces of Time, which, with huge fangs, are like the fire of universal annihilation, blazing with a radiance brighter than the combined radiance of a thousand suns, the great man seeks refuge only in the great Time.

☝
☝

228
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

अमी च त्वां धृतराष्ट्रस्य पुत्राः सर्वे सहैवावनिपालसंघैः ।
भीष्मो द्रोणः सूतपुत्रस्तथासौ सहास्मदीयैरपि योधमुख्यैः ॥११- २६॥
वक्त्राणि ते त्वरमाणा विशन्ति दंष्ट्राकरालानि भयानकानि ।
केचिद्विलग्ना दशनान्तरेषु संदृश्यन्ते चूर्णितैरुत्तमाङ्गैः ॥११- २७॥
amī ca tvāṁ dhṛtarāṣṭrasya putrāḥ sarvē sahaivāvanipālasaṁghaiḥ ।
bhīṣmō drōṇaḥ sūtaputrastathāsau sahāsmadīyairapi yōdhamukhyaiḥ ॥ 11-26॥
vaktrāṇi tē tvaramāṇā viśanti daṁṣṭrākarālāni bhayānakāni ।
kēcidvilagnā daśanāntarēṣu saṁdṛśyantē cūrṇitairuttamāṅgaiḥ ॥ 11-27॥

All the sons of Dhṛtarāṣṭra together with hosts of kings plunge into You. Bhīṣma, Droṇa, and that Sūtaputra [Karṇa], as well as our chief warriors, rush headlong and hurl themselves into Your vast mouths with terrifying fangs. Some of them I see hanging between Your teeth, with their heads crushed.

Blessed by Time Himself, the great man who is conscious of Time sees with perfect clarity that all creatures, from the very moment of birth, begin with all their might to move swiftly toward death. So strongly drawn by death, all beings, created by Time Himself, enter His terrifying mouths with dreadful fangs. Their gross bodies are crushed by the huge teeth of Time. They turn to dust, burning on funeral pyres or being interred. No one has ever been able to outlive Time.

यथा नदीनां बहवोऽम्बुवेगाः समुद्रमेवाभिमुखा द्रवन्ति ।
तथा तवामी नरलोकवीरा विशन्ति वक्त्राण्यभिविज्वलन्ति ॥११- २८॥
यथा प्रदीप्तं ज्वलनं पतङ्गा विशन्ति नाशाय समृद्धवेगाः ।
तथैव नाशाय विशन्ति लोकास्तवापि वक्त्राणि समृद्धवेगाः ॥११- २९॥
yathā nadīnāṁ bahavō’mbuvēgāḥ samudramēvābhimukhā dravanti ।
tathā tavāmī naralokavīrā viśanti vaktrāṇyabhivijvalanti ॥ 11-28॥
yathā pradīptaṁ jvalanaṁ pataṅgā viśanti nāśāya samṛddhavēgāḥ ।
tathaiva nāśāya viśanti lōkāstavāpi vaktrāṇi samṛddhavēgāḥ ॥ 11-29॥

Just as all rivers rush toward the ocean and merge with it, so do these heroes of the world of men enter Your gaping, fiery mouths. Like insects that with furious force rush toward the blazing fire for their destruction, so do these worlds with furious force enter Your mouths for their destruction.

**229**
**Chapter 11**

only to be burned, this entire world, drawn by a great force, plunges into Your mouths, only to disappear.

Directly contemplating this terrifying form of Time by His grace, these great men see that, like rivers striving with all their might toward the ocean only to vanish within it, all people—whether brave or timid, whether killed by someone or dying a natural death—are destroyed by Time itself. Just as insects, drawn by a flame, rush into it only to be annihilated, all beings, who are creations of Time, rush only into the jaws of Time.

*lēlihyasē grasamānaḥ samantāllōkānsamagrānvadanairjvaladbhiḥ ।*
*tējōbhirāpūrya jagatsamagraṁ bhāsastavōgrāḥ pratapanti viṣṇō ॥ 11-30॥*

Devouring all these worlds with Your blazing mouths, You lick them up from every side. Illuminating this entire world with boundless radiance, Your terrible heat scorches it, O Vishnu!

This entire universe is continuously contracting and being devoured by Time. The terrifying effulgence of Time, which manifests this entire world, simultaneously scorches it from all sides.

*ākhyāhi mē kō bhavānugrarūpō namō’stu tē dēvavara prasīda ।*
*vijñātumicchāmi bhavantamādyaṁ na hi prajānāmi tava pravṛttim ॥ 11-31॥*

"Tell me who You are, O Terrible-faced One, be gracious! O Supreme Lord! I bow before You. I wish to know You, O Eternal Essence, in Your true nature, for I do not know what You are."

Frightened by the direct perception of the terrifying

**230**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

form of the immeasurably radiant Time, the great man, having surrendered to Time, asks: "O Primal Form! O Lord of all gods! O Infinity surpassing infinity, who are You? What is Your true nature?"

*śrībhagavānuvāca*
*kālō’smi lōkakśayakṛtpravṛddhō lōkānsamāhartumiha pravṛttaḥ ।*
*ṛtē’pi tvāṁ na bhaviṣyanti sarvē yē’vasthitāḥ pratyanīkēṣu yōdhāḥ ॥ 11-32॥*

The Lord said:
"I am Death, Time, the destroyer of the universe. I have come here to annihilate all these people. All the warriors of the enemy army will perish even without your participation."

Time itself speaks of Itself to those who are conscious of Time: "I am Death, which destroys the entire universe. The past, present, and future hold no sway over Me. I alone always was, I am, and I alone will be. I create this world, and afterward I alone destroy it. Whatever is created, everything will certainly be destroyed!"

*tasmāttvamuttiṣṭha yaśō labhasva jitvā śatrūn bhuṅkśva rājyaṁ samṛddham ।*
*mayaivaitē nihatāḥ pūrvamēva nimittamātraṁ bhava savyasācin ॥ 11-33॥*

"Therefore—arise! Win glory and enjoy the kingdom, having conquered the enemy. They have all already been slain by Me. O Savyasachin!⁴ You are merely an instrument!"

Whoever is born, from the very moment of birth is destroyed by Time. Whether he meets death at someone's hands in war or under other circumstances, he dies by the will of Time. The killer is

⁴"Skilled archer"

**231**
**Chapter 11**

merely an instrument of Time. And even if no one kills him, death at the end of life is inevitable for everyone. All beings, from their very birth, are already slain by Time.

*drōṇaṁ ca bhīṣmaṁ ca jayadrathaṁ ca karṇaṁ tathānyānapi yōdhavīrān ।*
*mayā hatāṁstvaṁ jahi mā vyathiṣṭhā yudhyasva jētāsi raṇē sapatnān ॥ 11-34॥*

"Strike down Bhishma, Drona, Jayadratha, and Karna, as well as many other heroic warriors, who have already been slain by Me. Do not waver; you shall overcome your rivals in battle!"''

*sañjaya uvāca*
*ētacchrutvā vacanaṁ kēśavasya kṛtāñjalirvēpamānaḥ kirīṭī ।*
*namaskṛtvā bhūya ēvāha kṛṣṇaṁ sagadgadaṁ bhītabhītaḥ praṇamya ॥ 11-35॥*

Sanjaya said:
"Hearing this speech of Keshava, Kiriti bowed in fear and, trembling, with folded hands, spoke to Lord Shri Krishna, his voice choked, bowing again and again in great terror."

Having surrendered to Time, the great man who is conscious of Time, receiving by His grace the direct darshan of Time, observes in fear the terrifying scene of the absorption of all worlds by Time and beseeches Time.

**232**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*arjuna uvāca*
*sthānē hṛṣīkēśa tava prakīrtyā jagatprahṛṣyatyanurajyatē ca ।*
*rakśānsi bhītāni diśō dravanti sarvē namasyanti ca siddhasaṅghāḥ ॥ 11-36॥*

Arjuna said:
"O Hrishikesha! Truly the whole world rejoices, glorifying You in adoration! The rakshasas flee in terror in all directions, while the hosts of the righteous bow before You."

"O Parameshvara, only You and You alone exist in this world. The entire universe trembles under Your influence. You fill all beings with life! Ordinary people, concerned only with preserving their own lives, scatter in confusion and terror, but they will not escape nonetheless. Those who know You bow only before You!"

*kasmācca tē na namēranmahātman garīyasē brahmaṇō’pyādikartrē ।*
*ananta dēvēśa jagannivāsa tvamakśaraṁ sadasattatparaṁ yat ॥ 11-37॥*

O Mahatma, how could they not bow before You, the Creator of Brahma Himself and the greatest among all? For, O Limitless One, O Lord of all gods, O Abode of the Universe, all that is manifest, unmanifest, and even that which is beyond—all this are You.

"O Mahakala! You surpass the infinity that manifests infinity! Who here would not acknowledge Your supremacy? You are Infinite Time! Although You pervade everything in this world, You continue to abide outside it. Awakened consciousness and sleeping consciousness are merely Your inventions. O Endless One, You are That Supreme Indestructible!"

**233**
**Chapter 11**

*tvamādidēvaḥ puruṣaḥ purāṇastvamasya viśvasya paraṁ nidhānam ।*
*vēttāsi vēdyaṁ ca paraṁ ca dhāma tvayā tataṁ viśvamanantarūpa ॥ 11-38॥*

You are the primal Lord, the Eternal Purusha. You are the supreme Support of this universe, the knower, the knowable, and the ultimate goal. O Infinite One, the entire world is filled with You alone.

"You are the Beginning of all beginnings, the Eternal Purusha! You are the Guardian of this world! You are everything: the aspiration for knowledge, the process of knowledge, and true knowledge!"

*vāyuryamō’gnirvaruṇaḥ śaśāṅkaḥ prajāpatistvaṁ prapitāmahaśca ।*
*namō namastē’stu sahasrakṛtvaḥ punaśca bhūyō’pi namō namastē ॥ 11-39॥*

You are Vayu, Yama, Agni, Varuna, the Moon, Prajapati, and the great progenitor. I bow before You a thousand times, I bow before You again and again, once more and yet again.

"O Kala! You are manifest in the form of air; You Yourself are Death, as well as the god of death, Yamaraja! You are Agni, Varuna, the Moon, and the Lord of all people! You are the Father of the forefather! I bow before You a thousand times! Again and again I bow before You!"

*namaḥ purastādatha pṛṣṭhatastē namō’stu tē sarvata ēva sarvа ।*
*anantavīryāmitavikramastvaṁ sarvaṁ samāpnōṣi tatō’si sarvaḥ ॥ 11-40॥*

Salutations to You from the front and from behind! I bow before You from all sides! You are the infinitely omnipotent Lord. You fill the entire world with Yourself; You are the true nature of everything.

"O unbearably radiant Time! I bow before You in the past and the future! I bow before You always, in all

**234**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

times! Your power is infinite! You contain this entire world within Yourself! Everywhere—You and only You!"

*sakhēti matvā prasabhaṁ yaduktaṁ hē kṛṣṇa hē yādava hē sakhēti ।*
*ajānatā mahimānaṁ tavēdaṁ mayā pramādātpraṇayēna vāpi ॥ 11-41॥*
*yaccāvahāsārthamasatkṛtō’si vihāraśayyāsanabhōjanēṣu ।*
*ēkō’thavāpyacyuta tatsamakśaṁ tatkśāmayē tvāmahamapramēyam ॥ 11-42॥*

"But if, not knowing Your greatness, out of friendship I addressed You carelessly: 'Hey Krishna, hey Yadava, hey friend,'—if I offended You in private or in public, in moments of merriment, while sitting, wandering, or resting, I beg You, forgive me all such transgressions, O Indestructible One!"

"O Parameshvara! I beg You, forgive me for everything I have spoken about inexhaustible Time, not knowing Its greatness, out of arrogance or in a surge of emotion, in private or in public!"

*pitāsi lōkasya carācarasya tvamasya pūjyaśca gururgarīyān ।*
*na tvatsamō’styabhyadhikaḥ kutō’nyō lōkatrayē’pyapratimaprabhāva ॥ 11-43॥*

You are the Father of this moving and unmoving world, the supreme Guru of all teachers. In all three worlds there is no one who can compare with Your unparalleled greatness, and no one can be found who surpasses You.

"You are the Father of the entire world, the Guru among gurus, the most worshipful! All three worlds are manifested by You alone! Not one of Your manifestations can even come close to comparing with You!"

**235**
**Chapter 11**

*tasmātpraṇamya praṇidhāya kāyaṁ prasādayē tvāmahamīśamīḍyam ।*
*pitēva putrasya sakhēva sakhyuḥ priyaḥ priyāyārhasi dēva sōḍhum ॥ 11-44॥*

I bow with reverence before You and, prostrating myself, beg You for grace. O Lord! Pour out upon me the love that a father feels for his son, that friends feel for each other, and that a lover feels for his beloved.

"O Mahakala! O Unbearable Radiance! Kindling the fire of yoga, I offer You my life! O Ishvara! Reward me for this, pour out Your love upon me, love me as a father loves his son, as a friend loves a friend, and as one consumed with love loves his beloved!"

*adṛṣṭapūrvaṁ hṛṣitōsmi dṛṣṭvā bhayēna ca pravyathitaṁ manō mē ।*
*tadēva mē darśaya dēva rūpaṁ prasīda dēvēśa jagannivāsa ॥ 11-45॥*

I rejoice, having beheld what was never seen before. At the same time, my mind is overcome with confusion and terror. I pray, show me Your former divine form. O Lord of gods! O Abode of the Universe! I pray, be gracious!

"I am delighted and at the same time terrified at the sight of such a terrible radiance of that unbearably bright and fearsome manifestation of Yours! O Lord! I pray, show me that form of Yours which is beautiful! O Guardian of the world! I pray, be gracious! Grant me this reward!"

236  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
किरीटिनं गदिनं चक्रहस्तमिच्छामि त्वां द्रष्टुमहं तथैव ।  
तेनैव रूपेण चतुर्भुजेन सहस्रबाहो भव विश्वमूर्ते ॥११- ४६॥  
kirīṭinaṁ gadinaṁ cakrahastamicchāmi tvāṁ draṣṭumahaṁ tathaiva ।  
tēnaiva rūpēṇa caturbhujēna sahasrabāhō bhava viśvamūrtē ॥ 11-46॥  

“I desire to see You crowned, with scepter and disc in hand. O Thousand-armed One! O Universal Form! Reveal to me Your four-armed form.”  

“Before beholding this terrifying, radiant form, I contemplated Your image, crowned, with scepter and chakra in Your hands. I pray, reveal to me again that form of Yours! O Indivisible One! O possessor of a thousand arms, unmanifestly present throughout all creation! I pray, reveal to me once more that beautiful four-armed form of Yours which I contemplated in my mind after the piercing of Hridaya-granthi!”  

श्रीभगवानुवाच  
मया प्रसन्नेन तवार्जुनेदं रूपं परं दर्शितमात्मयोगात् ।  
तेजोमयं विश्वमनन्तमाद्यं यन्मे त्वदन्येन न दृष्टपूर्वम् ॥११- ४७॥  
śrībhagavānuvāca  
mayā prasannēna tavārjunēdaṁ rūpaṁ paraṁ darśitamātmayōgāt ।  
tējōmayaṁ viśvamanantamādyaṁ yanmē tvadanyēna na dṛṣṭapūrvam ॥ 11-47॥  

The Lord said:  
“O Arjuna! By My grace and the power of My yoga, you have beheld this unbearably radiant, Supreme Universal Form, which has no beginning or end, and which no one other than you has ever seen before.”  

Hearing this plea of the yogi, Time, who had known of it from the very beginning, having already shown that Form of His which cannot be seen without the successful completion of the final stage of this ancient yoga, once again manifests that four-armed form of Vāsudeva, which can be contemplated only by yogis established in the consciousness of the Void.  

☝  
☝  

237  
Chapter 11  
न वेदयज्ञाध्ययनैर्न दानैर्न च क्रियाभिर्न तपोभिरुग्रैः ।  
एवंरूपः शक्य अहं नृलोके द्रष्टुं त्वदन्येन कुरुप्रवीर ॥११- ४८॥  
na vēdayajñādhyayanairna dānairna ca kriyābhirna tapōbhirugraiḥ ।  
ēvanrūpaḥ śakya ahaṁ nṛlōkē draṣṭuṁ tvadanyēna kurupravīra ॥ 11-48॥  

“O Kuru-pravīra! No one in this mortal world is able to behold Me thus—neither by study of the Vedas, nor by performing sacrifices, nor by the path of charity, nor by performing rituals, nor through severe austerities.”  

In this world of mortals, it is impossible to know the terrifyingly radiant form of Time by performing the sacrificial rites described in the sacred scriptures, by mere study of the Vedas, by charity, by Vedic rituals, or by severe austerities. Only those who, by diligent practice, have passed through all the stages of this ancient yoga, can behold this immeasurable Form with the blessing of Time Himself.  

मा ते व्यथा मा च विमूढभावो दृष्ट्वा रूपं घोरमीदृङ्ममेदम् ।  
व्यपेतभीः प्रीतमनाः पुनस्त्वं तदेव मे रूपमिदं प्रपश्य ॥११- ४९॥  
mā tē vyathā mā ca vimūḍhabhāvō dṛṣṭvā rūpaṁ ghōramīdṛṅmamēdam ।  
vyapētabhīḥ prītamanāḥ punastvaṁ tadēva mē rūpamidaṁ prapaśya ॥ 11-49॥  

“Let not the sight of this terrifying Form disturb you; be fearless and peaceful, and again behold My former aspect.”  

To calm the frightened yogi, overwhelmed and stunned by the sight of the unbearably radiant form of Time, Mahākāla once again bestows the enchanting darśana of His most beautiful four-armed form of Vāsudeva.  

5 “Best of the Kurus”  
☝  
☝  

238  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
सञ्जय उवाच  
इत्यर्जुनं वासुदेवस्तथोक्त्वा स्वकं रूपं दर्शयामास भूयः ।  
आश्वासयामास च भीतमेनं भूत्वा पुनः सौम्यवपुर्महात्मा ॥११- ५०॥  
sañjaya uvāca  
ityarjunaṁ vāsudēvastathōktvā svakaṁ rūpaṁ darśayāmāsa bhūyaḥ ।  
āśvāsayāmāsa ca bhītamēnaṁ bhūtvā punaḥ saumyavapurmahātmā ॥ 11-50॥  

Sañjaya said:  
“Having spoken thus to Arjuna, Vāsudeva again assumed His beautiful form and encouraged him, who was stricken with fear.”  

The yogi, struck with fear at the sight of the terrifying, unbearably radiant form of Time, is freed from fear and regains peace by contemplating the most beautiful, luminous four-armed embodiment of Time, called Vāsudeva by the wise because of His presence in the heart of every being.  

अर्जुन उवाच  
दृष्ट्वेदं मानुषं रूपं तव सौम्यं जनार्दन ।  
इदानीमस्मि संवृत्तः सचेताः प्रकृतिं गतः ॥११- ५१॥  
arjuna uvāca  
dṛṣṭvēdaṁ mānuṣaṁ rūpaṁ tava saumyaṁ janārdana ।  
idānīmasmi saṁvṛttaḥ sacētāḥ prakṛtiṁ gataḥ ॥ 11-51॥  

Arjuna said:  
“O Janārdana! Beholding Your beautiful human form, I have regained my spirit and am fully composed.”  

After contemplating Vāsudeva, the most beautiful and auspicious four-armed human embodiment of that terrifying Time, the perfected yogi attains peace, established within himself.  

☝  
☝  

239  
Chapter 11  
श्रीभगवानुवाच  
सुदुर्दर्शमिदं रूपं दृष्टवानसि यन्मम ।  
देवा अप्यस्य रूपस्य नित्यं दर्शनकाङ्क्षिणः ॥११- ५२॥  
śrībhagavānuvāca  
sudurdarśamidaṁ rūpaṁ dṛṣṭavānasi yanmama ।  
dēvā apyasya rūpasya nityaṁ darśanakāṅkśiṇaḥ ॥ 11-52॥  

The Lord said:  
“To behold that Form of Mine which you have seen is an exceptional achievement. Even the gods constantly yearn to see It.”  

To have the ability to contemplate the terrifying, unbearably radiant, immeasurable form of Time is an exceptional achievement, as is the ability to see His beautiful four-armed embodiment. When yogis, through diligent practice, attain the level of Hridaya-granthi-bheda, they directly perceive the auspicious and enchanting four-armed embodiment of Time, radiant and beautiful.  

नाहं वेदैर्न तपसा न दानेन न चेज्यया ।  
शक्य एवंविधो द्रष्टुं दृष्टवानसि मां यथा ॥११- ५३॥  
nāhaṁ vēdairna tapasā na dānēna na cējyayā ।  
śakya ēvanvidhō draṣṭuṁ dṛṣṭavānasi māṁ yathā ॥ 11-53॥  

“That Form of Mine which you have beheld cannot be seen by studying the Vedas, nor by performing austerities, nor by the power of giving or sacrifice.”  

The unmanifest Parameśvara, in His terrifying, radiant form, as well as in His incredibly enchanting four-armed human aspect, cannot be comprehended by means of sacred scriptures, Vedic sacrifices, charity, or even by forcible restraint of the senses. This divine form of Vāsudeva, who dwells in the mind of everyone, can be perceived only by those great men, resolute in attaining samādhi, who have advanced far in the practice of the second stage of this ancient yoga. By knowing the true nature of Time with His blessing, through diligent practice of the third stage of yoga, they obtain the ability to directly contemplate the unbearably radiant, boundless form of Time, which fills the consciousness of the Void.  

☝  
☝  

240  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
भक्त्या त्वनन्यया शक्य अहमेवंविधोऽर्जुन ।  
ज्ञातुं द्रष्टुं च तत्त्वेन प्रवेष्टुं च परंतप ॥११- ५४॥  
bhaktyā tvananyayā śakya ahamēvaṁvidhō’rjuna ।  
jñātuṁ draṣṭuṁ ca tattvēna pravēṣṭuṁ ca parantapa ॥ 11-54॥  

“O Parantapa! Only by undivided devotion to Me is it possible to truly behold Me, to know My nature, and to undoubtedly attain Me.”  

Those great yogis who receive the direct darśana of Vāsudeva, who dwells in the mind of everyone, having become established in the consciousness of the Void through diligent practice of yoga, become His devoted followers. Such great yogis concentrate all the immeasurable consciousness of their awakened mind upon the consciousness of Time, which fills the Conscious Void, and thus, knowing His true nature, they are able to directly perceive the terrifying, unbearable radiance of Time. Such great men become conscious of Time and attain unity with Time.  

मत्कर्मकृन्मत्परमो मद्भक्तः सङ्गवर्जितः ।  
निर्वैरः सर्वभूतेषु यः स मामेति पाण्डव ॥११- ५५॥  
matkarmakṛnmatparamō madbhaktaḥ saṅgavarjitaḥ ।  
nirvairaḥ sarvabhūtēṣu yaḥ sa māmēti pāṇḍava ॥ 11-55॥  

“O Pāṇḍava! He who performs his actions for My sake alone, who relies solely on Me, remaining devoted to Me, without attachment, with a heart free from enmity towards all beings, undoubtedly attains Me.”  

The great man who is conscious of Time, concentrating all his boundless consciousness on Time, receives His direct darśana and thus becomes ardently devoted to Paramātman, to Time Himself. Observing all beings as His manifestations, he sees no difference between them and himself. Such a great man remains eternally devoted to Time. Being a follower of Time, performing all actions by the will of Time Himself, he becomes united with the Light of all lights, the unbearably radiant Time.  

The images of Lord Viṣṇu and His incarnations, Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa, Lord Śiva and Durgā, Kālī and other goddesses and gods, which can be found throughout India, are not merely products of imagination. In reality, they are what great men were able to perceive directly, having obtained the ability to contemplate Vāsudeva, who dwells in the heart of everyone, and subsequently the immeasurable, unbearably radiant, terrifying form of Time, through their diligent practice of yoga. Thus, the ancient sages attempted to leave an evident hint of the unmanifest Time, Parameśvara, so that an ordinary person, seeing these divine images symbolizing Time, might understand this clue and be inspired to know the true nature of Time.  

Those who are mired in empty debates about the formless and the formed do not realize that the images of deities are direct pointers to that unmanifest Time. They were established as symbols by great self-realized men out of compassion for the ordinary person.  

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे  
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे विश्वरूपदर्शनयोगो नामैकादशोऽध्यायः ॥ ११ ॥  
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē  
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē viśvarūpadarśanayōgō nāmaikādaśō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 11॥  

Om Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the eleventh chapter, entitled “The Yoga of the Vision of the Universal Form,” of the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which treats of the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.  

द्वादशोऽध्यायः भक्तियोगः  
dvādaśō’dhyāyaḥ bhaktiyōgaḥ  
Chapter 12  
THE YOGA OF SUPREME  
DEVOTION  

244  
अर्जुन उवाच  
एवं सततयुक्ता ये भक्तास्त्वां पर्युपासते ।  
ये चाप्यक्षरमव्यक्तं तेषां के योगवित्तमाः ॥१२- १॥  
arjuna uvāca  
ēvaṁ satatayuktā yē bhaktāstvāṁ paryupāsatē ।  
yē cāpyakśaramavyaktaṁ tēṣāṁ kē yōgavittamāḥ ॥ 12-1॥  

Arjuna said:  
“Who possesses the highest wisdom: those who worship You, or those who worship only the Unmanifest and the Imperishable?”  

Great men who have awakened the boundlessness of their mind and become established in the consciousness of the Void, upon piercing Hridaya-granthi, receive the direct darśana of Vāsudeva, who dwells in the mind of everyone. Some of them subsequently perceive the unbearably radiant, boundless, and terrifying form of Time, becoming conscious of Time with the blessing of Time Himself. Which of these sages, who have completed various stages of this ancient yoga, is greater?  

☝  
ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय  
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya  
Om Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya  

245  
Chapter 12  
श्रीभगवानुवाच  
मय्यावेश्य मनो ये मां नित्ययुक्ता उपासते ।  
श्रद्धया परयोपेतास्ते मे युक्ततमा मताः ॥१२- २॥  
śrībhagavānuvāca  
mayyāvēśya manō yē māṁ nityayuktā upāsatē ।  
śraddhayā parayōpētāstē mē yuktatamā matāḥ ॥ 12-2॥  

The Lord said:  
“Yogis who always worship Me, having fixed their mind on Me, endowed with supreme faith, are considered perfect.”  

Those great men who complete the practice of the second stage of this ancient yoga and become established in the consciousness of the Void receive the direct darśana of the radiant, incredibly beautiful four-armed human form of Vāsudeva. Such great men are preeminent among sādhakas.  

ये त्वक्षरमनिर्देश्यमव्यक्तं पर्युपासते ।  
सर्वत्रगमचिन्त्यं च कूटस्थमचलं ध्रुवम् ॥१२- ३॥  
संनियम्येन्द्रियग्रामं सर्वत्र समबुद्धयः ।  
ते प्राप्नुवन्ति मामेव सर्वभूतहिते रताः ॥१२- ४॥  
yē tvakśaramanirdēśyamavyaktaṁ paryupāsatē ।  
sarvatragamacintyaṁ ca kūṭasthamacalaṁ dhruvam ॥ 12-3॥  
saṁniyamyēndriyagrāmaṁ sarvatra samabuddhayaḥ ।  
tē prāpnuvanti māmēva sarvabhūtahitē ratāḥ ॥ 12-4॥  

“Those who are equal towards all and devoted to the welfare of all beings, who develop proper control over all the sense organs, and who worship the Secret, the All-pervading, the Kūṭastha, the Ever-Immovable, the Unmoving, the Unmanifest, and the Imperishable, truly attain Me.”
