Great yogis, transcending the limitations of the body, awaken the full consciousness of their mind and become established in the consciousness of the Void. Thereafter, they concentrate their awakened, boundless consciousness on that Truth of truths, which fills

**246**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

...contemplating the Void, and they receive the direct *darshan* of the Radiance of all radiance, the all-pervading, infinite *Kutastha*. Such yogis come to know His true nature, become imbued with devotion to Him, and, uniting with this great, radiant Time, themselves become like the soul of the entire world. Such great people are known as great souls who have realized *Kutastha*.

क्लेशोऽधिकतरस्तेषामव्यक्तासक्तचेतसाम् ।
अव्यक्ता हि गतिर्दुःखं देहवद्भिरवाप्यते ॥१२- ५॥
*klēśō’dhikatarastēṣāmavyaktāsaktacētasām ।*
*avyaktā hi gatirduḥkhaṁ dēhavadbhiravāpyatē ॥ 12-5॥*

The most arduous work awaits one who strives for the Unmanifest, for the hidden goal is difficult for the embodied to attain.

Striving to obtain the direct *darshan* of the immeasurable, radiant form of Time, great people diligently perform the practice of yoga. Freed from physical limitations, these yogis understand the full power of the practice, which helps awaken their dormant consciousness.

For ordinary people, whose intellect is limited by physical boundaries and who cannot even conceive of the Unmanifest, this ancient yoga, which leads to great results, is a painful ordeal.

ये तु सर्वाणि कर्माणि मयि संन्यस्य मत्पराः ।
अनन्येनैव योगेन मां ध्यायन्त उपासते ॥१२- ६॥
*yē tu sarvāṇi karmāṇi mayi saṁnyasya matparāḥ ।*
*ananyēnaiva yōgēna māṁ dhyāyanta upāsatē ॥ 12-6॥*

He who has renounced all his karma for My sake and found refuge in Me, constantly meditating on Me, worships Me alone with undivided devotion.

Great people who have transcended the level of *Hridaya-granthi-bheda*,

☝
☝

**247**
**Chapter 12**

practicing this ancient yoga, receive the direct *darshan* of the radiant, four-armed human incarnation of Vasudeva. Completely immersed in contemplation of Him, knowing death and renouncing all their desires, they attain the realization of Time.

तेषामहं समुद्धर्ता मृत्युसंसारसागरात् ।
भवामि नचिरात्पार्थ मय्यावेशितचेतसाम् ॥१२- ७॥
*tēṣāmahaṁ samuddhartā mṛtyusaṁsārasāgarāt ।*
*bhavāmi nacirātpārtha mayyāvēśitacētasām ॥ 12-7॥*

O Partha! Those whose minds are absorbed in Me, I swiftly deliver from this ocean of births and deaths.

The great *sthitaprajna*, devotees of Time, concentrate their consciousness on the consciousness of Time, which fills the Conscious Void. Thus, knowing the true nature of Time, they are freed from all their fears by the grace of the radiant Time. Fearless, they observe everywhere the play of Time itself and become established in That Unmanifest Eternal Truth.

मय्येव मन आधत्स्व मयि बुद्धिं निवेशय ।
निवसिष्यसि मय्येव अत ऊर्ध्वं न संशयः ॥१२- ८॥
*mayyēva mana ādhatsva mayi buddhiṁ nivēśaya ।*
*nivasiṣyasi mayyēva ata ūrdhvaṁ na sanśayaḥ ॥ 12-8॥*

Fix your mind on Me, direct your intellect to Me; then you shall dwell in Me alone – of this there is no doubt.

Great people know the true nature of Time by concentrating the entire boundlessness of their awakened mind on the consciousness of Time. Observing Time in the entire universe, they abide in Time itself. Such Time-conscious great souls overcome death by yogic power at the end of their lives and become established in immortality, attaining unity with Time.

☝
☝

**248**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

अथ चित्तं समाधातुं न शक्नोषि मयि स्थिरम् ।
अभ्यासयोगेन ततो मामिच्छाप्तुं धनंजय ॥१२- ९॥
*atha cittaṁ samādhātuṁ na śaknōṣi mayi sthiram ।*
*abhyāsayōgēna tatō māmicchāptuṁ dhanaṁjaya ॥ 12-9॥*

O Dhananjaya! If you cannot steadily fix your mind on Me [in Samadhi], then strive to attain Me through the practice of yoga [Abhyasa].

Great yogis who have not been able to realize Time, but who ardently desire to obtain the direct *darshan* of That unbearably radiant Infinity, having passed through *Hridaya-granthi*, continue to diligently perform the practice of the third stage of this ancient yoga.

अभ्यासेऽप्यसमर्थोऽसि मत्कर्मपरमो भव ।
मदर्थमपि कर्माणि कुर्वन्सिद्धिमवाप्स्यसि ॥१२- १०॥
*abhyāsē’pyasamarthō’si matkarmaparamō bhava ।*
*madarthamapi karmāṇi kurvansiddhimavāpsyasi ॥ 12-10॥*

If you are incapable even of practice, then accustom yourself to dedicating your actions to Me. Even performing karma for My sake, you shall attain perfection.

It happens that a yogi is unable to obtain the direct *darshan* of the radiant, immeasurable form of Time by performing the practice of the final stage of yoga in his current life. Even then, having already attained the level of *Hridaya-granthi-bheda* and being established in the consciousness of the unmanifest Void, he abides content within himself, directly contemplating Vasudeva, who dwells in the heart of every being.

अथैतदप्यशक्तोऽसि कर्तुं मद्योगमाश्रितः ।
सर्वकर्मफलत्यागं ततः कुरु यतात्मवान् ॥१२- ११॥
*athaitadapyaśaktō’si kartuṁ madyōgamāśritaḥ ।*
*sarvakarmaphalatyāgaṁ tataḥ kuru yatātmavān ॥ 12-11॥*

If you are incapable even of this, then be devoted to Me, established in yourself and renouncing the fruits of karma.

☝
☝

**249**
**Chapter 12**

If a yogi is unable to attain even *Hridaya-granthi-bheda*, to become established through it in the consciousness of the Void, and to receive the *darshan* of the four-armed form of Vasudeva, even then, through his diligent practice, he becomes dispassionate and learns of the boundlessness of his own mind. He rises above physical limitations and continues, through diligent practice, to strive for the attainment of *Hridaya-granthi-bheda*.

श्रेयो हि ज्ञानमभ्यासाज्ज्ञानाद्ध्यानं विशिष्यते ।
ध्यानात्कर्मफलत्यागस्त्यागाच्छान्तिरनन्तरम् ॥१२- १२॥
*śrēyō hi jñānamabhyāsājjñānāddhyānaṁ viśiṣyatē ।*
*dhyānātkarmaphalatyāgastyāgācchāntiranantaram ॥ 12-12॥*

Wisdom [Jnana] surpasses practice [Abhyasa]; contemplation [Dhyana] is superior to wisdom; and renunciation of the fruits of karma [Tyaga] surpasses contemplation. Renunciation gives immediate peace.

Wisdom comes with the awakening of the consciousness of the mind through the practice of yoga. The attainment of knowledge of That Infinite Truth and the experience of the *darshan* of Vasudeva leads to constant contemplation of Him. Through *dhyana*, the yogi becomes dispassionate and, as a result, rises above the desire for the fruits of karma. Such a great person lives in peace.

अद्वेष्टा सर्वभूतानां मैत्रः करुण एव च ।
निर्ममो निरहंकारः समदुःखसुखः क्षमी ॥१२- १३॥
*advēṣṭā sarvabhūtānāṁ maitraḥ karuṇa ēva ca ।*
*nirmamō nirahaṁkāraḥ samaduḥkhasukhaḥ kśamī ॥ 12-13॥*

He who is friendly, filled with compassion, and bears envy towards none, who has no sense of ownership or limitation of ego, who remains equanimous in happiness and sorrow,

A great person in the state of supreme peace sees himself and all beings as manifestations of the boundless, unmanifest Time. Despite having already freed himself from the sense of ownership, such a person is full of friendliness and compassion

☝
☝
☝

**250**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

towards all beings. Having overcome his physical boundaries, he does not cherish his ego with regard to the body. Understanding the relativity of happiness and sorrow, the great person rises above them and always abides in equanimity.

संतुष्टः सततं योगी यतात्मा दृढनिश्चयः ।
मय्यर्पितमनोबुद्धिर्यो मद्भक्तः स मे प्रियः ॥१२- १४॥
*saṁtuṣṭaḥ satataṁ yōgī yatātmā dṛḍhaniścayaḥ ।*
*mayyarpitamanōbuddhiryō madbhaktaḥ sa mē priyaḥ ॥ 12-14॥*

Always abiding in contentment, self-controlled, and firm in resolve, having fixed his mind and intellect on Me – such a devotee of Mine is dear to Me.

Transcending physical limitations through valiant practice, the great yogi becomes established in the consciousness of the Void and concentrates all his awakened, boundless consciousness on the unmanifest, indestructible Supreme Time. Having surrendered to Time and receiving the direct *darshan* of This unbearably radiant Infinity, he becomes dear to Time and therefore becomes dear to himself.

यस्मान्नोद्विजते लोको लोकान्नोद्विजते च यः ।
हर्षामर्षभयोद्वेगैर्मुक्तो यः स च मे प्रियः ॥१२- १५॥
*yasmānnōdvijatē lōkō lōkānnōdvijatē ca yaḥ ।*
*harṣāmarṣabhayōdvēgairmuktō yaḥ sa ca mē priyaḥ ॥ 12-15॥*

He who causes no distress to others and is not distressed himself, who is free from delight, envy, fear, anxiety, and other afflictions – that one is dear to Me.

Having attained unity with the entire universe, the great Time-conscious person causes no disturbance to anyone, and no one can disturb him. Nothing can enchant one who has already known all and observes himself in the entire universe, just as there are no causes for fear for such a sage. Such a great person unites with Time and becomes dear to himself.

☝
☝

**251**
**Chapter 12**

अनपेक्षः शुचिर्दक्ष उदासीनो गतव्यथः ।
सर्वारम्भपरित्यागी यो मद्भक्तः स मे प्रियः ॥१२- १६॥
*anapēkśaḥ śucirdakśa udāsīnō gatavyathaḥ ।*
*sarvārambhaparityāgī yō madbhaktaḥ sa mē priyaḥ ॥ 12-16॥*

He who depends on no one, is pure, skillful, detached, and serene, who has abandoned all his desires and surrendered to Me – that one is dear to Me.

A great person striving to know the unmanifest, eternal Time attains self-satisfaction by knowing Its true nature through diligent practice of yoga. Following this, all anxieties leave this great person. Such a sage, knowing Time, knows also everything existing in this universe, as well as beyond it. Having attained the goal of yogic practice and fulfilled all his desires, he overcomes the influence of karma and, uniting with Time, becomes dear to himself.

यो न हृष्यति न द्वेष्टि न शोचति न काङ्क्षति ।
शुभाशुभपरित्यागी भक्तिमान्यः स मे प्रियः ॥१२- १७॥
*yō na hṛṣyati na dvēṣṭi na śōcati na kāṅkśati ।*
*śubhāśubhaparityāgī bhaktimānyaḥ sa mē priyaḥ ॥ 12-17॥*

He who has transcended attraction and aversion, does not grieve nor desire, who has renounced both the auspicious and the inauspicious – such a devotee of Mine is dear to Me.

Such a great person desires nothing, for he has already attained everything. He is free from the influence of sensations such as delight, envy, the feeling of pleasant and unpleasant. Abiding in unity with Time, he himself is the embodiment of Time, and, devoted to himself, he becomes dear to himself.

☝
☝

**252**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

समः शत्रौ च मित्रे च तथा मानापमानयोः ।
शीतोष्णसुखदुःखेषु समः सङ्गविवर्जितः ॥१२- १८॥
*samaḥ śatrau ca mitrē ca tathā mānāpamānayōḥ ।*
*śītōṣṇasukhaduḥkhēṣu samaḥ saṅgavivarjitaḥ ॥ 12-18॥*

Impartial towards friends and foes, honour and dishonour, heat and cold, happiness and sorrow, abiding unattached,

A great Time-realized person attains unity with the entire universe. Being *Vishvatma*, he understands the relativity of such feelings as fame and disgrace, friendship and enmity, joy and sorrow, heat and cold. Abiding beyond these, he observes himself in the entire universe. Contemplating only himself in the whole universe, he himself becomes the manifestation of this Light of all light, the unmanifest, indestructible Brahman – Time.

तुल्यनिन्दास्तुतिर्मौनी सन्तुष्टो येन केनचित् ।
अनिकेतः स्थिरमतिर्भक्तिमान्मे प्रियो नरः ॥१२- १९॥
*tulyanindāstutirmaunī santuṣṭō yēna kēnacit ।*
*anikētaḥ sthiramatirbhaktimānmē priyō naraḥ ॥ 12-19॥*

He who sees no difference between blame and praise, who is silent, always content, attached to no abode, and of steady mind, devoted to Me – such a person is dear to Me.

A great person, contemplating himself in the entire universe, although he appears manifested, abides established in That Unmanifest which extends beyond the universe. Unwaveringly abiding in That unmanifest Immeasurability, such a great person becomes established in silence. Having already attained self-satisfaction, he becomes indifferent to fame and disgrace, blame and praise. For such a great, Time-conscious person, there is no particular place of abode in the world, for he has already united with the entire universe. He becomes exceedingly dear to the unmanifest Time, Parameshvara.

☝
☝

**253**
**Chapter 12**

*ye tu dharmyāmṛtamidaṁ yathōktaṁ paryupāsatē .
śraddadhānā matparamā bhaktāstē’tīva mē priyāḥ .. 12-20..*

“Filled with faith, devoted to Me, following the immortal wisdom of dharma that I have set forth, they are exceedingly dear to Me.”

Great men, firmly resolved to know the unmanifest Time, undertake the valiant practice of this ancient yoga in order to awaken their dormant, boundless consciousness. Through this, they attain self-realization, knowing the true nature of Time. Devoted to that Time, having surrendered themselves to Him, they know death through the body and become established in immortality, which is beyond death. Such great souls attain unity with the Light of all lights, the fearsome Time, and become exceedingly dear to Time itself.

*ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē bhaktiyōgō nāma dvādaśō’dhyāyaḥ .. 12..*

Om Tat Sat

Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the twelfth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Supreme Devotion,” of the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

☝

*trayōdaśō’dhyāyaḥ kśētrakśētrajñavibhāgayōgaḥ*

**Chapter 13**
**THE YOGA OF THE DISTINCTION BETWEEN THE FIELD AND THE KNOWER OF THE FIELD**

**256**

*śrībhagavānuvāca
idaṁ śarīraṁ kauntēya kśētramityabhidhīyatē .
ētadyō vētti taṁ prāhuḥ kśētrajña iti tadvidaḥ .. 13-1..*

The Lord said:
“O Kaunteya! This body is called the Field [Kṣetra]. He who knows it, the wise name the Knower of the Field [Kṣetrajña].”

This physical embodiment is the Field. The human mind, a manifestation of the indestructible Brahman, supported by this embodiment, is the Knower of the Field, which awakens its dormant capacities through the body. Great men, possessing a conception of the sleeping capacities of the mind and having sufficient resolve to awaken them, undertake the practice of this ancient yoga. Through practice, they rise above physical limitations and awaken their sleeping consciousness. Such great *sthitaprajña* indeed possess the knowledge of the Field and the Knower.

☝

*ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya*

Om Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya

**257**

**Chapter 13**

*kśētrajñaṁ cāpi māṁ viddhi sarvakśētrēṣu bhārata .
kśētrakśētrajñayōrjñānaṁ yattajjñānaṁ mataṁ mama .. 13-2..
tatkśētraṁ yacca yādṛkca yadvikāri yataśca yat .
sa ca yō yatprabhāvaśca tatsamāsēna mē śṛṇu .. 13-3..*

O Bhārata! Know Me alone as the Knower of all Fields. Only the knowledge of the Field and the Knower is true knowledge — such is My opinion. Now hear from Me in brief the description of the Field, Its nature and qualities, how It arose, and also of the Knower of that Field and His influence.

The body is the support of the mind and, therefore, being an instrument of the mind for obtaining experience and self-knowledge, is called Kṣetra. Now Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa describes the properties acquired by the body through birth, as well as the boundlessness of the mind, the creator of the body, which uses the body as a means of its manifestation.

*ṛṣibhirbahudhā gītaṁ chandōbhirvividhaiḥ pṛthak .
brahmasūtrapadaiścaiva hētumadbhirviniścitaiḥ .. 13-4..*

This knowledge has been sung in many ways and diversely by the sages and is described with particular fullness in the multi-significant verses of the Brahma Sūtra.

Being a manifestation of that indestructible, boundless Supreme Essence, Time, the human mind is also boundless. The great yogis of antiquity, who later came to be called ṛṣis, attempted to express the essence of the boundless mind and its creator, eternal Time, through various hymns and verses, known to us as the Vedas. They described that indestructible Brahman, Time, in symbolic form as the Brahma Sūtra for the sake of those seekers who would be ready to awaken their sleeping consciousness in order to understand these symbols.

☝

☝

**258**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

*mahābhūtānyahaṁkārō buddhiravyaktamēva ca .
indriyāṇi daśaikaṁ ca pañca cēndriyagōcarāḥ .. 13-5..*

The great elements, ahaṁkāra, intellect, and also the unmanifest, the ten organs of sense¹ together with the mind, and the objects of the five senses,

The boundlessness of the mind, the manifestation of the indestructible Brahman, Time, is embodied in this body. The five great elements (earth, water, fire, air, and ether) represent the five principal constituents of conscious Matter, serving as the main support for the manifestation of the universe, and they manifest to unite in the form of the body. The five organs of action are the main instruments of the mind for obtaining experience. The five organs of sense receive the five principal sensations through the following modes of perception: tactile, perception of form, taste, smell, and sound. The mind is the lord of these organs, being under the control of the intellect. The ego of ordinary people, limited by physical boundaries, and the boundless ego of yogis who have realized the boundlessness of the mind, united with the universe — all this abides in the body, and also outside it.

*icchā dvēṣaḥ sukhaṁ duḥkhaṁ saṁghātaścētanā dhṛtiḥ .
ētatkśētraṁ samāsēna savikāramudāhṛtam .. 13-6..*

Desire and aversion, happiness and sorrow, the aggregate of body and organs, consciousness, and dhṛti². Here is a brief description of the Field and Its qualities.

Ordinary people with limited intellect have a strong attachment to the body. In them, the desire to satisfy the sense organs prevails. This desire for sensory pleasures is itself the source of envy, joy, sorrow, and anger. Their consciousness, limited by physical boundaries, becomes the cause of accepting one birth after another. Such is the natural property of all embodied beings.

*amānitvamadambhitvamahiṁsā kśāntirārjavam .
ācāryōpāsanaṁ śaucaṁ sthairyamātmavinigrahaḥ .. 13-7..*

Humility and sincerity, non-violence, forbearance, simplicity, service to teachers, purity, steadfastness, and self-control,

A great man, by the practice of this ancient yoga awakening the sleeping capacities of his mind and, knowing its boundlessness, becoming established in the consciousness of Emptiness, knows the unmanifest truth of Time which fills It. Such a great man continues to abide in the body, while possessing a consciousness united with the entire universe. Seeing himself everywhere, he leaves the realm of pride and hypocrisy. Having attained an equal attitude towards all beings, he acquires fearlessness. Transcending violence, he radiates gentleness and utmost purity. His consciousness has expanded immeasurably; his intellect always remains steady. Having risen above physical limitations, he understands that the body, being a means for knowing the Unmanifest, is worthy of deep respect. He also understands what incredible grace his Guru has bestowed upon him by granting instruction in this ancient yoga, which, through self-knowledge, brings satisfaction within itself through practice.

¹Five organs of perception together with five organs of action
²“Resolve, willpower, self-control”

☝

**260**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

*indriyārthēṣu vairāgyamanahaṁkāra ēva ca .
janmamṛtyujarāvyādhiduḥkhadōṣānudarśanam .. 13-8..*

Indifference to the objects of the senses, absence of pride, the understanding that birth and death, old age and disease are inevitably accompanied by suffering,

Such a great man realizes the supremacy of the mind in the relationship of mind and body and transcends the limitations of the senses. Having realized the true nature of life, he becomes free from its allure. Having passed through death, such a great man has already known the nature of such misfortunes as birth and death, old age, disease, and all others that are experienced by ordinary people.

*asaktiranabhiṣvaṅgaḥ putradāragṛhādiṣu .
nityaṁ ca samacittatvamiṣṭāniṣṭōpapattiṣu .. 13-9..*

Detachment, non-attachment to son, wife, and home, equanimity in the face of pleasant and unpleasant events,

In the consciousness of great *sthitaprajña*, there is no place for possessive feelings towards spouse, children, relatives, and worldly wealth. They have already realized that unmanifest Time which gave birth to the entire universe. Those who have known This maintain balance everywhere and always remain established in equanimity.

☝

☝

**261**
**Chapter 13**

*mayi cānanyayōgēna bhaktiravyabhicāriṇī .
viviktadēśasēvitvamaratirjanasaṁsadi .. 13-10..*

Unwavering exclusive devotion to Me, a natural preference for living in a solitary place, and indifference to the company of people,

A great man makes a firm resolve to awaken his sleeping consciousness in order to know the true nature of Time. Then he diligently practices this ancient yoga on the path to achieving his goal. After passing through the Hṛdaya-granthi, he becomes established in the consciousness of boundless Emptiness and receives the direct darśana of the divine four-armed incarnation of Vāsudeva. Thus he becomes an exclusive devotee of Emptiness, and also of that truth of Time which fills It. Such great sages, being far above ordinary people in terms of consciousness, prefer to live in solitude.

*adhyātmajñānanityatvaṁ tattvajñānārthadarśanam .
ētajjñānamiti prōktamajñānaṁ yadató’nyathā .. 13-11..*

Constant self-knowledge, the realization of spiritual wisdom leading to the knowledge of Absolute Truth — all this I call knowledge. The opposite, know as ignorance.

This ancient yoga grants the direct experience of the Support of all supports, the great shining truth of Time, to those who practice it diligently. The passing through all stages of this yoga is called wisdom. In contrast, actions directed only towards obtaining sensory pleasures, which only strengthen physical limitations, are called ignorance.

☝

☝

**262**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

*jñēyaṁ yattatpravakśyāmi yajjñātvāmṛtamaśnutē .
anādi matparaṁ brahma na sattannāsadacyatē .. 13-12..*

Now I will tell you of That which is to be known. Those who know It attain immortality. That which is without beginning and lies beyond both the real and the unreal is called the Supreme Brahman.

Great men who have been able to lead their consciousness beyond physical limitations and become conscious of Time, concentrating their awakened consciousness on Time, become established in immortality, passing through death by means of the body. That great shining truth of Time, which abides beyond death, is indestructible and eternal, extending beyond both the real and the unreal.

*sarvataḥ pāṇipādaṁ tatsarvatō’kśiśirōmukham .
sarvataḥ śruti mallōkē sarvamāvṛtya tiṣṭhati .. 13-13..*

Everywhere are His hands and feet; everywhere His eyes, heads, mouths, and ears. That eternal Truth pervades the entire universe.

The yogi who has known the true nature of the ultimate, supreme, eternal unmanifest Time, the Light of all lights, in all Its boundlessness, attains unity with Him and becomes omniscient. His consciousness, merging with the consciousness of Time, fills all the gross and subtle worlds of this universe, as if he had eyes, mouths, hands, and feet everywhere.

☝

☝

**263**
**Chapter 13**

*सर्वेन्द्रियगुणाभासं सर्वेन्द्रियविवर्जितम् ।*
*असक्तं सर्वभृच्चैव निर्गुणं गुणभोक्तृ च ॥१३- १४॥*
*sarvēndriyaguṇābhāsaṁ sarvēndriyavivarjitam ।*
*asaktaṁ sarvabhṛccaiva nirguṇaṁ guṇabhōktṛ ca ॥ 13-14॥*

Perceiving all senses, yet not subject to them. Unattached, all-supporting, enjoying the guṇas, yet transcending them.

Such a great yogin, perfected, knowing the mind which is the support of all senses in all its vastness, becomes free from the power of the senses and is no longer enchanted by them. He becomes Nirguṇa, transcending all three guṇas. The consciousness of such a yogin, uniting with Time, appears as if manifest in the form of the entire world. For such a great person, there is no longer any difference between worldly pleasures and samādhi.

*बहिरन्तश्च भूतानामचरं चरमेव च ।*
*सूक्ष्मत्वात्तदविज्ञेयं दूरस्थं चान्तिके च तत् ॥१३- १५॥*
*bahirantaśca bhūtānāmacaraṁ caramēva ca ।*
*sūkśmatvāttadavijñēyaṁ dūrasthaṁ cāntikē ca tat ॥ 13-15॥*

He is within and outside all beings, He abides in eternal motion and at the same time is motionless. Being subtle, He is incomprehensible. Unmanifest, He abides near and yet far.

Great people who are conscious of Time have been able to comprehend that their limitless consciousness is the creator of all beings and, although present within them, at the same time abides outside them. It is both gross and subtle, and also That Unmanifest beyond the gross and subtle. Although to ordinary people It appears unreal, in reality It is the highest reality.

☝
☝

**264**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

*अविभक्तं च भूतेषु विभक्तमिव च स्थितम् ।*
*भूतभर्तृ च तज्ज्ञेयं ग्रसिष्णु प्रभविष्णु च ॥१३- १६॥*
*avibhaktaṁ ca bhūtēṣu vibhaktamiva ca sthitam ।*
*bhūtabhartṛ ca tajjñēyaṁ grasiṣṇu prabhaviṣṇu ca ॥ 13-16॥*

He is indivisible, yet appears divided among beings. He should be known as the Support of all living beings, the Destroyer and Creator of life.

Great people conscious of Time see how That Same Time manifests throughout the entire universe. Because of this, It appears as if divided, and although It is motionless, It seems to move. That truth of Time is the Creator of the whole world, its Protector and Destroyer.

*ज्योतिषामपि तज्ज्योतिस्तमसः परमुच्यते ।*
*ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं ज्ञानगम्यं हृदि सर्वस्य विष्ठितम् ॥१३- १७॥*
*jyōtiṣāmapi tajjyōtistamasaḥ paramucyatē ।*
*jñānaṁ jñēyaṁ jñānagamyaṁ hṛdi sarvasya viṣṭhitam ॥ 13-17॥*

He is the Light of all lights, He is described as beyond darkness. He is knowledge, the knowable, and That which is attained through knowledge. He abides in the mind of everyone.

The light of all lights, the unbearable radiant Time – the immortal Kūṭastha, to be perceived by overcoming the darkness of ignorance. Dwelling in the mind of both the wise and the ignorant, Vāsudeva is That Truth, realized by concentrating the entire limitlessness of the mind through awakening its dormant capacities.

*इति क्षेत्रं तथा ज्ञानं ज्ञेयं चोक्तं समासतः ।*
*मद्भक्त एतद्विज्ञाय मद्भावायोपपद्यते ॥१३- १८॥*
*iti kśētraṁ tathā jñānaṁ jñēyaṁ cōktaṁ samāsataḥ ।*
*madbhakta ētadvijñāya madbhāvāyōpapadyatē ॥ 13-18॥*

Thus is the brief description of the Field, knowledge, and the knowable. Realizing this, My devotee attains Me.

☝
☝

**265**
**Chapter 13**

Great people, having awakened their dormant consciousness and, through the body, having known infinity, concentrate all their limitless consciousness for the knowledge of Time. Such people attain unity with That Highest Truth, knowing It by means of Kṣetrajña, the mind abiding in the Kṣetra, the field of this body. Such yogīs are able to realize that this measureless Time is the cause of the manifestation of the immortal mind, as well as of Time Itself. Time also manifests the body. The visible properties of the body, which appears imperfect, are also manifestations of That Unmanifest.

*प्रकृतिं पुरुषं चैव विद्ध्यनादी उभावपि ।*
*विकारांश्च गुणांश्चैव विद्धि प्रकृतिसंभवान् ॥१३- १९॥*
*prakṛtiṁ puruṣaṁ caiva viddhyanādī ubhāvapi ।*
*vikārānśca guṇāṁścaiva viddhi prakṛtisambhavān ॥ 13-19॥*

Know that Prakṛti [Svabhāva] and Puruṣa are both beginningless; and know that all modifications and guṇas are born of Prakṛti.

The indestructible Brahman, Kāla, is called Prakṛti, because It manifests the entire universe, while Kṣetrajña, the mind knowing all its capacities through the body, is called Puruṣa.

*कार्यकरणकर्तृत्वे हेतुः प्रकृतिरुच्यते ।*
*पुरुषः सुखदुःखानां भोक्तृत्वे हेतुरुच्यते ॥१३- २०॥*
*पुरुषः प्रकृतिस्थो हि भुङ्‌क्ते प्रकृतिजान्गुणान् ।*
*कारणं गुणसङ्गोऽस्य सदसद्योनिजन्मसु ॥१३- २१॥*
*kāryakaraṇakartṛtvē hētuḥ prakṛtirucyatē ।*
*puruṣaḥ sukhaduḥkhānāṁ bhōktṛtvē hēturucyatē ॥ 13-20॥*
*puruṣaḥ prakṛtisthō hi bhuṅ‌ktē prakṛtijānguṇān ।*
*kāraṇaṁ guṇasaṅgō’sya sadasadyōnijanmasu ॥ 13-21॥*

Prakṛti is said to be the cause of effects and instruments, while Puruṣa is said to be the cause of experiencing various pleasures and pains, abiding in Prakṛti under the influence of the guṇas born of Prakṛti. The connection with the guṇas itself is the cause of births in good or evil wombs.

☝
☝

**266**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

The primordial nature of Time, which manifests the entire universe, is called Prakṛti. The measureless mind, manifested by Her, confines itself within a body for the purpose of self-knowledge and, with the help of this body, comprehends its full potential. Attaching itself to the sense organs, it experiences joy and sorrow, thus itself becoming the cause of the inevitability of new and new rebirths.

*उपद्रष्टानुमन्ता च भर्ता भोक्ता महेश्वरः ।*
*परमात्मेति चाप्युक्तो देहेऽस्मिन्पुरुषः परः ॥१३- २२॥*
*upadraṣṭānumantā ca bhartā bhōktā mahēśvaraḥ ।*
*paramātmēti cāpyuktō dēhē’sminpuruṣaḥ paraḥ ॥ 13-22॥*

The Witness, the Permitter, the Supporter, the Enjoyer, the Great Lord, and also called the Supreme Self – such is the Supreme Puruṣa in this body.

This limitless mind appears limited by the body, while at the same time abiding beyond it. Time, dwelling in the mind of everyone, encompasses both the limitation and the limitlessness of the mind. It manifests the body, sustains it, and then destroys it through death, all the while remaining outside it. Those who are able to independently comprehend their limitations, through diligent practice of yoga, attain limitlessness. Thus they reach the state of sthitaprajña, realizing the supreme Brahman, the soul of the Universal Soul – Paramātmā.

*य एवं वेत्ति पुरुषं प्रकृतिं च गुणैः सह ।*
*सर्वथा वर्तमानोऽपि न स भूयोऽभिजायते ॥१३- २३॥*
*ya ēvaṁ vētti puruṣaṁ prakṛtiṁ ca guṇaiḥ saha ।*
*sarvathā vartamānō’pi na sa bhūyō’bhijāyatē ॥ 13-23॥*

Those who know Puruṣa and Prakṛti together with Her guṇas are masters of themselves in all respects and are not born again.

The great yogī, having, through diligent practice of yoga, transcended physical limitations, abides in the consciousness of all-embracing

☝
☝
☝

**267**
**Chapter 13**

Emptiness. Thus, he is able to know the true essence of the primordial nature of Time. Blessed by Time, he receives Its direct darśana. Although he continues to perform his duties, inspiring ordinary people, such a sage is no longer bound by the necessity of taking a new birth.

*ध्यानेनात्मनि पश्यन्ति केचिदात्मानमात्मना ।*
*अन्ये सांख्येन योगेन कर्मयोगेन चापरे ॥१३- २४॥*
*dhyānēnātmani paśyanti kēcidātmānamātmanā ।*
*anyē sāṁkhyēna yōgēna karmayōgēna cāparē ॥ 13-24॥*

Some behold the Ātman within themselves through dhyāna. Others distinguish Him through Sāṅkhya, and still others see through the practice of yoga.

Great people, having independently awakened their own consciousness, concentrate it on the consciousness of Time and thus know His true nature.

Those who are unable to reach this level abide in the consciousness of Emptiness after passing through Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda. They receive the direct darśana of Vāsudeva and are able to constantly contemplate Him.

Others, unable to achieve even Hṛdaya-granthi-bheda, strive to awaken their dormant limitless consciousness through the practice of yoga and experience infinity, rising above physical limitations.

*अन्ये त्वेवमजानन्तः श्रुत्वान्येभ्य उपासते ।*
*तेऽपि चातितरन्त्येव मृत्युं श्रुतिपरायणाः ॥१३- २५॥*
*anyē tvēvamajānantaḥ śrutvānyēbhya upāsatē ।*
*tē’pi cātitarantyēva mṛtyuṁ śrutiparāyaṇāḥ ॥ 13-25॥*

Others, not possessing knowledge, worship, having heard of this from others. Devoted to listening, they too overcome death.

☝

**268**
**Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā**

One who yearns to awaken the dormant consciousness of his mind, through his aspiration to receive instruction in this ancient yoga, meets a great person who has realized Time. The great sage, who has known the true nature of the indestructible Brahman, bestows upon him instruction in this ancient practice. Listening about Time, he becomes exceedingly devoted to That Highest Truth. Such a person begins to ascend the steps of knowledge, practicing yoga. Freeing himself from the fear of death, he experiences his own limitlessness and becomes established in the infinity beyond death.

*यावत्संजायते किंचित्सत्त्वं स्थावरजङ्गमम् ।*
*क्षेत्रक्षेत्रज्ञसंयोगात्तद्विद्धि भरतर्षभ ॥१३- २६॥*
*yāvatsaṁjāyatē kiṁcitsattvaṁ sthāvarajaṅgamam ।*
*kśētrakśētrajñasaṁyōgāttadviddhi bharatarṣabha ॥ 13-26॥*

O best of the Bharatas! Know that all existence, moving and unmoving, in this world is born from the union of the Field and the Knower of the Field.

The great sthita-prajña realize that the entire universe, manifested by the supreme Brahman, Time, is embodied through the body and mind. When this Field of the body is cultivated by the intellect of the Knower with the plow of yogic practice and sown with the seeds of knowledge – the harvest of the mind's infinity, acquiring the knowledge of Time, springs forth.

*समं सर्वेषु भूतेषु तिष्ठन्तं परमेश्वरम् ।*
*विनश्यत्स्वविनश्यन्तं यः पश्यति स पश्यति ॥१३- २७॥*
*samaṁ sarvēṣu bhūtēṣu tiṣṭhantaṁ paramēśvaram ।*
*vinaśyatsvavinaśyantaṁ yaḥ paśyati sa paśyati ॥ 13-27॥*

He alone sees who contemplates the indestructible Parameśvara abiding undivided in all mortal beings. The great person realizes that this entire universe is a manifestation of the absolute reality of Time, Parameśvara,

☝
☝
☝

**269**
**Chapter 13**

who is its sole Creator and also Destroyer. Such a person conscious of Time sees Him everywhere. Only he who is able to contemplate This truly sees the truth.

*समं पश्यन्हि सर्वत्र समवस्थितमीश्वरम् ।*
*न हिनस्त्यात्मनात्मानं ततो याति परां गतिम् ॥१३- २८॥*
*samaṁ paśyanhi sarvatra samavasthitamīśvaram ।*
*na hinastyātmanātmānaṁ tatō yāti parāṁ gatim ॥ 13-28॥*

Contemplating Īśvara with equanimity, abiding equally everywhere, he does not destroy himself by his own hands and thus moves towards the supreme goal.

The great sthita-prajña knows himself through himself, thus also comprehending Īśvara who created him. Contemplating Him in the mind of every being and in the entire world, that great person always abides in equilibrium. Thus he attains unity with his Creator and reaches the supreme goal.

*प्रकृत्यैव च कर्माणि क्रियमाणानि सर्वशः ।*
*यः पश्यति तथात्मानमकर्तारं स पश्यति ॥१३- २९॥*
*prakṛtyaiva ca karmāṇi kriyamāṇāni sarvaśaḥ ।*
*yaḥ paśyati tathātmānamakartāraṁ sa paśyati ॥ 13-29॥*

He who sees that all actions are performed by Prakṛti alone, and contemplates the Self as non-doer – he alone truly sees.

The great person realizing Time recognizes all the natural qualities of Prakṛti, which arose from the Unmanifest, and distinguishes all actions of his body as being performed by the mind. Such a person is able to comprehend that Time, which manifests this entire world, abides unmanifest. It does everything, while doing nothing. Only one who has realized this is able to recognize That primordial Truth.

☝
☝

270  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
*yadā bhūtapṛthagbhāvamēkasthamanupaśyati*  
*tata ēva ca vistāraṁ brahma saṁpadyatē tadā* ॥ 13-30 ॥  

When all that appears divided is perceived as abiding in That and proceeding from That—at that time Brahman is realized.  

The great Time-conscious man cognizes the indestructible Time, the Light of every light, manifesting Itself in all the diversity of conscious Matter, embodying Itself in this universe. Having realized This, that great man attains unity with Time.  

*anāditvānnirguṇatvātparamātmāyamavyayaḥ*  
*śarīrasthō’pi kauntēya na karōti na lipyatē* ॥ 13-31 ॥  

O Kaunteya! That Supreme Being is free from the guṇas. The indestructible Paramātmā, though dwelling in the body, remains inactive beyond attachment.  

This unmanifest Time is eternal. It manifests all guṇas, but Itself abides beyond their sphere of influence. The entire universe is created and destroyed countless times, but that indestructible Time always exists. It is present in the body, yet is never limited by it. This Time does everything, while doing nothing.  

☝  
☝  

271  
Chapter 13  
*yathā sarvagataṁ saukśmyādākāśaṁ nōpalipyatē*  
*sarvatrāvasthitō dēhē tathātmā nōpalipyatē* ॥ 13-32 ॥  

Like space, which pervades everywhere but, being subtle, is bound by nothing, so too the Ātman, abiding in the body of each, remains unattached.  

The conscious Emptiness, containing within Itself and pervading all Matter, remains untouched by It. Despite Its all-pervading presence, sustaining all that is movable in the universe, It continues to abide beyond everything. Similarly, the Emptiness present in the body and the truth of Time that fills It remain outside the sphere of the body, as if simultaneously present within it yet not actually located there.  

*yathā prakāśayatyēkaḥ kṛtsnaṁ lōkamimaṁ raviḥ*  
*kśētraṁ kśētrī tathā kṛtsnaṁ prakāśayati bhārata* ॥ 13-33 ॥  

O Bhārata! As the single sun illumines this entire world, so does the light of the Knower illumine the entire Field.  

Just as the sun illumines the entire solar system, being the support of all life, the Kṣetrajña-mind bestows life upon the body-Kṣetra. The mind, the highest manifestation of the unmanifest, indestructible Brahman, of Time, is itself the embodiment of Time.  

☝  
☝  

272  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
*kśētrakśētrajñayōrēvamantaraṁ jñānacakśuṣā*  
*bhūtaprakṛtimōkśaṁ ca yē viduryānti tē param* ॥ 13-34 ॥  

Those who possess the eyes of wisdom see the difference between the Field and the Knower. They follow the path that leads all beings to the Supreme Goal from the bonds of existence.”  

Great men undertake diligent practice of yoga and thereby awaken their dormant infinite consciousness, rising above physical limitations. Such yogīs, established in the consciousness of Emptiness, cognize the true nature of Time that fills It. Having cognized all Matter manifested by Time, they realize the true nature of conscious Emptiness that contains It within Itself. Then they also cognize the all-pervading Time, the Creator of all, uniting with Time Itself.  

*ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē*  
*śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē kśētrakśētrajñavibhāgayōgō nāma trayōdaśō’dhyāyaḥ* ॥ 13 ॥  

Oṁ Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the thirteenth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of the Distinction between the Field and the Knower of the Field,” in the Upaniṣad of the Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which treats of the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.  

☝  

*caturdaśō’dhyāyaḥ guṇatrayavibhāgayōgaḥ*  
Chapter 14  
THE YOGA OF LIBERATION FROM THE THREE GUṆAS  

274  
*śrībhagavānuvāca*  
*paraṁ bhūyaḥ pravakśyāmi jñānānāṁ jñānamuttamam*  
*yajjñātvā munayaḥ sarvē parāṁ siddhimitō gatāḥ* ॥ 14-1 ॥  

The Lord said:  
“Now I shall again proclaim to you this supreme wisdom, the essence of all knowledge, having known which all sages have attained the highest perfection.”  

Now Lord Śrī Kṛṣṇa again speaks of the consciousness of Time, which can be realized through the practice of this ancient yoga, and of the stages of the manifestation of this consciousness. Of how the boundless mind, the embodiment of the indestructible Brahman, gradually confines itself within the body, so that by overcoming physical limitations it may attain liberation and, by cognizing death, unite with Time.  

☝  
*ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya*  
Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya  

275  
Chapter 14  
*idaṁ jñānamupāśritya mama sādharmyamāgatāḥ*  
*sargē’pi nōpajāyantē pralayē na vyathanti ca* ॥ 14-2 ॥  

Those who take refuge in this knowledge and attain My nature are not born again at the dawn of creation, nor are they distressed even at the dissolution of the universe.  

Those who perform the valiant practice of yoga become conscious of Time and cognize Its true nature, realizing all manifestations of Time. By cognizing death and freeing themselves from the fear of death, they unite with the consciousness of Time that fills the conscious Emptiness. Such great Time-conscious people are no longer bound by the obligation of birth; they are not distressed either during the manifestation of the universe or during its complete dissolution.  

*mama yōnirmahadbrahma tasmingarbhaṁ dadhāmyaham*  
*saṁbhavaḥ sarvabhūtānāṁ tatō bhavati bhārata* ॥ 14-3 ॥  

O Bhārata! I place the seed in My great infinite Womb, which gives birth to all beings.  

When this universe, this creation, did not exist, when there was nothing, neither real nor unreal, what existed then? Whence arose that which appeared as the universe? Many thinkers continue to engage in heated debate on this matter.  

Great men who perform intense practice of yoga and succeed in awakening their dormant consciousness concentrate it upon the consciousness of Time that fills the conscious Emptiness. Such yogīs know: whatever existed before the manifestation of this universe, it abode in the womb of Time. Time Itself became the cause of the conception of Time, and Time Itself took birth in the form of this universe. When its lifespan ends, this creation will be destroyed—Time will destroy Time by Time Itself, after which only Time will remain. Who but the great Time-conscious sages, the sthitaprajña, can realize this truth?  

☝  
☝  

276  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
*sarvayōniṣu kauntēya mūrtayaḥ saṁbhavanti yāḥ*  
*tāsāṁ brahma mahadyōnirahaṁ bījapradaḥ pitā* ॥ 14-4 ॥  

From whatever womb one may come into this world, that infinite Brahman is the Womb for all embodied beings, and I am the Seed-bestowing Father.  

Time Itself is the Mother, bearing in Her infinite Womb all beings that manifest in this universe. Time Itself is also the Father, fertilizing Time and giving conception to the entire universe.  

*sattvaṁ rajastama iti guṇāḥ prakṛtisaṁbhavāḥ*  
*nibadhnanti mahābāhō dēhē dēhinamavyayam* ॥ 14-5 ॥  

O Mahābāho! The three guṇas—sattva, rajas, and tamas—arising from Prakṛti, bind the eternal life through embodiment in the body.  

Great men who have united their consciousness with the consciousness of Time are able to realize that the human mind, the best manifestation of the supreme indestructible Brahman, is confined within the body under the influence of the three guṇas.  

☝  
☝  

277  
Chapter 14  
*tatra sattvaṁ nirmalatvātprakāśakamanāmayam*  
*sukhasaṅgēna badhnāti jñānasaṅgēna cānagha* ॥ 14-6 ॥  

O Anagha! Among them, the purest sattva is luminous and flawless. It binds through a strong desire for spiritual bliss and wisdom.  

Sattva, one of the three guṇas under whose influence the boundless consciousness is confined within the body, inspires one to overcome physical limitations and cognize the true nature of Time by awakening the dormant capacities of the mind. The influence of sattvaguṇa alone grants the happiness of realizing spiritual wisdom.  

*rajō rāgātmakaṁ viddhi tṛṣṇāsaṅgasamudbhavam*  
*tannibadhnāti kauntēya karmasaṅgēna dēhinam* ॥ 14-7 ॥  

O Kaunteya! Know rajoguṇa, full of passion, to be born of craving and attachment. It binds the embodied being through attachment to action.  

The great sthitaprajña fully realizes the mystery of the interconnection of the senses and the mind and understands that the awakened mind gains experience through only a small part of itself—the conscious mind.  

Rajoguṇa endows the intellect with attachment to the senses. This craving binds the intellect with an insatiable desire for ever more sense objects and is considered the cause of the limitation of the boundless consciousness by the body and organs.  

☝  
☝  

278  
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā  
*tamastvajñānajaṁ viddhi mōhanaṁ sarvadēhinām*  
*pramādālasyanidrābhistannibadhnāti bhārata* ॥ 14-8 ॥  

O Bhārata! Know tamoguṇa, which deludes all embodied beings, to be born of ignorance. It entangles through madness, laziness, and sleep.  

Such is the influence of the guṇa due to which a large part of the mind’s capacities is plunged into sleep. The guṇa that deludes the boundless consciousness of the mind, entangling it in ignorance, is called tamoguṇa by the great sthitaprajña.  

*sattvaṁ sukhē saṁjayati rajaḥ karmaṇi bhārata*  
*jñānamāvṛtya tu tamaḥ pramādē saṁjayatyuta* ॥ 14-9 ॥  

O Arjuna! Sattvaguṇa binds to happiness, rajoguṇa to activity, and tamoguṇa leads to madness, veiling wisdom.  

Sattva inspires the awakening of the dormant consciousness and is therefore considered bestower of bliss. Rajas confines the measureless consciousness of the mind within the limits of the body and compels it to perform actions for the satisfaction of the senses. Tamas envelops the measureless consciousness in laziness and, deluding it, leads to madness.  

*rajastamaścābhibhūya sattvaṁ bhavati bhārata*  
*rajaḥ sattvaṁ tamaścaiva tamaḥ sattvaṁ rajastathā* ॥ 14-10 ॥  

O Bhārata! Sattvaguṇa prevails over rajoguṇa and tamoguṇa; rajoguṇa overcomes sattvaguṇa and tamoguṇa; and tamoguṇa suppresses sattvaguṇa and rajoguṇa.  

☝  
☝

**279**
**Chapter 14**

If a person is inspired by sattvaguna, he transcends rajoguna and tamoguna. When tamoguna strengthens, enveloping all mental faculties, sattvaguna and rajoguna seemingly cease to exist due to the sleeping state of such a person's consciousness. When rajoguna comes into force, endowing the senses with power over the mind, it dominates both sattvaguna and tamoguna.

सर्वद्वारेषु देहेऽस्मिन्प्रकाश उपजायते ।
ज्ञानं यदा तदा विद्याद्विवृद्धं सत्त्वमित्युत ॥१४- ११॥
sarvadvārēṣu dēhē'sminprakāśa upajāyatē ।
jñānaṁ yadā tadā vidyādvivṛddhaṁ sattvamityuta ॥ 14-11॥

At the time when all the gates of the body are illumined by wisdom, sattvaguna is elevated.

Through the body, the great man acquires awareness of the mind's sovereign role in the relationship between mind and senses, and he realizes that dormant boundlessness within him. Sattvaguna predominates in the consciousness of such a person.

लोभः प्रवृत्तिरारम्भः कर्मणामशमः स्पृहा ।
रजस्येतानि जायन्ते विवृद्धे भरतर्षभ ॥१४- १२॥
lōbhaḥ pravṛttirārambhaḥ karmaṇāmaśamaḥ spṛhā ।
rajasyētāni jāyantē vivṛddhē bharatarṣabha ॥ 14-12॥

O best of the Bharatas! The predominance of rajoguna gives rise to an inclination towards activity born of greed, restlessness, and lust.

The ordinary man, however, who gives preference to the senses, remains ignorant of the boundlessness of his mind. All his intentions are permeated by a strong desire for the satisfaction of the sense organs. Yielding to lust, he falls into the trap of temporary pleasures when his attempts are successful, and is bound by grief and suffering when he encounters an obstacle on the path of sense gratification. The great sages see that a person in such a state is limited by rajoguna.

☝
☝
☝

**280**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

अप्रकाशोऽप्रवृत्तिश्च प्रमादो मोह एव च ।
तमस्येतानि जायन्ते विवृद्धे कुरुनन्दन ॥१४- १३॥
aprakāśō'pravṛttiśca pramādō mōha ēva ca ।
tamasyētāni jāyantē vivṛddhē kurunandana ॥ 14-13॥

O Kurunandana! The increase of tamas is the cause of darkness, inertia, madness, and delusion.

A pitiable person, most of whose mental faculties are asleep, who is only slightly aware even of the capabilities of his own body, foolish, devoid of common sense, and devoting his entire life only to sleep and food – such a deluded one is seen by the wise as being overcome by tamoguna.

यदा सत्त्वे प्रवृद्धे तु प्रलयं याति देहभृत् ।
तदोत्तमविदां लोकानमलान्प्रतिपद्यते ॥१४- १४॥
yadā sattvē pravṛddhē tu pralayaṁ yāti dēhabhṛt ।
tadōttamavidāṁ lōkānamalānpratipadyatē ॥ 14-14॥

If the embodied one dies when sattvaguna predominates, he attains the excellent, pure worlds of the wise.

The predominance of sattvaguna inspires a person to know his own boundlessness, rising above physical limitations. Such a great man performs the valiant practice of yoga and attains samadhi. Knowing the true nature of death, he establishes himself in that unmanifest supreme Truth which abides beyond physical limits, or else attains other divine worlds according to the level of his achievement.

रजसि प्रलयं गत्वा कर्मसङ्गिषु जायते ।
तथा प्रलीनस्तमसि मूढयोनिषु जायते ॥१४- १५॥
rajasi pralayaṁ gatvā karmasaṅgiṣu jāyatē ।
tathā pralīnastamasi mūḍhayōniṣu jāyatē ॥ 14-15॥

One who meets death in rajoguna is born among those attached to action. One who dies in tamoguna is born among the foolish.

☝
☝

**281**
**Chapter 14**

A person in whom rajoguna predominantly prevails gives preference to the body and senses throughout his life and abides in constant fear of death. An insecure person, led by rajoguna, displays a strong attachment to life at the time of death and, after death, is reborn again among people overcome by rajoguna with a limited mind.
The fool, who wastes his life under the influence of tamoguna, does not understand even after his death what has happened to him. The one in whom tamoguna dominates remains in an unconscious state both during death and after it, and is reborn among fools.
Those enslaved by lust, as well as fools, catch only a weak glimpse of their boundlessness after they encounter death and are reborn again many times. After this glimpse, sattvaguna begins to blossom in their lives, and they enter upon the path leading to the knowledge of their boundlessness.

कर्मणः सुकृतस्याहुः सात्त्विकं निर्मलं फलम् ।
रजसस्तु फलं दुःखमज्ञानं तमसः फलम् ॥१४- १६॥
karmaṇaḥ sukṛtasyāhuḥ sāttvikaṁ nirmalaṁ phalam ।
rajasastu phalaṁ duḥkhamajñānaṁ tamasaḥ phalam ॥ 14-16॥

It is said that the fruit of good karma is righteous and pure, the fruit of rajas is sorrow, and of tamas – ignorance.

It is considered that through yogic practice performed with sincere intention, the human mind is inspired by the idea of awakening its sleeping boundless consciousness to know the immaculate truth of eternal Time.
Actions performed under the influence of rajoguna lead to the limitation of consciousness by the body and organs, keeping a person in fear of death throughout his life. Such actions become the cause of deep despondency at the mere thought of life's end.
Those abiding under the influence of tamoguna spend their lives in ignorance, which is directly the result of their vicious actions.

☝
☝

**282**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

सत्त्वात्संजायते ज्ञानं रजसो लोभ एव च ।
प्रमादमोहौ तमसो भवतोऽज्ञानमेव च ॥१४- १७॥
sattvātsaṁjāyatē jñānaṁ rajasō lōbha ēva ca ।
pramādamōhau tamasō bhavatō'jñānamēva ca ॥ 14-17॥

Sattvaguna leads to wisdom, rajoguna inevitably leads to greed, and tamoguna is the cause of madness, delusion, and ignorance.

Sattvaguna inspires one to know That Unknown which abides beyond physical limits, and this inspiration itself gives rise to wisdom. Rajoguna confines consciousness within physical boundaries, generating desire for sense objects, which becomes the cause of great fear and sorrow at the moment of death. A person whose sleeping consciousness is under the influence of tamoguna, overcome by madness and delusion, continues to remain in ignorance.

ऊर्ध्वं गच्छन्ति सत्त्वस्था मध्ये तिष्ठन्ति राजसाः ।
जघन्यगुणवृत्तिस्था अधो गच्छन्ति तामसाः ॥१४- १८॥
ūrdhvaṁ gacchanti sattvasthā madhyē tiṣṭhanti rājasāḥ ।
jaghanyaguṇavṛttisthā adhō gacchanti tāmasāḥ ॥ 14-18॥

Those inclined to sattva move upward, the rajasic remain in the middle, and the lot of the tamasic, the vicious, those with the lowest inclinations, becomes downfall.

Those led by sattva undertake the valiant practice of yoga in order to know unmanifest Time by awakening their immeasurable consciousness. They develop the ability to leave the body through yogic power, and, knowing death through the body, they enjoy immortality beyond physical limits.
Those who possess a rajasic intellect believe in the superiority of the body and senses and cannot even conceive of That unmanifest Presence beyond the body. Stricken with fear, they cannot experience That boundlessness beyond physical limits even at

☝
☝

**283**
**Chapter 14**

the moment of their death. They are reborn again and again, taking one birth after another.
Those, however, who possess a tamasic consciousness and are not endowed even with a glimpse of the immeasurability of their mind and the divinity of the body, commit the most base actions for their own low gratification. After their death, they continue to abide in an unconscious state. Then they languish long in hell, and, finally coming to consciousness, they assume lower forms of life, being born among ghosts and demons.

नान्यं गुणेभ्यः कर्तारं यदा द्रष्टानुपश्यति ।
गुणेभ्यश्च परं वेत्ति मद्भावं सोऽधिगच्छति ॥१४- १९॥
nānyaṁ guṇēbhyaḥ kartāraṁ yadā draṣṭānupaśyati ।
guṇēbhyaśca paraṁ vētti madbhāvaṁ sō'dhigacchati ॥ 14-19॥

When the seer beholds no agent of action other than the gunas, and knows Him who abides beyond the gunas, he attains My nature.

When the great sthithaprajna becomes conscious of Time, knowing Its true nature, he perceives the dominion of these three gunas throughout the world. He understands that there is nothing else in the world that performs actions except these three gunas. It is only the influence of the gunas that impels all actions. Great men who have known the true nature of all three gunas transcend them and become "nirguna." Knowing the true nature of Time, such great souls attain unity with Him.

गुणानेतानतीत्य त्रीन्देही देहसमुद्भवान् ।
जन्ममृत्युजरादुःखैर्विमुक्तोऽमृतमश्नुते ॥१४- २०॥
guṇānētānatītya trīndēhī dēhasamudbhavān ।
janmamṛtyujarāduḥkhairvimuktō'mṛtamaśnutē ॥ 14-20॥

The embodied one, transcending these three gunas, the cause of his embodiment, enjoys the nectar of immortality, being completely freed from the sufferings associated with birth, old age, and death."

☝

**284**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

The great man, capable of awakening the entire boundlessness of his mind, transcends sattva, rajas, and tamas. Knowing the true nature of death and, with its help, freeing himself from all sufferings connected with physical limitations, he enjoys immortality.

अर्जुन उवाच
कैर्लिङ्गैस्त्रीन्गुणानेतानतीतो भवति प्रभो ।
किमाचारः कथं चैतांस्त्रीन्गुणानतिवर्तते ॥१४- २१॥
arjuna uvāca
kairliṅgaistrīnguṇānētānatītō bhavati prabhō ।
kimācāraḥ kathaṁ caitāṁstrīnguṇānativartatē ॥ 14-21॥

Arjuna said:
"O Prabho! How am I to know one who has transcended these gunas? How does he act? How does he surpass them?"

श्रीभगवानुवाच
प्रकाशं च प्रवृत्तिं च मोहमेव च पाण्डव ।
न द्वेष्टि संप्रवृत्तानि न निवृत्तानि काङ्क्षति ॥१४- २२॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
prakāśaṁ ca pravṛttiṁ ca mōhamēva ca pāṇḍava ।
na dvēṣṭi saṁpravṛttāni na nivṛttāni kāṅkśati ॥ 14-22॥

The Lord said:
"O Pandava! He does not seek to reject illumination, activity, or delusion when they arise, nor does he long for them when they depart.

He who has awakened, through the valiant practice of yoga, the sleeping consciousness of his mind in all its boundlessness, sees the entire universe as a manifestation of That unmanifest, indestructible Brahman. He understands that these three gunas also have arisen from Him. The great man who has attained such steadfastness feels neither contempt nor any attraction towards these gunas.

☝
☝

**285**
**Chapter 14**

उदासीनवदासीनो गुणैर्यो न विचाल्यते ।
गुणा वर्तन्त इत्येव योऽवतिष्ठति नेङ्गते ॥१४- २३॥
udāsīnavadāsīnō guṇairyō na vicālyatē ।
guṇā vartanta ityēva yō'vatiṣṭhati nēṅgatē ॥ 14-23॥

Indifferent, undisturbed by the gunas, knowing that only the gunas act, he ever abides steady and unwavering.

The great man, having known the true nature of the fundamental cause of the universe, Time, passing through the stages of this ancient yoga, establishes himself in the Unmanifest beyond the three gunas. He understands that it is these three gunas that impel all actions that are performed in this universe. Such a great sthithaprajna, indifferent to the gunas, ever abides established in the consciousness of Time.

समदुःखसुखः स्वस्थः समलोष्टाश्मकाञ्चनः ।
तुल्यप्रियाप्रियो धीरस्तुल्यनिन्दात्मसंस्तुतिः ॥१४- २४॥
samaduḥkhasukhaḥ svasthaḥ samalōṣṭāśmakāñcanaḥ ।
tulyapriyāpriyō dhīrastulyanindātmasaṁstutiḥ ॥ 14-24॥

Unchanged in joy and sorrow, self-abiding, looking equally on dust, stone, and gold, courageous, accepting alike the desirable and the undesirable, blame and praise.

The great man has known the Self through himself and has established himself in the Self itself. For him, joy and sorrow, dust and gold, the desirable and the undesirable, blame and praise – are without distinction. For such an unwavering man, all these states are merely different manifestations of That one unmanifest Presence.

☝
☝

286
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā
*mānāpamānayōstulyastulyō mitrāripakśayōḥ ।  
sarvārambhaparityāgī guṇātītaḥ sa ucyatē ॥ 14-25॥*

Unchanging in both honour and dishonour, impartial to friends and foes, having renounced all undertakings—such a sage is said to be beyond the guṇas.

For the great man who is aware of Time, honour and dishonour, friends and foes, beginning and end—all are but manifestations of that one Presence. Such a sage abides beyond sattva, rajas, and tamas, and is therefore considered to have transcended the guṇas.

*māṁ ca yō’vyabhicārēṇa bhaktiyōgēna sēvatē ।  
sa guṇānsamatītyaitānbrahmabhūyāya kalpatē ॥ 14-26॥*

He who with unwavering devotion worships Me through yoga, transcends these guṇas and becomes worthy of union with Brahman.

The great man sets out on the path of this ancient yoga for the sake of knowing the true nature of unmanifest Time. Receiving instruction from a great sage who has realised Brahman, he begins to awaken the full consciousness of his mind through the practice of this discipline. Then such a yogī receives the direct darśana of that radiant Truth of Time and becomes exceedingly devoted to Her, concentrating all his awakened consciousness upon that Truth. That great man goes far beyond sattva, rajas, and tamas, attaining union with the Light of all light, the great, shining, inexhaustible Time.

☝
☝

287
Chapter 14

*brahmaṇō hi pratiṣṭhāhamamṛtasyāvyayasya ca ।  
śāśvatasya ca dharmasya sukhasyaikāntikasya ca ॥ 14-27॥*

“I am the Eternal Law, the Imperishable Brahman, the Immortal, the foundation of supreme bliss.”

The Light of all light, unbearably brilliant, immeasurable, inexhaustible Time—that Eternal, Imperishable Law. It itself manifests in the form of death and sustains the entire universe by but a small part of itself. The one joy in all this vast world is to know Its true nature.

*ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē  
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē guṇatrayavibhāgayōgō nāma caturdaśō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 14॥*

Oṁ Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the fourteenth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Liberation from the Three Guṇas,” of the Upaniṣad known as Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā, which treats of the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

☝

*Pañcadaśō’dhyāyaḥ Puruṣōttamayōgaḥ*

Chapter 15
THE YOGA OF THE SUPREME BEING

290
*śrībhagavānuvāca  
ūrdhvamūlamadhaḥśākhamaśvatthaṁ prāhuravayam ।  
chandāṁsi yasya parṇāni yastaṁ vēda sa vēdavit ॥ 15-1॥*

The Lord said:  
“With roots above and branches below, this Aśvattha tree is said to be imperishable. The Vedas are its leaves. He who knows this knows the wisdom of the Vedas.”

The human brain, the abode of the mind, a manifestation of the indestructible, immeasurable Time, is situated in the head and is the root of this body, which is like a tree. The suṣumṇā, extending downward, is its trunk. The nerves surrounding the suṣumṇā are its branches, through which the mind acquires experience. Upon these branches blossom the leaves of desire.

This embodiment, like a tree, is the finest creation of unmanifest Time. It serves as a refuge for the mind, carefully nurturing within it the boundless, indestructible consciousness of Time. For this reason, ordinary people perceive their perishable body as if it were eternal. Only that great man who, through the practice of yoga, has awakened his boundless

☝
*ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya*  
Oṁ Namo Bhagavate Vāsudevāya

291
Chapter 15

consciousness in its fullness, and having known this physical embodiment, is considered a sage.

*adhaścōrdhvaṁ prasṛtāstasya śākhā guṇapravṛddhā viṣayapravālāḥ ।  
adhaśca mūlānyanusaṁtatāni karmānubandhīni manuṣyalōkē ॥ 15-2॥*

On its branches, nourished by the guṇas and spreading upward and downward, the buds of passion swell. The roots, which bind one to actions, penetrate the world of mortals.

The tree of the human body, subject to the influence of the three guṇas or, in other words, nourished by these three guṇas, has nerve-like branches upon which blossom the buds of lust and the shoots of attachment. These nerves extend downward from the mind to all organs and back from the organs to the mind. They stretch upward, downward, and in all directions within this body. Those very branches are the cause of the ordinary man’s imprisonment within the body and his bondage to the ties of karma.

*na rūpamasyēha tathōpalabhyatē nāntō na cādirna ca saṁpratiṣṭhā ।  
aśvatthamēnaṁ suvirūḍhamūlamasaṅgaśastrēṇa dṛḍhēna chittvā ॥ 15-3॥*

Its form here is not thus perceived, for it has neither beginning, nor end, nor foundation. Having cut down this deeply rooted Aśvattha tree with the sharp sword of detachment,

People of limited consciousness do not go beyond desires and attachments—the leaves growing on this tree-like body. Due to this limitation, they cannot obtain even a glimpse of the boundless, sleeping consciousness of their own mind, which manifests through the body. Although their consciousness is limited by this body, such people know neither the beginning nor the end of their physical boundaries.

☝
☝

292
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

Great sages, under the influence of sattvaguṇa, are able to catch a glimpse of the infinity contained within their body. Therefore, receiving instruction in this ancient science of yoga from a great Guru who has realised Brahman, they steadfastly adhere to the practice for awakening their mind. Soon these people begin to know the true nature of infinite Time, which manifests the mind, rising above physical limitations and thereby awakening their consciousness in its fullness.

*tataḥ padaṁ tatparimārgitavyaṁ yasmingatā na nivartanti bhūyaḥ ।  
tamēva cādyaṁ puruṣaṁ prapadyē yataḥ pravṛttiḥ prasṛtā purāṇī ॥ 15-4॥*

One should seek that path leading to the place from which there is no return, taking refuge in that Supreme Puruṣa who gave rise to this ancient practice.

Great men who transcend physical limitations are able to awaken their dormant consciousness for the sake of knowing the true nature of the Light of all light, the boundless and indestructible Time, which manifests the entire universe. Those among them who have succeeded in concentrating their awakened consciousness upon the truth of Time become aware of Time. Thus they know the true nature of Time and attain union with It. They are no longer obliged to confine themselves within the bonds of the physical body.

*nirmānamōhā jitasaṅgadōṣā adhyātmanityā vinivṛttakāmāḥ ।  
dvandvairvimuktāḥ sukhaduḥkhasaṁjñairgacchantyamūḍhāḥ padamavyaṁ tat ॥ 15-5॥*

Those who are free from pride, delusion, and the sin of attachment, who abide always in a spiritual state, who have renounced lust and the dualities of pleasure and pain—such a sage attains that imperishable state.

Great men who have known the boundlessness of their mind, transcending physical limitations through the study of the relationship between body and mind, rise above attachment to the body and become free from all their desires. Such sages truly realise the relativity of happiness and sorrow. In them, who have already awakened their sleeping consciousness, there is no place for ignorance. These great yogīs attain union with Time, concentrating upon It all their consciousness, awakened through the practice of yoga.

*na tadbhāsayatē sūryō na śaśāṅkō na pāvakaḥ ।  
yadgatvā na nivartantē taddhāma paramaṁ mama ॥ 15-6॥*

Neither the Sun, nor the Moon, nor fire can illumine that My Supreme Abode. Those who reach It never return.

Devoted sādhakas of yoga, through their intense practice, directly perceive the unbearably radiant, terrifyingly immeasurable Time, the Light of all light, which with but a small particle of itself bestows radiance upon both the Sun and the Moon. Attaining union with It, such yogīs are never again confined within physical limits.

*mamaivāṁśō jīvalōkē jīvabhūtaḥ sanātanaḥ ।  
manaḥṣaṣṭhānīndriyāṇi prakṛtisthāni karṣati ॥ 15-7॥*

This eternal fragment of Mine, becoming a living being in the world of mortals, draws to itself the mind and the five senses, which abide in Prakṛti.

☝
☝

294
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

The body contains within itself the boundless mind—the finest manifestation of that unmanifest, infinite Supreme Truth, Time. That boundless mind, possessing eternal consciousness and striving to know itself in its fullness through the conscious mind and the sense organs, limits itself within physical bounds for this purpose.

*śarīraṁ yadavāpnōti yaccāpyutkrāmatīśvaraḥ ।  
gṛhitvaitāni saṁyāti vāyurgandhānivāśayāt ॥ 15-8॥*

When the Lord of the body transcends the limitations of the body, having made use of its capacities, He carries away with Him the senses and the mind, just as the wind carries away fragrance from its source.

Just as the perception of fragrance is possible only through the air (and the presence of fragrance proves the presence of air), so too is the boundlessness of the mind perceived through the limited body, by means of the conscious mind, the senses, and the intellect. The limitations of the body, however, are understood through the awakening of the sleeping consciousness of the mind in its fullness.

*śrōtraṁ cakśuḥ sparśanaṁ ca rasanaṁ ghrāṇamēva ca ।  
adhiṣṭhāya manaścāyaṁ viṣayānupasēvatē ॥ 15-9॥*

Using the ears, eyes, skin, nose, tongue, and mind, He enjoys the objects of the senses.

The boundless mind, also called Ātman by the ancient sages, perceives sound, visual form, touch, taste, smell, and all experiences connected with these sensations through the conscious mind and the five sense organs.

☝
☝
☝

295
Chapter 15

*utkrāmantaṁ sthitaṁ vāpi bhuñjānaṁ vā guṇānvitam ।  
vimūḍhā nānupaśyanti paśyanti jñānacakśuṣaḥ ॥ 15-10॥*

Bewildered by the guṇas, fools cannot see Him, whether He abides in the body and enjoys the objects of the senses, or departs from this body. Only those with the eyes of wisdom see Him.

Only great men, who have risen above physical limitations and become established in the consciousness of Emptiness, having awakened all their sleeping consciousness, can comprehend the transcendent boundlessness of their own mind, the essence of its limitation by physical bounds, and its true nature. Through the body, they are able to comprehend the objects of the senses and the influence of the three guṇas.

*yatantō yōginaścainaṁ paśyantyātmanyavasthitam ।  
yatantō’pyakṛtātmānō nainaṁ paśyantyacētasaḥ ॥ 15-11॥*

Yogīs who are reconciled with themselves and disposed towards themselves can see Him. The unintelligent, who are not self-aware, cannot see Him, even if they try.

Great yogīs, who awaken the sleeping consciousness of their boundless mind through the practice of yoga, come to know through self-realisation that unmanifest, eternal Truth which manifests them. Ordinary people, however, who do not strive to awaken the sleeping capacities of the mind, are unable even to imagine that boundlessness of consciousness inherent in their own intellect.

☝
☝

**296**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*yadādityagataṁ tējō jagadbhāsayatē’khilam*
*yaccandramasi yaccāgnau tattējō viddhi māmakam* ॥ 15-12 ॥

Know: the radiance of the Sun, which illumines the entire world, the light of the Moon and the flame of fire proceed from Me.

Great men, through steadfast practice of yoga, establish themselves in samadhi and become *sthitaprajña*. They are able to understand that That great Time, like the unbearable radiance of the Sun, is Itself the Source of the light of the Sun, the Moon, and fire, as well as the Creator of all worlds. It is this great Radiance that gives birth to the Universe. It also manifests in the form of a golden aura surrounding the heads of great men who realize Time.

*gāmāviśya ca bhūtāni dhārayāmyahamōjasā*
*puṣṇāmi cauṣadhīḥ sarvāḥ sōmō bhūtvā rasātmakaḥ* ॥ 15-13 ॥

Having entered the Earth, I support all living beings with My power. I endow medicinal herbs with properties, becoming the succulent Soma.

The unmanifest, indestructible Supreme Truth is the foundation of the motion and life of all planets and constellations. By Its splendor, in the form of Earth, It supports all beings. Becoming the Juice of all juices, It fills all medicines with healing power.

*ahaṁ vaiśvānarō bhūtvā prāṇināṁ dēhamāśritaḥ*
*prāṇāpānasamāyuktaḥ pacāmyannaṁ caturvidham* ॥ 15-14 ॥

I take the form of the fire of digestion in embodied beings and digest the four kinds of food, uniting with prana and apana.

☝
☝

**297**
**Chapter 15**

The unmanifest Time, Vasudeva, dwells in the heart of each and, with the help of prana and apana, consumes as food the four aims of human life, called *dharma*, *artha*, *kāma*, and *moksha*.

*sarvasya cāhaṁ hṛdi saṁniviṣṭō mattaḥ smṛtirjñānamapōhanaṁ ca*
*vēdaiśca sarvairahamēva vēdyō vēdāntakṛdvēdavidēva cāham* ॥ 15-15 ॥

I abide in the heart of everyone. Memory and wisdom – both dissolve in Me. I am That which is known through knowledge. I am the Creator of supreme knowledge. I am the Supreme Knower.

The unmanifest eternal Time abides in the heart of each in the form of Vasudeva. Manifesting the mind, It is all knowledge preserved in memory, as well as the wisdom that liberates from duality, the knower, the known, and the result of knowledge. Time is also the cause of the fading of memory and wisdom with the passage of time.

*dvāvimau puruṣau lōkē kśaraścākśara ēva ca*
*kśaraḥ sarvāṇi bhūtāni kūṭasthō’kśara ucyatē* ॥ 15-16 ॥

There are only two Purushas in this world: the perishable and the eternal. All creatures are perishable, and only Kutastha is considered eternal.

Two fundamental principles exist in this visible world. The first is the body, which supports the boundless consciousness of the mind, but is itself limited and therefore subject to destruction. The second is Vasudeva, who endows this mortal body with mind and dwells in the heart of every being. Eternal and imperishable, He is called by yogis the indestructible Kutastha.

☝
☝
☝

**298**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*uttamaḥ puruṣastvanyaḥ paramātmētyudāhṛtaḥ*
*yō lōkatrayamāviśya bibhartyavyaya īśvaraḥ* ॥ 15-17 ॥

But beyond all three worlds, pervading, supporting, and filling them, I abide – Paramatma, the Supreme Purusha.

The eternal unmanifest Time, the Supreme Purusha, remains transcendent to both the perishable body and even the eternal Kutastha. It exists as if not existing. It manifests all worlds and sustains their existence. Only great men who realize Time know Its true nature.

*yasmātkśaramatītō’hamakśarādapi cōttamaḥ*
*atō’smi lōkē vēdē ca prathitaḥ puruṣōttamaḥ* ॥ 15-18 ॥

Know Me as transcendent to both the perishable and the eternal, under the name Purushottama. Thus am I called in the world and in the sacred texts.

Great men who realize Time know that the unmanifest Time abides outside the visible world, which appears perishable. It also abides outside the Conscious Void, filled with the consciousness of the Void. Devotees of yoga, who through their valiant practice have become realizers of Time, have directly contemplated That boundless embodiment of Time and given It the name Purushottama.

☝
☝

**299**
**Chapter 15**

*yō māmēvamasaṁmūḍhō jānāti puruṣōttamam*
*sa sarvavidbhajati māṁ sarvabhāvēna bhārata* ॥ 15-19 ॥

O Bharata! Freed from delusion, he who knows Me as the Supreme Purusha – such a sage worships Me with his whole being.

Great men, transcending physical limitations through intense yogic practice, awaken the infinite consciousness of their mind and, concentrating it on the unmanifest truth of Time, with His blessing directly perceive Time Itself. They know Its true nature and become realizers of Time. Such sages, contemplating Him everywhere and established in His presence, by all their actions worship only Time.

*iti guhyatamaṁ śāstramidamuktaṁ mayānagha*
*ētad‌buddhvā buddhimānsyātkṛtakṛtyaśca bhārata* ॥ 15-20 ॥

O Anagha! I have revealed to you this most secret knowledge. O Bharata! He who comprehends this becomes established in wisdom, having accomplished all that is to be done.”

Those great men who, through valiant practice of yoga, have awakened the hidden consciousness of the sleeping mind within their body, contemplate the supremely secret, most radiant Time, which manifests the consciousness of the body, and know Its true essence. Such great souls who realize Time transcend all desires and attain self-satisfaction.

☝
☝

**300**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē*
*śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē puruṣōttamayōgō nāma pañcadaśō’dhyāyaḥ* ॥ 15 ॥

Om Tat Sat
Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the fifteenth chapter, entitled “The Yoga of the Supreme Being,” of the Upanishad called “Shrimad Bhagavad Gita,” which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

*ṣōḍaśō’dhyāyaḥ daivāsurasampadvibhāgayōgaḥ*

**Chapter 16**
**THE YOGA OF THE DISTINCTION BETWEEN**
**THE DIVINE AND THE DEMONIC**

**302**

*śrībhagavānuvāca*
*abhayaṁ sattvasaṁśuddhirjñānayōgavyavasthitiḥ*
*dānaṁ damaśca yajñaśca svādhyāyastapa ārjavam* ॥ 16-1 ॥

The Lord said:
“Fearlessness, purity of natural qualities, steadfastness in knowledge and yoga, charity, self-control, self-sacrifice, self-study, tapas, and simplicity,

Great men who realize Time, through the practice of yoga, free themselves from physical limitations and, establishing themselves in samadhi, become fearless, attaining unity with the entire universe. Such great men, awakening all the consciousness of their mind, are purified from the vice of ignorance. Having realized their true nature, immersed in self-knowledge, they continue to perform the practice of this ancient yoga in order to inspire others. Those who have known the true nature of Time bestow their blessings upon seekers of this ancient teaching and thus perform the austerity of the gift of knowledge.

☝

*ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya*

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**303**
**Chapter 16**

*ahiṁsā satyamakrōdhastyāgaḥ śāntirapaiśunam*
*dayā bhūtēṣvalōluptvaṁ mārdavaṁ hrīracāpalam* ॥ 16-2 ॥

Non-violence, truthfulness, absence of anger, renunciation, peacefulness, non-censure, compassion towards all beings, freedom from greed, gentleness, modesty, and resoluteness,

Great men who have awakened the full consciousness of their mind have already renounced their limitation. Fulfilling all their desires and attaining their goal – the realization of Time – they become free from anger and attain peace. Knowing the nature of this supreme Truth, such men become established in It, therefore everything they say also proves to be truth. They censure no one, understanding that all three gunas are merely manifestations of Time. Established in Infinity, they appear unwavering; their physical as well as mental state is marked by extreme gentleness and calm.

*tējaḥ kśamā dhṛtiḥ śaucamadrōhō nātimānitā*
*bhavanti saṁpadaṁ daivīmabhijātasya bhārata* ॥ 16-3 ॥

Brilliance and splendor, forgiveness, fortitude, purity, freedom from malice and pride – such, O Bharata, are the qualities of one born with a divine nature.

Knowing the true nature of the Light of all light, the unbearably radiant Time, such great men themselves begin to emit radiance. Upon careful observation, it can be seen as a golden aura above the heads of such great men. Having known the true essence of the material world and established in equanimity, they are full of compassion and look upon all as equals. Purified by the fire of yoga, they constantly contemplate the supreme

☝
☝

**304**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

radiant Time manifested in all beings and thus become free from pride.

All these traits can be observed in those great men who have attained divinity by knowing the true nature of the unbearably radiant Time.

*dambhō darpō’bhimānaśca krōdhaḥ pāruṣyamēva ca*
*ajñānaṁ cābhijātasya pārtha saṁpadamāsurīm* ॥ 16-4 ॥

O son of Pritha! Hypocrisy, arrogance and pride, anger, harshness, as well as ignorance – these are the traits of one born with a demonic nature.

Ordinary people, the greater part of whose mental faculties sleep, have the habit of becoming irritated over trifles. They consider themselves cleverer than everyone else and are filled with pride. Cherishing many petty desires, they spend their lives in anger and caustic speech. Such people, abiding in ignorance of their hidden divinity, are known for their demonic inclinations.

*daivī saṁpadvimōkśāya nibandhāyāsurī matā*
*mā śucaḥ saṁpadaṁ daivīmabhijātō’si pāṇḍava* ॥ 16-5 ॥

It is considered that divine qualities lead to liberation, while demonic ones bind in fetters. O Pandava! Do not grieve, for you are born with a divine nature.

Great men who have risen above physical limitations, through diligent practice of yoga, come to know the divine presence of Time within themselves. They pass through death and, thus freed from attachment to life, become *jivanmukta* even while living. Such men do not grieve for those who

☝
☝

# Chapter 16

is limited by physical boundaries, ignorant of its own divinity, and has demonic tendencies.

द्वौ भूतसर्गौ लोकेऽस्मिन्दैव आसुर एव च ।
दैवो विस्तरशः प्रोक्त आसुरं पार्थ मे शृणु ॥१६-६॥

dvau bhūtasargau lōkē'smindaiva āsura ēva ca ।
daivō vistaraśaḥ prōkta āsuraṁ pārtha mē śṛṇu ॥ 16-6॥

O Partha! Only two kinds of beings exist in this world – divine and demonic. The divine nature has been described in detail; now hear from Me about the demonic.

Only two types of personalities are found among men. The first are the great *sthitaprajña*, those who have independently attained divinity by awakening their immeasurable consciousness. The second type are demonic people, abiding in ignorance of the infinity hidden within their bodies.

Having analyzed in detail the characteristics of the great *sthitaprajña*, Lord Shri Krishna now tells Arjuna about the traits of demonic people for the benefit of future generations.

प्रवृत्तिं च निवृत्तिं च जना न विदुरासुराः ।
न शौचं नापि चाचारो न सत्यं तेषु विद्यते ॥१६-७॥

pravṛttiṁ ca nivṛttiṁ ca janā na vidurāsurāḥ ।
na śaucaṁ nāpi cācārō na satyaṁ tēṣu vidyatē ॥ 16-7॥

Demonic personalities know neither what should be done nor what should not be done. There is in them neither purity, nor morality, nor truth.

People with a demonic nature and limited intellect cannot understand throughout their entire lives what they should do and what they should not do. They are incapable of obtaining even a glimpse of the infinity hidden within them. The capacities of their mind remain asleep, therefore true knowledge constantly eludes them, and purity remains unattainable. Without having known the essence of life, such people merely waste it in vain.

☝
☝

306
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

असत्यमप्रतिष्ठं ते जगदाहुरनीश्वरम् ।
अपरस्परसंभूतं किमन्यत्कामहैतुकम् ॥१६-८॥

asatyamapratiṣṭhaṁ tē jagadāhuranīśvaram ।
aparasparasaṁbhūtaṁ kimanyatkāmahaitukam ॥ 16-8॥

They say: "This world is unreal: there is in it neither foundation, nor a Creator governing it, nor any other cause for its origin except accidental copulation arising from mutual lust."

People of limited intellect, whose consciousness sleeps, have no conception of the essence of that unmanifest Time which manifests this universe. They suppose that this world arises from the union of man and woman and from the combination of various chemical elements. The chief interest in the lives of such people is the attainment of sexual pleasure. The recollections of great men who are aware of Time, pointing toward the unmanifest Time, they consider to be lies and flights of fancy.
