Their intellect is limited only by the boundaries of the body, therefore they consider the fulfillment of arising sensual desires to be the only truth. Such people cannot imagine anything that extends beyond the limits of the sense organs.

एतां दृष्टिमवष्टभ्य नष्टात्मानोऽल्पबुद्धयः ।
प्रभवन्त्युग्रकर्माणः क्षयाय जगतोऽहिताः ॥१६-९॥

ētāṁ dṛṣṭimavaṣṭabhya naṣṭātmānō'lpabuddhayaḥ ।
prabhavantyugrakarmāṇaḥ kśayāya jagatō'hitāḥ ॥ 16-9॥

Overshadowed by such a vision, devoid of reason, having lost their true essence, they are absorbed in cruel, suffering-causing actions and are born to destroy the world.

Such fools experience delight in causing the maximum possible harm to an enemy who in any way obstructs the satisfaction of their sensual desires. These cruel people are born again and again in this world only to be destroyed again and again by death.

☝
☝

307
Chapter 16

काममाश्रित्य दुष्पूरं दम्भमानमदान्विताः ।
मोहाद्‌गृहीत्वासद्ग्राहान्प्रवर्तन्तेऽशुचिव्रताः ॥१६-१०॥

kāmamāśritya duṣpūraṁ dambhamānamadānvitāḥ ।
mōhād‌gṛhītvāsadgrāhānpravartantē'śucivratāḥ ॥ 16-10॥

Full of hypocrisy, pride, and madness, absorbed in insatiable lust in attempts to satisfy desires that can never be satisfied, leading depraved lives, guided by the call of false impulses, they fall through ignorance into the trap of illusion.

Giving preference only to sexual pleasures, they perform all their actions solely for their attainment. The desires of such limited people always remain unsatisfied. Bewildered, for the sake of fulfilling them, these demonic people engage in rituals meant to propitiate spirits and ghosts, or become followers of those who worship ghosts, cherishing the hope of realizing their own desires through them. Such fools consider actions that gratify spirits and ghosts to be a great spiritual teaching.

चिन्तामपरिमेयां च प्रलयान्तामुपाश्रिताः ।
कामोपभोगपरमा एतावदिति निश्चिताः ॥१६-११॥

cintāmaparimēyāṁ ca pralayāntāmupāśritāḥ ।
kāmōpabhōgaparamā ētāvaditi niścitāḥ ॥ 16-11॥

Burdened until death with endless anxieties, they continue to indulge in lust and desire and are deeply convinced that this is the highest goal.

Due to their mental limitation, such people spend their entire lives in worry, abiding in terror of death. Continuing to dream of sexual pleasures, they consider only these to be supreme. They think of themselves as great sages, asserting that the enjoyment of copulation is like the joy of knowing the unmanifest Brahman.

☝
☝

308
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

आशापाशशतैर्बद्धाः कामक्रोधपरायणाः ।
ईहन्ते कामभोगार्थमन्यायेनार्थसञ्चयान् ॥१६-१२॥

āśāpāśaśatairbaddhāḥ kāmakrōdhaparāyaṇāḥ ।
īhantē kāmabhōgārthamanyāyēnārthasañcayān ॥ 16-12॥

Bound by the fetters of hundreds of desires, such lustful and wrathful people try to accumulate wealth by unrighteous means in their striving to satisfy their senses.

In hope of fulfilling their numerous desires, such people fall into their nets and become angry when they cannot fulfill them. They suppose that greater wealth will allow them to fulfill all desires without hindrance. Such reckless, demonic people, insatiably thirsting for ever more wealth, willingly commit the most heinous crimes.

इदमद्य मया लब्धमिमं प्राप्स्ये मनोरथम् ।
इदमस्तीदमपि मे भविष्यति पुनर्धनम् ॥१६-१३॥

idamadya mayā labdhamimaṁ prāpsyē manōratham ।
idamastīdamapi mē bhaviṣyati punardhanam ॥ 16-13॥

"I have obtained this today; now I shall fulfill this desire; I possess such wealth, but I shall acquire even more."

Such people always reason as follows: "I have enjoyed this today, and tomorrow I shall obtain even greater pleasure. Today I have this vast fortune, but in the future I shall accumulate even more. I will prove to everyone in the world that I am the greatest man in all the world! Fools are all those who do not recognize my greatness." They continue to waste their lives on such meaningless fantasies.

☝
☝

309
Chapter 16

असौ मया हतः शत्रुर्हनिष्ये चापरानपि ।
ईश्वरोऽहमहं भोगी सिद्धोऽहं बलवान्सुखी ॥१६-१४॥

asau mayā hataḥ śatrurhaniṣyē cāparānapi ।
īśvarō'hamahaṁ bhōgī siddhō'haṁ balavānsukhī ॥ 16-14॥

"I have slain this enemy; I shall slay others as well; I am the Supreme Lord, I am the enjoyer, I am perfect, I am mighty and happy."

Considering themselves the greatest, they see an enemy in anyone who even slightly hinders the fulfillment of their desires, and they become filled with vanity and pride, destroying or suppressing him. Imagining themselves the most powerful, they make grandiose declarations of their greatness and ask whether anyone can defeat them: "Who in this world is as great as I? Who here enjoys as I do? I am the most powerful and wise! I am exceedingly happy; who here can be happier than I?"

आढ्योऽभिजनवानस्मि कोऽन्योऽस्ति सदृशो मया ।
यक्ष्ये दास्यामि मोदिष्य इत्यज्ञानविमोहिताः ॥१६-१५॥

āḍhyō'bhijanavānasmi kō'nyō'sti sadṛśō mayā ।
yakśyē dāsyāmi mōdiṣya ityajñānavimōhitāḥ ॥ 16-15॥

"I am wealthy and of noble birth. Who else here compares with me? I will perform *yajña*, give alms, and rejoice in celebration" – thus speak those driven mad by ignorance.

Such fools become filled with vanity, considering the traditions of their clan to be the best. Their madness only increases when they hear praise directed at them from other fools who place their hopes in them. Falling under the influence of hired *karmakāṇḍīs*¹, hearing their false praise, they perform certain rituals, which only further feeds their false pride.

¹Priests who perform sacrificial rituals

☝
☝

310
Shrimad Bhagavad Gita

अनेकचित्तविभ्रान्ता मोहजालसमावृताः ।
प्रसक्ताः कामभोगेषु पतन्ति नरकेऽशुचौ ॥१६-१६॥

anēkacittavibhrāntā mōhajālasamāvṛtāḥ ।
prasaktāḥ kāmabhōgēṣu patanti narakē'śucau ॥ 16-16॥

Preoccupied with numerous thoughts, entangled in the net of illusion, and obsessively attached to sexual pleasure, they fall swiftly into hell.

Confined within physical boundaries, abiding in slavery to their own sense organs, occupied only with the fulfillment of their fleeting desires, entangled in the nets of illusion and considering the sexual act the only pleasure, such people waste themselves in vain. With distorted minds, seized by fear, they fall swiftly into hell when death comes to them.

आत्मसंभाविताः स्तब्धा धनमानमदान्विताः ।
यजन्ते नामयज्ञैस्ते दम्भेनाविधिपूर्वकम् ॥१६-१७॥

ātmasaṁbhāvitāḥ stabdhā dhanamānamadānvitāḥ ।
yajantē nāmayajñaistē dambhēnāvidhipūrvakam ॥ 16-17॥

Arrogant, intoxicated with wealth and vanity, they perform sacrifices for show, without following the sacred injunctions.

Such people possess distorted notions of their own importance and consider themselves the greatest. Even having obtained a small amount of wealth, overcome by passionate desires, they sacrifice themselves to the fire of anger.

☝
☝

311
Chapter 16

अहंकारं बलं दर्पं कामं क्रोधं च संश्रिताः ।
मामात्मपरदेहेषु प्रद्विषन्तोऽभ्यसूयकाः ॥१६-१८॥

ahaṁkāraṁ balaṁ darpaṁ kāmaṁ krōdhaṁ ca saṁśritāḥ ।
māmātmaparadēhēṣu pradviṣantō'bhyasūyakāḥ ॥ 16-18॥

Immersed in egoism, violence, pride, lust, and anger, they are filled with envy toward Me, who abides in their own bodies and in the bodies of other embodied beings.

Consuming their lives in the fire of anger, perpetually discontented, striving only for the fulfillment of their desires, such people are always inclined to blame others. They cannot even conceive of Vāsudeva, who abides in their hearts.

तानहं द्विषतः क्रुरान्संसारेषु नराधमान् ।
क्षिपाम्यजस्रमशुभानासुरीष्वेव योनिषु ॥१६-१९॥

tānahaṁ dviṣataḥ krurānsaṁsārēṣu narādhamān ।
kśipāmyajasramaśubhānāsurīṣvēva yōniṣu ॥ 16-19॥

Again and again I cast these envious, cruel, lowest of men into demonic wombs.

Such low, self-hostile, despicable people are unable to awaken their boundlessness and know the true nature of Time. They spend their entire lives trembling before death, and having died, they languish long in hell, only to be born again in a demonic family.

आसुरीं योनिमापन्ना मूढा जन्मनि जन्मनि ।
मामप्राप्यैव कौन्तेय ततो यान्त्यधमां गतिम् ॥१६-२०॥

āsurīṁ yōnimāpannā mūḍhā janmani janmani ।
māmaprāpyaiva kauntēya tatō yāntyadhamāṁ gatim ॥ 16-20॥

O Kaunteya! Such fools do not attain Me, but receiving birth after birth in demonic wombs, they sink lower and lower.

☝
☝

**312**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

Again and again after death, such fools with sleeping consciousness undergo hellish torments, and then again and again they are born into families possessing the lowest of low intellects.

त्रिविधं नरकस्येदं द्वारं नाशनमात्मनः ।
कामः क्रोधस्तथा लोभस्तस्मादेतत्त्रयं त्यजेत् ॥१६- २१॥

trividhaṁ narakasyēdaṁ dvāraṁ nāśanamātmanaḥ ।
kāmaḥ krōdhastathā lōbhastasmādētattrayaṁ tyajēt ॥ 16-21॥

Lust, anger, and greed – these are the three paths of self-destruction, leading to hell. One must renounce all three.

Fools who exalt themselves, possessing sleeping consciousness, cannot understand that the cause of all their suffering, as well as that which prevents them from experiencing the divine boundlessness of their own mind, are three principal tendencies. The first is their constant thirst for sexual satisfaction and indulgence in various petty desires. The second is the striving to accumulate even greater wealth in order to fulfill these desires. The third is the habit of becoming angry when their greed is not satiated. These three fundamental predispositions conceal the divine infinity from the embodied. After death, such people fall into hell precisely because of lust, anger, and greed. Great people, who have realized their limitation and are moving forward toward infinity, strive to renounce these three primary limiting tendencies.

एतैर्विमुक्तः कौन्तेय तमोद्वारैस्त्रिभिर्नरः ।
आचरत्यात्मनः श्रेयस्ततो याति परां गतिम् ॥१६- २२॥

ētairvimuktaḥ kauntēya tamōdvāraistribhirnaraḥ ।
ācaratyātmanaḥ śrēyastatō yāti parāṁ gatim ॥ 16-22॥

O Kaunteya! Freed from these three paths leading to darkness, a man becomes reconciled with himself and thus attains the Supreme Goal.

He who has recognized that these three paths lead to hell, limiting consciousness to the body and keeping it attached to the objects of the senses, frees himself from these predispositions by knowing their essence. He performs diligent practice of yoga to awaken the sleeping boundlessness of the mind, and then concentrates his awakened mind on the unmanifest, indestructible Time, the Light of all light. Knowing Its true nature, such a yogi attains unity with It.

यः शास्त्रविधिमुत्सृज्य वर्तते कामकारतः ।
न स सिद्धिमवाप्नोति न सुखं न परां गतिम् ॥१६- २३॥

yaḥ śāstravidhimutsṛjya vartatē kāmakārataḥ ।
na sa siddhimavāpnōti na sukhaṁ na parāṁ gatim ॥ 16-23॥

He who violates the injunctions of the scriptures and indulges his whims attains neither perfection, nor happiness, nor the Supreme Goal.

A man who violates the injunctions of the sacred scriptures and, out of vanity, considers the wisdom contained within them to be merely a product of imagination, remains trapped in lust, anger, and greed. Throughout his entire life, he can neither free himself from the fear of death nor know That unmanifest beyond it. Such an unfortunate person is incapable of experiencing true happiness in all his life.

तस्माच्छास्त्रं प्रमाणं ते कार्याकार्यव्यवस्थितौ ।
ज्ञात्वा शास्त्रविधानोक्तं कर्म कर्तुमिहार्हसि ॥१६- २४॥

tasmācchāstraṁ pramāṇaṁ tē kāryākāryavyavasthitau ।
jñātvā śāstravidhānōktaṁ karma kartumihārhasi ॥ 16-24॥

Therefore, let the scriptures be your authority in determining what should be done and what should not be done. Knowing what is prescribed by the ordinances of the scriptures, you should perform actions in this world."

All sacred scriptures are the personal experience of the great saints of antiquity, preserved in words as a gift for future generations. Out of compassion for all those who in the future will wish to understand these hints, the great sages, established in the consciousness of the Void and having experienced the direct perception of Time, preserved a description of the path by which they walked towards the knowledge of Time.

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे दैवासुरसंपद्विभागयोगो नाम षोडशोऽध्यायः ॥१६॥

ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē daivāsurasampadvibhāgayōgō nāma ṣōḍaśō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 16॥

  Om Tat Sat  
Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the sixteenth chapter, entitled "The Yoga of the Distinction Between the Divine and the Demonic," of the Upanishad of the Shrimad Bhagavad Gita, which treats of the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

सप्तदशोऽध्यायः श्रद्धात्रयविभागयोगः
saptadaśō’dhyāyaḥ śraddhātrayavibhāgayōgaḥ
Chapter 17
THE YOGA OF THE THREE TYPES OF FAITH

**316**
अर्जुन उवाच
ये शास्त्रविधिमुत्सृज्य यजन्ते श्रद्धयान्विताः ।
तेषां निष्ठा तु का कृष्ण सत्त्वमाहो रजस्तमः ॥१७- १॥

arjuna uvāca
yē śāstravidhimutsṛjya yajantē śraddhayānvitāḥ ।
tēṣāṁ niṣṭhā tu kā kṛṣṇa sattvamāhō rajastamaḥ ॥ 17-1॥

Arjuna said:
"O Krishna! What is the faith of those who worship with devotion, though not following the injunctions of the scriptures? Is it sattvic, rajasic, or tamasic?"

श्रीभगवानुवाच
त्रिविधा भवति श्रद्धा देहिनां सा स्वभावजा ।
सात्त्विकी राजसी चैव तामसी चेति तां शृणु ॥१७- २॥

śrībhagavānuvāca
trividhā bhavati śraddhā dēhināṁ sā svabhāvajā ।
sāttvikī rājasī caiva tāmasī cēti tāṁ śṛṇu ॥ 17-2॥

The Lord said:
"The natural faith of the embodied is of three types: sattvic, rajasic, and tamasic. Hear now their description.

ॐ नमो भगवते वासुदेवाय
ōṁ namō bhagavatē vāsudēvāya 
  Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya

**317**
**Chapter 17**

The faith of people whose consciousness is limited by the body is sattvic, rajasic, and tamasic. Now Lord Shri Krishna describes these three types of faith.

Those who realize their limitation by physical boundaries and strive, through the practice of yoga, to awaken their boundless consciousness in order to overcome these limitations, are considered to possess sattvic faith.

Those who give preference to the body possess limited intellect, are obsessed with satisfying their senses, and act only with this aim. Driven by sensual pleasures, they are considered to possess rajasic faith.

And of those whose greater part of consciousness abides in a sleeping state, who do not know why or for what purpose they act, it is said that their faith is tamasic.

सत्त्वानुरूपा सर्वस्य श्रद्धा भवति भारत ।
श्रद्धामयोऽयं पुरुषो यो यच्छ्रद्धः स एव सः ॥१७- ३॥

sattvānurūpā sarvasya śraddhā bhavati bhārata ।
śraddhāmayō’yaṁ puruṣō yō yacchraddhaḥ sa ēva saḥ ॥ 17-3॥

O Bharata! The faith of everyone corresponds to his nature. Man is made of faith – as a man's faith is, so is he.

Only one's own mind impels a man to activity, manifesting through the body together with the infinite consciousness contained within it. People who know of the boundlessness of their mind, as well as those who do not even suspect it – all are impelled to action by the direct influence of the mind. Since the level of consciousness of different people differs, the faith that fills their actions is also different, corresponding to it. As is the individual level of a man's consciousness, so too is the direction of his actions.

**318**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

यजन्ते सात्त्विका देवान्यक्षरक्षांसि राजसाः ।
प्रेतान्भूतगणांश्चान्ये यजन्ते तामसा जनाः ॥१७- ४॥

yajantē sāttvikā dēvānyakśarakśānsi rājasāḥ ।
prētānbhūtagaṇānścānyē yajantē tāmasā janāḥ ॥ 17-4॥

Sattvic people worship the gods, rajasic people seek to propitiate yakshas and rakshasas, while tamasic people, trembling, appease spirits and ghosts.

Sattvic people burn with the desire to know the nature of Vasudeva, who lives in the heart of every being, awakening their full consciousness.

Those who are considered rajasic are occupied only with maintaining their own body, applying effort more than anything else to appeasing the senses and satiating self-conceit.

And people with tamasic consciousness spend their lives with a minimal level of awareness, for the sake of food and sex, eternally abiding in fear of the ghosts they worship.

अशास्त्रविहितं घोरं तप्यन्ते ये तपो जनाः ।
दम्भाहंकारसंयुक्ताः कामरागबलान्विताः ॥१७- ५॥

aśāstravihitaṁ ghōraṁ tapyantē yē tapō janāḥ ।
dambhāhaṁkārasaṁyuktāḥ kāmarāgabalānvitāḥ ॥ 17-5॥

Driven by pride and hypocrisy, overcome by passion and lust, such people perform terrible austerities, violating the injunctions of the scriptures.

Fools consider the histories of the sacred scriptures, which preserve the wisdom and experiences of the sages of antiquity who realized Time, as well as the methods for knowing truth mentioned therein, to be fiction. Overcome by lust, filled with vanity and arrogance, they strive only to gratify the body and senses and continue to burn in the terrible fire of anger.

**319**
**Chapter 17**

कर्षयन्तः शरीरस्थं भूतग्राममचेतसः ।
मां चैवान्तःशरीरस्थं तान्विद्ध्यासुरनिश्चयान् ॥१७- ६॥

karṣayantaḥ śarīrasthaṁ bhūtagrāmamacētasaḥ ।
māṁ caivāntaḥśarīrasthaṁ tānviddhyāsuraniścayān ॥ 17-6॥

Such fools, abiding in delusion, torment the material elements in the form of their own body and Me, who abides within their bodies. Know them to be of demonic inclinations.

The boundless consciousness of such people abides in a sleeping state, limiting itself only to sensual pleasures. Possessing demonic traits, by their actions they defile Vasudeva, who is hidden within them.

आहारस्त्वपि सर्वस्य त्रिविधो भवति प्रियः ।
यज्ञस्तपस्तथा दानं तेषां भेदमिमं शृणु ॥१७- ७॥

āhārastvapi sarvasya trividhō bhavati priyaḥ ।
yajñastapastathā dānaṁ tēṣāṁ bhēdamimaṁ śṛṇu ॥ 17-7॥

Even the food that a man prefers is of three types, as are yajna, charity, and austerity. Hear from Me about their distinguishing characteristics.

It is considered that people possessing sattvic, rajasic, and tamasic traits prefer different kinds of food. Based on these three mental predispositions, all their actions can also be divided into three categories.

आयुःसत्त्वबलारोग्यसुखप्रीतिविवर्धनाः ।
रस्याः स्निग्धाः स्थिरा हृद्या आहाराः सात्त्विकप्रियाः ॥१७- ८॥

āyuḥsattvabalārōgyasukhaprītivivardhanāḥ ।
rasyāḥ snigdhāḥ sthirā hṛdyā āhārāḥ sāttvikapriyāḥ ॥ 17-8॥

Juicy, oily, long-lasting, and appetizing food, which bestows longevity, strength, health, happiness, and cheerfulness, is preferred by sattvic people.

**320**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

Food that does not spoil with prolonged storage, is oily and juicy, conducive to longevity, and pleasant to look upon – this is what sattvic people, inspired to awaken their boundless consciousness, prefer to eat.

कट्‌वम्ललवणात्युष्णतीक्ष्णरूक्षविदाहिनः ।
आहारा राजसस्येष्टा दुःखशोकामयप्रदाः ॥१७- ९॥

kaṭ‌vamlalavaṇātyuṣṇatīkśṇarūkśavidāhinaḥ ।
āhārā rājasasyēṣṭā duḥkhaśōkāmayapradāḥ ॥ 17-9॥

Food that is bitter, sour, salty, very hot, pungent, dry, and burning, bringing grief, suffering, and disease, is dear to the rajasic.

People with rajasic traits love food that is excessively spicy, salty, and heavy, which helps to kindle the fire of passion in the body. Such food, besides the enjoyment of its taste, brings such people grief and suffering, being the cause of physical ailments.

यातयामं गतरसं पूति पर्युषितं च यत् ।
उच्छिष्टमपि चामेध्यं भोजनं तामसप्रियम् ॥१७- १०॥

yātayāmaṁ gatarasaṁ pūti paryuṣitaṁ ca yat ।
ucchiṣṭamapi cāmēdhyaṁ bhōjanaṁ tāmasapriyam ॥ 17-10॥

Tamasic people, on the other hand, value food that is spoiled and stale, prepared long ago, whose juices have dried up, as well as food left over by others and unclean.

Food that is stale and unclean, which begins to spoil three hours after its preparation, such as the meat of animals, imparts a foul odor to the body. Food for the preparation of which pieces of dead bodies are used, as well as alcohol obtained from the decomposition of spoiled ingredients – all this food is extremely dear to people possessing tamasic traits.

# Chapter 17

## 321

अफलाकाङ्क्षिभिर्यज्ञो विधिदृष्टो य इज्यते ।
यष्टव्यमेवेति मनः समाधाय स सात्त्विकः ॥१७-११॥

*aphalākāṅkśibhiryajñō vidhidṛṣṭō ya ijyatē ।
yaṣṭavyamēvēti manaḥ samādhāya sa sāttvikaḥ ॥ 17-11॥*

The yajña that corresponds to the injunctions of the sacred scriptures, performed as it should be and without desire for gain, is sāttvic.

Those who have realized their limitations, having understood the clues left by the ancient sages in the sacred texts, possess a firm intention to awaken their immeasurable consciousness. They strive to receive initiation into the practice of yoga and then receive it through their efforts. As a result of this practice, such people become free from all their desires. The yajña of yogic practice, performed to attain this state, is considered sāttvic.

अभिसंधाय तु फलं दम्भार्थमपि चैव यत् ।
इज्यते भरतश्रेष्ठ तं यज्ञं विद्धि राजसम् ॥१७-१२॥

*abhisaṁdhāya tu phalaṁ dambhārthamapi caiva yat ।
ijyatē bharataśrēṣṭha taṁ yajñaṁ viddhi rājasam ॥ 17-12॥*

O best of the Bharatas! The yajña driven only by pride and performed for the sake of profit, know to be rājasic.

Actions that only strengthen the limitation of consciousness by physical boundaries, performed solely for the attainment of sensory satisfaction and that increase hypocrisy and vanity, are called rājasic.

विधिहीनमसृष्टान्नं मन्त्रहीनमदक्षिणम् ।
श्रद्धाविरहितं यज्ञं तामसं परिचक्षते ॥१७-१३॥

*vidhihīnamasṛṣṭānnaṁ mantrahīnamadakśiṇam ।
śraddhāvirahitaṁ yajñaṁ tāmasaṁ paricakśatē ॥ 17-13॥*

But that which is performed without faith, without distribution of gifts, contrary to the injunctions of the scriptures, inconsistently and carelessly – such a yajña is considered tāmasic.

## 322
### Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

Uns systematic and carelessly performed actions, done unconsciously, not even thought through beforehand and performed without faith, are tāmasic.

देवद्विजगुरुप्राज्ञपूजनं शौचमार्जवम् ।
ब्रह्मचर्यमहिंसा च शारीरं तप उच्यते ॥१७-१४॥

*dēvadvijaguruprājñapūjanaṁ śaucamārjavam ।
brahmacaryamahiṁsā ca śārīraṁ tapa ucyatē ॥ 17-14॥*

Worship of the gods, the twice-born, the guru, and the wise; purity, simplicity, celibacy, and non-violence – these pertain to austerity of the body.

Those who have received instruction in yoga from a great Guru who has realized Brahman begin practice to know the true nature of the infinite unmanifest Time. They feel sincere respect for other sādhakas, for the Guru, and for the other sages who have realized Brahman.

Having fully realized the sacredness and importance of the body, they observe celibacy, restraining through the practice of yoga the loss of the key element of the body, in order to succeed in awakening their infinite consciousness. Awakening, the consciousness of such people becomes free from attraction to their own body and to the bodies of others. Such great people, established in non-violence, perform physical austerity in order to comprehend the Boundless through the body.

अनुद्वेगकरं वाक्यं सत्यं प्रियहितं च यत् ।
स्वाध्यायाभ्यसनं चैव वाङ्मयं तप उच्यते ॥१७-१५॥

*anudvēgakaraṁ vākyaṁ satyaṁ priyahitaṁ ca yat ।
svādhyāyābhyasanaṁ caiva vāṅmayaṁ tapa ucyatē ॥ 17-15॥*

The utterance of words that are gentle, truthful, kind, benevolent, and supported by constant practice of self-inquiry – such is austerity pertaining to speech.

## 323
### Chapter 17

Great people, who awaken the infinity of their consciousness through the body, speak only the truth, thereby approaching That Supreme Truth. They are constantly engaged in self-study, and their benevolent speech inspires others.

मनः प्रसादः सौम्यत्वं मौनमात्मविनिग्रहः ।
भावसंशुद्धिरित्येतत्तपो मानसमुच्यते ॥१७-१६॥

*manaḥ prasādaḥ saumyatvaṁ maunamātmavinigrahaḥ ।
bhāvasaṁśuddhirityētattapō mānasamucyatē ॥ 17-16॥*

Contentment, gentleness, silence, self-control, and purity of thought – know these as austerity of the mind.

Great people experience boundless happiness when their conscious mind comprehends the infinity of the intellect. Abiding in That Infinity, such people are of few words and appear serene and peaceful. Having known their limitations, they become established in boundlessness and, through their awakened consciousness, attain holiness of mind.

श्रद्धया परया तप्तं तपस्तत्त्रिविधं नरैः ।
अफलाकाङ्क्षिभिर्युक्तैः सात्त्विकं परिचक्षते ॥१७-१७॥

*śraddhayā parayā taptaṁ tapastattrividhaṁ naraiḥ ।
aphalākāṅkśibhiryuktaiḥ sāttvikaṁ paricakśatē ॥ 17-17॥*

Performed by those who have attained perfection, with exceptional devotion and without desire for results, these three kinds of austerity constitute sāttvic tapasyā.

Great sthita-prajña, who have attained dispassion and become established in samādhi through the practice of yoga, have called the diligent performance of the three fundamental stages of this yoga sāttvic tapas.

## 324
### Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

सत्कारमानपूजार्थं तपो दम्भेन चैव यत् ।
क्रियते तदिह प्रोक्तं राजसं चलमध्रुवम् ॥१७-१८॥

*satkāramānapūjārthaṁ tapō dambhēna caiva yat ।
kriyatē tadiha prōktaṁ rājasaṁ calamadhruvam ॥ 17-18॥*

But the disordered and unstable austerity performed for show, for the sake of recognition, honor, and admiration – know this in the world as rājasic.

People confined within physical limits and possessing limited intellect burn in the fire of rage. They are enslaved by insatiable arrogance, striving to conquer ever more respect, which they scarcely deserve, and to obtain ever greater sensory pleasures. All such actions, performed by limited gross consciousness and yielding only temporary results, are called rājasic tapasyā.

मूढग्राहेणात्मनो यत्पीडया क्रियते तपः ।
परस्योत्सादनार्थं वा तत्तामसमुदाहृतम् ॥१७-१९॥

*mūḍhagrāhēṇātmanō yatpīḍayā kriyatē tapaḥ ।
parasyōtsādanārthaṁ vā tattāmasamudāhṛtam ॥ 17-19॥*

But austerity performed foolishly and forcibly, through self-torture or for the destruction of others, is called tāmasic.

Actions performed by people with an inert mind, consumed by their own stupidity and causing harm to themselves and others, are called tāmasic.

## 325
### Chapter 17

दातव्यमिति यद्दानं दीयतेऽनुपकारिणे ।
देशे काले च पात्रे च तद्दानं सात्त्विकं स्मृतम् ॥१७-२०॥

*dātavyamiti yaddānaṁ dīyatē'nupakāriṇē ।
dēśē kālē ca pātrē ca taddānaṁ sāttvikaṁ smṛtam ॥ 17-20॥*

Giving performed with a sense of duty, without desire for reward, to one who is worthy, in a suitable place and at the proper time, is considered sāttvic.

Sāttvic giving is the gift of instruction in yoga with a proper assessment of the seeker's capacity. It is performed by the great sages who are conscious of Time, who have already transcended physical limitations and have concentrated upon the unmanifest truth of Time the full measurelessness of their awakened mind. This gift is intended only for one who is determined to know the true nature of Time, awakening the infinity of the mind by overcoming physical limitations.

यत्तु प्रत्युपकारार्थं फलमुद्दिश्य वा पुनः ।
दीयते च परिक्लिष्टं तद्दानं राजसं स्मृतम् ॥१७-२१॥

*yattu pratyupakārārthaṁ phalamuddiśya vā punaḥ ।
dīyatē ca parikliṣṭaṁ taddānaṁ rājasaṁ smṛtam ॥ 17-21॥*

But giving performed in expectation of reward or with an eye to profit, reluctantly and insultingly, is called rājasic.

People of limited intellect help others in the expectation that the recipient will continue to thank them and will serve them throughout their life. Such help, as well as giving done in an insulting manner and causing suffering – all such actions performed with an eye to mutual benefit are called rājasic.

## 326
### Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

अदेशकाले यद्दानमपात्रेभ्यश्च दीयते ।
असत्कृतमवज्ञातं तत्तामसमुदाहृतम् ॥१७-२२॥

*adēśakālē yaddānamapātrēbhyaśca dīyatē ।
asatkṛtamavajñātaṁ tattāmasamudāhṛtam ॥ 17-22॥*

But a gift offered to one who is unworthy, in an unsuitable place, at an improper time, disrespectfully and without regard – consider this tāmasic.

Whatever people do who are unable to distinguish the worthy from the unworthy and who, through their recklessness, cause harm to themselves and others, this invariably has a detrimental effect on someone. In the hope of even a small profit, they commit the most heinous acts without hesitation. All actions of such people are called tāmasic.

ॐतत्सदिति निर्देशो ब्रह्मणस्त्रिविधः स्मृतः ।
ब्राह्मणास्तेन वेदाश्च यज्ञाश्च विहिताः पुरा ॥१७-२३॥

*ōṁtatsaditi nirdēśō brahmaṇastrividhaḥ smṛtaḥ ।
brāhmaṇāstēna vēdāśca yajñāśca vihitāḥ purā ॥ 17-23॥*

"Om Tat Sat" – thus is Brahman designated, the primordial source of the scriptures, the creator of the sages who have known Him, and the cause of yajña.

That omnipresent unmanifest Brahman, the infinite Time, which sādhakas can come to know through the successful practice of the three stages of this ancient yoga, is designated by the symbol "Om."

The great sages of antiquity, who succeeded in realizing This Truth and attaining unity with It, preserved for the benefit of future seekers the indications of This supreme Truth in the sacred texts through the words "Om Tat Sat."

## 327
### Chapter 17

तस्मादोमित्युदाहृत्य यज्ञदानतपःक्रियाः ।
प्रवर्तन्ते विधानोक्ताः सततं ब्रह्मवादिनाम् ॥१७-२४॥

*tasmādōmityudāhṛtya yajñadānatapaḥkriyāḥ ।
pravartantē vidhānōktāḥ satataṁ brahmavādinām ॥ 17-24॥*

Therefore, in accordance with the scriptures, those who have known Brahman begin every yajña, giving, and austerity with the word "Om."

The methods of yoga that lead to the knowledge of the unmanifest Truth of Time through the overcoming of physical limits were indicated by the great souls conscious of Time and arose from that same unmanifest truth of Time, designated by the symbol "Om."

तदित्यनभिसन्धाय फलं यज्ञतपःक्रियाः ।
दानक्रियाश्च विविधाः क्रियन्ते मोक्षकाङ्क्षिभिः ॥१७-२५॥

*tadityanabhisandhāya phalaṁ yajñatapaḥkriyāḥ ।
dānakriyāśca vividhāḥ kriyantē mōkśakāṅkśibhiḥ ॥ 17-25॥*

With the word "Tat," those striving for liberation perform these actions without thought of reward.

The consciousness of Time, whose symbol is "Om," fills the consciousness of the Void. It is present everywhere, designated by the word "Tat." To become established in It, people aspiring to samādhi perform the practice of the various stages of the ancient yoga.

सद्भावे साधुभावे च सदित्येतत्प्रयुज्यते ।
प्रशस्ते कर्मणि तथा सच्छब्दः पार्थ युज्यते ॥१७-२६॥

*sadbhāvē sādhubhāvē ca sadityētatprayujyatē ।
praśastē karmaṇi tathā sacchabdaḥ pārtha yujyatē ॥ 17-26॥*

"Sat" indicates the eternal nature of Truth and one who follows It. Similarly, this word is used in auspicious rituals.

Great people, having successfully passed through the stages of yoga, became established in the consciousness of the Void and were able to obtain the direct darśana of Its four-armed embodiment.

## 328
### Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

They used the symbolic word "Sat" to indicate the unmanifest Time that fills the Void, knowing Its true nature. They succeeded in realizing that in this entire world there is but one truth – That unbearably radiant Truth of unmanifest Time.

यज्ञे तपसि दाने च स्थितिः सदिति चोच्यते ।
कर्म चैव तदर्थीयं सदित्येवाभिधीयते ॥१७-२७॥

*yajñē tapasi dānē ca sthitiḥ saditi cōcyatē ।
karma caiva tadarthīyaṁ sadityēvābhidhīyatē ॥ 17-27॥*

Those established in yajña, giving, and austerity are also called "Sat," as are the actions that lead to the attainment of this.

This universe, which is manifested by the supreme, indestructible Brahman, Time; all three stages of the ancient yoga that lead to Its knowledge; as well as the practice of these stages and instruction in them to the worthy – all these manifestations of unmanifest Time are called by the word "Sat."

अश्रद्धया हुतं दत्तं तपस्तप्तं कृतं च यत् ।
असदित्युच्यते पार्थ न च तत्प्रेत्य नो इह ॥१७-२८॥

*aśraddhayā hutaṁ dattaṁ tapastaptaṁ kṛtaṁ ca yat ।
asadityucyatē pārtha na ca tatprētya nō iha ॥ 17-28॥*

O Pārtha! Yajña, giving, austerity, or other actions performed without faith are considered "Asat." They have no power either in this world or beyond it."

All actions that only strengthen physical limitations and are performed solely for the satisfaction of the senses are called "Asat." People absorbed in such actions possess limited intellect, consider the sleeping infinite consciousness of their mind to be a fabrication, and do not believe in it. Established in "Asat," not having known death, they spend their lives in fear, which leads them only to greater fear beyond the threshold of death.

**329**
**Chapter 17**

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे श्रद्धात्रयविभागयोगो नाम सप्तदशोऽध्यायः ॥१७॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē śraddhātrayavibhāgayōgō nāma saptadaśō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 17॥

Om Tat Sat
Thus ends the dialogue between Krishna and Arjuna in the seventeenth chapter, "The Yoga of the Threefold Faith," of the Upanishad called "Shrimad Bhagavad Gita," which describes the knowledge of Brahman and the science of yoga.

अष्टादशोऽध्यायः मोक्षसंन्यासयोगः
aṣṭādaśō’dhyāyaḥ mōkṣasaṁnyāsayōgaḥ
Chapter 18
THE YOGA OF LIBERATION THROUGH RENUNCIATION

**332**
अर्जुन उवाच
संन्यासस्य महाबाहो तत्त्वमिच्छामि वेदितुम् ।
त्यागस्य च हृषीकेश पृथक्केशिनिषूदन ॥१८- १॥
arjuna uvāca
saṁnyāsasya mahābāhō tattvamicchāmi vēditum ।
tyāgasya ca hṛṣīkēśa pṛthakkēśiniṣūdana ॥ 18-1॥

Arjuna said:
"O Mahabaho! I wish to know, O Hrishikesha, O Keshinishudana¹, the essence of sannyasa and of renunciation, separately from each other."

"O Mahabaho! I wish to know the truth of sannyasa, as well as that which is called renunciation, separately. I beg you, explain this to me."

श्रीभगवानुवाच
काम्यानां कर्मणां न्यासं संन्यासं कवयो विदुः ।
सर्वकर्मफलत्यागं प्राहुस्त्यागं विचक्षणाः ॥१८- २॥
śrībhagavānuvāca
kāmyānāṁ karmaṇāṁ nyāsaṁ saṁnyāsaṁ kavayō viduḥ ।
sarvakarmaphalatyāgaṁ prāhustyāgaṁ vicakśaṇāḥ ॥ 18-2॥

The Lord said:
"The wise know the abandonment of actions motivated by desire as sannyasa; the discerning declare the renunciation of the fruits of all actions as tyaga."

Great men who have transcended physical limitations and awakened the dormant consciousness of their mind in its fullness, in the process of knowing the interrelation of the body and senses with the mind, understood that all desires arise from the mind. Through this knowledge, their desires dissolve in the mind itself. Such yogis, knowing the true nature of sannyasa, know the Creator of all, the unmanifest, imperishable Brahman, the Time abiding beyond the mind, and are known as established in sannyasa. Those who are able to become established in dispassion, having cast off their own limitation as a result of the practice of yoga, are known as those who have renounced the fruits of all their karma.

त्याज्यं दोषवदित्येके कर्म प्राहुर्मनीषिणः ।
यज्ञदानतपःकर्म न त्याज्यमिति चापरे ॥१८- ३॥
tyājyaṁ dōṣavadityēkē karma prāhurmanīṣiṇaḥ ।
yajñadānatapaḥkarma na tyājyamiti cāparē ॥ 18-3॥

Some say: "All actions are full of defects, and therefore they should be abandoned." Others explain: "Yajna, charity, and austerities should not be abandoned."

Others, who are unable to understand the truth of the origin of karma, are blinded by the radiance of those who are conscious of Time and, observing their state of relative inaction, suppose, even without performing yogic practice, that all karma is full of defects, and therefore it should be abandoned. The great ones conscious of Time have realized the truth and understood the interrelation of the organs and the mind. As a result of the practice of yoga, they have realized the true essence of the yajna of self-control; however, they do not consider it necessary to abandon practice, in order to inspire new seekers, and they continue their austerity of bestowing instructions in this teaching of yoga upon the worthy.

¹ "Conqueror of the demon Keshi"

**334**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

निश्चयं शृणु मे तत्र त्यागे भरतसत्तम ।
त्यागो हि पुरुषव्याघ्र त्रिविधः संप्रकीर्तितः ॥१८- ४॥
niścayaṁ śṛṇu mē tatra tyāgē bharatasattama ।
tyāgō hi puruṣavyāghra trividhaḥ saṁprakīrtitaḥ ॥ 18-4॥

O best of the Bharatas! Hear My decisive opinion on renunciation, which is declared to be of three kinds.

Lord Shri Krishna Himself communicates to seekers His judgment concerning the fundamental nature of renunciation through Arjuna. Since there are three types of personalities, renunciation is also found to be of three kinds.

यज्ञदानतपःकर्म न त्याज्यं कार्यमेव तत् ।
यज्ञो दानं तपश्चैव पावनानि मनीषिणाम् ॥१८- ५॥
yajñadānatapaḥkarma na tyājyaṁ kāryamēva tat ।
yajñō dānaṁ tapaścaiva pāvanāni manīṣiṇām ॥ 18-5॥

Yajna, charity, and austerities should not be abandoned – they must be performed; they purify the wise.

The great sthita-prajnas kindle the fire of yoga in their body and, offering their limitations as a sacrifice into it, awaken the boundlessness of their own dormant consciousness through resolute practice of yoga. Focusing that awakened infinity on the imperishable Brahman, the truth of Time, they attain Its realization. These great men do not abandon yogic practice, in order to inspire other sadhakas and seekers of yoga, and they bestow this great teaching upon the worthy, who in turn rise from the darkness of ignorance and become purified by performing this practice.

**335**
**Chapter 18**

एतान्यपि तु कर्माणि सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा फलानि च ।
कर्तव्यानीति मे पार्थ निश्चितं मतमुत्तमम् ॥१८- ६॥
ētānyapi tu karmāṇi saṅgaṁ tyaktvā phalāni ca ।
kartavyānīti mē pārtha niścitaṁ matamuttamam ॥ 18-6॥

O Partha! But even these actions should be performed, having abandoned attachment and expectation of results; such is My firm and supreme opinion.

Only those great men who, through yoga, have become free from desires and, knowing sannyasa, have realized the true nature of Time, can thus renounce the results of all their actions. Only such exceptional sthita-prajnas truly renounce karma. Only such great men, established in self-control, can be a source of inspiration for others.

नियतस्य तु संन्यासः कर्मणो नोपपद्यते ।
मोहात्तस्य परित्यागस्तामसः परिकीर्तितः ॥१८- ७॥
niyatasya tu saṁnyāsaḥ karmaṇō nōpapadyatē ।
mōhāttasya parityāgastāmasaḥ parikīrtitaḥ ॥ 18-7॥

Prescribed action should not be abandoned. Abandoning it out of delusion is declared to be tamasic.

The great ones conscious of Time preserved this ancient practice of yoga in the sacred scriptures, expressing their experience and memories in words. Abandonment of this practice, which through the knowledge of sannyasa gives the experience of the true nature of Time, abandonment even of the attempt to know Him, is called tamasic renunciation.

**336**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

दुःखमित्येव यत्कर्म कायक्लेशभयात्त्यजेत् ।
स कृत्वा राजसं त्यागं नैव त्यागफलं लभेत् ॥१८- ८॥
duḥkhamityēva yatkarma kāyaklēśabhayāttyajēt ।
sa kṛtvā rājasaṁ tyāgaṁ naiva tyāgaphalaṁ labhēt ॥ 18-8॥

If someone abandons actions, considering them to be productive of suffering or from fear of bodily discomfort, then due to such rajasic renunciation, he does not obtain the fruit of his self-sacrifice.

Abandonment of this great yogic practice out of fear of physical discomfort, instead of realizing its importance, is called rajasic renunciation. As a result of this, such people spend their entire lives in fear of death, remaining limited by physical boundaries.

कार्यमित्येव यत्कर्म नियतं क्रियतेऽर्जुन ।
सङ्गं त्यक्त्वा फलं चैव स त्यागः सात्त्विको मतः ॥१८- ९॥
kāryamityēva yatkarma niyataṁ kriyatē’rjuna ।
saṅgaṁ tyaktvā phalaṁ caiva sa tyāgaḥ sāttvikō mataḥ ॥ 18-9॥

O Arjuna! When a person performs prescribed actions as his duty, having become free from attachment and the desire for results, then his renunciation is considered sattvic.

Great men were able to become free from desires by practicing yoga, in accordance with the sacred scriptures, in order to transcend their physical boundaries and awaken the infinite consciousness of their mind. Attaining the state of nishkama, they become established in samadhi and realize that unmanifest supreme Truth of Time, focusing upon It their boundless consciousness awakened by their own practice of yoga. The renunciation of their limitation, performed by such great men, as well as the abandonment of the fruits of action which naturally accompanies their state, is called sattvic self-sacrifice.

**337**
**Chapter 18**

न द्वेष्ट्यकुशलं कर्म कुशले नानुषज्जते ।
त्यागी सत्त्वसमाविष्टो मेधावी छिन्नसंशयः ॥१८- १०॥
na dvēṣṭyakuśalaṁ karma kuśalē nānuṣajjatē ।
tyāgī sattvasamāviṣṭō mēdhāvī chinnasaṁśayaḥ ॥ 18-10॥

The intelligent person, abiding in sattva-guna, does not hate unskillful actions nor become attached to skillful ones.

The great sthita-prajnas realize the true nature of the imperishable Brahman, Time, which manifests all creation, and see everywhere in the universe only that supreme Truth. Established in self-control, such great men are not captivated by manifestations of skill nor do they regard the absence of skill with contempt. They know that the difference between the presence and absence of skill is relative, for both the one and the other are merely different manifestations of that one Presence.

न हि देहभृता शक्यं त्यक्तुं कर्माण्यशेषतः ।
यस्तु कर्मफलत्यागी स त्यागीत्यभिधीयते ॥१८- ११॥
na hi dēhabhṛtā śakyaṁ tyaktuṁ karmāṇyaśēṣataḥ ।
yastu karmaphalatyāgī sa tyāgītyabhidhīyatē ॥ 18-11॥

Since it is impossible for the embodied one to completely abandon activity, only he who has renounced the fruits of his actions is considered to have attained renunciation.

Ordinary people, whose consciousness is confined within physical boundaries, have not the slightest idea of the true boundlessness of their consciousness. They remain attached to the objects of the senses, performing their actions only to satisfy the desire for their fruits, and therefore remain limited within physical confines. In contrast, great men who perform the practice of yoga to awaken their dormant infinite consciousness, having caught a glimpse of it, become free from desires and renounce their limitation.

**338**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

अनिष्टमिष्टं मिश्रं च त्रिविधं कर्मणः फलम् ।
भवत्यत्यागिनां प्रेत्य न तु संन्यासिनां क्वचित् ॥१८- १२॥
aniṣṭamiṣṭaṁ miśraṁ ca trividhaṁ karmaṇaḥ phalam ।
bhavatyatyāgināṁ prētya na tu sannyāsināṁ kvacit ॥ 18-12॥

The actions of those who have not attained renunciation yield three kinds of fruits: favorable, unfavorable, and mixed. Sannyasis, however, are free from all three.

Ignorant people continue to fear death throughout their lives. Whatever good or bad deeds they perform to satisfy the impulses of the body, to which they are attached, they only continue to strengthen their pride and vanity. Such people, after death, are destined to reap the fruits of all such actions in subtle worlds, such as heaven or hell. Great men, who become fearless by knowing the true nature of sannyasa, become free from all desires. Such sthita-prajnas understand the relativity of good and bad and therefore abandon the striving for the fruits of karma. These great yogis, after death, enjoy immortality, passing through death by means of death.

पञ्चैतानि महाबाहो कारणानि निबोध मे ।
सांख्ये कृतान्ते प्रोक्तानि सिद्धये सर्वकर्मणाम् ॥१८- १३॥
pañcaitāni mahābāhō kāraṇāni nibōdha mē ।
sāṁkhyē kṛtāntē prōktāni siddhayē sarvakarmaṇām ॥ 18-13॥

O Mahabaho! The wise distinguish five factors for every action. Learn of them from Me.

The great sthita-prajnas, having known the fundamental essence of life, described five principal causes that give rise to activity and lead to its results.

**339**
**Chapter 18**

अधिष्ठानं तथा कर्ता करणं च पृथग्विधम् ।
विविधाश्च पृथक्चेष्टा दैवं चैवात्र पञ्चमम् ॥१८- १४॥
adhiṣṭhānaṁ tathā kartā karaṇaṁ ca pṛthagvidham ।
vividhāśca pṛthakcēṣṭā daivaṁ caivātra pañcamam ॥ 18-14॥

They are: the substratum (the body and its field of experience), the agent, the various instruments (the senses), the distinct and manifold efforts, and the fifth – daiva (the divine, Providence).

This body and the mind receiving experience through the body, the sense organs supplying the mind with various experiences, the separate efforts for acquiring various objects of the senses, and Vasudeva dwelling in the mind of each, eternally abiding in all that is enumerated, while simultaneously remaining transcendent to it – these are the five principal means manifesting life, which are the cause both of the arising of karma and of liberation from it.

शरीरवाङ्‌मनोभिर्यत्कर्म प्रारभते नरः ।
न्याय्यं वा विपरीतं वा पञ्चैते तस्य हेतवः ॥१८- १५॥
śarīravāṅ‌manōbhiryatkarma prārabhatē naraḥ ।
nyāyyaṁ vā viparītaṁ vā pañcaitē tasya hētavaḥ ॥ 18-15॥

Whatever action a man undertakes with body, speech, or mind, whether it be righteous or the reverse, these five are its causes.

Whatever a person does, whether he strengthens his physical limitations or awakens his infinite consciousness, rising above the limitations of the body, these very five components give rise to all his actions.

**340**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*tatraivaṁ sati kartāramātmānaṁ kēvalaṁ tu yaḥ |
paśyatyakṛtabuddhitvānna sa paśyati durmatiḥ || 18-16 ||*

But he who, contrary to this, due to ignorance, considers only himself the doer—he is a fool, devoid of vision.

Ordinary people do not know about these five constituents that give rise to every action, and because of their limited intellect, they consider only themselves the doers. Their consciousness sleeps, therefore they do not possess proper understanding even of their own actions.

*yasya nāhaṅkṛtō bhāvō buddhiryasya na lipyatē |
hatvāpi sa imāmllōkānna hanti na nibadhyatē || 18-17 ||*

He who is free from egoism and the imperfection of attachment, even destroying entire worlds, does not kill and is not bound.

A great person who has awakened his boundless consciousness through the regular practice of yoga and has realized the true nature of Time becomes dispassionate and sees in the entire universe only manifestations of Time. Uniting with that Truth which gives rise to the entire universe, he kills no one, even while committing killing.

*jñānaṁ jñēyaṁ parijñātā trividhā karmacōdanā |
karaṇaṁ karma kartēti trividhaḥ karmasaṁgrahaḥ || 18-18 ||*

Knowledge, the object of knowledge, and the knower—these are the three impulses to action. The work performed by the senses, the action, and the doer—these are the three aspects of karma.

☝
☝

**341**
**Chapter 18**

The process of cognition, the object of cognition, and the cognizer—these three causes impel action. The doer, the nature of the action, and the action itself—together these three constituents bring karma to its result.

*jñānaṁ karma ca kartā ca tridhaiva guṇabhēdataḥ |
prōcyatē guṇasaṁkhyānē yathāvacchṛṇu tānyap || 18-19 ||*

In accordance with the guṇas, there are three kinds of knowledge, activity, and performer. Now hear their exhaustive description.

The sages have spoken of three types of object of knowledge, process of cognition, and cognizer in accordance with the guṇas.

*sarvabhūtēṣu yēnaikaṁ bhāvamavyayamīkśatē |
avibhaktaṁ vibhaktēṣu tajjñānaṁ viddhi sāttvikam || 18-20 ||*

When that Eternal Presence, which abides as if divided in all beings, is perceived as indivisible—this is called sāttvic knowledge.

Great people, having known their physical limitations, awaken their infinite consciousness through the practice of yoga. Then they concentrate this infinite consciousness on that unmanifest Truth and everywhere behold only eternal Time, understanding that the entire universe is Its manifestation. This knowledge of theirs is called sāttvic.

☝
☝
☝

**342**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*pṛthaktvēna tu yajjñānaṁ nānābhāvānpṛthagvidhān |
vētti sarvēṣu bhūtēṣu tajjñānaṁ viddhi rājasam || 18-21 ||*

But that knowledge by which the entire diversity of various states of being in all creatures is perceived as divided—consider this rājasic.

People whose consciousness is confined within physical limits, having no conception of the boundlessness of their mind, consider the objects of the senses to be separate from the mind. They are unable to know the mind standing behind the senses, which receives experience. Not knowing the unmanifest Truth that manifests the universe, they see the Universe full of diverse, disparate objects. Such knowledge of theirs is called rājasic.

*yattu kṛtsnavadēkasminkāryē saktamahaitukam |
atattvārthavadalpaṁ ca tattāmasamudāhṛtam || 18-22 ||*

But knowledge which is wholly obsessed with only some one action, false, trivial, and without principle—this is considered tāmasic.

People, the greater part of whose consciousness abides in sleep, have a particular addiction to gratifying some specific sense organ. They are incapable of catching even a glimpse of the mind standing behind these senses. The trivial knowledge of such people is considered tāmasic.

☝
☝

**343**
**Chapter 18**

*niyataṁ saṅgarahitamarāgadvēṣataḥ kṛtam |
aphalaprēpsunā karma yattatsāttvikamucyatē || 18-23 ||*

Activity that is performed as a duty, by a person freed from attraction and aversion, who does not desire its fruit—this is called sāttvic.

Great people who have been able to know their boundless consciousness, having freed themselves from desires through the practice of yoga, and to comprehend by means of that awakened consciousness the true nature of the unmanifest Brahman, Time, which manifests the entire visible world, perform actions only to inspire others. Such karma is called sāttvic.

*yattu kāmēpsunā karma sāhaṁkārēṇa vā punaḥ |
kriyatē bahulāyāsaṁ tadrājasamudāhṛtam || 18-24 ||*

Performed with great effort for the sake of obtaining sensual pleasures or out of arrogance—such activity is considered rājasic.

People of limited intellect, who consider the body and sense organs as primary, perform actions only for their gratification. Such activity, which strengthens their self-satisfaction and vanity and holds consciousness within the body, is called rājasic.

☝
☝

**344**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*anubandhaṁ kśayaṁ hiṁsāmanavēkśya ca pauruṣam |
mōhādārabhyatē karma yattattāmasamucyatē || 18-25 ||*

And activity that brings destruction and suffering, performed in delusion, without consideration of capacity and consequences—this is called tāmasic.

Karma which brings harm to the one who performs it, as well as to others; that which leads to violence; and karma born of delusion, whose sole aim is the fulfillment of some particular desire without any assessment of one's own strength—this is considered tāmasic.

*muktasaṅgōnahaṁvādī dhṛtyutsāhasamanvitaḥ |
siddhyasiddhyōrnirvikāraḥ kartā sāttvika ucyatē || 18-26 ||*

A doer who is free from attachment and egoism, full of resolve and enthusiasm, unchanging in success and failure—this is considered sāttvic.

Great people who have awakened the boundless consciousness of their mind, have attained the realization of themselves as a manifestation of the indestructible truth of Time, and have regularly with patience and perseverance performed the practice of yoga for the knowledge of that Supreme Truth. They become fearless, having known through their constant practice the true nature of death. Such great people already know the relativity of success and failure, or, in other words, of existence and non-existence. Such great people perform karma only for the inspiration of others, since they have already risen above the necessity to perform any karma for themselves. Such great people are considered to be performing sāttvic activity.

☝
☝

**345**
**Chapter 18**

*rāgī karmaphalaprēpsurlubdhō hiṁsātmakō’śuciḥ |
harṣaśōkānvitaḥ kartā rājasaḥ parikīrtitaḥ || 18-27 ||*

A doer filled with attachment, who passionately craves the fruits of his actions, full of greed and cruelty, impure and subject to joys and sorrows—this is called rājasic.

He whose consciousness is bound by physical limits, who obsessively indulges the gratification of the senses, is ready to respond to any irritation with violence, and is full of impurity due to his sleeping consciousness. Not knowing the relativity of joy and grief, such a doer becomes elated by the satisfaction of his desires and wallows in sorrow when his desires are not fulfilled. Such people strive only for the satiation of their senses, thus only strengthening their pride and vanity. Performing trivial actions, they are known as those performing rājasic karma.

*ayuktaḥ prākṛtaḥ stabdhaḥ śaṭhō naiṣkṛtikō’lasaḥ |
viṣādī dīrghasūtrī ca kartā tāmasa ucyatē || 18-28 ||*

Unfocused, self-satisfied, coarse-minded, deceitful, cunning, destructive of others' well-being for his own interests, lazy, gloomy, and sluggish—such a doer is called tāmasic.

A person, the greater part of whose consciousness sleeps, who has not received even elementary education, full of falsehood, of unjustifiably high opinion of himself despite his recklessness, lazy and depressed, as he requires too much time even for simple actions—this is called a tāmasic doer.

☝
☝

**346**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*buddhērbhēdaṁ dhṛtēścaiva guṇatastrividhaṁ śṛṇu |
prōcyamānamaśēṣēṇa pṛthaktvēna dhanaṁjaya || 18-29 ||*

O Dhanañjaya! Now hear the exhaustive and detailed description of the three types of intellect and their corresponding resolve [dhāraṇā] according to the guṇas.

Now Lord Shri Krishna speaks of the three different levels of intellect and concentration of consciousness.

*pravṛttiṁ ca nivṛttiṁ ca kāryākāryē bhayābhayē |
bandhaṁ mōkśaṁ ca yā vētti buddhiḥ sā pārtha sāttvikī || 18-30 ||*

O Pārtha! The intellect that discriminates between the favorable and the unfavorable, knows action and inaction, comprehends fear and fearlessness, bondage and liberation—this is sāttvic.

The intellect which catches a glimpse of that vast consciousness that remains limited by the body, impels one to awaken that sleeping consciousness. Knowing the true nature of death, it rises above physical limitations and understands what is fear and what is fearlessness. Having realized the limitation of its own consciousness and that of others, it knows the unmanifest infinity extending beyond the body. Such an intellect is considered sāttvic.

*yayā dharmamadharmaṁ ca kāryaṁ cākāryamēva ca |
ayathāvatprajānāti buddhiḥ sā pārtha rājasī || 18-31 ||*

But the intellect that does not distinguish between dharma and adharma and is unable to grasp the true essence of favorable and unfavorable actions—consider this rājasic.

☝
☝

**347**
**Chapter 18**

And for the limited intellect, which cannot realize the mystery of the interconnection of the body and sense organs, death is incomprehensible, and therefore life too is not understood by it. It cannot even properly know what should be done and what should not be done. Such is the rājasic intellect.

*adharmaṁ dharmamiti yā manyatē tamasāvṛtā |
sarvārthānviparītānśca buddhiḥ sā pārtha tāmasī || 18-32 ||*

But that intellect which, shrouded by tamoguṇa, takes adharma for dharma and interprets everything perversely—know this, O Pārtha, as tāmasic.

The intellect with sleeping consciousness, full of the darkness of ignorance, which continues to fear death, gives preference to maintaining life at any cost, and perversely understands the utterances of the great sthita-prajña—such an intellect is considered tāmasic.

*dhṛtyā yayā dhārayatē manaḥprāṇēndriyakriyāḥ |
yōgēnāvyabhicāriṇyā dhṛtiḥ sā pārtha sāttvikī || 18-33 ||*

The unshakable resolve which, through the practice of yoga, sustains the coordinated activities of the mind, prāṇa, and senses—this is called sāttvic.

The boundless consciousness that is the result of the practice of yoga makes the intellect steady. Rising above physical limitations, such an intellect begins to hold the unmanifest infinity within itself and acts as a stimulus to know the true nature of Time through diligent practice of yoga, accomplished by the fusion of mind and prāṇa. The consciousness that sustains this boundlessness is called sāttvic.

☝
☝
☝

**348**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*yayā tu dharmakāmārthāndhṛtyā dhārayatē’rjuna ।
prasaṅgēna phalākāṅkśī dhṛtiḥ sā pārtha rājasī ॥ 18-34॥*

O Arjuna! The resolve with which a person follows dharma for the attainment of sensory pleasures [kama] and the accumulation of wealth [artha], desiring the fruits of his actions, know that to be rajasic.

The intellect, due to the limitation of consciousness by the body, holds onto the desire to satisfy the senses, false vanity, and pride. A person possessing such an intellect cannot free himself from attachments and continues to stubbornly hold only physical limitations within his consciousness. Such dharana is called rajasic.

*yayā svapnaṁ bhayaṁ śōkaṁ viṣādaṁ madamēva ca ।
na vimuñcati durmēdhā dhṛtiḥ sā pārtha tāmasī ॥ 18-35॥*

O Partha! The resolve, however, with which the impious continue to dwell in oblivion, grief, irritation, and madness, only strengthening their fears, is tamasic.

An ignorant person with a sleeping consciousness, due to his stupidity, indulges in madness, holding within his sleeping consciousness a multitude of fears, sorrows, and remaining in a state of dejection. Life is like a dream for him, for he does not know its essence. Such resolve is tamasic.

☝
☝

**349**
**Chapter 18**

*sukhaṁ tvidānīṁ trividhaṁ śṛṇu mē bharatarṣabha ।
Abhyāsādramatē yatra duḥkhāntaṁ ca nigacchati ॥ 18-36॥*

O best of the Bharatas! Now hear from Me about the three kinds of happiness that grant delight and put an end to suffering. Great men who, through the practice of yoga, have made their consciousness boundless and have known the true essence of life and death, have described three kinds of happiness.

*yattadagrē viṣamiva pariṇāmē’mṛtōpamam ।
tatsukhaṁ sāttvikaṁ prōktamātmabuddhiprasādajam ॥ 18-37॥*

That which is like poison at first, but in the end resembles the nectar of immortality – such happiness, born from the knowledge of the Atman, is considered sattvic.

In the beginning, when physical limitations are strong, the ancient yoga, performed with the firm intention to transcend them and know the true nature of death, may seem like poison. However, in its essence, it is the nectar of immortality, for it grants true knowledge of death and becomes the cause for abiding in the unmanifest consciousness of Time beyond it. Therefore, the satisfaction or joy from the practice of this yoga is called sattvic.

☝
☝

**350**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*viṣayēndriyasaṁyōgādyattadagrē’mṛtōpamam ।
pariṇāmē viṣamiva tatsukhaṁ rājasaṁ smṛtam ॥ 18-38॥*

But the happiness born from the contact of the sense organs with their objects, which is like nectar at first but like poison in the end, know that to be rajasic.

Consciousness limited by the satisfaction of the body and senses considers the fulfillment of desires to be the greatest joy. The result of such actions becomes the inability to know death, together with a strong attachment to the satisfaction of the senses. Therefore, the wise consider such joy to be like poison.

*yadagrē cānubandhē ca sukhaṁ mōhanamātmanaḥ ।
nidrālasyapramādōtthaṁ tattāmasamudāhṛtam ॥ 18-39॥*

But the happiness which, both in the beginning and in the end, only leads to delusion, born from drowsiness, laziness, and negligence, is called tamasic.

People with a sleeping consciousness, incapable of reflection, find happiness in idleness and sleep. Because of this, they remain in delusion throughout their entire lives. The inclination towards joy of this type is called tamasic.

*na tadasti pṛthivyāṁ vā divi dēvēṣu vā punaḥ ।
sattvaṁ prakṛtijairmuktaṁ yadēbhiḥ syāttribhirguṇaiḥ ॥ 18-40॥*

There is no being on earth, nor in heaven, nor even among the gods, who is free from the three gunas born of Prakriti. There is no one in this mortal world, nor in the subtle worlds beyond it, who transcends the three gunas – sattva, rajas, and tamas – manifested by Time Itself.

☝
☝
☝

**351**
**Chapter 18**

*brāhmaṇakśatriyaviśāṁ śūdrāṇāṁ ca parantapa ।
karmāṇi pravibhaktāni svabhāvaprabhavairguṇaiḥ ॥ 18-41॥*

O Parantapa! The duties of brahmins, kshatriyas, vaishyas, and shudras are determined by the gunas born of their own nature.

The mind, the boundless manifestation of the supreme indestructible Brahman, manifests to receive particular kinds of experience according to the three gunas through four types of embodiments (brahmins, kshatriyas, vaishyas, and shudras). Due to the difference in the gunas constituting these embodiments, their goals and duties leading to these goals are also different.

*śamō damastapaḥ śaucaṁ kśāntirārjavamēva ca ।
jñānaṁ vijñānamāstikyaṁ brahmakarma svabhāvajam ॥ 18-42॥*

Serenity, self-control, tapas, purity, forgiveness, sincerity, wisdom, knowledge, and faith – these are the natural duties of brahmins.

Those whose attachment to the senses disappears with the understanding of the connection between body and mind, as a result attain physical and mental purity. Such people strive to awaken their consciousness through the body and develop faith in the unmanifest indestructible Brahman, learning of Him from great men who are conscious of Time. Sattvaguna impels them to make efforts to know the true nature of Time through concentrating their entire consciousness upon Him. They become free from envy, realizing that this entire universe is born of That Unmanifest Supreme Being, and engage in awakening the sleeping consciousness of their mind, rising above physical limitations. Then they concentrate their awakened consciousness on the unmanifest truth of Time and thus know His true nature.

Only such people are capable of giving spiritual instruction to others. All these qualities manifest naturally in brahmins. As explained earlier in the fourth chapter, that part of humanity living between Israel and India, belonging to the Caucasian race but not fair-skinned, constitutes the brahmins of this Earth.

*śauryaṁ tējō dhṛtirdākśyaṁ yuddhē cāpyapalāyanam ।
dānamīśvarabhāvaśca kśātraṁ karma svabhāvajam ॥ 18-43॥*

Fearlessness, splendor, self-possession, awareness, courage, compassion, and the ability to lead – know these as the duties of kshatriyas, born of their own nature.

Natural fearlessness, strength, the ability to patiently perform one's duties for a long time, fighting in wars, steadfastness, not shrinking from accepting any challenge, even one unrelated to combat, offering help to others, and the ability to lead – these traits are naturally found in the kshatriya class. Their duties are also in accordance with these characteristic traits. Looking at humanity as a whole, we find that these are the innate traits of the white race. They are the kshatriyas of this planet.

☝

**353**
**Chapter 18**

*kṛṣigaurakśyavāṇijyaṁ vaiśyakarma svabhāvajam ।
paricaryātmakaṁ karma śūdrasyāpi svabhāvajam ॥ 18-44॥*

Agriculture, cattle-rearing, and trade are the natural duties of vaishyas. Service is the inherited duty of shudras.

Observing the inhabitants of the Earth of the Mongoloid race, possessing yellow skin, leads to the natural conclusion that the innate predisposition of vaishyas towards agriculture, animal husbandry, the ability to conduct trade, and diligence are characteristic of this race. They are all the vaishyas of this Earth.

The natural duty of shudras is to serve the three aforementioned classes. They also lag behind in the level of mental development compared to the representatives of the other three varnas, but in service they prove to be physically stronger. All these signs are naturally found among representatives of the black race. The majority of people of the black race are the natural-born shudras of this Earth.

*svē svē karmaṇyabhirataḥ sansiddhiṁ labhatē naraḥ ।
svakarmanirataḥ siddhiṁ yathā vindati tacchṛṇu ॥ 18-45॥*

A person devoted to his own natural duty attains perfection [siddhi]. Hear now about this!

Born into any of these four varnas and having realized his physical limitations in the striving to awaken the boundless consciousness of the unmanifest mind beyond them, he is able to awaken the hidden potentialities of his mind. Thus, he can know the unmanifest Time through his own practice of yoga, performed for the awakening of That Immeasurable Consciousness.

☝
☝

**354**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*yataḥ pravṛttirbhūtānāṁ yēna sarvamidaṁ tatam ।
svakarmaṇā tamabhyarcya siddhiṁ vindati mānavaḥ ॥ 18-46॥*

Only he becomes perfect who dedicates all his actions to That Eternal Truth, which gave rise to all beings and pervades this entire world.

The unmanifest indestructible Brahman, which gave birth to this entire world, is present everywhere, being the Creator of the universe. Man unites with This Light of all lights, Time, by awakening his consciousness and concentrating it upon Him.

*śrēyānsvadharmō viguṇaḥ paradharmātsvanuṣṭhitāt ।
svabhāvaniyataṁ karma kurvannāpnōti kilbiṣam ॥ 18-47॥*

Better is one's own duty, though imperfect, than another's duty well-performed. Performing the duty prescribed by providence, a person does not incur sin.

Although at first it may seem that the karma performed for awakening the boundless consciousness of the mind is not worth performing, still it is better to continue performing it than to remain limited by physical boundaries. For he who tries to know the boundlessness of the mind by breaking the barriers of physical limitations does not stain himself with the sin of ignorance born from the desire to indulge the senses and to pander to his hypocrisy and pride.

☝
☝

**355**
**Chapter 18**

*सहजं कर्म कौन्तेय सदोषमपि न त्यजेत् ।*
*सर्वारम्भा हि दोषेण धूमेनाग्निरिवावृताः ॥१८- ४८॥*
*sahajaṁ karma kauntēya sadōṣamapi na tyajēt ।*
*sarvārambhā hi dōṣēṇa dhūmēnāgnirivāvṛtāḥ ॥ 18-48॥*

O Kaunteya! Even if imperfect, follow your duty! Like fire enveloped by smoke, all action is full of defects.

The results of yoga, which elevates one beyond physical boundaries, may appear to possess defects at the beginning of practice, because ordinary people and beginners in yoga alike cannot imagine its unmanifest results. And yet, inspired by the example of great beings, one should not abandon actions that lead to complete peace through the knowledge of unmanifest Time. The ancient yoga that leads beyond the limitations of the body may seem imperfect, just as when kindling a fire one first encounters dirty smoke, which disappears soon after the fire blazes more strongly. This is because the ordinary person remains in fear of death throughout his life, giving preference to his body. Due to this fear that clouds vision, yoga, which leads to the knowledge of death, appears as something imperfect.

*असक्तबुद्धिः सर्वत्र जितात्मा विगतस्पृहः ।*
*नैष्कर्म्यसिद्धिं परमां संन्यासेनाधिगच्छति ॥१८- ४९॥*
*asaktabuddhiḥ sarvatra jitātmā vigataspṛhaḥ ।*
*naiṣkarmyasiddhiṁ paramāṁ saṁnyāsēnādhigacchati ॥ 18-49॥*

He whose intellect is free from attachment, who has mastered his mind and freed himself from material desires, attains through death the supreme perfection of inaction.

He who regularly performs the valiant practice of yoga, adhering with firm faith to the words of great beings who have known Brahman, transcends physical limitations and fully comprehends the boundlessness of the mind. Such a great man, freeing himself from desires after realizing the true nature of death, comes to know That Unmanifest Truth.

**356**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*सिद्धिं प्राप्तो यथा ब्रह्म तथाप्नोति निबोध मे ।*
*समासेनैव कौन्तेय निष्ठा ज्ञानस्य या परा ॥१८- ५०॥*
*siddhiṁ prāptō yathā brahma tathāpnōti nibōdha mē ।*
*samāsēnaiva kauntēya niṣṭhā jñānasya yā parā ॥ 18-50॥*

O Kaunteya! Now learn from Me in brief how the self-realized man attains Brahman, the supreme abode of knowledge.

Lord Shri Krishna now speaks of how great men awaken the sleeping consciousness of their mind, breaking through physical barriers, and then come to know that unmanifest, limitless, eternal Radiance of all radiance, Time, by concentrating their boundless consciousness upon It.

*बुद्ध्या विशुद्ध्या युक्तो धृत्यात्मानं नियम्य च ।*
*शब्दादीन्विषयांस्त्यक्त्वा रागद्वेषौ व्युदस्य च ॥१८- ५१॥*
*विविक्तसेवी लघ्वाशी यतवाक्कायमानसः ।*
*ध्यानयोगपरो नित्यं वैराग्यं समुपाश्रितः ॥१८- ५२॥*
*buddhyā viśuddhyā yuktō dhṛtyātmānaṁ niyamya ca ।*
*śabdādīnviṣayāṁstyaktvā rāgadvēṣau vyudasya ca ॥ 18-51॥*
*viviktasēvī laghvāśī yatavākkāyamānasaḥ ।*
*dhyānayōgaparō nityaṁ vairāgyaṁ samupāśritaḥ ॥ 18-52॥*

Endowed with supreme intellect, with resolve controlling himself, abstaining from sense objects, free from attraction and aversion, dwelling in solitude, moderate in eating, he whose mind, speech, and body are under his control, continuously immersed in self-contemplation and abiding under the shelter of vairāgya,

Great men, regularly practicing the ancient yoga, realize the supremacy of the mind in the relationship of mind and body, and attain flawlessness of intellect as a result of awakening their immeasurable consciousness and overcoming limitation. Such

**357**
**Chapter 18**

sages gain complete control over their own body and mind. They realize the relativity of love and hate, rising far above the objects of the senses. These great men, leaving the company of those with limited intellect, abide in a solitary place and partake of sattvic food. Transcending physical limitations, completely renouncing all sensual desires, they perform the valiant practice of yoga for establishment in the consciousness of Emptiness.

*अहंकारं बलं दर्पं कामं क्रोधं परिग्रहम् ।*
*विमुच्य निर्ममः शान्तो ब्रह्मभूयाय कल्पते ॥१८- ५३॥*
*ahaṁkāraṁ balaṁ darpaṁ kāmaṁ krōdhaṁ parigraham ।*
*vimucya nirmamaḥ śāntō brahmabhūyāya kalpatē ॥ 18-53॥*

He who has attained peace, having abandoned vanity, power, pride, lust, possessiveness, and the sense of ownership, becomes worthy of unity with Brahman.

Great men exert effort in this valiant practice of yoga for establishment in the consciousness of Emptiness, and having become established in it, become indifferent to all desires, anger, the tendency to hoard, and pride in the boundless power of their mind. Through the attainment of the consciousness of Emptiness, they become peaceful, ever abiding in That Supreme Immeasurability.

*ब्रह्मभूतः प्रसन्नात्मा न शोचति न काङ्क्षति ।*
*समः सर्वेषु भूतेषु मद्भक्तिं लभते पराम् ॥१८- ५४॥*
*brahmabhūtaḥ prasannātmā na śōcati na kāṅkśati ।*
*samaḥ sarvēṣu bhūtēṣu madbhaktiṁ labhatē parām ॥ 18-54॥*

United with Brahman, with a joyful self, he neither grieves nor desires. Equal towards all beings, he attains supreme devotion to Me.

The great man abiding in the ultimate infinity also comes to know the true nature of Time which fills it.

**358**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

All desires of such a man are fulfilled, and therefore he appears exceedingly happy. This perfected man becomes supremely devoted to Time, everywhere contemplating That great, unbearably radiant Time, Parameshvara.

*भक्त्या मामभिजानाति यावान्यश्चास्मि तत्त्वतः ।*
*ततो मां तत्त्वतो ज्ञात्वा विशते तदनन्तरम् ॥१८- ५५॥*
*bhaktyā māmabhijānāti yāvānyaścāsmi tattvataḥ ।*
*tatō māṁ tattvatō jñātvā viśatē tadanantaram ॥ 18-55॥*

Through his devotion he comes to know My true nature, and having known Me, he enters into Me.

Directly observing That Light of all light, the unbearably radiant Time, and realizing Its sovereign influence through the knowledge of Its true nature, such a yogi attains unity with It.

*सर्वकर्माण्यपि सदा कुर्वाणो मद्व्यपाश्रयः ।*
*मत्प्रसादादवाप्नोति शाश्वतं पदमव्ययम् ॥१८- ५६॥*
*sarvakarmāṇyapi sadā kurvāṇō madvyapāśrayaḥ ।*
*matprasādādavāpnōti śāśvataṁ padamavyayam ॥ 18-56॥*

He who is ever devoted to Me, performing all his duties, attains the eternal, imperishable Abode by My grace.

He who realizes the true nature of That immeasurable Light of all light, the unbearably radiant Time, remains devoted only to It, contemplating It everywhere. Such a man performs all his duties, inspired only by Time, and himself becomes the embodiment of Time, uniting with It by Its grace.

**359**
**Chapter 18**

*चेतसा सर्वकर्माणि मयि संन्यस्य मत्परः ।*
*बुद्धियोगमुपाश्रित्य मच्चित्तः सततं भव ॥१८- ५७॥*
*cētasā sarvakarmāṇi mayi saṁnyasya matparaḥ ।*
*buddhiyōgamupāśritya maccittaḥ satataṁ bhava ॥ 18-57॥*

Mentally dedicating all actions to Me, remaining devoted to Me, take refuge in Buddhi-Yoga, constantly fixing your mind on Me.

The great man who is conscious of Time becomes an example to be followed, inspiring beginning practitioners of yoga. Inspired by him, diligent sādhakas, having found refuge in Time Itself, begin to know the true nature of death, transcending physical limits.

*मच्चित्तः सर्वदुर्गाणि मत्प्रसादात्तरिष्यसि ।*
*अथ चेत्त्वमहंकारान्न श्रोष्यसि विनङ्क्ष्यसि ॥१८- ५८॥*
*maccittaḥ sarvadurgāṇi matprasādāttariṣyasi ।*
*atha cēttvamahaṁkārānna śrōṣyasi vinaṅkśyasi ॥ 18-58॥*

Fixing your mind on Me, by My grace you will cross over all difficulties. But know that you will perish if, out of egoism, you do not heed Me.

By the grace of Time, the yogi places his mind in It, performing the practice of yoga, and, transcending physical limits, overcomes the barrier of death. Thus, surpassing death, he enjoys the nectar of immortality.

But he who, due to his limited intellect, considers sensual pleasures of primary importance and does not strive to awaken his sleeping consciousness in order to know death, is destroyed again and again by his fear of death.

**360**
**Shrimad Bhagavad Gita**

*यदहंकारमाश्रित्य न योत्स्य इति मन्यसे ।*
*मिथ्यैष व्यवसायस्ते प्रकृतिस्त्वां नियोक्ष्यति ॥१८- ५९॥*
*yadahaṁkāramāśritya na yōtsya iti manyasē ।*
*mithyaiṣa vyavasāyastē prakṛtistvāṁ niyōkśyati ॥ 18-59॥*

If, heeding your egoism, you think, "I will not fight," vain is such your resolve; you will be engaged in battle by your own nature.

He whose intellect is confined within physical limits, who does not resolve to know death and awaken his boundless consciousness, does not understand that sooner or later his own mind will impel him to practice yoga for the awakening of his immeasurable consciousness.

*स्वभावजेन कौन्तेय निबद्धः स्वेन कर्मणा ।*
*कर्तुं नेच्छसि यन्मोहात्करिष्यस्यवशोऽपि तत् ॥१८- ६०॥*
*svabhāvajēna kauntēya nibaddhaḥ svēna karmaṇā ।*
*kartuṁ nēcchasi yanmōhātkariṣyasyavaśō’pi tat ॥ 18-60॥*

O Kaunteya! Bound by your own action born of your own nature, even against your will you will do that which, out of delusion, you do not wish to do.

A man deceived by the desire for sensual pleasures, even while remaining confined by physical limits, will sooner or later begin to try to awaken his immeasurable consciousness, driven by the boundless intellect hidden within him.

*ईश्वरः सर्वभूतानां हृद्देशेऽर्जुन तिष्ठति ।*
*भ्रामयन्सर्वभूतानि यन्त्रारूढानि मायया ॥१८- ६१॥*
*īśvaraḥ sarvabhūtānāṁ hṛddēśē’rjuna tiṣṭhati ।*
*bhrāmayansarvabhūtāni yantrārūḍhāni māyayā ॥ 18-61॥*

O Arjuna! The Lord abides in the heart of all beings, and by His Māyā spins all beings mounted on a machine.

That unmanifest Ruler of all, the Light of all light, abides in the heart of every being and, like a mechanism, governs this embodiment through the mind.

**361**
**Chapter 18**

*तमेव शरणं गच्छ सर्वभावेन भारत ।*
*तत्प्रसादात्परां शान्तिं स्थानं प्राप्स्यसि शाश्वतम् ॥१८- ६२॥*
*tamēva śaraṇaṁ gaccha sarvabhāvēna bhārata ।*
*tatprasādātparāṁ śāntiṁ sthānaṁ prāpsyasi śāśvatam ॥ 18-62॥*

O Bhārata! Seek refuge in Him alone with your whole being. By His grace you will attain supreme peace and the Eternal Abode.

He who resolutely performs the practice of yoga in order to know the Ruler of this body, which is like a mechanism, catching a glimpse of Him, awakens the immeasurable consciousness of his mind. Through this he understands that the manifestation of the entire world is a sacred gift of Vāsudeva. The great man who attains supreme peace, realizing this, merges with that unmanifest Vāsudeva, the embodiment of Time.

*इति ते ज्ञानमाख्यातं गुह्याद्‌गुह्यतरं मया ।*
*विमृश्यैतदशेषेण यथेच्छसि तथा कुरु ॥१८- ६३॥*
*iti tē jñānamākhyātaṁ guhyād‌guhyataraṁ mayā ।*
*vimṛśyaitadaśēṣēṇa yathēcchasi tathā kuru ॥ 18-63॥*

Thus have I revealed to you this most secret knowledge, the Secret of all secrets. Reflect deeply upon it, and then act as you wish.

Great beings conscious of Time have expressed this supremely secret knowledge through the sacred scriptures in symbolic form for the benefit of all humanity.

*सर्वगुह्यतमं भूयः शृणु मे परमं वचः ।*
*इष्टोऽसि मे दृढमिति ततो वक्ष्यामि ते हितम् ॥१८- ६४॥*
*sarvaguhyatamaṁ bhūyaḥ śṛṇu mē paramaṁ vacaḥ ।*
*iṣṭō’si mē dṛḍhamiti tatō vakśyāmi tē hitam ॥ 18-64॥*

Hear once again from Me these words of secret wisdom. I proclaim them for your benefit, for you are very dear to Me.

Now all this secret knowledge is set forth once again for the benefit of

362
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

humanity as a whole and especially for those who can understand
these instructions and be inspired to know the unmanifest Truth
of Time.

मन्मना भव मद्भक्तो मद्याजी मां नमस्कुरु ।
मामेवैष्यसि सत्यं ते प्रतिजाने प्रियोऽसि मे ॥१८- ६५॥
manmanā bhava madbhaktō madyājī māṁ namaskuru ।
māmēvaiṣyasi satyaṁ tē pratijānē priyō’si mē ॥ 18-65॥

Fix your mind on Me, be devoted to Me, bow down before
Me, dedicating all actions to Me. You will surely attain
Me. I promise you this, for you are dear to Me.

“Focus the boundless consciousness of your mind on the Light of every
light, the unbearably dazzling Time. Dedicate your devotion to Him.
Place upon Time Itself the four life-duties performed by your body. Bow
down before that unmanifest, great, eternal Time, realizing the unity of
past, present, and future. By doing this through the practice of ancient
yoga, you will become exceedingly dear to Time Itself.”

सर्वधर्मान्परित्यज्य मामेकं शरणं व्रज ।
अहं त्वां सर्वपापेभ्यो मोक्षयिष्यामि मा शुचः ॥१८- ६६॥
sarvadharmānparityajya māmēkaṁ śaraṇaṁ vraja ।
ahaṁ tvāṁ sarvapāpēbhyō mōkśayiṣyāmi mā śucaḥ ॥ 18-66॥

Seek refuge in Me alone, abandoning all other duties. I will
liberate you from all your sins. Do not worry.

“Renounce the limitations of the body and senses that restrain
the mind. Awaken the boundless consciousness of your mind and
focus that consciousness on the unbearably dazzling Time.
Through this, know the true nature of Time and surrender yourself to It.
Time, the primordial Supreme Lord, will surely free you
from the sin of ignorance, born of limited consciousness.
Do not worry.”

☝
☝

363
Chapter 18

इदं ते नातपस्काय नाभक्ताय कदाचन ।
न चाशुश्रूषवे वाच्यं न च मां योऽभ्यसूयति ॥१८- ६७॥
idaṁ tē nātapaskāya nābhaktāya kadācana ।
na cāśuśrūṣavē vācyaṁ na ca māṁ yō’bhyasūyati ॥ 18-67॥

Do not reveal this secret to one who is not inclined to austerity, who is not
devoted, who does not wish to listen, nor to one who is ill-disposed toward Me.

This ancient teaching of yoga leads to the direct perception
of the unbearable, super-brilliant Time through the awakening of the
boundless consciousness of the intellect. Instructions in
this secret practice should never be given to one who does not
possess the mind for it, who is not disposed toward Time due to
laziness arising from bad intentions, to that person
who does not have even a glimpse of their hidden boundlessness,
nor desires to know it.

य इमं परमं गुह्यं मद्भक्तेष्वभिधास्यति ।
भक्तिं मयि परां कृत्वा मामेवैष्यत्यसंशयः ॥१८- ६८॥
ya imaṁ paramaṁ guhyaṁ madbhaktēṣvabhidhāsyati ।
bhaktiṁ mayi parāṁ kṛtvā māmēvaiṣyatyasaṁśayaḥ ॥ 18-68॥

But he who, worshipping Me, sows this secret knowledge among
My devotees, will undoubtedly attain Me.

A devotee of Time alone, a great Time-realized
person, gives instructions in this supremely secret
teaching of yoga to people who strive to overcome physical limitations,
awaken the boundless consciousness of their mind, and know the
truth of Time. Such a great soul, contemplating the truth of Time in every
creature, transcends death, uniting with
this dazzlingly radiant Time.

☝
☝

364
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

न च तस्मान्मनुष्येषु कश्चिन्मे प्रियकृत्तमः ।
भविता न च मे तस्मादन्यः प्रियतरो भुवि ॥१८- ६९॥
na ca tasmānmanuṣyēṣu kaścinmē priyakṛttamaḥ ।
bhavitā na ca mē tasmādanyaḥ priyatarō bhuvi ॥ 18-69॥

No one among men can be more pleasing to Me, and there is
none dearer to Me in this world.

अध्येष्यते च य इमं धर्म्यं संवादमावयोः ।
ज्ञानयज्ञेन तेनाहमिष्टः स्यामिति मे मतिः ॥१८- ७०॥
adhyēṣyatē ca ya imaṁ dharmyaṁ saṁvādamāvayōḥ ।
