jñānayajñēna tēnāhamiṣṭaḥ syāmiti mē matiḥ ॥ 18-70॥

Whoever studies this our spiritual dialogue, I will be honored by that
sacrifice of knowledge; such is My principle.

श्रद्धावाननसूयश्च शृणुयादपि यो नरः ।
सोऽपि मुक्तः शुभाँल्लोकान्प्राप्नुयात्पुण्यकर्मणाम् ॥१८- ७१॥
śraddhāvānanasūyaśca śṛṇuyādapi yō naraḥ ।
sō’pi muktaḥ śubhāṁllōkānprāpnuyātpuṇyakarmaṇām ॥ 18-71॥

A man filled with faith, listening without envy, will also be
liberated and attain the pure worlds of the righteous.

कच्चिदेतच्छ्रुतं पार्थ त्वयैकाग्रेण चेतसा ।
कच्चिदज्ञानसंमोहः प्रनष्टस्ते धनंजय ॥१८- ७२॥
kaccidētacchrutaṁ pārtha tvayaikāgrēṇa cētasā ।
kaccidajñānasaṁmōhaḥ pranaṣṭastē dhanaṁjaya ॥ 18-72॥

O Pārtha! Have you listened with single-minded attention?
Has the delusion born of your ignorance been dispelled, O Dhanañjaya?”

365
Chapter 18

अर्जुन उवाच
नष्टो मोहः स्मृतिर्लब्धा त्वत्प्रसादान्मयाच्युत ।
स्थितोऽस्मि गतसन्देहः करिष्ये वचनं तव ॥१८- ७३॥
arjuna uvāca
naṣṭō mōhaḥ smṛtirlabdhā tvatprasādānmayācyuta ।
sthitō’smi gatasandēhaḥ kariṣyē vacanaṁ tava ॥ 18-73॥

Arjuna said:
“O Acyuta! By Your grace, my delusion is dispelled, and I have
regained my true memory. I am free from doubt and ready to
fulfill all that You have said.”

सञ्जय उवाच
इत्यहं वासुदेवस्य पार्थस्य च महात्मनः ।
संवादमिममश्रौषमद्भुतं रोमहर्षणम् ॥१८- ७४॥
sañjaya uvāca
ityahaṁ vāsudēvasya pārthasya ca mahātmanaḥ ।
saṁvādamimamaśrauṣamadbhutaṁ rōmaharṣaṇam ॥ 18-74॥

Sañjaya said:
“Thus I heard this wondrous, thrilling dialogue between Lord
Vāsudeva and the great Arjuna.

व्यासप्रसादाच्छ्रुतवानेतद्गुह्यमहं परम् ।
योगं योगेश्वरात्कृष्णात्साक्षात्कथयतः स्वयम् ॥१८- ७५॥
vyāsaprasādācchrutavānētadguhyamahaṁ param ।
yōgaṁ yōgēśvarātkṛṣṇātsākśātkathayataḥ svayam ॥ 18-75॥

By the grace of Vyāsa, I personally came to know the secret of this great yoga,
as it was spoken by the Lord of Yoga, Kṛṣṇa Himself.

366
Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā

राजन्संस्मृत्य संस्मृत्य संवादमिममद्भुतम् ।
केशवार्जुनयोः पुण्यं हृष्यामि च मुहुर्मुहुः ॥१८- ७६॥
rājansansmṛtya saṁsmṛtya saṁvādamimamadbhutam ।
kēśavārjunayōḥ puṇyaṁ hṛṣyāmi ca muhurmuhuḥ ॥ 18-76॥

O King! Remembering again and again this wonderful dialogue
between Keśava and Arjuna, I rejoice repeatedly.

तच्च संस्मृत्य संस्मृत्य रूपमत्यद्भुतं हरेः ।
विस्मयो मे महान् राजन्हृष्यामि च पुनः पुनः ॥१८- ७७॥
tacca saṁsmṛtya saṁsmṛtya rūpamatyadbhutaṁ harēḥ ।
vismayō mē mahān rājanhṛṣyāmi ca punaḥ punaḥ ॥ 18-77॥

And when my mind returns to that wondrous form of Lord Hari,
I am filled with great wonder, and I rejoice again and again.

यत्र योगेश्वरः कृष्णो यत्र पार्थो धनुर्धरः ।
तत्र श्रीर्विजयो भूतिर्ध्रुवा नीतिर्मतिर्मम ॥१८- ७८॥
yatra yōgēśvaraḥ kṛṣṇō yatra pārthō dhanurdharaḥ ।
tatra śrīrvijayō bhūtirdhruvā nītirmatirmama ॥ 18-78॥

Where Kṛṣṇa, the Lord of yoga, and where Arjuna, the great archer,
there is certain victory, prosperity, and unwavering morality.
Such is my conviction.”

ॐ तत्सदिति श्रीमद्भगवद्गीतासूपनिषत्सु ब्रह्मविद्यायां योगशास्त्रे
श्रीकृष्णार्जुनसंवादे मोक्षसंन्यासयोगो नामाष्टादशोऽध्यायः ॥१८॥
ōṁ tatsaditi śrīmadbhagavadgītāsūpaniṣatsu brahmavidyāyāṁ yōgaśāstrē
śrīkṛṣṇārjunasaṁvādē mōkśasaṁnyāsayōgō nāmāṣṭādaśō’dhyāyaḥ ॥ 18॥

  Oṁ Tat Sat
Thus concludes the dialogue between Kṛṣṇa and Arjuna in the eighteenth
chapter, entitled “The Yoga of Liberation through Self-Renunciation,” of the
Upaniṣad “Śrīmad Bhagavad Gītā,” which expounds the knowledge of
Brahman and the science of yoga.

Other Publications by the Author

“Haṭha Yoga Pradīpikā” by Svātmārāma:
Instructions on Kriyā Yoga

“Haṭha Yoga Pradīpikā” is the most enigmatic of the ancient
texts on yoga, detailing all the steps on the path
to self-realization. This book is unique in that the
translation and commentary are given for the first time by a realized yogi.
The commentaries reveal in detail the step-by-step execution of the
practice of kriyā yoga in the interpretation of the fifth Guru of the
Paramparā of Babaji.

“Yoga Darśana”:
A Yogic Commentary

“Yoga Sūtras” of Patañjali, also known as “Yoga
Darśana,” is the foundational text of the yogic tradition,
one of the six traditional schools of Indian philosophical
thought. Four short chapters contain 196 sūtras of the quintessence
of yogic wisdom.
Despite its brevity, it is the most poetic and inspiring
work among the sacred texts of yoga. Only a
practitioner who has attained the stages described in the book can fully
comprehend the essence of the text — and Shailendra Sharma brilliantly reveals
its profound meaning to the reader.

“Śiva Sūtras”:
A Yogic Commentary

About 250 years ago, the Kashmiri brāhmaṇa Vasugupta received
instructions in a dream from Lord Śiva Himself — to find a large
stone in a cave on the hill of Śaṅkara. It was said that the
spiritual knowledge thus obtained, bestowed by Śiva Himself, Vasugupta
was to absorb and spread for the benefit of people. The

next day, 77 sūtras engraved on the stone were
found. They represent brief yet multifaceted and
concise aphorisms on the precise methods of realization. Guided by the
knowledge gained after long years of steadfast yogic practice,
Shailendra Sharma provides a profound revelation of the essence
of this sacred text in his commentaries.

“Thorns and Roses”
A collection of aphorisms and thoughts, a bouquet of flowers and thorns from the garden
of being, the wisdom of life that only a yogi can convey.

“The Wayfarer”
Our spirit is an eternal traveler. Overcoming difficulties and
trials on the path to a metaphysical goal — the edge of the horizon,
the author shares his observations and experiences with other travelers
in the form of inspiring poems.

“At the Right Hand of God”
A collection of darśanas (daily conversations with disciples and visitors)
illuminates the widest range of topics discussed over the last
20 years. Describing powerful techniques of Kriyā Yoga,
pointing the way to the discovery of your own immortal
substance, transforming conventional notions of God,
Time, and Creation, this book is for seekers of truth.

These books are available at:
www.gurujibooks.com   www.amazon.com
More detailed information about the author can be found at:
www.shailendrasharma.com
